# vbuff - 500+ Problems, Improvements, and Things Done Wrong (extends docs/code-audit-top-50.md)

> This picks up where [`docs/code-audit-top-50.md`](code-audit-top-50.md) (items 1-50) left off: **506** 
> additional, distinct items covering SOLID/DRY architecture, security, platform parity, storage, 
> concurrency, performance, testing, Rust idiom, configuration UX, GUI/visual design, documentation, and 
> dependency/extensibility concerns - numbered 51-556 so the two files together form one continuous, 
> non-overlapping catalog against the current codebase. Generated by 16 parallel category agents, each 
> instructed to ground every `problem`-kind item in an actual file/line and to avoid anything already in 
> the first 50, then critiqued by a second pass per category that re-read the cited source before 
> accepting each claim. A verification pass sampled 40 `problem` items for a final adversarial check; 
> roughly half of that sample could not complete (provider rate-limiting), so treat unverified `problem` 
> items as reviewed-once (by the critique pass) rather than independently double-checked - if you're about 
> to act on one, a quick read of the cited file first is still worth it. `improvement`/`idea` items are 
> forward-looking recommendations in the same spirit as `docs/mistakes-top-500.md` and `docs/ideas-top-300.md`.

Severity: 🔴 critical · 🟠 high · 🟡 medium · 🟢 low. Kind is noted inline as `[problem]`, `[improvement]`, or `[idea]`.

## Security & privacy (additional, beyond docs/code-audit-top-50.md's first 10)

51. **Config and DB files are created with process umask, never hardened to 0600** `[problem]` 🟠 `[high]` - Config::save() (src/config.rs:72-80) calls std::fs::write(&path, text) and Store::open_default() (crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:38-44) calls std::fs::create_dir_all + Connection::open, with no permission-setting call anywhere in either crate. A grep for set_permissions/Permissions/mode( across src/ and crates/ returns zero hits. On a multi-user Linux box with a permissive umask (022, or 002 on distros with group-writable homes), history.db and config.toml end up world- or group-readable, exposing the full plaintext clip history (already flagged as unencrypted in top-50 item 1) to any other local user who can read the path. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:38-44 (open_default); src/config.rs:72-80 (save); grep -rn 'set_permissions|Permissions|mode(' src crates -> no matches._
52. **config_path() and default_db_path() are independently reimplemented and can diverge on Linux** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - src/config.rs:92-96 resolves the config dir via the `dirs` crate's dirs::config_dir(), while crates/vbuff-store/src/paths.rs:8-41 hand-rolls its own resolution (reading XDG_DATA_HOME/HOME directly), with the file's own comment stating this is 'to avoid a hard `dirs` dependency' in that crate. If XDG_CONFIG_HOME and XDG_DATA_HOME point to directories with different ownership or permission characteristics (a shared/mounted directory, a differently-permissioned tmpfs), config.toml and history.db land in two locations governed by two independent path-resolution code paths with no test asserting they agree, and no reconciliation logic if they don't. _Evidence: src/config.rs:92-96 (config_path via dirs::config_dir); crates/vbuff-store/src/paths.rs:8-41 (default_db_path, hand-rolled XDG_DATA_HOME/HOME resolution, comment explicitly avoiding the `dirs` crate)._
53. **Neither config_path() nor default_db_path() validates the resolved directory is owned by the current user** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - Both config_path() (src/config.rs:92-96) and default_db_path() (crates/vbuff-store/src/paths.rs:8-41) trust environment variables (XDG_CONFIG_HOME, XDG_DATA_HOME, HOME, APPDATA) unconditionally, with no check that the resolved directory's owner matches the current uid or that it is not a symlink into another user's tree. A misconfigured or stale HOME (e.g. a shared CI runner, a container reusing a cached environment) silently redirects the entire clip history into a directory the running user does not actually control, with no error surfaced anywhere in Config::load_or_create or Store::open_default. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/paths.rs:20-35 (std::env::var_os("HOME")/"XDG_DATA_HOME" used directly, no ownership check); src/config.rs:93-95 (dirs::config_dir() used the same way, no ownership check)._
54. **toml::from_str on config.toml has no size cap before parsing** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - Config::load_or_create() (src/config.rs:58-69) does std::fs::read_to_string(&path) followed by toml::from_str with no upper bound on file size. Since config.toml lives in a user-writable directory, a corrupted or maliciously grown file (e.g. left over from a crash mid-write during save()) is read fully into memory before the TOML parser even runs, giving a trivial local memory-exhaustion vector on every vbuff startup. _Evidence: src/config.rs:58-69 (load_or_create: std::fs::read_to_string then toml::from_str, no length check)._
55. **Config::save() is not atomic; a crash mid-write can corrupt config.toml and prevent startup** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - Config::save() (src/config.rs:72-80) writes directly to the final config_path() via std::fs::write, which truncates-then-writes in place rather than write-to-temp-then-rename. A crash, power loss, or disk-full condition during that write leaves a truncated config.toml; on the next launch, Config::load_or_create (src/config.rs:60-63) finds path.exists() true and toml::from_str hard-errors, which main() (src/main.rs:47, .context("loading config")?) propagates as a fatal startup error with no fallback to defaults - a corrupted config file permanently prevents vbuff from starting until the user manually deletes it. _Evidence: src/config.rs:72-80 (save: std::fs::write, no temp+rename); src/main.rs:47 (Config::load_or_create().context("loading config")? - fatal on parse error)._
56. **WAL mode is enabled with no checkpoint call anywhere, so deleted clip bytes can persist in the -wal sidecar file** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - Store::from_connection (crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:58-64) enables WAL mode via pragma_update(None, "journal_mode", "WAL"), which causes SQLite to create history.db-wal and history.db-shm sibling files. No PRAGMA wal_checkpoint call exists anywhere in lib.rs's delete/clear/clear_all/enforce_cap, and neither sidecar file is covered by any permission-hardening (there is none for the main DB file either, per the separate umask finding). WAL pages can retain recently-committed data - including a clip's bytes after Store::delete removes its row from the main file - until SQLite's own automatic checkpoint eventually runs, so a user who deletes a sensitive clip and assumes it is gone may still have its bytes recoverable from the -wal file on disk. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:59 (pragma_update ... "journal_mode", "WAL"); no PRAGMA wal_checkpoint call anywhere in lib.rs's delete (162-168), clear (171-175), clear_all (178-181), or enforce_cap (201-219)._
57. **delete()/clear()/clear_all() issue plain SQL DELETE with no secure_delete pragma or VACUUM** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - Store::delete (lib.rs:162-168), Store::clear (lib.rs:171-175), and Store::clear_all (lib.rs:178-181) all issue plain SQL DELETE statements. Standard SQLite semantics mean a deleted row's bytes remain in the B-tree pages (marked free, not zeroed) until a future INSERT reuses that page or VACUUM runs; from_connection (lib.rs:58-64) sets journal_mode/synchronous/foreign_keys pragmas but never PRAGMA secure_delete, and no code path anywhere calls VACUUM. A user who explicitly deletes a sensitive clip reasonably expects the bytes to be gone from disk; they remain recoverable via an SQLite page-level or raw-file forensic read until the space happens to be reused. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:162-181 (delete/clear/clear_all: plain DELETE, no PRAGMA secure_delete); crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:58-64 (from_connection: journal_mode/synchronous/foreign_keys pragmas set, secure_delete never set)._
58. **rusqlite insert errors are logged with Display formatting that risks echoing clipboard content into logs** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - The capture thread logs `tracing::warn!("insert failed: {e}")` (src/capture.rs:91) for any Store::insert error. rusqlite's error Display impls can include the failing SQL and, on some error paths, representations of bound-parameter context. One of the bound parameters on that exact INSERT is `preview` - up to 512 characters of the user's actual clipboard content (crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:97, clip.preview(512), bound at lib.rs:115 as the `preview` column). A future rusqlite/libsqlite3 error path that surfaces parameter context in its Display string would leak clipboard content into the tracing log stream, an unencrypted, access-control-free sink by default. _Evidence: src/capture.rs:91 (tracing::warn!("insert failed: {e}") on Store::insert error); crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:97,106-118 (insert binds clip.preview(512) - up to 512 chars of raw clip content - as a positional execute parameter)._
59. **init_tracing() defaults to "info" with no redaction layer, and RUST_LOG is fully environment-controlled** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - init_tracing() (src/main.rs:94-97) builds an EnvFilter straight from RUST_LOG (falling back to "info" if unset or invalid) and installs tracing_subscriber::fmt() with no field-redaction layer, no custom Visit implementation, and no allowlist of which fields are safe to print. Any future `tracing::debug!`/`info!` call added anywhere in the workspace that includes a clip's text becomes trivially enabled by setting RUST_LOG=debug in the launching environment - there is no structural guard in the logging setup itself that would prevent clipboard content from reaching stdout/a log file if such a call were ever added. _Evidence: src/main.rs:94-97 (init_tracing: EnvFilter::try_from_default_env, tracing_subscriber::fmt().with_env_filter(filter).init() - no custom Layer, no redaction)._
60. **main.rs logs the user's configured hotkey combo at info level, establishing a pattern of unfiltered Config field logging** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - main() (src/main.rs:48) does `tracing::info!(?config.hotkey, config.poll_interval_ms, "vbuff starting")`, printing the configured hotkey string at the default info verbosity (on by default per init_tracing()'s "info" fallback). This is minor on its own, but it establishes that individual Config sub-fields get dumped into logs at default verbosity with no review of which fields are safe to surface; Config also holds `excluded_apps` (potentially naming password managers the user runs), which a future `?config` or `?config.excluded_apps` debug print would disclose just as readily, given no redaction exists anywhere in the logging setup. _Evidence: src/main.rs:48 (tracing::info!(?config.hotkey, config.poll_interval_ms, "vbuff starting"))._
61. **Malformed content_hash length is the only defended corruption case; kind and timestamp columns silently miscoerce instead of failing** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - row::raw_to_clip (crates/vbuff-store/src/row.rs:39-66) explicitly guards content_hash.len() == 32 and returns StoreError::Corrupt otherwise, but two other columns silently substitute a default on bad data rather than rejecting the row: kind_from_int (row.rs:93-104) maps any out-of-range i64 discriminant - including negative values, trivially reachable by hand-editing history.db with the sqlite3 CLI - to ContentKind::Other via its wildcard arm instead of erroring, and created_at/updated_at (row.rs:48-50) silently substitute chrono::Utc::now() for any timestamp DateTime::from_timestamp_millis rejects (e.g. out-of-range millisecond values) instead of surfacing StoreError::Corrupt. A corrupted or tampered DB file can silently resurface clips with wrong kind badges and fabricated timestamps rather than being flagged as corrupt, while only the content_hash column gets that protection. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/row.rs:93-104 (kind_from_int: `_ => ContentKind::Other` swallows any invalid discriminant including negative values); crates/vbuff-store/src/row.rs:48-50 (created_at/updated_at silently substitute Utc::now() on a bad timestamp instead of erroring); contrast with row.rs:42-47 (content_hash length IS checked and does return StoreError::Corrupt)._
62. **serde_json flavor deserialization has no size guard, decoded fully into memory on every popup-open and every capture** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - serde_clip::flavors_from_json (crates/vbuff-store/src/serde_clip.rs:18-20) calls serde_json::from_str(json) directly on the `flavors` TEXT column with no pre-check on the string's length. Since flavors are stored as a JSON array-of-numbers encoding of Vec<u8> (the file's own doc comment calls this 'bulky'), a corrupted or tampered row with an oversized `flavors` value is decoded fully into memory by every call to Store::list (crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:124-136, used by both list() and load_recent()), which runs on every popup open, after every capture insert, and at startup - an oversized flavors blob is a repeatable memory-exhaustion trigger on ordinary use, not a one-off parse failure. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/serde_clip.rs:18-20 (flavors_from_json: serde_json::from_str with no size/depth guard); crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:124-136 (list/load_recent -> row::collect_clips -> raw_to_clip -> flavors_from_json for every returned row)._
63. **image::load_from_memory in the thumbnail builder has no decompression-bomb guard** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - build_thumbnail (crates/vbuff-gui/src/thumbnail.rs:50-70) calls image::load_from_memory(bytes) on the encoded-image branch (PNG/JPEG/BMP per Cargo.toml's image feature set) with no pixel-count or dimension limit before decoding, then calls img.to_rgba8() to materialize the full decoded buffer. A crafted small PNG/JPEG with a large declared width*height (a classic decompression bomb), captured from any source app or written directly into the clips table given the missing file-permission hardening noted elsewhere, is decoded to its full uncompressed size in memory the moment its row scrolls into view in the popup, with no cap and no graceful error path other than an eventual allocation failure. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-gui/src/thumbnail.rs:63-64 (image::load_from_memory(bytes).ok()?; img.to_rgba8() - no image::io::Limits or max-pixel check before decode)._
64. **Raw-RGBA thumbnail path multiplies width*height with no overflow or upper-bound check before slicing** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - build_thumbnail's raw-RGBA branch (crates/vbuff-gui/src/thumbnail.rs:56-61) computes `w * h * 4` (usize multiplication from dimensions parsed out of the `image/x-vbuff-rgba;width=...;height=...` mime string by parse_rgba_dims) and only guards `bytes.len() < w * h * 4` before slicing `&bytes[..w * h * 4]`. parse_rgba_dims (crates/vbuff-types/src/rgba.rs:19-30) accepts any value each half of the mime string's width=/height= fields parse to, with no upper bound. On a 32-bit build target (nothing in Cargo.toml restricts this workspace to 64-bit) a crafted or corrupted mime string can overflow the usize product and wrap to a value that passes the length check but is smaller than the intended slice, producing a panic or an incorrect-size ColorImage rather than a clean rejection; even on 64-bit, an absurd width/height pair (e.g. near usize::MAX on one dimension) triggers the same unchecked-multiplication overflow path. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-gui/src/thumbnail.rs:57-61 (let (w,h) = parse_rgba_dims(...); if w==0||h==0||bytes.len() < w*h*4 { return None }; ...&bytes[..w*h*4] - plain `*` operator, no checked_mul, no independent upper bound on w/h); crates/vbuff-types/src/rgba.rs:19-30 (parse_rgba_dims: width/height parsed via str::parse with no range check)._
65. **Popup window sets always-on-top and transparency but never excludes itself from screen capture** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - run_gui's ViewportBuilder (src/gui.rs:28-34) sets with_transparent(true) and with_always_on_top() but never calls any platform API to exclude the window from screen capture (e.g. macOS's NSWindowSharingNone, or Windows' SetWindowDisplayAffinity(WDA_EXCLUDEFROMCAPTURE)). Since the popup renders raw clipboard history - unencrypted per top-50 item 1, with no concealed-marker honoring per top-50 item 3 - any concurrent screen share, screen recording, or remote-desktop session active while the user summons vbuff's popup broadcasts the entire visible clip history, passwords included, to everyone watching. _Evidence: src/gui.rs:28-34 (egui::ViewportBuilder::default().with_title("vbuff").with_inner_size([520.0,600.0]).with_decorations(false).with_transparent(true).with_always_on_top().with_visible(false) - no capture-exclusion viewport command or platform call anywhere in gui.rs)._
66. **Tray menu's live pause-state and clip-count labels are readable by any local process via platform accessibility APIs** `[idea]` 🟢 `[low]` - Tray::sync_state (src/tray.rs:66-74) sets menu item text and enabled state to reflect the live `paused` flag and `clip_count` on every polled frame. On platforms exposing accessibility/UI-automation APIs (macOS AXUIElement, Windows UI Automation, X11 menu introspection), any other local process - not just an assistive-technology client - can read those tray-menu labels without any special privilege, learning how many clips vbuff currently has stored and whether capture is paused. A minor local side-channel that a privacy-focused clipboard manager should not expose unauthenticated by default. _Evidence: src/tray.rs:66-74 (Tray::sync_state: self.pause.set_text(...), self.copy_latest.set_enabled(clip_count > 0), self.clear_history.set_enabled(clip_count > 0) - live state readable via each platform's accessibility tree with no gating)._
67. **copy_latest_clip re-broadcasts the most recent clip to the system clipboard with none of the capture-time gating rules re-applied** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - copy_latest_clip (src/actions.rs:36-48) reads shared.lock().unwrap().clips.first().cloned() and writes it straight to the system clipboard via a freshly-opened ArboardClipboard, with none of the checks spawn_capture_thread applies on the way in (config.skip_whitespace_only, config.is_excluded). Today config.is_excluded never actually gates anything on the capture side either, since captured.source_app is always None (top-50 item 4/16), so this finding is really about a structural inconsistency worth fixing before source_app is ever wired up: the tray's "Copy Latest" action has an entirely separate write path from the popup's Paste action (actions.rs:60-79) and neither re-validates the clip's origin against the user's own policy at the point of re-exposure. _Evidence: src/actions.rs:36-48 (copy_latest_clip: shared.lock().unwrap().clips.first().cloned() then cb.write(&clip.flavors) directly - no config.is_excluded or skip_whitespace_only check, and no config: &Config parameter at all)._
68. **No CHECK constraints on kind/pinned/favorite columns; any out-of-range INTEGER is accepted silently** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - The clips table schema (crates/vbuff-store/src/schema.rs:21-37) declares `kind INTEGER NOT NULL`, `pinned INTEGER NOT NULL DEFAULT 0`, `favorite INTEGER NOT NULL DEFAULT 0` with no CHECK(kind BETWEEN 0 AND 8) or CHECK(pinned IN (0,1)) constraint at the SQL level. Combined with kind_from_int's silent fallback to ContentKind::Other for any out-of-range value (a separate finding above) and row::row_to_clip's `row.get::<_, i64>(8)? != 0` treatment of pinned/favorite (row.rs:33-34, any nonzero value reads as true), a tampered row with e.g. `pinned = 2` or `kind = -99` is accepted silently at both the SQL and Rust layers rather than rejected, weakening the database's own ability to signal tampering independent of file-permission hardening. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/schema.rs:21-37 (CREATE TABLE clips: no CHECK constraints on kind/pinned/favorite); crates/vbuff-store/src/row.rs:33-34 (pinned/favorite: `!= 0` accepts any nonzero as true)._
69. **Store::open() accepts an arbitrary caller-supplied Path with no canonicalization or symlink check** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - Store::open(path: &Path) (crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:47-50) passes the given path straight to rusqlite::Connection::open with no canonicalize() call and no rejection of symlinks. Store::open_default() (lib.rs:38-44) is the only caller in the shipped binary and always passes a fixed default_db_path(), so today's wiring is not directly exploitable, but the public open() API itself offers no defense-in-depth: if history.db in the data directory were ever replaced with a symlink by another local process (plausible given the missing directory-permission hardening noted separately), open_default() would silently open and write through it to wherever the symlink points. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:47-50 (open: Connection::open(path) with no canonicalize()/symlink_metadata check); crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:38-44 (open_default: std::fs::create_dir_all(parent) then Self::open(&path), same gap for the parent dir)._
70. **create_dir_all on the config/data parent directories does not restrict the directory's own mode** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - Both Store::open_default() (crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:40-42, std::fs::create_dir_all(parent)) and Config::save() (src/config.rs:74-76, std::fs::create_dir_all(parent)) create the containing `vbuff/` directory itself with the default umask-derived mode, not just the files inside it. Even if the files were separately hardened to 0600 (they are not, per the file-permission finding above), a world-readable+executable parent directory still lets other local users enumerate the directory listing (confirming vbuff is in use, seeing modification timestamps) and traverse into any WAL/SHM sidecar files even if the main DB file itself were locked down. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:40-42 (open_default: std::fs::create_dir_all(parent).map_err(StoreError::Io)? - no explicit mode set); src/config.rs:74-76 (save: std::fs::create_dir_all(parent)? - same gap)._
71. **cargo audit flags tray-icon's Linux GTK3 dependency chain as unmaintained across 7 advisories (RUSTSEC-2024-0412/0413/0415/0416/0418/0419/0420)** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - Running `cargo audit` against this exact Cargo.lock reports seven separate RUSTSEC unmaintained-crate advisories (gdk, gdk-sys, gtk, gtk-sys, gtk3-macros, atk, atk-sys, all pinned at 0.18.2) pulled in transitively via tray-icon 0.24.1's Linux backend. `cargo tree --target x86_64-unknown-linux-gnu -i gtk` confirms two paths: gtk 0.18.2 <- libappindicator 0.9.0 <- tray-icon 0.24.1 <- vbuff, and gtk 0.18.2 <- muda 0.19.3 <- tray-icon 0.24.1 <- vbuff. The `tray` feature is enabled by default (Cargo.toml `default = ["tray"]`), so every default Linux build ships an unmaintained GUI toolkit binding with no upstream security patches, in the exact codepath that renders vbuff's own tray menu. _Evidence: `cargo audit` output (verified by running it against this Cargo.lock): RUSTSEC-2024-0412/0413/0415/0416/0418/0419/0420 for gdk/atk/gtk/gtk-sys/atk-sys/gdk-sys/gtk3-macros 0.18.2; `cargo tree --target x86_64-unknown-linux-gnu -i gtk` -> gtk 0.18.2 <- libappindicator 0.9.0 <- tray-icon 0.24.1 <- vbuff, and gtk 0.18.2 <- muda 0.19.3 <- tray-icon 0.24.1; Cargo.toml line 69 `default = ["tray"]`._
72. **cargo audit flags proc-macro-error and ttf-parser as unmaintained in this exact lockfile** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - Beyond the GTK chain, `cargo audit` against Cargo.lock flags proc-macro-error 1.0.4 and ttf-parser 0.25.1 as unmaintained, both pulled in transitively through the eframe/egui font-rendering stack. Neither is a currently-known-exploitable CVE, but both are supply-chain risk specific to this project's actually pinned versions, not a generic 'keep deps updated' observation - ttf-parser in particular sits on the font-parsing hot path for every glyph the popup renders, so an unmaintained parser there is a plausible future memory-safety gap with no upstream fix incoming. _Evidence: `cargo audit` output (verified against this Cargo.lock): RUSTSEC-2024-0370 (proc-macro-error 1.0.4, unmaintained since 2024-09-01), RUSTSEC-2026-0192 (ttf-parser 0.25.1, unmaintained); Cargo.lock confirms proc-macro-error = 1.0.4 and ttf-parser = 0.25.1._
73. **cargo audit flags glib 0.18.5 as unsound (RUSTSEC-2024-0429), shipped via the default-on tray feature** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - `cargo audit` reports glib 0.18.5 (pulled in by the same GTK3 chain as the unmaintained-crate findings above, via tray-icon's Linux backend) as having a soundness advisory in its Iterator/DoubleEndedIterator impls for VariantStrIter. Unlike the unmaintained warnings, this is a specific known-unsound-code advisory, not just a staleness flag, and it ships in every default-feature Linux build of vbuff via the tray icon. _Evidence: `cargo audit` output (verified against this Cargo.lock): RUSTSEC-2024-0429, glib 0.18.5, 'Unsoundness in Iterator and DoubleEndedIterator impls for glib::VariantStrIter'; Cargo.lock confirms glib = 0.18.5, same dependency chain as the GTK3 findings._
74. **rusqlite's `bundled` feature means SQLite's own CVE exposure rides on whatever libsqlite3-sys vendors, with no separate audit trail** `[idea]` 🟡 `[medium]` - Cargo.toml pins rusqlite with only the `bundled` feature (workspace.dependencies: `rusqlite = { version = "0.37", features = ["bundled"] }`), which compiles a vendored SQLite amalgamation via libsqlite3-sys (locked at 0.35.0 per Cargo.lock) rather than linking the OS-provided libsqlite3. This means vbuff's actual SQLite version - and its exposure to any future SQLite CVE - is entirely determined by whatever amalgamation libsqlite3-sys 0.35.0 happens to vendor, not by the host OS's patched system library; a security-conscious release process needs to track libsqlite3-sys version bumps specifically (not just `cargo update`) to pick up SQLite security fixes, since `cargo audit`'s advisory DB does not separately track the vendored C library's CVEs the way OS package managers track libsqlite3-dev. _Evidence: Cargo.toml: `rusqlite = { version = "0.37", features = ["bundled"] }` (workspace.dependencies); Cargo.lock: `libsqlite3-sys` version = "0.35.0"._
75. **No documented process for re-running cargo audit; the ten live RUSTSEC advisories are invisible without manually running it** `[idea]` 🟢 `[low]` - README.md's pre-PR checklist (line 242) only mentions `cargo fmt`, `cargo clippy`, and `cargo test --workspace`; nothing in README.md, architecture.md, or recommendation.md runs or documents `cargo audit`/`cargo deny`, and there is no CI config to run it either (top-50 item 36). The ten live RUSTSEC advisories confirmed above (7x GTK3 chain, proc-macro-error, ttf-parser, glib unsoundness) are all currently invisible to a contributor unless they think to run cargo audit manually; adding it to the documented pre-PR checklist would surface dependency-chain drift like the tray-icon->gtk path before it accumulates further. _Evidence: README.md:242 lists only cargo fmt/clippy/test as the pre-PR checklist; grep for 'audit'/'cargo-deny' across README.md, architecture.md, and recommendation.md returns no matches._
76. **Store::insert's SELECT-then-branch dedup lookup has no ON CONFLICT handling for the UNIQUE content_hash index** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - Store::insert (crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:71-121) does a SELECT-then-UPDATE-or-INSERT sequence: it queries for an existing content_hash (lib.rs:75-82), then either UPDATEs that row or falls through to a plain INSERT (lib.rs:99-119) with no ON CONFLICT clause. This is a distinct gap from top-50 item 37 (which covers insert/enforce_cap not sharing one transaction across the two calls in capture.rs): within insert() itself, if two Store handles on the same file (no single-instance guard exists per top-50 item 41) race to insert identical new content, the second one's SELECT can miss the first's just-inserted row and then hit the UNIQUE INDEX idx_clips_hash constraint (schema.rs:35) on its own INSERT, which insert() has no retry or conflict-resolution branch for - the race surfaces as an opaque StoreError::Sqlite instead of being folded into the intended dedup-bump behavior. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:71-121 (insert: SELECT existing content_hash at 75-82, INSERT with no ON CONFLICT clause at 99-119); crates/vbuff-store/src/schema.rs:35 (CREATE UNIQUE INDEX idx_clips_hash ON clips(content_hash) - the constraint that fires on a race, unhandled in insert())._
77. **A single corrupted id column value aborts the entire list()/load_recent() call, not just that one row** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - raw_to_clip (crates/vbuff-store/src/row.rs:40) maps a ClipId::parse failure to `StoreError::Corrupt("bad ulid in db".into())` with no indication of which row's id value failed or what it actually was. row::collect_clips (row.rs:69-77) propagates that error via `?` on the first bad row it hits, and Store::list (lib.rs:124-136) - the only implementation behind both list() and load_recent() - has no per-row skip/recovery path. One corrupted id anywhere in the table (from disk corruption, a crash mid-write, or direct tampering given the missing file-permission hardening elsewhere) takes down the popup's ability to load any history at all, with an error message too generic to identify which row to fix without manual sqlite3 inspection. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/row.rs:40 (raw_to_clip: ClipId::parse(&raw.id).map_err(|_| StoreError::Corrupt("bad ulid in db".into())) - no row id/seq included in the error); crates/vbuff-store/src/row.rs:69-77 (collect_clips: `out.push(raw_to_clip(row?)?);` - the `?` aborts the whole batch on the first bad row)._
78. **No test seeds a corrupted/tampered row to verify main()'s actual startup behavior on a damaged history.db** `[idea]` 🟡 `[medium]` - main() (src/main.rs:51-55) calls Store::open_default().context("opening store")? followed by store.enforce_cap(...).context(...)? and store.load_recent(GUI_LIMIT).context(...)? - all three `?`-propagated as fatal startup errors via anyhow::Context. Given the corruption-handling gaps identified elsewhere (kind_from_int's silent Other fallback for out-of-range values, raw_to_clip's all-or-nothing ClipId-parse failure that aborts the whole batch), there is no test anywhere in vbuff-store's test module (crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:226-364) that seeds a deliberately malformed row - every test there builds well-formed Clip values through the local make_clip() helper. A security-relevant corruption-handling policy (fail closed and warn vs. skip the bad row and continue) should be an explicit, tested decision rather than whatever the current `?` chain happens to produce. _Evidence: src/main.rs:51-55 (three `?`-chained Store calls at startup, all fatal via anyhow::Context, no corrupted-row recovery path); crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:226-364 (tests module: every test uses make_clip(), none construct a RawRow or raw SQL insert with malformed data directly)._
79. **Store::clear_all() is dead code with zero call sites and zero test coverage, so pinned clips can never actually be wiped through any exposed path** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - Store::clear_all() (crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:178-181) deletes every row unconditionally, including pinned/favorite ones - the only Store method that can remove a pinned clip. A grep across the entire workspace shows it is never called from src/actions.rs, src/gui.rs, src/tray.rs, or anywhere else; the tray's ClearHistory action and the popup's ClearAll UiAction both call the pinned-preserving Store::clear() instead (src/gui.rs:117, src/actions.rs:94). It also has no test in vbuff-store's test module. This means there is currently no way for a user to actually purge a pinned clip they regret pinning short of individually deleting it - a real gap for a privacy-sensitive tool where 'wipe everything' should be an available emergency action, and a library method that exists for that purpose is unreachable and unverified. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:178-181 (clear_all: DELETE FROM clips, no pinned exemption); grep -rn 'clear_all' across src/ and crates/ shows only the definition at lib.rs:178, no call sites anywhere; src/gui.rs:117 and src/actions.rs:94 both call store.clear() (pinned-preserving) instead._
80. **enigo paste-back has no foreground-window check; the synthesized Cmd/Ctrl+V lands wherever OS focus happens to be after a fixed 120ms delay** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - EnigoPaste::paste (crates/vbuff-platform/src/paste.rs:30-48) synthesizes a modifier+V keystroke via enigo's OS-level key-injection APIs with zero knowledge of which window currently has focus - it never queries the actual foreground application. actions.rs schedules the keystroke a fixed 120ms after hiding the popup (src/actions.rs:74-77, already flagged generally in top-50 item 40 as an unverified timing guess) with no verification step confirming focus actually returned to the app the user was in. If any other window - a spotlight-style launcher, a lock-screen prompt, a re-focus-stealing notification - grabs focus during that window, vbuff synthesizes a paste keystroke into that unrelated, potentially sensitive context (a password field, a terminal, a chat app) rather than the user's intended target, with no confirmation, undo, or focus-mismatch detection. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-platform/src/paste.rs:30-48 (paste(): enigo key-injection with no foreground-window query or verification); src/actions.rs:74-77 (ctx.send_viewport_cmd(Visible(false)); pending_paste scheduled for Instant::now() + 120ms - fixed timer, no focus confirmation before gui.rs:139-150 fires the keystroke)._
81. **The whitespace-skip capture gate only suppresses one exact payload hash, not the pattern going forward, letting a flapping source re-trigger capture every tick** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - spawn_capture_thread's gate ordering (src/capture.rs:46-72) computes the content hash and checks it against last_hash (capture.rs:54-57) before applying skip_whitespace_only (capture.rs:60-66) and is_excluded (capture.rs:67-72); both gate branches update last_hash to the just-skipped hash (capture.rs:64, capture.rs:70) before continuing. Because only the exact hash that was just skipped is remembered, a source app that alternates between a whitespace-only payload and distinct real content on every poll tick has every one of its real-content copies captured and inserted, since each new value produces a hash that doesn't match the last skipped one - the whitespace gate suppresses one specific string, not a durable per-source policy, so a rapidly-flapping clipboard source defeats it on every other tick. _Evidence: src/capture.rs:54-72 (hash computed and compared against last_hash before skip_whitespace_only is checked; the skip branch sets last_hash = Some(hash) at capture.rs:64, so only that exact hash is ever suppressed on the next poll, not the source pattern generally)._
82. **The 50ms poll-interval floor is an unexplained magic number that is still fast enough to enable timing-based inference of copy activity** `[idea]` 🟢 `[low]` - spawn_capture_thread clamps the configured interval with `config.poll_interval_ms.max(50)` (src/capture.rs:37), so any config value below 50 is silently raised to a 50ms poll with no comment explaining the choice. At a sustained 50ms cadence, an unprivileged local process observing vbuff's own CPU/IO activity (e.g. sampling /proc/<pid>/stat, or watching history.db's mtime) can infer roughly when the user copies data and correlate it against its own concurrently observed activity - a low-severity but concrete timing side channel that a documented minimum-interval floor, with an explicit rationale, would at least make an informed trade-off about rather than an accidental one. _Evidence: src/capture.rs:37 (let interval = Duration::from_millis(config.poll_interval_ms.max(50)); - unexplained 50ms floor, no comment tying it to any timing-inference consideration)._
83. **Flavor::as_text runs full UTF-8 validation with no length cap, invoked on every clip on every search keystroke** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - Flavor::as_text (crates/vbuff-types/src/lib.rs:199-203) calls std::str::from_utf8(b) over the full inline byte buffer with no size limit. This is invoked from Clip::primary_text (lib.rs:258-262, used by Clip::preview on every Store::insert, lib.rs:97) and from vbuff-core's searchable_text (crates/vbuff-core/src/filter.rs:79-89), which is called once per clip on every call to filter::search - i.e. every GUI keystroke in the popup's search box. A large flavor whose mime happens to start with `text/` (nothing validates that a `text/*`-labeled flavor's bytes are bounded before this point, and there is no per-item size cap per top-50 item 27) forces a full UTF-8 validation pass over the whole buffer on every keystroke across the visible history, an easy CPU-cost amplifier for one large captured 'text' blob. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-types/src/lib.rs:199-203 (as_text: std::str::from_utf8(b).ok() over the full body with no length guard); crates/vbuff-core/src/filter.rs:79-89 (searchable_text calls clip.primary_text() -> as_text() for every clip on every search() call, i.e. every GUI keystroke)._
84. **content_hash_hex allocates a new String per byte via format! instead of writing into the pre-sized buffer** `[improvement]` 🟢 `[low]` - Clip::content_hash_hex (crates/vbuff-types/src/lib.rs:284-291) builds the 64-character hex digest with `for b in &self.content_hash { s.push_str(&format!("{b:02x}")); }`, allocating a small String on every iteration via format! instead of writing into the already-capacitated `s` directly (e.g. via `use std::fmt::Write; write!(s, "{b:02x}")`, which avoids the 32 extra heap allocations entirely). This is a performance nit rather than a security bug, but content_hash_hex exists specifically so a user or a future 'verify integrity' UI can visually confirm two clips are byte-identical before trusting a paste - a security-adjacent use case that needlessly slow hex formatting discourages calling from any hot path (e.g. a dedup-debugging view over the full history). _Evidence: crates/vbuff-types/src/lib.rs:284-291 (content_hash_hex: `for b in &self.content_hash { s.push_str(&format!("{b:02x}")); }` - one heap allocation per byte instead of a direct write! into the pre-capacitated String)._

---

## SOLID: Single Responsibility violations

85. **vbuff_types::Clip mixes data model with presentation formatting** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - Clip::preview() (crates/vbuff-types/src/lib.rs:270-282) formats a UI-facing single-line string ('[image, N bytes]', whitespace collapsing, ellipsis truncation via truncate_chars) directly on the plain-data struct that vbuff-store also calls to build its cached SQL preview column (`let preview = clip.preview(512);` in Store::insert, crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:97) and that vbuff-core's ranking never touches. The reason to change 'how a preview line looks' (a GUI/rendering concern) is now entangled with the reason to change 'what a Clip is' (a storage/domain concern), and a change to the GUI-facing truncation width would also alter what gets persisted as the SQL search seed. Split: move preview()/truncate_chars into a `vbuff_core::preview` module that takes `&Clip` and returns a String, leaving vbuff-types with only field accessors like primary_text()/primary_image(). _Evidence: crates/vbuff-types/src/lib.rs:270-282, function `Clip::preview`, and `truncate_chars` at lib.rs:296-304; called from crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:97 (`Store::insert`)._
86. **ContentKind couples the domain enum to two independent UI-rendering surfaces** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - ContentKind::icon() (emoji glyph for egui rows) and ContentKind::label() (short display string) both live on the same enum as the classification discriminant vbuff-core assigns and vbuff-store persists as an integer (row.rs kind_to_int/kind_from_int). vbuff-core's own filter.rs even calls `.label()` as a search-projection input (searchable_text, filter.rs:87), so a change to display copy silently changes what text is searchable. Any change to visual iconography or copy wording requires touching vbuff-types, which every non-GUI crate also depends on. Split: move icon()/label() into a lookup table owned by vbuff-gui (e.g. crate::theme::kind_glyph(kind) / kind_label(kind)), leaving ContentKind as a bare classification enum in vbuff-types, and have filter.rs project a stable machine name instead of the display label. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-types/src/lib.rs:94-124, `impl ContentKind { fn icon() ... fn label() ... }`; consumed as search input at crates/vbuff-core/src/filter.rs:87 (`parts.push(clip.meta.kind.label().to_string());`)._
87. **hotkey.rs bundles registration/lifecycle, a 42-arm key-name lookup table, and combo-string parsing in one module** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - crates/vbuff-platform/src/hotkey.rs has three independently-changeable concerns stacked in one file: (1) GlobalHotkeyBackend's register/unregister lifecycle against the global-hotkey crate, (2) the static key_to_code() mapping table (A-Z, 0-9, three named keys), and (3) parse_combo()'s human-string tokenizer ('Cmd+Shift+V' -> KeyCombo). Adding a new named key only touches (2), adding a new modifier alias only touches (3), and swapping the hotkey backend crate only touches (1) - yet all three currently force a diff to the same file and share its module doc. Split: extract key_to_code/combo_to_hotkey into `keycode.rs` and parse_combo into `combo_parse.rs`, leaving hotkey.rs with only the `GlobalHotkeyBackend` struct and its trait impl. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-platform/src/hotkey.rs:34-53 (GlobalHotkeyBackend register/unregister), :75-120 (key_to_code lookup table), :127-147 (parse_combo tokenizer), all in one file._
88. **vbuff-core::classify.rs bundles MIME-based dispatch with three unrelated text heuristics** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - detect_kind() decides content kind from MIME flavors (image/file/html/rtf precedence), then hands off to detect_text_kind(), which in turn calls three independent, differently-motivated heuristics in the same file: is_url() (scheme/www prefix matching), is_color_hex() (hex digit-count matching), and looks_like_code() (line-structure/token heuristic scored by symbol density and indentation). Each heuristic has its own tunable rules that will evolve independently (e.g. adding more code-indicator tokens vs. adding more URL schemes) but currently share one file and one test module. Split: `classify/mime.rs` for MIME-based detect_kind, `classify/url.rs`, `classify/color.rs`, `classify/code.rs` each owning one heuristic and its own tests, re-exported from `classify/mod.rs`. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-core/src/classify.rs:78-155, three separate heuristic functions `is_url`, `is_color_hex`, `looks_like_code` plus MIME dispatch in `detect_kind` (lines 13-57), all in one file._
89. **gui.rs's run_gui both drives the eframe event loop and interprets tray menu semantics** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - run_gui() (src/gui.rs:21-159) is responsible for owning/ticking the eframe loop, AND for pattern-matching every `TrayAction` variant to decide what each tray click means (Show -> request_show, CopyLatest -> copy_latest_clip, ClearHistory -> lock+clear+refresh, TogglePause -> toggle_pause, Quit -> close+exit). That mapping is domain/action-translation logic, not event-loop plumbing, and it duplicates the same kind of match `crate::actions::handle_action` already does for `UiAction`s from the popup just a few lines later (gui.rs:133-136). A hotkey-loop refactor and a 'what does clicking Quit do' change currently land in the same function, and the module's own doc comment ('No capture-thread or tray-menu-building code lives here') does not mention tray-action *interpretation*, which is exactly what this block does. Split: move the `match action { TrayAction::... }` block into `crate::actions::handle_tray_action(action, ...)`, mirroring `handle_action`, so gui.rs only calls `handle_tray_action(action, ...)` per tray event. _Evidence: src/gui.rs:107-130, the `for action in t.poll() { match action { ... } }` block inline inside `run_gui`._
90. **run_gui also owns process-lifetime exit control alongside window/event plumbing** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - Inside the same eframe closure that polls hotkeys, tray, and popup actions, the Quit tray-action arm calls `std::process::exit(0)` directly (src/gui.rs:126), making process termination a side effect buried inside event-loop code rather than a decision returned up to `main()`. This means anything that needs to run on shutdown (the hotkey-unregister cleanup that already sits just below this closure at lines 153-156) is bypassed for the Quit path specifically, since exit(0) never returns from the closure. Split: have the closure set a `should_quit` flag / send a viewport-close command only, and let `run_gui`'s existing post-loop cleanup (hotkey unregister) and `main` decide how to exit. _Evidence: src/gui.rs:124-127, `crate::tray::TrayAction::Quit => { ctx.send_viewport_cmd(...); std::process::exit(0); }`, versus the hotkey-unregister cleanup at gui.rs:153-156 that this path skips._
91. **capture.rs's spawn_capture_thread mixes poll-loop scheduling, capture-gate policy, and store persistence orchestration** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - The single closure passed to std::thread::spawn in spawn_capture_thread (src/capture.rs:27-102) does four distinct jobs inline: (1) timing/scheduling (sleep(interval), pause check), (2) reading and hashing the clipboard, (3) applying capture-gate business rules (skip_whitespace_only, is_excluded), and (4) persistence orchestration (lock store, insert, enforce_cap, reload, update shared GUI state). A change to capture-gate policy (e.g. adding a new skip rule) requires editing the same closure as a change to how the poll loop is scheduled or how results are persisted, and the module doc's claim to 'own the poll loop, the capture-gate rules... and inserting new clips' (capture.rs:1-5) is itself an admission that one file/closure owns three separable responsibilities. Split: extract a pure `fn should_capture(captured: &CapturedClipboard, hash: [u8;32], last_hash: Option<[u8;32]>, config: &Config) -> bool` (testable without a thread or a store) and a `fn persist_and_refresh(store: &Mutex<Store>, shared: &SharedState, clip: &Clip, max_history: usize)` helper, leaving the closure as just scheduling + calling those two. _Evidence: src/capture.rs:39-101, single closure body doing sleep/pause-check, hash-compare, gate rules (lines 60-72), and store insert/enforce_cap/reload (lines 88-100) in sequence; module doc at capture.rs:1-5 names all of these as one module's job._
92. **Store struct owns both SQL query orchestration and the enforce_cap eviction-policy calculation** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - Store::enforce_cap (crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:201-219) computes the overflow count (`total - max_history`) and encodes the 'pinned=0 AND favorite=0, oldest first' eviction ordering directly in a hand-written SQL string, i.e. Store both executes queries (its stated job per the crate doc at lib.rs:8-11: 'orchestrates queries against an open connection') and re-derives the eviction policy that vbuff_core::eviction::evict already encodes as pure data-in/data-out logic (the two are cross-checked only by a test, `enforce_cap_matches_pure_eviction_policy`, lib.rs:328-363, not by sharing code). The overflow-count arithmetic and DELETE ORDER BY clause are policy, not query orchestration. Split: move just the `let overflow = total - max_history;` decision and the ORDER BY column choice into a small `crates/vbuff-store/src/eviction_sql.rs` that documents it as 'SQL restatement of vbuff_core::eviction policy,' so Store::enforce_cap becomes 'call eviction_sql::build_delete(), execute it.' _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:201-219, `Store::enforce_cap` computing `overflow` and embedding the ORDER BY/LIMIT eviction policy inline in the SQL literal; cross-checked only by the test at lib.rs:328-363._
93. **vbuff-store's schema.rs migrate() couples DDL execution with the version-gating control flow for future migrations** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - schema::migrate() (crates/vbuff-store/src/schema.rs:16-43) both reads/writes PRAGMA user_version (migration bookkeeping) and inlines the actual CREATE TABLE/INDEX DDL text for version 1 in the same function body via one big `if version < 1 { execute_batch(...) }`. As soon as a second migration is added, the same function will need to grow additional `if version < N` branches interleaved with more inline SQL, mixing 'decide which migrations to run' with 'what each migration's SQL is.' Split: extract each version's DDL into its own `const MIGRATION_V1: &str = ...` (and later `MIGRATION_V2`, etc.) so `migrate()` becomes a version-gated dispatcher over a list of named migration constants, not a function that also authors SQL inline. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/schema.rs:16-43, `pub(crate) fn migrate` combining PRAGMA version-check control flow with an inline multi-statement DDL string literal._
94. **row.rs's raw_to_clip both decodes rows AND supplies fallback/repair policy for corrupt timestamps** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - raw_to_clip() (crates/vbuff-store/src/row.rs:39-66) is nominally 'map a RawRow into a Clip' but also makes a data-integrity policy decision inline: `chrono::DateTime::from_timestamp_millis(raw.created_at).unwrap_or_else(chrono::Utc::now)` silently substitutes 'now' for an unparseable created_at instead of surfacing StoreError::Corrupt the way the adjacent content_hash-length check does two lines later (`return Err(StoreError::Corrupt(...))`). Deciding whether a bad timestamp is a silent-repair case or a hard error is a policy call, not a mapping concern, and it is inconsistent with the sibling field's stricter handling in the very same function (and `updated_at`, two lines further, silently falls back to `created_at` instead of `Utc::now()` - a third, different repair policy for a third field). Split: extract a `fn parse_timestamp_or_corrupt(millis: i64, field: &str) -> Result<DateTime<Utc>>` policy helper (consistent with the content_hash check) so raw_to_clip only calls decoding helpers rather than embedding the repair-vs-reject decision inline. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/row.rs:48-50 (silent `unwrap_or_else(chrono::Utc::now)` fallback for created_at) and row.rs:50 (`unwrap_or(created_at)` for updated_at, a third repair strategy) vs. row.rs:43-47 (hard `Err(StoreError::Corrupt(...))` for content_hash) in the same function._
95. **ArboardClipboard::write() encodes flavor-selection policy inside the platform I/O backend** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - ClipboardBackend::write() on ArboardClipboard (crates/vbuff-platform/src/clipboard.rs:59-93) is responsible for the raw OS write, but it also decides *which* flavor to write when a Clip has several ('Prefer text; fall back to image' - the comment on lines 60-61 admits this is a policy choice forced by arboard's single-flavor API). That preference-ordering decision belongs with capture/paste policy (already living in src/actions.rs), not inside the OS-facing backend, which should just take an already-resolved single flavor and write it. Split: add a pure `fn pick_write_flavor(flavors: &[Flavor]) -> Option<&Flavor>` in vbuff-core (unit-testable without a live clipboard), and have `ArboardClipboard::write` take the pre-selected flavor as its parameter instead of a full slice it must search. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-platform/src/clipboard.rs:59-93, `ClipboardBackend::write` for `ArboardClipboard` searching `flavors.iter().find(...)` twice (lines 64, 74) to choose which single flavor to send to arboard._
96. **ArboardClipboard::read() mixes raw OS reads with vbuff's own flavor-selection/ordering policy** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - The same read() method (crates/vbuff-platform/src/clipboard.rs:30-57) that talks to arboard also encodes the policy 'only attempt an image read if flavors is empty' (comment: 'to avoid spurious image reads on text-only clipboards on some platforms') - a heuristic about capture behavior, not a raw-I/O concern. This mirrors the write-side violation above: the backend that should be a thin OS adapter instead carries capture-ordering policy that changes independently of which OS API is called. Split: have read() unconditionally attempt every OS-level read it can and return all of them; move the 'skip image read if text present' decision into `vbuff_core` alongside any future multi-flavor capture policy. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-platform/src/clipboard.rs:44-51, the `if flavors.is_empty() && let Ok(img) = ...` guard with its policy-justifying comment._
97. **EnigoPaste::paste() combines OS-level key synthesis with paste-combo modifier-selection policy** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - PasteBackend::paste() on EnigoPaste (crates/vbuff-platform/src/paste.rs:29-49) both drives the enigo key-press/release sequence (I/O) and decides *which* modifier key to use by calling `paste_modifier()` (crates/vbuff-platform/src/lib.rs:35-44), a `#[cfg(target_os = ...)]`-gated policy function that itself lives in the crate root rather than being passed in. The OS-adapter and the platform-choice policy are two different reasons to change (a new enigo API version vs. deciding that some future Linux desktop should use a different modifier), but they are compiled into the same call chain with no seam to override the modifier in tests - notably, `Config::paste_modifier: String` (src/config.rs:21-22) already exists as a user-configurable override field but is never read anywhere in the paste path, since `paste()` always calls the hardcoded `paste_modifier()` function instead. Split: change `paste()` to take the modifier as a constructor/method parameter (`EnigoPaste::new(modifier: Modifier)`), moving the `#[cfg(target_os)]` decision (and the unused config override) to the call site in src/gui.rs where EnigoPaste is constructed. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-platform/src/paste.rs:31 `let modifier_key = match paste_modifier() { ... }` calling into lib.rs's target_os-gated `pub fn paste_modifier()` (lib.rs:35-44) from inside the OS-adapter's own paste() method._
98. **Config struct mixes user-tunable settings with derived/lookup logic (is_excluded) and file I/O (load_or_create/save)** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - src/config.rs's `Config` struct is simultaneously (a) a serde-mapped settings record, (b) the owner of business logic that evaluates exclusion rules (`is_excluded`, config.rs:83-88, substring/case-insensitive matching), and (c) the owner of filesystem I/O for loading/saving itself (`load_or_create`/`save`, config.rs:58-80, which touch `std::fs` and `config_path()` directly). A change to how exclusion matching works and a change to where/how the TOML file is written are unrelated concerns that currently both require editing this one struct's impl block. Split: keep `Config` as a plain serde struct; move `is_excluded` into vbuff-core (it is pure, OS-agnostic policy identical in spirit to `eviction`/`filter`) as `vbuff_core::exclusion::is_excluded(source_app, &excluded_apps)`, and move `load_or_create`/`save`/`config_path` into a small `src/config_io.rs` that only knows about paths and TOML serialization. _Evidence: crates/config.rs:82-88 (`Config::is_excluded`, a matching-policy method) coexisting with config.rs:56-80 (`Config::load_or_create`/`Config::save`, filesystem I/O) and the struct's serde field definitions (config.rs:12-28) all in one `impl Config` block._
99. **main.rs still couples process bootstrapping (tracing init, store hydration, hotkey registration) with the composition-root wiring in one function** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - `fn main()` (src/main.rs:44-91), despite the file's own module doc claiming 'this file only does startup wiring' with each concern already split into named modules, still does five sequentially-different setup jobs inline in one function body: initializing tracing, loading config, opening+hydrating the store, constructing shared GUI state, spawning the capture thread, AND registering the global hotkey with its own error-handling branch - before finally handing off to run_gui. Because these are all one-shot startup steps for different subsystems (logging, persistence, concurrency, OS hotkey registration), a change to how the hotkey is registered risks colliding in review/diff noise with a change to how the store is opened, even though the two are unrelated. Split: extract `fn init_store(config: &Config) -> anyhow::Result<(Store, Vec<Clip>)>` and `fn init_hotkey(config: &Config) -> anyhow::Result<(GlobalHotkeyBackend, Option<u32>)>` so `main()` reads as a flat sequence of named steps rather than inlining each subsystem's setup logic. _Evidence: src/main.rs:44-91, single `fn main()` body sequentially inlining tracing init call (line 45), config load (line 47), store open+enforce_cap+load_recent (lines 51-56), AppState construction (lines 59-64), capture-thread spawn (lines 70-75), and hotkey backend construction+registration with its own match arm (lines 79-88)._
100. **PopupApp::update's revision-change block mixes selection-state reset with thumbnail-cache eviction policy** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - Inside `PopupApp::update` (crates/vbuff-gui/src/app.rs:103-168), the block that fires on a revision change (lines 121-126) does two conceptually separate jobs at once: resetting keyboard-selection state (`self.selected = 0`) and computing `live_ids` to call `self.thumbnails.retain_only(&live_ids)`, i.e. GPU-cache eviction policy triggered by, but conceptually distinct from, noticing the data changed. The preceding comment (lines 118-120) already names both jobs explicitly, so the two responsibilities are at least documented together, but they still live in one unnamed conditional block rather than being callable/testable independently - a change to when thumbnails get pruned currently has to be read/edited inside the same `if revision != self.last_revision` block that also resets selection. Split: extract `fn on_data_changed(&mut self, clips: &[Clip])` that performs both the selection reset and the thumbnail prune as two clearly separated statements (or two calls), so the top-level `update` body calls one named step instead of an inline anonymous block. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-gui/src/app.rs:121-126, the `if revision != self.last_revision { self.last_revision = revision; self.selected = 0; let live_ids = ...; self.thumbnails.retain_only(&live_ids); }` block combining selection-reset with texture-cache pruning._
101. **render_panel draws both the header/search-bar chrome and the scrollable results list in one method** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - `PopupApp::render_panel` (crates/vbuff-gui/src/render.rs:21-85) is a single method responsible for three visually and logically separate regions: the search TextEdit + focus-stealing logic (lines 31-48), the status/clear/pause button row (lines 50-61), and the virtualized results list or empty state (lines 64-84). Each region has its own independent reason to change (e.g. adding a filter dropdown to the header vs. changing row virtualization batch size), yet all three are inlined in one function with no named sub-steps, unlike `render_row`/`render_empty_state`, which the same file already factors out as separate methods. Split: factor the header into `fn render_header(&mut self, ui, paused) -> …` and the status row into `fn render_status_row(&mut self, ui, paused, total)`, consistent with the existing `render_row`/`render_empty_state` decomposition already present in this file. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-gui/src/render.rs:21-85, `render_panel` inlining the search box, the status/button row, and the results-list dispatch in one method body, contrasted with the file's own `render_row` (lines 104-187) and `render_empty_state` (lines 90-101) being properly factored out._
102. **render_row mixes layout/positioning math with click-to-action wiring for three separate widgets** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - `PopupApp::render_row` (crates/vbuff-gui/src/render.rs:104-187) both lays out the row (badge width reservation, kind icon vs. thumbnail vs. color-swatch branching, vertical stack) AND directly pushes `UiAction`s from inside the layout closures for three independent interactions: clicking the preview label (Paste, line 157), clicking the delete button (Delete, line 176), and clicking the pin button (SetPinned, lines 180-183) - each a different action with different semantics, decided inline at the exact point of widget placement. A change to 'what happens when you click delete' and a change to 'how wide is the badge column' are unrelated concerns currently interleaved in one 83-line function. Split: have render_row return a `Vec<UiAction>` (or take a `&mut Vec<UiAction>` sink function) built from a small `row_click_actions(clip, resp_preview, resp_delete, resp_pin) -> Vec<UiAction>` helper, separating 'what got clicked' from 'where is it drawn.' _Evidence: crates/vbuff-gui/src/render.rs:157, :176, :180-183, three separate `self.actions.push_back(UiAction::...)` calls interleaved with widget-placement code inside one `render_row` method._
103. **ThumbnailCache::build_thumbnail conflates two unrelated image-decoding pipelines behind one function** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - `build_thumbnail` (crates/vbuff-gui/src/thumbnail.rs:50-70) branches on MIME to run either vbuff's own raw-RGBA decode path (parsing dimensions out of the `image/x-vbuff-rgba` MIME string and slicing bytes directly) or the general-purpose `image` crate's PNG/JPEG/BMP decode path, with the branch and both full decode implementations inlined in one function. These are two independent decoders with independent failure modes (malformed dimension string vs. malformed image container) that happen to both produce an `egui::ColorImage`. Split: extract `fn decode_raw_rgba(mime: &str, bytes: &[u8]) -> Option<egui::ColorImage>` and `fn decode_encoded_image(bytes: &[u8]) -> Option<egui::ColorImage>` as named siblings, leaving `build_thumbnail` as a two-line dispatcher plus the `ctx.load_texture` call. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-gui/src/thumbnail.rs:56-67, the `if flavor.mime.starts_with("image/x-vbuff-rgba") { ... } else { ... }` branch inlining two independent decode implementations in one function body._
104. **StoreError conflates transport-layer errors (SQLite/IO/JSON) with a data-integrity/domain error variant in one enum** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - `StoreError` (crates/vbuff-store/src/error.rs:6-27) has three `#[from]`/`#[source]`-derived infrastructure error wrappers (Sqlite, Io, Json) alongside `NoDataDir`, plus a fifth variant, `Corrupt(String)`, that represents a domain-level data-integrity violation detected by application code in row.rs (bad ULID at row.rs:40, wrong-length content_hash at row.rs:46) rather than a failure surfaced by an underlying library. Every caller matching on `StoreError` must handle 'a dependency failed' and 'our own invariant was violated' as if they were the same kind of thing, even though the appropriate response differs (retry/log vs. treat-as-corruption/repair). Split: keep `StoreError` for infrastructure failures only; introduce a distinct `IntegrityError` (or nest `Corrupt` as `StoreError::Data(DataError)` wrapping a sub-enum with `BadUlid`/`BadHashLength` variants) so integrity violations are a separably-matchable case. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/error.rs:6-27, `Corrupt(String)` variant (used at row.rs:40 and :46 for two different integrity checks) declared alongside `#[from] rusqlite::Error` / `#[source] std::io::Error` / `#[from] serde_json::Error` infrastructure wrappers in the same enum._
105. **vbuff-store's schema.rs docstring records a data-modeling rationale that belongs in vbuff-types, not the migration module** `[improvement]` 🟢 `[low]` - The module doc on crates/vbuff-store/src/schema.rs:1-6 explains a domain-modeling tradeoff ('a single clips table whose flavors column holds the flavor set as a JSON blob... the full normalized item/flavor split from the architecture can be migrated to later') that is really about the shape of `Clip`/`Flavor` as a domain concept, not about migration mechanics. Because this rationale lives only as a comment in the migration file, anyone changing vbuff-types' Flavor model has no signal from that crate that a related normalization decision is tracked in vbuff-store; grepping `crates/vbuff-types/src/lib.rs` for any mention of 'normalize' or 'schema' or a pointer to vbuff-store turns up nothing. Concretely: add a short doc-comment cross-reference in vbuff-types/src/lib.rs's `Flavor` type pointing at schema.rs's rationale (or vice versa) so the two independently-changeable decisions (Rust type shape vs. SQL storage shape) are discoverable from either side without already knowing to look in the other crate. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/schema.rs:1-6 module doc describing a `Flavor`/normalization tradeoff that is not referenced anywhere in crates/vbuff-types/src/lib.rs._
106. **vbuff-core::filter.rs's score_clip both defines the ranking algorithm and the searchable-text projection policy** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - `filter::search` delegates scoring to `score_clip`, which itself calls `searchable_text(clip)` (crates/vbuff-core/src/filter.rs:79-89) to decide *what fields* participate in search (primary_text, source_app, kind label, joined with spaces) - a projection/policy decision independent of the scoring math (position-based bonuses, prefix bonus, word-boundary bonus, length penalty) that dominates the rest of the file. Adding a new searchable field and tuning the scoring formula are two different reasons to change that currently sit in the same small file with no clear seam. Split: keep `searchable_text` as-is but move it (and any future per-field weighting) into a `filter/projection.rs`, leaving `filter.rs` with only the scoring/ranking algorithm operating over an already-projected string. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-core/src/filter.rs:54-76 (`score_clip`, pure ranking-score math) calling into :79-89 (`searchable_text`, field-selection policy) within the same file._
107. **vbuff-gui's view.rs bundles a time-formatting algorithm with an unrelated string-parsing algorithm for app names** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - crates/vbuff-gui/src/view.rs contains `relative_time` (bucketing a duration into now/Nm/Nh/Nd/Nw/Nmo/Ny display strings, lines 6-37) and `short_app_name` (stripping bundle-id/path formatting to a display name, lines 42-53) as the file's only two functions. Both are 'pure rendering helpers' per the module doc, but they format two semantically unrelated inputs (a timestamp vs. a source-app identifier) with no shared logic, sharing a file only because both happen to be small formatting utilities used by render.rs. A change to time-bucket thresholds and a change to bundle-id-vs-path detection are unrelated concerns; keeping them in one file makes the module's actual single responsibility ('relative time formatting') ambiguous once a third unrelated formatter is added later. Split: move `short_app_name` into its own `app_name.rs` so `view.rs` (or its rename to `time.rs`) has exactly one formatting responsibility. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-gui/src/view.rs:6-37 (`relative_time`) and :42-53 (`short_app_name`), two unrelated formatting algorithms in one file whose only shared trait is 'small pure helper used by render.rs'._
108. **Tray struct owns both menu construction/wiring and menu-label state-sync policy** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - `Tray::new` (src/tray.rs:30-63) builds the menu structure (item creation, ordering, separators) and wires up the icon, while `Tray::sync_state` (src/tray.rs:66-74) encodes UI-state-to-label policy ('Resume capture' vs. 'Pause capture' text, enabling/disabling Copy Latest and Clear History based on `clip_count > 0`) on the same struct. A change to menu layout (e.g. adding a new item) and a change to what conditions disable which existing item are different concerns that happen to both require editing `Tray`'s methods, and `sync_state`'s enablement policy ('disable Copy Latest and Clear History when count == 0') is domain logic duplicated nowhere else for verification. Split: keep `Tray` as pure OS menu plumbing (new/poll), and move the label/enablement decisions into a small pure `fn tray_labels(paused: bool, clip_count: usize) -> TrayLabels { pause_text, copy_enabled, clear_enabled }` that `sync_state` just applies, making the policy independently unit-testable without constructing a real `TrayIcon`. _Evidence: src/tray.rs:66-74, `Tray::sync_state` embedding label-text and enablement policy directly against OS menu-item handles, inside the same struct as `Tray::new`'s menu-construction code (lines 30-63)._
109. **vbuff-store's integration.rs test helper make_clip duplicates domain-construction logic already owned by the unit tests in lib.rs** `[improvement]` 🟢 `[low]` - crates/vbuff-store/tests/integration.rs defines its own `make_clip(text: &str) -> Clip` helper (lines 7-25) that is structurally identical to the `make_clip` already defined in crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs's `#[cfg(test)] mod tests` (lines 232-247), including the same `ClipMeta::now(ContentKind::Text, ...)` construction pattern (they differ only in the placeholder source-app string, 'test.app' vs 'integration.test'). Two independently-maintained copies of 'how do we build a minimal valid Clip for a test' is exactly the kind of drift that is easy to fix in one copy and leave silently stale in the other; a change to `Clip`'s required fields (e.g. adding a new mandatory field) risks being fixed in one copy and not the other until CI catches it. Split: promote one `make_clip`/`ClipBuilder` test helper into a `#[cfg(test)] pub fn` in vbuff-types (or a small `test-support` feature) that both the unit tests and the integration test import. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/tests/integration.rs:7-25 and crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:232-247, two separately-maintained `make_clip` helpers with the same shape._
110. **vbuff-platform's traits.rs mixes trait/interface definitions with a concrete data-transformation type (CapturedClipboard)** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - crates/vbuff-platform/src/traits.rs is documented as 'Trait definitions for the four platform backends, plus shared key types' (line 1), but it also owns `CapturedClipboard` (lines 33-46), a concrete struct with its own behavior (`is_empty()`) that is a data-transfer object produced by `ClipboardBackend::read()` implementations, not an interface contract. The reason to add a new platform trait (interface design) and the reason to change what a capture snapshot carries are different concerns bundled in one file. Split: move `CapturedClipboard` into its own `capture.rs` alongside `ClipboardBackend`'s return type usage, leaving `traits.rs` to define only `ClipboardBackend`/`HotkeyBackend`/`PasteBackend`/`KeyCombo`/`Modifier`. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-platform/src/traits.rs:33-46, `pub struct CapturedClipboard { ... } impl CapturedClipboard { pub fn is_empty(&self) -> bool ... }` defined in the same file as the three backend traits._
111. **src/actions.rs's handle_action function is a single dispatcher whose UiAction::Paste arm embeds a multi-step protocol not shared with the other five arms** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - `handle_action` (src/actions.rs:51-105) dispatches six `UiAction` variants, but the `Paste` arm (lines 60-79) is qualitatively different from the other five: it performs a clip lookup, a clipboard write, a viewport visibility change, AND schedules a `PendingPaste` with a hardcoded timing delay - a four-step protocol - while `SetPinned`/`Delete`/`ClearAll`/`TogglePause`/`Hide` are each a single store call plus refresh. Bundling a multi-step, timing-sensitive protocol into the same flat `match` as simple one-line handlers means a future paste-sequencing change has to be found and edited inside a generic-looking dispatcher rather than a named function. Split: extract `fn start_paste_sequence(id: ClipId, store: &..., shared: &..., ctx: &egui::Context) -> Option<PendingPaste>` so the `Paste` arm is one call, matching the shape of the other five arms. _Evidence: src/actions.rs:60-79, the `UiAction::Paste(id) => { ... }` arm containing a four-step protocol (lookup, write, hide, schedule) inlined directly in the match, versus the other five arms each being one store call plus `refresh_snapshot`._
112. **vbuff-types' Flavor struct mixes raw payload storage with MIME-category predicate logic** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - `Flavor` (crates/vbuff-types/src/lib.rs:171-204) is the plain data holder for `(mime, body)`, but its impl block also owns `is_text()`/`is_image()`/`as_text()`, which encode MIME-string category-matching policy ('starts_with("text/") || mime == "text"', 'starts_with("image/")') that vbuff-core's classify.rs independently re-implements its own MIME matching logic for the same purpose (e.g. classify.rs:21-29 pattern-matches `f.mime.as_str()` directly for file/html/rtf categories rather than calling a Flavor predicate). MIME-category policy is defined in one place (Flavor) but reimplemented ad hoc in another (classify.rs) with no shared vocabulary. Split: centralize all MIME-category predicates (text/image/html/rtf/file-list) as free functions in a `vbuff_types::mime` module that both `Flavor`'s convenience methods and `classify::detect_kind` call, instead of `Flavor` half-owning the policy and classify.rs re-deriving the rest inline. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-types/src/lib.rs:188-196 (`Flavor::is_text`/`is_image`) versus crates/vbuff-core/src/classify.rs:21-29 independently pattern-matching `f.mime.as_str()` for file/html/rtf categories without reusing any Flavor predicate._
113. **PopupApp struct itself still couples UI-widget state with data-fetch/action-queue responsibilities despite the file split** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - Even after the app.rs/render.rs/input.rs split, `PopupApp` (crates/vbuff-gui/src/app.rs:25-50) is a single struct holding three different kinds of state with three different lifecycles: transient widget state (`query`, `selected`, `shown_at`, `request_focus_next_frame`), a side-effect outbox (`actions: VecDeque<UiAction>`), and a resource cache (`thumbnails: ThumbnailCache`). Because all three live as fields on one struct that `render.rs`/`input.rs` both mutate via `impl PopupApp` blocks (crate-visibility `pub(crate)` fields), any method touching any one of the three has unrestricted access to mutate the other two, so 'this method only builds the action queue' cannot be enforced by the type system - e.g. `render_row` (render.rs) both draws AND pushes to `self.actions` AND indirectly touches `self.thumbnails` via `get_or_build`. Split: introduce an explicit `struct WidgetState { query, selected, shown_at, focus_next_frame }` field grouping distinct from an `actions: ActionQueue` newtype and `thumbnails: ThumbnailCache`, so each collaborator module can be given a narrower `&mut` borrow instead of the whole `PopupApp`. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-gui/src/app.rs:25-50, `struct PopupApp` combining widget-interaction fields (`query`, `selected`, `shown_at`, `request_focus_next_frame`), an action outbox (`actions`), and a GPU resource cache (`thumbnails`) as flat sibling fields with no internal grouping._
114. **vbuff-core crate doc claims a 4-module clean split but filter.rs and classify.rs each already do more than their one-line crate-doc description promises** `[idea]` 🟢 `[low]` - crates/vbuff-core/src/lib.rs's module doc (lines 6-9) describes `filter` as 'case-insensitive search + ranking' and `classify` as 'heuristic content-kind detection,' each stated as a single responsibility - but as detailed above, `filter.rs` actually owns both a scoring algorithm and a text-projection policy, and `classify.rs` owns MIME dispatch plus three independent text heuristics. Once the splits proposed above (filter/projection.rs, classify/{mime,url,color,code}.rs) are done, update crates/vbuff-core/src/lib.rs's doc comment to list the finer-grained submodules so the crate doc stays an accurate map of responsibilities rather than describing four modules that each secretly contain 2-4 sub-concerns. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-core/src/lib.rs:6-9, doc comment listing `filter` and `classify` as single-line responsibilities that undersell (and thus obscure) the multiple concerns each file currently holds._
115. **config.rs's exclusion feature has its matching policy in Config but its consumption gate scattered in capture.rs with no shared abstraction** `[improvement]` 🟢 `[low]` - `Config::is_excluded` (config.rs:83-88) defines the matching algorithm, but the decision of *when* to apply it during capture is a separate `if let Some(app) = &captured.source_app && config.is_excluded(app)` inline check in capture.rs:67-72, with no shared 'capture gate' abstraction connecting the two - the same pattern repeats for the unrelated `skip_whitespace_only` check immediately above it (capture.rs:60-66), each gate being its own ad hoc `if` block against `config` fields directly in the poll loop. As more capture-gate rules are added, each will likely be pasted in as another standalone `if` block in the same closure rather than composed. Concretely: define a `trait CaptureGate { fn should_skip(&self, captured: &CapturedClipboard, config: &Config) -> bool; }` in vbuff-core with `WhitespaceGate`/`ExclusionGate` implementations, and have capture.rs iterate a `Vec<Box<dyn CaptureGate>>` instead of hand-written sequential ifs, so adding a new gate never touches the poll-loop closure body. _Evidence: src/capture.rs:59-72, two structurally-identical but independently-written `if ... { last_hash = Some(hash); continue; }` gate blocks (whitespace-only check and exclusion check) with no shared abstraction, each reaching directly into `config` fields._
116. **vbuff-store's Store struct combines connection-lifecycle ownership with every CRUD/query method as inherent impls, with no read/write separation** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - `Store` (crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:31-220) is the sole type for opening a connection (open/open_default/open_in_memory/from_connection) AND every subsequent operation: writes (insert, set_pinned, set_favorite, delete, clear, clear_all, enforce_cap) and reads (list, load_recent, count) are all inherent methods on the same struct with no grouping. This is milder than a true SRP violation since all methods do genuinely belong to 'the store,' but the eviction-policy comment on `enforce_cap` (lib.rs:191-200) already acknowledges enforce_cap is conceptually distinct maintenance/policy logic bolted onto the same struct as simple CRUD. As the store grows, continuing to add every new concern as another inherent method on one `Store` will make the struct the same kind of do-everything type the file-level splits elsewhere in this codebase were meant to avoid. Idea: once a second maintenance operation is added (e.g. VACUUM scheduling, index rebuild), extract a `StoreMaintenance<'a>(&'a Store)` wrapper for cap-enforcement/maintenance methods, keeping `Store` itself to connection lifecycle + CRUD. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:35-220, single `impl Store` block spanning connection-opening methods (:38-64), CRUD (:71-189), and cap-enforcement maintenance logic (:201-219) with no internal grouping or sub-type._
