117. **vbuff-gui crate doc undersells that `input.rs` also encodes quick-pick keybinding-to-index policy, not just 'turn keys into actions'** `[idea]` 🟢 `[low]` - input.rs's module doc says it 'turns key presses into selection changes and queued UiActions,' but `handle_keys` (input.rs:15-55) also hardcodes the Cmd/Ctrl+1..9 quick-pick keybinding table (`QUICK_PICK_KEYS`, lines 35-45) inline as a local const array duplicating the ordering assumption already expressed by `theme::QUICK_PICK_SLOTS` and rendered visually by render.rs's badge-drawing code (render.rs:125-129). The keybinding-to-row-index mapping is a distinct, independently-testable piece of policy ('digit N selects filtered[N-1]') currently inlined inside the same function that also handles Escape/arrows/Enter, and it is not unit-tested anywhere (input.rs has no `#[cfg(test)]` module at all, unlike color.rs/view.rs in this same crate, both of which do). Idea: extract `fn quick_pick_key_to_index(key: Key) -> Option<usize>` as a small pure function with its own unit tests, matching the testing rigor already applied to `view.rs`/`color.rs`/`eviction.rs` in this same codebase. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-gui/src/input.rs:35-52, the inline `QUICK_PICK_KEYS` array and its enumerate-and-match loop, with no accompanying `#[cfg(test)]` module in the file (contrast with color.rs/view.rs in the same crate, both of which have tests)._

---

## SOLID: Open/Closed & Dependency Inversion violations

118. **ContentKind::icon()/label() are closed match arms baked into the data type itself** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - vbuff_types::ContentKind is a plain enum, and vbuff-types/src/lib.rs:94-124 defines icon() and label() as exhaustive match statements directly on it. Adding a new kind (e.g. Markdown, Password, Path) requires editing this enum's inherent impl AND every other exhaustive match on ContentKind across crates (row.rs kind_to_int/kind_from_int, classify.rs's return sites, render.rs's `== ContentKind::Color` special-case). There is no trait like `impl KindPresentation for ContentKind` seam or registry; the type and its rendering metadata are fused, so vbuff-types (a plain data model crate per its own module doc) now owns UI-facing emoji/label strings that keep it coupled to every future kind. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-types/src/lib.rs:94-124 (icon/label exhaustive matches on ContentKind, verified)._
119. **kind_to_int/kind_from_int in the store hand-encode the ContentKind discriminant instead of deriving it** `[problem]` 🟠 `[high]` - row.rs:79-105 maintains two hand-written exhaustive matches mapping ContentKind to/from an i64 SQL column. Every new ContentKind variant requires a synchronized edit in both directions here, in addition to icon()/label() in vbuff-types and the classify.rs detection logic. Nothing enforces the two matches stay in sync (e.g. Text=0 in one but accidentally reused in the other), and there is no compile-time exhaustiveness check tying the encoding to the enum's variant count since kind_from_int uses a catch-all `_ => ContentKind::Other`. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/row.rs:79-105 (kind_to_int / kind_from_int, verified)._
120. **detect_kind's MIME-precedence chain is a hardcoded if/for ladder, not a pluggable rule list** `[problem]` 🟠 `[high]` - classify.rs:13-56 implements kind detection as an ordered sequence of hardcoded checks (image MIME, then file-list MIME substrings, then html/rtf fallback, then text heuristics) inlined directly in detect_kind's body. There is no `ClassifierRule` trait or ordered Vec<Box<dyn Rule>> that a new kind (e.g. detecting JSON, or a Password kind from a concealed marker) could be added to; adding one means inserting another `for f in flavors { ... return ContentKind::X }` block into this exact function and re-reasoning about precedence relative to every existing check. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-core/src/classify.rs:13-56 (detect_kind's hardcoded precedence ladder, verified)._
121. **looks_like_code / is_url / is_color_hex are free functions, not swappable Classifier strategies** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - detect_text_kind (classify.rs:60-75) calls is_url, is_color_hex, looks_like_code as free functions in a fixed if/else chain with implicit priority (url beats color beats code). A new text heuristic (e.g. detecting JSON, a phone number, or a Markdown snippet) can only be added by editing this function's body and manually deciding where in the chain it goes; there is no `TextClassifier: fn(&str) -> Option<ContentKind>` trait object list that new heuristics register into, so classify.rs's authors are the only ones who can extend detection and every addition risks silently reordering existing precedence. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-core/src/classify.rs:60-75 (detect_text_kind's if-else chain over is_url/is_color_hex/looks_like_code, verified)._
122. **render_row special-cases ContentKind::Color with a direct equality check instead of a per-kind row renderer** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - render.rs:137-146 does `if clip.meta.kind == ContentKind::Color { draw_color_swatch(...) } else if thumbnail ... else { icon glyph }`. Every new kind that wants a custom leading visual (e.g. a File kind showing a folder-count badge, or a Code kind showing a language badge) must be added as another `else if clip.meta.kind == ContentKind::X` branch inside this one function, growing an if-else ladder that mixes GUI rendering with content-kind branching. There is no `RowVisual` trait keyed by kind that each kind's presentation could implement independently. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-gui/src/render.rs:136-146 (render_row's ContentKind::Color special case, verified)._
123. **Clip::preview()'s fallback chain hardcodes exactly two content shapes (text, image), leaving every other kind to the generic MIME fallback** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - Clip::preview (vbuff-types/src/lib.rs:270-282) special-cases primary_text() and primary_image() by name, falling back to `[{mime}]` for anything else (File, Rtf, Html, Color, Code all currently degrade to the generic MIME-bracket format even though ContentKind already distinguishes them). A new kind that deserves its own preview format (e.g. a File kind rendering a filename list, or a Color kind rendering the swatch hex) requires adding another named `primary_X()`/branch pair to this exact method rather than dispatching through a per-kind preview strategy. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-types/src/lib.rs:256-282 (Clip::primary_text/primary_image/preview, verified)._
124. **ThumbnailCache::build_thumbnail branches on MIME prefix instead of dispatching through a decoder registry** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - build_thumbnail (thumbnail.rs:50-70) is a two-way if/else: `image/x-vbuff-rgba` gets special-cased raw-RGBA decoding, everything else goes through the generic `image` crate loader. Adding a new image representation (e.g. an SVG preview, or a spilled-body thumbnail once Body::Spilled is implemented) means adding another `if flavor.mime.starts_with(...)` branch to this one function; there is no `ImageDecoder` trait keyed by MIME prefix that new formats could register against, and Body::Spilled is explicitly given up on at the top (`Body::Spilled { .. } => return None`). _Evidence: crates/vbuff-gui/src/thumbnail.rs:50-70 (build_thumbnail's MIME-prefix if/else, verified)._
125. **The four platform backends have traits, but the wiring depends on the concrete impl types, defeating the seam** `[problem]` 🟠 `[high]` - vbuff-platform/src/traits.rs's own doc comment says the traits are 'the seam at which native per-OS backends can later be swapped in,' but src/capture.rs:13,28, src/actions.rs:10,43,69, src/main.rs:36,79, and src/gui.rs:13,25,42 all import and construct the concrete `ArboardClipboard`, `GlobalHotkeyBackend`, `EnigoPaste` types directly rather than `Box<dyn ClipboardBackend>` / `Box<dyn HotkeyBackend>` / `Box<dyn PasteBackend>`. Adding a native macOS NSPasteboard backend later means either changing every one of these call sites' concrete type or introducing a factory now that the wiring already bypassed - the trait exists but nothing in the binary is actually programmed against it. _Evidence: src/capture.rs:13,28; src/actions.rs:10,43,69; src/main.rs:36,79; src/gui.rs:13,25,42 (concrete ArboardClipboard/GlobalHotkeyBackend/EnigoPaste dependencies instead of the trait objects, all verified)._
126. **The Store type is a concrete struct with no trait boundary; every caller in src/ names vbuff_store::Store directly** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - vbuff-store/src/lib.rs's Store is a plain struct (not behind a `ClipStore` trait) holding just a `rusqlite::Connection`. main.rs, capture.rs, actions.rs, and gui.rs all take `Arc<Mutex<Store>>` by concrete type. There is no seam for an alternate backend (e.g. a future encrypted-at-rest store using sqlcipher, flagged as aspirational-only in docs/code-audit-top-50.md item 1) to be swapped in without touching every function signature in src/ that currently reads `Arc<Mutex<Store>>`. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:31-33 (Store struct, no trait, verified); src/capture.rs:22, src/actions.rs:53, src/gui.rs:22 (concrete Arc<Mutex<Store>> parameters throughout, verified)._
127. **EvictionPolicy is a single hardcoded struct/algorithm; there is no eviction-strategy trait to add a new policy** `[problem]` 🟠 `[high]` - eviction.rs's evict() function (lines 38-59) is one fixed algorithm (count-cap, oldest-updated-first, pinned/favorite exempt) parameterized only by `max_history: usize` on the `EvictionPolicy` struct (lines 10-22). There is no `EvictionStrategy` trait with `evict(&self, clips: &[Clip]) -> Vec<ClipId>` that alternate policies (size-based cap in bytes, per-kind retention limits, LRU-with-decay, time-based expiry) could implement and be swapped into the pure evict() call site. Adding any new eviction policy means writing a second free function and threading a new enum/flag through this module. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-core/src/eviction.rs:10-22,38-59 (EvictionPolicy struct and single evict() function, no strategy trait, verified)._
128. **Schema migrations are one hardcoded `if version < N` block per version, with the entire DDL inlined in a single function** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - schema.rs's migrate() (lines 16-43) is a single function containing one `if version < 1 { conn.execute_batch("CREATE TABLE...") }` block with the full CREATE TABLE/CREATE INDEX DDL as an inline string literal. There is no `Migration { version, up: fn(&Connection) -> Result<()> }` list that migrate() iterates over; adding schema v2 (e.g. a `tags` column, or splitting `flavors` into a normalized table per architecture.md's target design) means adding a second `if version < 2 { ... }` block to this same function and hoping it does not disturb the v1 block above it, rather than appending an independent migration step to an ordered list. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/schema.rs:16-43 (migrate's single hardcoded if-block per version, verified)._
129. **hotkey.rs's key_to_code is a giant closed match from key names to Code, with no registry for platform-specific extra keys** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - key_to_code (hotkey.rs:75-120) is a 39-arm match statement (26 letters, 10 digits, plus Space/Enter-Return/Tab) hardcoding every supported key name to a global_hotkey::Code variant. Extending the supported key set (e.g. F1-F12, arrow keys, media keys) means editing this one match directly; there is no lookup table or trait indirection separating 'which key strings vbuff recognizes' from 'this specific global-hotkey crate's Code enum,' so replacing the hotkey backend crate later (the stated goal per traits.rs's module doc) means rewriting this entire mapping function rather than swapping an implementation behind a stable key-name abstraction. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-platform/src/hotkey.rs:75-120 (key_to_code's 39-arm match, verified)._
130. **parse_combo's modifier-token matching is inlined into the same function as key/modifier separation, coupling token vocabulary to parsing logic** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - parse_combo (hotkey.rs:127-147) matches modifier token strings ('ctrl'/'control', 'alt'/'option'/'opt', etc.) inline inside the loop that also decides 'this token is the main key.' Adding a new modifier alias, or supporting a differently-shaped combo string format (e.g. `<C-M-v>` Emacs-style, which a config-import feature might want), requires editing this one function's match arms rather than plugging a new tokenizer/parser strategy behind `KeyCombo::parse` abstraction. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-platform/src/hotkey.rs:127-147 (parse_combo's inline modifier-token match, verified)._
131. **Config is a single flat struct with fields for every feature; there is no per-feature settings trait or extension point** `[improvement]` 🟡 `[medium]` - src/config.rs's Config struct hardcodes six top-level, unrelated fields (hotkey, poll_interval_ms, max_history, paste_modifier, excluded_apps, skip_whitespace_only) flattened into one TOML document with one Default impl. Every future feature (per-kind retention overrides, an eviction-strategy choice, a classifier rule toggle) adds another field to this exact struct and its Default impl, coupling unrelated feature configs into one growing blob with no versioned or namespaced sub-config seam (e.g. `[eviction]`, `[classify]` TOML tables owned by their respective crates) that new capabilities could plug into independently. _Evidence: src/config.rs:12-41 (flat Config struct + single Default impl, verified)._
132. **search()'s scoring function is a single hardcoded heuristic with no pluggable ranking strategy** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - filter.rs's score_clip (lines 54-76) hardcodes one fixed scoring formula (base 100, position penalty, prefix bonus, word-boundary bonus, length penalty) with no `RankingStrategy` trait that a future fuzzy-match engine, a recency-weighted ranker, or a per-kind boost (e.g. rank Color/Url matches higher) could implement and swap in. Any change to ranking behavior requires editing this one function's arithmetic directly, and searchable_text (lines 79-89) hardcodes exactly which Clip fields feed the search index (primary_text, source_app, kind label) with no extensible field-contributor list a new kind's custom searchable projection could hook into. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-core/src/filter.rs:54-89 (score_clip's fixed formula, searchable_text's fixed field list, verified)._
133. **Tray menu items and TrayAction variants are a fixed, hand-paired enum/struct with no way to add an action without touching three places** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - tray.rs's TrayAction enum (lines 7-13), the Tray struct's per-item MenuId fields (lines 16-26), Tray::new's menu-building sequence (lines 30-63), and Tray::poll's if/else id-matching ladder (lines 77-93) are four separate places that must all be edited in lockstep to add one new tray action (e.g. 'Open Settings'). There is no `TrayMenuItem { label, action, enabled_when }` data-driven list that Tray::new could iterate to build the menu and Tray::poll could iterate to match ids, so every new tray action means editing the enum, adding a struct field, adding a menu.append call, and adding an if-else arm. _Evidence: src/tray.rs:7-13 (TrayAction enum), 16-26 (Tray fields), 30-63 (Tray::new), 77-93 (Tray::poll's id-matching ladder) - all verified._
134. **gui.rs's run_simple_native closure hardcodes tray-action handling inline instead of dispatching through a handler map** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - run_gui's main closure matches each TrayAction variant inline with hand-written side effects (Show -> request_show, CopyLatest -> copy_latest_clip, ClearHistory -> lock+clear+refresh, TogglePause -> toggle_pause, Quit -> exit). This mirrors the UiAction dispatch in actions.rs::handle_action but is a third parallel dispatch point (in addition to Tray's own enum and the menu-building code flagged separately) that must be extended whenever TrayAction grows a variant, with no shared `Action -> effect` table that both the UiAction and TrayAction dispatchers could share despite representing overlapping operations (both have a 'clear history' and a 'toggle pause'). _Evidence: src/gui.rs:100-130 (inline TrayAction match inside run_gui's closure, verified)._
135. **PlatformError is one flat enum shared by all four backends, with no per-backend error type a new backend could extend independently** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - vbuff-platform/src/error.rs's PlatformError has one variant per backend (Clipboard, Hotkey, Paste, BadCombo, Empty), each wrapping a stringly-typed message. A new backend (e.g. a native NSPasteboard implementation that wants structured error info like 'permission denied' vs 'no such pasteboard type') has nowhere to add a typed variant without editing this shared enum and touching every existing match on PlatformError; there is no `#[from]`-composable per-backend error type (e.g. `ClipboardError`, `HotkeyError`) that ClipboardBackend/HotkeyBackend/PasteBackend trait methods could return instead, keeping backend-specific error detail out of a shared type that every backend must agree to extend together. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-platform/src/error.rs:6-27 (single flat PlatformError enum for all four backend kinds, verified)._
136. **CapturedClipboard is a single fixed struct (flavors + source_app); a new per-capture metadata field ripples through every backend and caller** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - traits.rs's CapturedClipboard (lines 33-39) hardcodes exactly two fields. Adding new capture-time metadata a future native backend could supply (e.g. a concealed/transient-type hint per docs/code-audit-top-50.md item 3, or a per-flavor origin timestamp) requires adding a field to this shared struct, which then requires every ClipboardBackend impl (currently just ArboardClipboard) to populate or default it, and every caller (capture.rs) to know about it - there is no extensible metadata bag (e.g. a `HashMap<String, String>` sideband or a builder pattern) that a richer backend could populate without changing the struct's shape for every implementor. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-platform/src/traits.rs:33-39 (CapturedClipboard's fixed two-field struct, verified)._
137. **ArboardClipboard::write is a hardcoded two-branch priority chain (text, then RGBA image) with no per-flavor writer strategy** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - clipboard.rs's ClipboardBackend::write impl (lines 59-92) is `if text-flavor exists { write text } else if rgba-flavor exists { write image } else { Err(Empty) }`. Adding support for writing another flavor type back to the system clipboard (e.g. HTML, RTF, or file-list paste-back, all currently unsupported per docs/code-audit-top-50.md item 15) means adding another `if let Some(...) = flavors.iter().find(...)` branch to this exact function; there is no `FlavorWriter` trait keyed by MIME that new flavor types could register against, so every future write capability grows this one method's branch count. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-platform/src/clipboard.rs:59-92 (ArboardClipboard::write's hardcoded text/RGBA-image branch chain, verified)._
138. **ArboardClipboard::read hardcodes an exclusive text-then-image capture order that structurally prevents adding a third flavor** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - clipboard.rs's read() (lines 30-57) only attempts get_image() `if flavors.is_empty()` after the text check - i.e. it is wired as mutually exclusive text-or-image, not a list of independent flavor readers. A new flavor source (e.g. reading HTML alongside text, once a native backend supports it) cannot be added as an independent, composable read step without restructuring this function's control flow; there is no `Vec<Box<dyn FlavorReader>>` list that read() iterates and unions, only this one function's early-exit-shaped logic. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-platform/src/clipboard.rs:30-57 (ArboardClipboard::read's exclusive text-or-image logic, verified)._
139. **PopupApp::filtered hardcodes vbuff_core::search as the one and only ranking algorithm the GUI can use** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - app.rs's filtered (lines 91-94) imports and calls `search(clips, &self.query)` from vbuff_core directly with no injected ranking strategy. A future feature like fuzzy search, a saved-filter/tag search mode, or per-kind search scoping (mentioned across the ideas backlog) has no seam to plug an alternate SearchStrategy into PopupApp; the concrete free function is called by name from the one place that needs ranked results. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-gui/src/app.rs:91-94 (PopupApp::filtered calling vbuff_core's search function directly, verified)._
140. **UiAction is one flat enum handled by one giant match in handle_action; every new user action grows both in lockstep** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - state.rs's UiAction enum (lines 41-54) and actions.rs's handle_action match (lines 59-104) are two files that must be edited together for every new user-facing action (e.g. a Favorite/Unfavorite toggle - `favorite` exists as a Clip/Store field but has no UiAction variant or handler arm, or a future Tag action). There is no `Action: fn(&mut AppContext)` trait/closure-based command pattern that render.rs or input.rs could push without also requiring a new match arm in actions.rs; the enum and its handler are two parallel closed lists. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-gui/src/state.rs:41-54 (UiAction enum, verified); src/actions.rs:59-104 (handle_action's matching match, verified)._
141. **Modifier enum has four hardcoded platform-agnostic variants, but paste.rs and hotkey.rs each independently re-map them to their own backend's key type** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - traits.rs's Modifier enum (Control/Alt/Shift/Meta) is consumed by two separate hand-written match statements: hotkey.rs's combo_to_hotkey (lines 56-65, mapping to global_hotkey::Modifiers) and paste.rs's PasteBackend::paste (lines 31-36, mapping to enigo::Key). Adding a fifth modifier (e.g. a Fn key on some keyboards, or AltGr) requires editing both backend crates' independent match statements in lockstep with no shared `Modifier -> target-type` conversion trait (e.g. `impl From<Modifier> for global_hotkey::Modifiers` / `impl From<Modifier> for enigo::Key`) that would let each backend own its own mapping without both being touched by the trait definition's author. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-platform/src/hotkey.rs:56-65 (combo_to_hotkey's Modifier match, verified); crates/vbuff-platform/src/paste.rs:31-36 (paste's Modifier match, verified)._
142. **paste_modifier() hardcodes a single cfg(target_os) branch instead of deferring to Config's already-present paste_modifier field** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - vbuff-platform/src/lib.rs's paste_modifier() (lines 35-44) is compiled with `#[cfg(target_os = "macos")]` returning Meta, else Control - a compile-time-fixed OS/modifier pairing baked into the platform crate. Config already has a `paste_modifier: String` field (config.rs:22) intended to let the user override this, but nothing in src/gui.rs or src/actions.rs ever reads config.paste_modifier or passes it into EnigoPaste; grep confirms `paste_modifier` (the config field) is only ever set and serialized, never read outside config.rs. The override path does not exist because the platform crate's own function is not parameterizable - it is a closed cfg-gated function, not an injected `Modifier` value the caller can supply. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-platform/src/lib.rs:35-44 (paste_modifier's cfg-gated closed function, verified); crates/vbuff-platform/src/paste.rs:31 (EnigoPaste::paste calls the closed paste_modifier() rather than taking a Modifier parameter, verified); src/config.rs:22 (paste_modifier field never read anywhere in src/, verified via grep)._
143. **GlobalHotkeyBackend only ever registers a single show/hide hotkey id; there is no seam for a second bound action (e.g. capture-on-demand)** `[improvement]` 🟢 `[low]` - main.rs registers exactly one hotkey and stores its id in a local `hotkey_id: Option<u32>` passed straight through to run_gui. HotkeyBackend::register/unregister are per-combo (traits.rs:65-68), which is a reasonable trait shape, but nothing in src/ maintains an id-to-action map; adding a second bound hotkey (docs/code-audit-top-50.md item 8 notes README promises a manual capture-on-demand hotkey that does not exist) would require inventing a `HashMap<u32, HotkeyAction>` from scratch in main.rs/gui.rs rather than there being an existing extension point for multiple registered actions. This is a distinct OCP gap from item 8's documentation-vs-reality mismatch: even if the feature were built today, the current single-id plumbing has no registry to extend. _Evidence: src/main.rs:79-90 (single hotkey_id, no action-keyed registry, verified); crates/vbuff-platform/src/traits.rs:62-69 (HotkeyBackend is per-combo but nothing multiplexes ids to actions, verified)._
144. **Flavor::is_text()/is_image() hardcode exactly two MIME-prefix predicates on the type itself, with every new predicate added the same way** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - vbuff-types/src/lib.rs's Flavor impl (lines 188-196) hardcodes `is_text()` (mime.starts_with("text/") || mime == "text") and `is_image()` (mime.starts_with("image/")) as inherent methods. classify.rs, clipboard.rs, and thumbnail.rs all call these two predicates by name; a new predicate (e.g. `is_html()`, `is_rtf()`, `is_file_list()`) that classify.rs currently reimplements ad hoc via raw `mime.contains("html")` string checks (classify.rs:43,46) has no consistent home - some MIME predicates live on Flavor, others are inlined string checks scattered in classify.rs, meaning there is no single `FlavorKind` extension point new predicates plug into uniformly. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-types/src/lib.rs:188-196 (Flavor::is_text/is_image, the only two MIME predicates on the type, verified); crates/vbuff-core/src/classify.rs:43,46 (html/rtf detected via ad hoc mime.contains instead of a Flavor predicate, verified)._
145. **Store's list()/load_recent() ordering (pinned DESC, updated_at DESC, seq DESC) is hardcoded SQL with no pluggable sort/list strategy** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - Store::list (vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:124-136) hardcodes its ORDER BY clause directly in the SQL string. There is no `ListQuery`/`SortStrategy` abstraction a future feature (sort-by-size, sort-by-kind-then-recency, or a 'recently used' MRU view distinct from 'recently captured') could supply; every new ordering mode requires either a new hardcoded method on Store (mirroring list/load_recent) or editing this SQL string directly, with callers (capture.rs, actions.rs, main.rs) all calling the one fixed method by name. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:123-141 (Store::list/load_recent's hardcoded ORDER BY, verified)._
146. **detect_kind's file-list detection is four hand-written MIME substring checks with no OS-specific detector plugged in via a trait** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - classify.rs:22-26 checks four hardcoded string patterns (`text/uri-list`, `.contains("file-url")`, `.contains("Filenames")`, `application/x-file-list`) inline to recognize a file-list flavor across different OS clipboard conventions (macOS NSFilenamesPboardType, Windows CF_HDROP-derived, X11 uri-list). Since these are OS-specific MIME conventions, they naturally belong behind the platform crate's future native backends (per the architecture doc's stated direction), but today they are hardcoded as string literals inside the OS-agnostic vbuff-core crate itself - meaning a new OS convention requires editing vbuff-core rather than the platform crate registering its own MIME vocabulary through some FileListDetector seam. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-core/src/classify.rs:20-29 (four hardcoded MIME substring checks for file-list detection, verified)._
147. **is_url's SCHEMES list is a fixed &'static [&str] array with no extension point for config-defined or discovered schemes** `[improvement]` 🟢 `[low]` - classify.rs:84-86 hardcodes exactly eight URI schemes (http, https, ftp, ftps, file, mailto, ssh, git) as a const array inside is_url. A user who frequently copies `slack://`, `vscode://`, `tel:`, or `zoommtg://` links gets no Url classification for them, and there is no Config-driven or pluggable scheme list is_url consults - extending scheme recognition means editing this const array in vbuff-core directly, coupling a user-extensible preference to a compiled-in constant. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-core/src/classify.rs:84-86 (SCHEMES const array, no extension point, verified)._
148. **actions.rs's handle_action takes an egui::Context parameter, coupling a store/clipboard side-effect dispatcher to a specific GUI framework type** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - handle_action's signature (actions.rs:51-58) takes `ctx: &egui::Context` purely to call `ctx.send_viewport_cmd`/`ctx.request_repaint_after` inside the UiAction::Paste arm. This means the action-dispatch layer, which otherwise only touches Store/ClipboardBackend, cannot be reused or unit-tested without an egui context, and if the GUI framework is ever swapped (the crate's own doc frames egui/eframe as the current popup implementation, not a permanent commitment), every call site of handle_action and its signature must change. A `ViewportControl` trait (show/hide/request-repaint) that PopupApp's egui glue implements would let handle_action depend on an abstraction instead of the concrete eframe type. _Evidence: src/actions.rs:51-58 (handle_action's `ctx: &egui::Context` parameter, verified), 74,78 (direct egui::ViewportCommand/request_repaint_after calls, verified)._

---

## SOLID: Liskov Substitution & Interface Segregation issues

149. **HotkeyBackend has no way to report 'this platform cannot do hotkeys at all', forcing every future backend to fake success or fake an error** `[problem]` 🟠 `[high]` - The trait's only two methods return Result<u32> and Result<()> - there is no capability query and no 'unsupported' error variant that is distinguishable at the type level from 'a specific combo failed to register' (both map to PlatformError::Hotkey(String), a stringly-typed catch-all). A hypothetical future backend that genuinely cannot register global hotkeys on some session (no compositor grant, no portal) has exactly two honest-ish options: return Ok(some_id) that does nothing (an LSP-violating postcondition weakening), or return Err on every call including calls that are individually well-formed, which callers (main.rs:82-88) will read as 'bad combo' rather than 'hotkeys unsupported here'. Nothing in the trait or PlatformError lets an implementor say 'this operation is categorically unavailable' distinctly from 'this specific call failed'. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-platform/src/traits.rs:62-69 (HotkeyBackend has only register/unregister, no capability probe); crates/vbuff-platform/src/error.rs:12-14 (single Hotkey(String) variant used for both per-call and structural failures)._
150. **PasteBackend::paste has no way to express 'permanently unavailable' vs 'this attempt failed', so callers can't distinguish a doomed environment from a transient glitch** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - On macOS without the Accessibility permission, every EnigoPaste::paste() call silently drops the keystroke at the OS level rather than erroring (per the module's own doc comment), so PlatformError::Paste is never actually raised for the one case that matters most. The trait gives implementors no channel to say 'I constructed fine but this environment will never let paste succeed' - a single fallible operation is asked to carry both transient-failure and structural-unavailability semantics, and this impl can't even use the Err path for the structural case because the OS doesn't tell it paste failed. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-platform/src/paste.rs:6-8 ('this requires the Accessibility permission to be granted... otherwise the keystroke is silently dropped by the OS'); crates/vbuff-platform/src/traits.rs:72-75 (PasteBackend::paste: Result<()> is the only signal, and it isn't raised in the dropped-keystroke case)._
151. **ClipboardBackend::write's implicit 'pick one flavor' behavior is a silent narrowing that violates the trait's own multi-flavor doc comment** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - The trait's doc comment says 'Write a flavor set back to the clipboard' (plural, implying it writes the set), but ArboardClipboard::write (clipboard.rs:59-92) can only ever persist exactly one flavor - text if present, else a single RGBA image - and any other flavors in the passed slice are dropped with no error, no return value indicating what was dropped, and no log. A caller holding a clip with both text/plain and text/html flavors calls write(&clip.flavors) expecting the trait's stated multi-flavor behavior and gets single-flavor behavior with no feedback that narrowing happened. This violates the interface's implied postcondition (all flavors written) in a way that's invisible from the Result<()> return type. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-platform/src/traits.rs:53-54 ('Write a flavor set back to the clipboard (for paste-back)'); crates/vbuff-platform/src/clipboard.rs:59-92 (write picks exactly one of text-or-image, dropping every other flavor in the slice silently)._
152. **CapturedClipboard.source_app is a shared trait-return field that zero implementors can populate, advertising a capability the interface doesn't actually offer** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - CapturedClipboard (traits.rs:32-46) is the shared return type for every ClipboardBackend::read() implementation and carries `source_app: Option<String>` with a doc comment promising 'the frontmost application's identifier, if the backend could learn it'. arboard exposes no API to learn the frontmost app, so ArboardClipboard::read unconditionally sets it to None. The field's presence in the shared trait-level struct means every caller of the trait must defensively assume source_app is always None rather than being able to rely on the interface contract even conditionally - an Interface Segregation problem distinct from the fact that no capture-time value ever flows through it: source-app attribution shouldn't be bundled into the same struct as flavor reading when the trait offers no way for an implementor to declare whether it supports that capability at all. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-platform/src/traits.rs:32-39 (CapturedClipboard.source_app is part of the ClipboardBackend::read return type, with no per-implementor capability flag); crates/vbuff-platform/src/clipboard.rs:53-56 (ArboardClipboard::read always returns source_app: None)._
153. **HotkeyBackend forces a single show/hide-hotkey use case onto a general (combo) -> id registration API, making 'register a second unrelated hotkey' silently collide** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - register() takes an arbitrary KeyCombo and returns an opaque u32 id, which reads as a general-purpose 'register any number of hotkeys' API. But global-hotkey's HotKey::id() (vendored crate) computes the id as `(mods.bits() << 16) | key as u32` - a deterministic function of (mods, key), not an allocation counter - so calling register() twice with the *same* combo from two different GlobalHotkeyBackend instances (e.g. a future 'manual capture hotkey' registered alongside the show/hide one with an accidentally identical combo) returns the same id from both, and GlobalHotkeyBackend::registered (a HashMap<u32, HotKey> keyed by that id) can only track one of them - a later unregister(id) for the wrong logical hotkey unregisters whichever HotKey happens to be sitting in the map for that id. The trait's register/unregister pair implies id-scoped independent registrations (like a subscription handle), but the concrete id space is combo-scoped, not registration-scoped, which is a leaky abstraction the trait signature hides. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-platform/src/traits.rs:62-69 (register returns Result<u32> as if u32 is a unique registration handle); crates/vbuff-platform/src/hotkey.rs:16-19,35-43 (registered: HashMap<u32, HotKey> keyed by HotKey::id()); vendored global-hotkey-0.8.0/src/hotkey.rs:95-104 (id is `(mods.bits() << 16) | key as u32`, a deterministic function of mods+key, not an allocation)._
154. **HotkeyBackend::register's own doc comment bakes in the single show/hide use case, so the trait's stated contract isn't actually general-purpose despite its signature** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - register()'s doc comment reads 'Register the given combo *as the show/hide hotkey*. Returns the opaque platform id of the registered hotkey' (traits.rs:63-64) - the contract itself names one specific application-level purpose, not a general 'register any hotkey' operation, even though the method signature (`fn register(&mut self, combo: &KeyCombo) -> Result<u32>`) has no parameter distinguishing 'this is the show/hide hotkey' from any other combo a caller might register. A future caller registering a second, unrelated hotkey (e.g. a manual-capture combo) is calling a method whose documented contract doesn't actually describe what they're doing - the interface was never generalized past its first caller, which is exactly the kind of narrow, single-client-shaped interface ISP warns against. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-platform/src/traits.rs:62-65 (register's doc comment: 'Register the given combo as the show/hide hotkey', despite the method having no way to express or distinguish hotkey purpose/role)._
155. **ClipboardBackend, HotkeyBackend, and PasteBackend all reuse PlatformError's single stringly-typed variant per domain, so no implementor can distinguish retryable from permanent failures at the type level** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - PlatformError::Clipboard(String), ::Hotkey(String), and ::Paste(String) each collapse every possible failure mode of their trait (permission denied, device busy, malformed input, backend not constructed, OS API unavailable) into a single opaque string. Every trait method (read, write, register, unregister, paste) shares this shape, so a caller (gui.rs:141-145, main.rs:82-88) can only ever tracing::warn! the string - there's no way to match on the error to decide 'retry', 'prompt for permission', or 'give up permanently', even though those are semantically very different outcomes the trait's own doc comments allude to (e.g. paste.rs's own module comment describes a permission-based permanent failure mode that the type system can't express). _Evidence: crates/vbuff-platform/src/error.rs:7-27 (Clipboard/Hotkey/Paste/BadCombo/Empty are all opaque single-String variants); crates/vbuff-platform/src/traits.rs:49-75 (every trait method returns the same flat Result<_, PlatformError>)._
156. **KeyCombo/Modifier are declared in traits.rs as if they were HotkeyBackend-neutral, but Modifier::Meta's doc comment is macOS/Windows-specific, leaking one platform's semantics into a supposedly cross-platform type** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - Modifier::Meta's doc comment reads 'Command (macOS) / Super / Windows key' (traits.rs:19-20) - this is fine as documentation, but the enum has no way to represent that on Linux/X11 'Super' often means something different from either macOS Cmd or the Windows key (window-manager-reserved on many WMs), and paste_modifier() in lib.rs collapses the whole non-macOS world to Modifier::Control unconditionally. Any future Linux-native HotkeyBackend that wants Super as the modifier (common on GNOME/KDE clipboard-manager conventions) has no Modifier variant that means 'the platform's native Super key distinct from Ctrl', so it either misuses Meta (whose doc comment describes it as a macOS/Windows concept) or the type has to grow a new variant just for that backend - evidence the shared enum was designed around two platforms' key models, not a genuine cross-platform abstraction. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-platform/src/traits.rs:19-20 (Meta doc comment names macOS and Windows specifically, omitting Linux); crates/vbuff-platform/src/lib.rs:35-44 (paste_modifier hardcodes Meta for macOS, Control for 'not macOS' with no Linux Super case)._
157. **ClipboardBackend::write's Err(PlatformError::Empty) return path conflates 'you gave me nothing to write' with 'the clipboard itself is empty', reusing one error variant for two different call sites' meanings** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - PlatformError::Empty's doc comment says 'The clipboard held no readable content' (error.rs:24-26), which describes a read()-time condition. But ArboardClipboard::write returns that same variant at clipboard.rs:91 when the *input* flavors slice has no text and no RGBA-prefixed inline flavor - i.e. a write-time 'nothing writable was supplied' condition, not a clipboard-emptiness condition. A caller matching on PlatformError::Empty to special-case 'OS clipboard is empty' after a read() will get false positives from write() call sites reusing the same variant for an unrelated situation, since the trait doesn't scope error variants per-method. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-platform/src/error.rs:24-26 (Empty documented as a read-time 'clipboard held no readable content' condition); crates/vbuff-platform/src/clipboard.rs:91 (write() returns Err(PlatformError::Empty) for an unwritable input flavor set, not an empty OS clipboard)._
158. **HotkeyBackend::unregister's contract silently accepts unknown ids as success, hiding programmer errors that ClipboardBackend/PasteBackend would surface** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - GlobalHotkeyBackend::unregister (hotkey.rs:45-52) does `if let Some(hotkey) = self.registered.remove(&id) { ...unregister... }; Ok(())` - calling unregister with an id that was never registered (typo, double-unregister, id from a different backend instance) returns Ok(()) unconditionally, not an error. This is inconsistent with the sibling traits in the same module: ClipboardBackend::write does return Err(PlatformError::Empty) when given unwritable input, and PasteBackend::paste propagates enigo errors. HotkeyBackend is the outlier that defines 'no-op on invalid input' as success, which is an undocumented part of the trait's actual (vs. stated) contract - the doc comment ('Unregister a previously registered hotkey by id') implies the id was previously registered, but the impl doesn't enforce or signal violation of that precondition. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-platform/src/hotkey.rs:45-52 (unregister returns Ok(()) for any id not present in `registered`, including ids that were never registered); crates/vbuff-platform/src/traits.rs:67-68 (doc comment implies the id argument denotes 'a previously registered hotkey')._
159. **ClipboardBackend and PasteBackend both require &mut self for operations that are logically read-only or stateless, over-constraining every future implementor's internal concurrency model** `[improvement]` 🟢 `[low]` - ClipboardBackend::read(&mut self) and PasteBackend::paste(&mut self) take &mut self even though arboard's Clipboard::get_text/get_image and enigo's key() don't logically need exclusive mutable access to backend state - EnigoPaste holds no mutable fields that read/paste actually mutates beyond the underlying FFI handle. Because the trait bakes in &mut self, any future implementation that wants to be Arc<Backend> + shared across threads (e.g. a Wayland backend using an async data-control connection polled from a background task, sharing the same connection for both read and a hypothetical watch-for-changes API) is forced into an internal Mutex/RefCell it wouldn't otherwise need, purely to satisfy a signature the trait imposes rather than one the operation requires. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-platform/src/traits.rs:51,74 (ClipboardBackend::read and PasteBackend::paste both take &mut self); crates/vbuff-platform/src/clipboard.rs, crates/vbuff-platform/src/paste.rs (neither impl's fields are mutated by the respective operation beyond the underlying library handle)._
160. **HotkeyBackend bundles registration bookkeeping (id allocation, storage) into the trait contract instead of segregating 'ask OS to register' from 'track what's registered', forcing every implementor to reinvent the same map** `[improvement]` 🟢 `[low]` - Because register() returns only an opaque u32 and unregister() takes only that u32, every implementor is forced to independently maintain its own id -> native-handle map internally (GlobalHotkeyBackend's `registered: HashMap<u32, HotKey>` is exactly this). A cleaner ISP split would separate a narrow 'combo -> native registration' trait from the bookkeeping (which could live once in vbuff-platform as a generic wrapper any backend can compose), so a future backend author isn't required to reimplement id-tracking correctness (including the id-collision bug noted elsewhere) from scratch for every new platform. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-platform/src/traits.rs:62-69 (HotkeyBackend's register/unregister shape forces per-impl id bookkeeping); crates/vbuff-platform/src/hotkey.rs:16-19 (GlobalHotkeyBackend's own HashMap<u32, HotKey> is exactly this bookkeeping, duplicated per-implementor by trait design)._
161. **ClipboardBackend::write's implicit priority order (text over image) is a policy decision hardcoded into the trait's sole implementation with no way for callers to express intent** `[improvement]` 🟢 `[low]` - The trait signature `write(&mut self, flavors: &[Flavor]) -> Result<()>` gives callers no way to say 'prefer image' or 'write flavor X specifically' - ArboardClipboard::write unilaterally decides text always wins over image (clipboard.rs:62-72 checks is_text() first, falls through to RGBA only if no text flavor exists at all). A caller with an image-only clip that also happens to carry an incidental text/plain fallback (e.g. an OCR'd caption) has no way through this interface to force the image to be written instead. Since the trait exposes no per-call preference and CapturedClipboard/Flavor carry no priority field either, this ordering is a silent, unconfigurable policy wired into one specific backend, which the trait's signature neither documents nor allows a caller to override. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-platform/src/clipboard.rs:59-92 (write() has a fixed if-text-then-image priority with no caller-controllable parameter); crates/vbuff-platform/src/traits.rs:53-54 (write's signature offers no priority/selection parameter)._
162. **A future native macOS ClipboardBackend that reads concealed/transient pasteboard hints has no way to signal 'skip this capture' through the current trait, since read() must return a CapturedClipboard or an Err** `[idea]` 🟡 `[medium]` - Per docs/code-audit-top-50.md item 3, nothing currently checks NSPasteboard's ConcealedType/TransientType hints, but when that support is added, the natural place is inside a native ClipboardBackend::read(). The current trait forces read() to return either Ok(CapturedClipboard) (which callers in capture.rs treat as 'store this') or Err (which callers treat as a failure to log/retry) - there is no third outcome meaning 'I successfully read the clipboard and deliberately decline to surface it because it's marked concealed.' Extending the trait now with a variant like CapturedClipboard::Suppressed { reason } (or an enum ReadOutcome { Captured(CapturedClipboard), Suppressed(SuppressReason), Empty }) would let every future backend express 'this pasteboard write should never reach storage' without overloading Ok(empty flavors) (ambiguous with 'nothing was on the clipboard') or Err (ambiguous with 'the read failed'). _Evidence: crates/vbuff-platform/src/traits.rs:49-55 (ClipboardBackend::read returns Result<CapturedClipboard>, with no third outcome for a deliberate skip) cross-referenced with docs/code-audit-top-50.md item 3 (no concealed/transient hint checking exists yet)._
163. **Design an ISP-narrow HotkeyRegistration handle type instead of a bare u32 id, so unregister can't be called against the wrong backend instance or a stale/foreign id** `[idea]` 🟡 `[medium]` - Because register() returns a bare u32 with no lifetime or backend tie, nothing at the type level stops main.rs/gui.rs from calling hotkey_backend_a.unregister(id_from_backend_b) - especially relevant once a second HotkeyBackend implementation exists (e.g. a portal-based one alongside GlobalHotkeyBackend) and the app has to choose one at startup; a copy-paste bug wiring the wrong backend's id would compile fine and silently no-op (per the id-acceptance finding above). A newtype like `struct HotkeyHandle(u32)` tied to `PhantomData<Backend>` or simply requiring `unregister(self, handle: HotkeyHandle)` (consuming, not borrowing, the handle) would make cross-backend id misuse a compile error instead of a silent runtime no-op. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-platform/src/traits.rs:62-69 (register returns a bare u32 with no type-level tie to the issuing backend instance)._
164. **Split ClipboardBackend into a narrow ClipboardReader/ClipboardWriter pair so a future capture-only or paste-only backend isn't forced to stub the half it can't honestly implement** `[idea]` 🟡 `[medium]` - Every current caller either only reads (capture.rs's polling thread) or only writes (actions.rs's paste/copy-latest handlers) - no single call site both reads and writes through the same ClipboardBackend instance. But the trait bundles both under one Send trait, so a future specialized backend (e.g. a Wayland wlr-data-control listener that can watch/read selection-offer events but has no sane 'write' story because Wayland write requires becoming a selection source with its own event loop) would have to implement a write() it cannot honestly support, and would face the same 'what do I return' dilemma already visible in the fat-trait problems above. Splitting into `trait ClipboardReader: Send { fn read(&mut self) -> Result<CapturedClipboard>; }` and `trait ClipboardWriter: Send { fn write(&mut self, flavors: &[Flavor]) -> Result<()>; }` (with ArboardClipboard implementing both, since it legitimately can) lets a read-only or write-only backend implement exactly the capability it has, and lets capture.rs/actions.rs depend on only the capability they use rather than the union. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-platform/src/traits.rs:49-55 (ClipboardBackend bundles read and write in one trait); src/capture.rs and src/actions.rs each only ever call one of the two methods per call site, never both on the same instance._
165. **Add a HotkeyBackend::is_supported() / capability probe so callers can distinguish 'not registered because it failed' from 'not registered because this platform has no working hotkey path' before ever calling register()** `[idea]` 🟡 `[medium]` - main.rs currently only learns a hotkey didn't register by calling register() and inspecting the Err (main.rs:82-88); on a session where the underlying registration mechanism can never succeed, there's still no way to warn the user proactively before attempting. A `fn capability(&self) -> HotkeyCapability` method (returning e.g. Native, Unsupported, RequiresPermission) queried once at startup would let main.rs decide whether to even attempt registration, and would let a future settings UI show 'global hotkey unavailable in this session' instead of only ever reacting to a failed register() call after the fact. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-platform/src/traits.rs:62-69 (HotkeyBackend has no capability-query method, only register/unregister) cross-referenced with src/main.rs:82-88 (register() is the only signal main.rs has to decide whether the hotkey is usable)._
166. **PasteBackend has no capability/permission-check method, so the Accessibility-permission gap (docs/code-audit-top-50.md #10) can't be fixed without also touching the trait** `[idea]` 🟡 `[medium]` - Fixing the 'no accessibility-permission onboarding' gap already logged in the audit requires knowing, before calling paste(), whether the permission is granted - but PasteBackend exposes no such query, only the fallible paste() action itself, which (per the module doc) doesn't even fail when the permission is missing. Adding `fn can_paste(&self) -> bool` (backed on macOS by `AXIsProcessTrusted()`) to the trait would let the app show an onboarding prompt (deep-linking to System Settings > Privacy > Accessibility) before the user ever notices paste silently doing nothing, and would give the trait a way to express the permission-gated nature of the operation that its current single fallible method cannot. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-platform/src/traits.rs:72-75 (PasteBackend has only the fallible paste() method, no capability/permission query) cross-referenced with docs/code-audit-top-50.md item 10 (no accessibility-permission onboarding exists)._
167. **Give KeyCombo a validate()/is_representable() method so parse_combo's happy-path construction and a future backend's key_to_code-style rejection don't diverge silently** `[idea]` 🟢 `[low]` - parse_combo (hotkey.rs:127-147) can construct a KeyCombo containing any string in `.key` (it doesn't check against key_to_code's known-key table at parse time - that check only happens later, inside combo_to_hotkey at register() time). That means a KeyCombo value can exist in a 'looks valid, but no current or future backend can actually represent it' state for an arbitrary amount of time between config load and hotkey registration, and a second backend (e.g. a Linux-native one with its own different key-name table) would have to reimplement its own validation with no shared contract to conform to. Moving validation onto KeyCombo itself (or a small trait every backend's key-mapper implements) would let callers check representability once, independent of which concrete HotkeyBackend ends up registering it. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-platform/src/hotkey.rs:127-147 (parse_combo builds KeyCombo with no validation against key_to_code) and hotkey.rs:75-120 (key_to_code's table is the only validation, applied later inside combo_to_hotkey at register-time)._
168. **CapturedClipboard's is_empty() only checks flavors.is_empty(), so a future backend that captures only source_app metadata has no honest way to report partial captures through the shared type** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - traits.rs:41-46 defines is_empty() as `self.flavors.is_empty()`, ignoring source_app entirely. If any future ClipboardBackend legitimately captures source_app (attribution) without flavors (e.g. it observed a clipboard-owner change but the read of actual bytes failed or was concealed), CapturedClipboard::is_empty() reports true, discarding the source_app information as if nothing useful was captured at all, even though the struct has a documented field specifically meant to carry that partial information. The shared type's own convenience method doesn't account for the full shape of the struct it belongs to. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-platform/src/traits.rs:32-46 (CapturedClipboard.source_app exists as a documented field, but is_empty() at line 43-45 only inspects flavors, silently treating a source_app-only capture as empty)._
169. **HotkeyBackend::register takes &KeyCombo by reference but the trait gives implementors no way to reject combos they structurally cannot bind, forcing every implementor into the same single BadCombo string bucket as a genuine parse failure** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - PlatformError::BadCombo (error.rs:20-22) is documented as 'A key combo string could not be parsed' - a parse-time concern - but combo_to_hotkey (hotkey.rs:66-67) also returns BadCombo for a KeyCombo that parsed fine syntactically but whose key isn't in key_to_code's table (e.g. any punctuation key, function keys F1-F12, arrow keys - none are mapped). That's a capability gap, not a parse failure, yet both conditions produce the identical error variant with no field to distinguish them. A caller cannot tell 'the user typed garbage in config' from 'the user's combo is valid but this backend's key table is incomplete', which matters because the UI response should differ (fix your config vs. this key isn't supported yet). _Evidence: crates/vbuff-platform/src/error.rs:20-22 (BadCombo documented as a parse-time error); crates/vbuff-platform/src/hotkey.rs:66-67 (combo_to_hotkey reuses BadCombo for 'unknown key' - a capability gap in key_to_code's match, not a string-parsing failure) and hotkey.rs:75-120 (key_to_code has no F-keys, arrows, punctuation, or Backspace/Delete/Escape)._
170. **ClipboardBackend is declared Send but not Sync with no documented reasoning, silently leaving every implementor's concurrency contract to guesswork** `[improvement]` 🟢 `[low]` - `pub trait ClipboardBackend: Send` (traits.rs:49) only requires Send, meaning trait objects/generic call sites can move a ClipboardBackend across threads but never share a &ClipboardBackend between threads without wrapping it in a Mutex (which is exactly what capture.rs and actions.rs each do independently, each constructing its own ArboardClipboard rather than sharing one). This is a minor case of the trait under-specifying its concurrency contract in the other direction from the &mut self issue above: because &mut self is required for read()/write() anyway, Sync would be moot for calling read/write concurrently, but the absence of any documented reasoning here (no comment explains why Send-only, not Send + Sync) means every future implementor has to guess whether they're expected to support any concurrent access pattern at all. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-platform/src/traits.rs:49 (`pub trait ClipboardBackend: Send` - no Sync bound, no comment on the concurrency contract); crates/vbuff-platform/src/clipboard.rs:17-19 (ArboardClipboard's single field, `clipboard: Clipboard`, has no stated thread-safety story beyond what arboard itself documents)._
171. **The module doc in lib.rs promises a 'TrayBackend' trait as part of the same seam as the other three, but no such trait exists anywhere in traits.rs - the documentation describes an interface that was never factored out** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - lib.rs's module doc comment lists four bullet points describing the trait seam: ClipboardBackend, HotkeyBackend, PasteBackend, and 'TrayBackend - a status-bar/tray icon (tray-icon, app crate)'. traits.rs defines exactly three traits; there is no TrayBackend trait anywhere in vbuff-platform, and the actual tray implementation (src/tray.rs, gated behind the `tray` feature) is a concrete struct with no trait abstraction at all - main.rs and gui.rs reference `crate::tray::Tray` directly, not any platform-crate trait. The doc comment describes a fourth member of the ISP-relevant trait seam that doesn't exist, which is itself a discoverability problem for anyone using this doc comment to reason about what abstractions are actually swappable. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-platform/src/lib.rs:9-12 (module doc lists ClipboardBackend, HotkeyBackend, PasteBackend, and TrayBackend as the four seam traits); crates/vbuff-platform/src/traits.rs (only three traits are defined: ClipboardBackend, HotkeyBackend, PasteBackend - no TrayBackend anywhere in the crate); src/tray.rs:16 (`pub(crate) struct Tray` - a concrete struct, not a trait)._
172. **GlobalHotkeyBackend::register mutates internal state (inserts into `registered`) with an ordering invariant that the trait neither requires nor documents, so a future implementor or refactor could silently desync bookkeeping from OS state** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - register() (hotkey.rs:35-43) calls `self.manager.register(hotkey)?` first, and only inserts into `self.registered` after that succeeds - so today the ordering happens to be safe. But nothing in the HotkeyBackend trait contract states or enforces that 'the internal registration table and the OS-level registration must never diverge'; that's purely an implementation detail of this one impl, invisible at the trait level. A different implementor (or a future refactor of this one, e.g. to batch-register several hotkeys) could easily insert into its bookkeeping map before confirming OS success, silently producing a HotkeyBackend where `unregister(id)` 'succeeds' (removes from the map, calls the OS unregister) for an id whose OS-level registration never actually took effect - and the trait provides no way to catch or forbid that at the type level; it's an invariant that exists only by convention in one file. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-platform/src/hotkey.rs:35-43 (register's ordering - OS call before map insert - is correct today but is a convention, not something HotkeyBackend's contract in traits.rs:62-69 requires or documents)._
173. **KeyCombo has no Hash derive despite being the natural key for detecting 'this combo is already registered', forcing every implementor to roll its own equality-based dedup logic like GlobalHotkeyBackend's accidental id-collision workaround** `[improvement]` 🟢 `[low]` - KeyCombo derives Clone, Debug, PartialEq, Eq (traits.rs:24-30) but not Hash, even though the natural way to detect 'this combo is already registered' (relevant to the id-collision problem noted elsewhere) is to key a map by KeyCombo itself rather than by a backend-specific opaque id. Because Hash is missing, GlobalHotkeyBackend can't use `HashMap<KeyCombo, u32>` for dedup/lookup and instead relies entirely on the downstream HotKey::id() collision behavior (which is accidental, not designed) to avoid double-registering. Adding `Hash` to the derive list (and documenting that modifiers order shouldn't affect equality, which today it does since `modifiers: Vec<Modifier>` compares order-sensitively) would let any implementor build a correct, self-contained combo -> registration map without depending on the underlying crate's id scheme. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-platform/src/traits.rs:24-30 (KeyCombo derives Clone, Debug, PartialEq, Eq but not Hash; modifiers: Vec<Modifier> makes equality order-sensitive, e.g. [Control, Shift] != [Shift, Control] even though they denote the same combo)._
174. **Adding a richer ClipboardBackend for HTML/RTF capture would have to widen CapturedClipboard.flavors semantics with no way to express partial/best-effort capture, since Vec<Flavor> gives no per-flavor success/failure signal** `[idea]` 🟢 `[low]` - When docs/code-audit-top-50.md item #15 (no RTF/HTML capture) is eventually fixed by a richer backend, that backend will often be able to read *some* offered MIME types but fail on others mid-capture (e.g. a delayed-render HTML representation that times out while plain text succeeded). The current CapturedClipboard.flavors: Vec<Flavor> has no way to report 'text/plain captured fine, text/html was offered but failed to realize' - it can only report the flavors that fully succeeded, silently. A `flavors: Vec<Result<Flavor, FlavorReadError>>` (or a separate `partial_failures: Vec<String>` field) would let a richer backend honestly report partial capture instead of quietly downgrading to whatever subset happened to work, which every future implementor would otherwise have to solve ad hoc (or not at all, which is the current pattern). _Evidence: crates/vbuff-platform/src/traits.rs:32-39 (CapturedClipboard.flavors: Vec<Flavor> has no per-flavor error/partial-success channel) cross-referenced with docs/code-audit-top-50.md item 15 (no RTF/HTML capture path exists yet, so this gap hasn't surfaced in practice)._
175. **PasteBackend::paste's single method can't express 'paste as plain text' vs 'paste with formatting', a distinction the flavor-rich clipboard model (vbuff_types::Flavor) already supports on the write side but the trait discards on the paste side** `[idea]` 🟢 `[low]` - ClipboardBackend::write accepts `flavors: &[Flavor]`, preserving (in principle) multiple representations, but PasteBackend::paste() takes no arguments at all - it just synthesizes a keystroke, relying entirely on whatever was already written to the OS clipboard by a prior write() call. There is no way through this trait pair to say 'paste this specific flavor', which matters for a plain-text-only paste feature (a common clipboard-manager option: 'paste and match style'). Since write() already silently narrows to one flavor (see the fat-trait finding on write), and paste() carries no flavor selection of its own, the two operations compound: by the time paste() fires, the flavor choice was already made unilaterally by write(), and paste() has no way to second-guess or select differently even in principle. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-platform/src/traits.rs:53-54 (write takes flavors: &[Flavor]) versus traits.rs:74 (paste() takes no arguments at all, so flavor selection is entirely write()'s unilateral decision)._
176. **Introduce a HotkeyEventSource trait (or associated receiver type) so the app doesn't reach past HotkeyBackend into a crate-global GlobalHotKeyEvent::receiver() static, which breaks substitutability entirely for any second implementor** `[idea]` 🟠 `[high]` - HotkeyBackend only covers (un)registration by design (its own doc comment says so explicitly: 'Event delivery uses the backing crate's global receiver; callers poll it from their event loop... The trait therefore only covers (un)registration'). But that means gui.rs's actual event consumption (`GlobalHotKeyEvent::receiver().try_recv()`, gui.rs:92) bypasses the HotkeyBackend trait entirely and calls a `global_hotkey`-crate-specific global static directly. This is the sharpest LSP violation in the module: swapping GlobalHotkeyBackend for any other HotkeyBackend implementor (a portal-based backend, a mock for tests) would compile fine (the trait object substitutes cleanly) but silently produce zero hotkey events at runtime, because the actual event stream was never abstracted - it's hardcoded to one crate's global receiver regardless of which HotkeyBackend is in play. A trait method like `fn events(&self) -> &dyn HotkeyEventReceiver` (or requiring the backend to expose an mpsc::Receiver-like handle) would make substitutability real instead of superficial. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-platform/src/hotkey.rs:1-5 (module doc: 'Events are delivered through its process-global receiver... The trait therefore only covers (un)registration'); src/gui.rs:11,92 (`use global_hotkey::GlobalHotKeyEvent;` and `GlobalHotKeyEvent::receiver().try_recv()` called directly, bypassing the HotkeyBackend abstraction entirely)._
177. **main.rs and gui.rs depend on the concrete GlobalHotkeyBackend type in their function signatures rather than `impl HotkeyBackend` / `dyn HotkeyBackend`, so the trait exists but nothing in the codebase actually programs against it** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - run_gui's signature (gui.rs:21-27) takes `mut hotkey_backend: GlobalHotkeyBackend` by concrete type, not `impl HotkeyBackend` or `Box<dyn HotkeyBackend>`; main.rs constructs `GlobalHotkeyBackend::new()` directly (main.rs:79) and passes the concrete type through. Despite HotkeyBackend being imported and its trait methods (register/unregister) being called via the trait (main.rs:82, gui.rs:155), the surrounding function boundaries never actually accept the trait - they accept one specific struct. Combined with the direct GlobalHotKeyEvent::receiver() call noted separately, this means the trait is decorative at the call-site level: there is currently no code path in the binary that could substitute a different HotkeyBackend implementor without editing run_gui's and main()'s signatures, which undercuts the stated purpose in traits.rs's module doc ('the seam at which native per-OS backends can later be swapped in'). _Evidence: src/gui.rs:21-27 (`pub(crate) fn run_gui(... mut hotkey_backend: GlobalHotkeyBackend ...)` - concrete type, not a trait bound); src/main.rs:79 (`GlobalHotkeyBackend::new()` constructed and passed through by concrete type all the way to run_gui)._
178. **ArboardClipboard::new() and EnigoPaste::new() each define their own inherent constructor outside either trait, so 'which backend can even be constructed on this platform' is entirely outside the ClipboardBackend/PasteBackend abstraction** `[improvement]` 🟢 `[low]` - Both concrete backends expose an inherent `fn new() -> Result<Self>` that is not part of ClipboardBackend or PasteBackend (the traits only define the post-construction operations). Every call site that wants to construct 'whichever backend the platform supports' (main.rs:79, gui.rs:42, actions.rs:43,69) has to know the concrete type up front and call its inherent constructor - there is no trait-level factory method or associated function the traits define, so 'try to construct a working backend, falling back to alternates' logic (relevant once a second ClipboardBackend or PasteBackend implementor exists) has no shared shape to conform to; each call site would have to hardcode its own try-A-then-B chain rather than the trait providing e.g. a `fn try_new() -> Option<Self>` convention all implementors follow identically. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-platform/src/clipboard.rs:21-26 (ArboardClipboard::new, inherent, not part of ClipboardBackend); crates/vbuff-platform/src/paste.rs:20-27 (EnigoPaste::new, inherent, not part of PasteBackend); crates/vbuff-platform/src/traits.rs (neither trait declares any constructor-shaped associated function)._
179. **EnigoPaste::paste's partial-failure handling (release the modifier even if the key-click failed, but still propagate the click error) is a recovery policy invisible at the PasteBackend trait level, so a different implementor could leave the modifier key stuck down without violating the trait's stated contract** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - paste() (paste.rs:38-47) is careful to call `self.enigo.key(modifier_key, Direction::Release)` even when the preceding `Key::Unicode('v')` click failed, specifically to avoid leaving Cmd/Ctrl physically 'held down' from the OS's perspective if the middle step errors. This is exactly the right thing to do, but it's a behavior the PasteBackend trait itself neither requires nor documents - `fn paste(&mut self) -> Result<()>` says nothing about what state the keyboard must be left in on failure. A different implementor (or this one, after a future edit) could return Err from the press step without ever releasing, and still satisfy the trait's type signature; nothing catches that regression because 'never leave a stuck modifier key' is a contract that exists only as a code comment in one impl, not as anything the trait forces or tests verify. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-platform/src/paste.rs:38-47 ('Always release the modifier even if the 'v' click failed' - a hand-written invariant with no trait-level enforcement); crates/vbuff-platform/src/traits.rs:72-75 (PasteBackend's contract says nothing about keyboard-state cleanup on partial failure)._

---

## DRY: concrete duplicated logic

180. **Store::insert -> enforce_cap -> load_recent -> set_clips sequence duplicated between capture.rs and actions.rs/gui.rs** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - capture.rs's spawn_capture_thread (lines 88-100) inlines: lock store, insert, call store.enforce_cap(config.max_history), call store.load_recent(GUI_LIMIT), then shared.lock().unwrap().set_clips(clips). actions.rs's refresh_snapshot (lines 108-112) is a second, separately-written implementation of the tail half of that same sequence (load_recent + set_clips), called from three of the four UiAction arms plus gui.rs:118's tray ClearHistory handler. The capture thread does not call refresh_snapshot even though its last two lines are identical to it; it has its own copy of load_recent+set_clips (capture.rs:95-99) instead of reusing the existing helper. _Evidence: src/capture.rs:88-100 (esp. 95-99) duplicates src/actions.rs:108-112 (refresh_snapshot) instead of calling it; gui.rs:118 shows refresh_snapshot's actual call-site pattern._
181. **Two independent 'resolve OS base directory then join("vbuff")' implementations** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - crates/vbuff-store/src/paths.rs's dirs_data_dir() (lines 14-41) hand-rolls per-OS env-var lookups (HOME/APPDATA/XDG_DATA_HOME) specifically to avoid depending on the `dirs` crate, then default_db_path() does `dir.join("vbuff").join("history.db")`. src/config.rs's config_path() (lines 92-95) calls `dirs::config_dir()` (the `dirs` crate, already a workspace dependency used by the root binary) then does the identical `dir.join("vbuff").join(...)`. The `.join("vbuff")` convention and the two-tier 'resolve base dir, then append vbuff/<file>' shape is duplicated with two different resolution strategies for what should be one project-wide convention (e.g. a shared `vbuff_app_dir()` helper), risking the config dir and data dir silently disagreeing on a given OS if either implementation is tweaked later. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/paths.rs:8-41 vs src/config.rs:92-95._
182. **Test-only Clip-builder helper reimplemented four times with near-identical bodies** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - `make_clip(text: &str) -> Clip` in crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:232-247 and the near-identical `make_clip` in crates/vbuff-store/tests/integration.rs:7-25 both build a single-text-flavor Clip via `Flavor::inline("text/plain...", ...)` + `content_hash_from_flavors` + `ClipId::new()` + `ClipMeta::now(...)`. crates/vbuff-core/src/filter.rs:96-105's `text_clip` and crates/vbuff-core/src/eviction.rs:70-86's `clip` build the same shape (id/flavors/content_hash/meta/pinned/favorite struct literal) with only the hash left as `[0u8;32]` since vbuff-core cannot depend on its own hash module's test-only helper distinction. None of these are behind a shared `#[cfg(test)]` test-fixture module even within the same crate (store's own unit tests and its integration test each define `make_clip` from scratch), so a field added to `Clip` requires updating four separate copies of this constructor to keep compiling. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:232-247, crates/vbuff-store/tests/integration.rs:7-25, crates/vbuff-core/src/filter.rs:96-105, crates/vbuff-core/src/eviction.rs:70-86._
183. **'oldest-first, pinned-first' ordering encoded independently in SQL ORDER BY and Rust sort_by_key three separate times** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - The *recency* ordering rule 'pinned first, then by time' appears as raw SQL in Store::list (crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:130, `ORDER BY pinned DESC, updated_at DESC, seq DESC`) and, inverted for oldest-first eviction, again in Store::enforce_cap (line 212, `ORDER BY updated_at ASC, seq ASC`), while vbuff_core::filter::search (crates/vbuff-core/src/filter.rs:43-48) encodes the pinned-then-score comparator in Rust as `b.clip.pinned.cmp(&a.clip.pinned).then_with(...)`. There is no single named 'clip ordering policy' either language calls into; each of the three call sites re-derives the pinned-first convention from scratch in its own syntax, independent of the separately-flagged eviction-predicate duplication (is_protected vs. the SQL WHERE pinned=0 AND favorite=0 clause). _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:130 and :212 vs crates/vbuff-core/src/filter.rs:43-48._
184. **kind_to_int/kind_from_int match arms in row.rs structurally duplicate the ContentKind variant list already enumerated in icon()/label() in vbuff-types** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - crates/vbuff-types/src/lib.rs's ContentKind::icon() (lines 96-108) and ::label() (lines 111-123) each list all 9 ContentKind variants in one match. crates/vbuff-store/src/row.rs's kind_to_int (79-91) and kind_from_int (93-105) list the same 9 variants a third and fourth time, this time pairing each with an arbitrary integer discriminant. Because Rust's `#[derive]` cannot give an enum without explicit discriminants a stable wire-format integer, every new ContentKind variant must be manually added to four separate match arms across two crates in the right order, with nothing enforcing that row.rs's mapping and vbuff-types's variant list stay in sync (a forgotten arm in kind_from_int already silently falls through to `_ => ContentKind::Other`, masking the gap). _Evidence: crates/vbuff-types/src/lib.rs:96-123 (icon/label match arms) vs crates/vbuff-store/src/row.rs:79-105 (kind_to_int/kind_from_int match arms)._
185. **Bundle-id vs path-style app-name shortening in view.rs duplicates the substring-matching shape used by Config::is_excluded** `[improvement]` 🟢 `[low]` - crates/vbuff-gui/src/view.rs's short_app_name (lines 42-53) and src/config.rs's Config::is_excluded (lines 82-88) both exist to normalize/compare the same `source_app` identifier string (a macOS bundle id, a Windows exe path, or an X11 WM_CLASS), but each independently reinvents its own idea of 'the meaningful part of this string' - one strips to the last dotted/slash component for display, the other does a raw substring match for exclusion. Once source_app actually gets populated (currently hardcoded to None at capture time), both will operate on the same real-world strings; introduce one `vbuff_core::source_app` module with a canonical `normalize(source_app: &str) -> &str` (or similar) that both display-shortening and exclusion-matching build on, so 'com.apple.Safari' and '/Applications/Safari.app' are recognized as the same app consistently instead of each caller guessing independently.
186. **GUI_LIMIT is a raw constant duplicated by cross-reference instead of one load path in three call sites** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - `GUI_LIMIT: usize = 1000` is defined once in src/constants.rs, but it is applied at three separate call sites that each independently import and use it: main.rs:55 (`store.load_recent(GUI_LIMIT)` at startup), capture.rs:95 (`store.load_recent(GUI_LIMIT)` after every insert), and actions.rs:109 (`store.load_recent(GUI_LIMIT)` inside refresh_snapshot). This is a distinct concern from GUI_LIMIT's value being unrelated to config.max_history: even with the constant itself unchanged, nothing structurally forces all three call sites to keep calling `load_recent` with the same argument - a future edit to only two of the three (e.g. someone hand-editing capture.rs to `load_recent(500)` for a quick experiment) silently produces a GUI snapshot whose size depends on which code path last refreshed it, with no compiler or test signal. The three call sites should route through one `fn reload_gui_snapshot(store, shared)` (which refresh_snapshot already almost is) rather than each independently calling `load_recent(GUI_LIMIT)`. _Evidence: src/main.rs:55, src/capture.rs:95, src/actions.rs:109 - three independent `load_recent(GUI_LIMIT)` call sites._
187. **Modifier-to-native-enum match arms duplicated three times over for the same four-variant Modifier enum** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - crates/vbuff-platform's own `Modifier` enum (traits.rs:11-21, 4 variants: Control/Alt/Shift/Meta) is translated to and from third-party representations in three separate places: hotkey.rs's combo_to_hotkey (lines 58-64) maps every Modifier variant to `global_hotkey::hotkey::Modifiers::{CONTROL,ALT,SHIFT,META}`, paste.rs's EnigoPaste::paste (lines 31-36) maps every Modifier variant to `enigo::Key::{Control,Alt,Shift,Meta}`, and hotkey.rs's own parse_combo (lines 136-140) maps lowercase token strings back into the same four Modifier variants. All three enumerate the identical 4 arms; a 5th Modifier variant added later must be remembered in all three independently, and none is exhaustive by any compiler guarantee beyond 'both enums happen to have exactly 4 cases today' (the string-token match even has a silent catch-all `_ => key = Some(...)` that would swallow a typo'd 5th modifier name instead of erroring). _Evidence: crates/vbuff-platform/src/hotkey.rs:58-64 (combo_to_hotkey) and :136-140 (parse_combo) vs crates/vbuff-platform/src/paste.rs:31-36 (EnigoPaste::paste)._
188. **map_err(|e| PlatformError::X(e.to_string())) boilerplate repeated 10 times across three files instead of a helper/From impl** `[improvement]` 🟢 `[low]` - Every fallible call into arboard/global-hotkey/enigo in vbuff-platform is wrapped in the identical shape `.map_err(|e| PlatformError::Clipboard(e.to_string()))` / `::Hotkey(...)` / `::Paste(...)`, appearing at clipboard.rs:24,70,88 (3), hotkey.rs:26,39,49 (3), and paste.rs:24,40,45,46 (4) - 10 occurrences total of 'stringify the underlying error and wrap it in my variant.'
