Add a small `trait ResultExt<T> { fn platform_err(self, ctor: fn(String) -> PlatformError) -> Result<T>; }` (or three `From<X> for PlatformError` impls using `#[from]` on typed errors instead of `.to_string()`) in vbuff-platform/src/error.rs so each call site is `.platform_err(PlatformError::Clipboard)?` and the error variant's wrapping strategy lives in one place instead of being copy-pasted at every call site, which also currently throws away the original error's type/backtrace by eagerly stringifying it inline every time.
189. **PendingPaste's fixed 120ms delay literal is disconnected from gui.rs's poll-loop tick literals it must outlast** `[idea]` 🟢 `[low]` - src/actions.rs:76 hardcodes `Duration::from_millis(120)` for the paste-back delay, while src/gui.rs independently hardcodes the ticker interval (`Duration::from_millis(100)`, gui.rs:68) and the hidden-window repaint cadence (`Duration::from_millis(100)`, gui.rs:89) and the paste-pending repaint cadence (`Duration::from_millis(20)`, gui.rs:148, duplicated again in actions.rs:78). Separately from whether 120ms is the right value (a correctness question), these four millisecond literals are load-bearing relative to each other - the paste delay must be long enough to survive at least one tick of the repaint cadence, or the pending-paste check could fire late - but nothing expresses that relationship in code; a future edit to the ticker interval alone could silently change how many frames the pending-paste check gets. Pull all four into named constants in one place (e.g. `constants.rs`) with a comment stating the ordering constraint, instead of four independent magic-number literals across two files. _Evidence: src/actions.rs:76,78 vs src/gui.rs:68,89,148 - four independent millisecond-Duration literals with an implicit ordering dependency._
190. **Focus/grace-period Instant-based timing pattern in app.rs is a bespoke reimplementation of the same 'schedule a delayed action across frames' shape as PendingPaste in actions.rs** `[improvement]` 🟢 `[low]` - crates/vbuff-gui/src/app.rs's `shown_at: Option<Instant>` plus the grace_elapsed check (app.rs:135-138, `t.elapsed().as_millis() > 250`) and src/actions.rs's `PendingPaste { at: Instant::now() + Duration::from_millis(120) }` plus its `Instant::now() >= p.at` check in gui.rs:139-140 are two independently-invented ways of expressing the same 'has enough wall-clock time passed since I recorded a timestamp' pattern, one comparing an elapsed Duration to a threshold and the other comparing two Instants directly. A single `struct Deadline` (or `fn elapsed_past(since: Instant, threshold: Duration) -> bool`) shared by both would remove the need to re-derive the comparison direction (elapsed-vs-threshold vs now-vs-deadline) correctly at each of the two call sites.
191. **Clip-lookup-by-id linear scan pattern duplicated instead of a shared accessor on the shared state** `[improvement]` 🟢 `[low]` - src/actions.rs:65 does `s.clips.iter().find(|c| c.id == id).cloned()` to resolve a ClipId to a Clip for the Paste action, while crates/vbuff-gui/src/app.rs:163 builds a full `HashMap<ClipId, &Clip>` every frame for the same purpose (row lookup during rendering) via `clips.iter().map(|c| (c.id, c)).collect()`. Both are solving 'given the current clip list and an id, get the Clip,' but one is an O(n) linear scan done once per paste and the other is an O(n) hashmap rebuild done every single frame while the popup is open; neither reuses the other, and there is no single `AppState::find(&self, id: ClipId) -> Option<&Clip>` method on the shared state type that both could call into, despite AppState (crates/vbuff-gui/src/state.rs) being the natural owner of that lookup. _Evidence: src/actions.rs:65 vs crates/vbuff-gui/src/app.rs:163._
192. **egui::Layout::right_to_left(egui::Align::Center) action-row idiom repeated identically in render.rs's header and row rendering** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - The exact same egui idiom `ui.with_layout(egui::Layout::right_to_left(egui::Align::Center), |ui| { ... })` for a right-aligned button cluster appears twice in crates/vbuff-gui/src/render.rs: once for the header's Clear-all/Pause buttons (lines 52-60) and again for the row's Delete/Pin buttons (lines 174-184). Both are 'render a cluster of small_buttons right-aligned within the current row,' differing only in which buttons and actions are pushed; a small `fn right_aligned_buttons(ui, buttons: &[(&str, Option<&str>, UiAction)])` or similar in render.rs would remove the need to re-derive the same Layout call and closure shape at both sites, especially since a third such cluster is likely the first thing added when any new row action ships. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-gui/src/render.rs:52-60 vs crates/vbuff-gui/src/render.rs:174-184._
193. **HashSet<String> of live clip ids built identically in one place with no reusable accessor for future per-clip caches** `[improvement]` 🟢 `[low]` - crates/vbuff-gui/src/app.rs:124 builds `let live_ids: HashSet<String> = clips.iter().map(|c| c.id.to_string_repr()).collect();` specifically to prune the thumbnail cache via ThumbnailCache::retain_only. If a second per-clip cache is ever added (e.g. a future syntax-highlighting cache for Code-kind clips, or a decoded-RTF cache), it will need to rebuild the identical `live_ids` set independently since nothing exposes 'the current live id set' as a reusable value off of AppState or PopupApp - it's inlined at the one call site that happens to need it today. Hoist it into a `fn live_ids(clips: &[Clip]) -> HashSet<String>` (or better, `HashSet<ClipId>` to avoid the string round-trip) in state.rs or app.rs so cache-pruning logic added later starts from a shared primitive instead of re-deriving the id-collection idiom.
194. **String-based ClipId key used as the HashMap key in ThumbnailCache while app.rs's clip_by_id keys on the native ClipId, duplicating the 'index clips by id' concern with two different key representations** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - crates/vbuff-gui/src/thumbnail.rs's ThumbnailCache stores `HashMap<String, Option<TextureHandle>>` keyed by `clip.id.to_string_repr()` (thumbnail.rs:16, 28), while crates/vbuff-gui/src/app.rs's clip_by_id lookup (app.rs:163) and the live_ids set (app.rs:124) both derive the same clip-identity index within the same file, one keeping the native ClipId (line 163) and the other converting to String (line 124). ClipId already implements Hash+Eq (vbuff-types/src/lib.rs:26), so the String round-trip in thumbnail.rs is not just a duplicate-of-app.rs's indexing scheme but an unnecessary allocation-per-lookup version of the same 'HashMap keyed by clip identity' pattern used natively one file over. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-gui/src/thumbnail.rs:16 (`HashMap<String, ...>` keyed by `to_string_repr()`) vs crates/vbuff-gui/src/app.rs:163 (`HashMap<ClipId, &Clip>` keyed by the native, already-Hash+Eq ClipId)._
195. **'strip a known prefix/suffix' idiom reimplemented per-caller in three unrelated parsing functions, and two of them define the same #rgb-hex validity rule with different coverage** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - crates/vbuff-gui/src/view.rs's short_app_name does `last.strip_suffix(".app").unwrap_or(last)` (view.rs:52), crates/vbuff-core/src/classify.rs's is_color_hex does `s.strip_prefix('#')` (classify.rs:100), and crates/vbuff-gui/src/color.rs's parse_hex_color does the identical `s.strip_prefix('#')?` (color.rs:15) for the exact same '#rgb/#rrggbb/#rrggbbaa' format that classify.rs already validates via is_color_hex. Since color.rs's parse_hex_color re-derives hex-length validity (matching on `hex.len()` being 3/6/8) independently of classify.rs's is_color_hex (matching on `3 | 4 | 6 | 8` - note color.rs is also missing the 4-digit `#rgba` case that classify.rs's own is_color_hex already accepts as valid), a clip whose text is a valid 4-digit `#rgba` color per detect_text_kind would be classified as ContentKind::Color but then fail to render a swatch in color.rs's parse_hex_color, silently falling back to Color32::GRAY - a direct behavioral consequence of the same validation rule being written twice with different coverage. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-core/src/classify.rs:99-104 (`is_color_hex`, accepts 3|4|6|8 digit lengths) vs crates/vbuff-gui/src/color.rs:14-33 (`parse_hex_color`, only handles 3|6|8, silently drops 4-digit `#rgba`)._
196. **content_hash_hex hand-writes a byte-to-hex format loop instead of using a shared hex-encoding helper** `[improvement]` 🟢 `[low]` - crates/vbuff-types/src/lib.rs's Clip::content_hash_hex (lines 285-291) hand-writes a `for b in &self.content_hash { s.push_str(&format!("{b:02x}")) }` loop to hex-encode a 32-byte array - a generic 'bytes to lowercase hex string' operation with no name of its own, reimplemented from scratch here even though the workspace already takes a `blake3` dependency one crate away (vbuff-core/src/hash.rs's `hasher.finalize()` returns a `blake3::Hash`, whose upstream type already provides a `to_hex()` method). Since content_hash is stored as a raw `[u8; 32]` rather than `blake3::Hash` specifically to keep vbuff-types blake3-independent, the hex-formatting is duplicated logic reinventing what the upstream type already provides one crate over, and any future second byte-array-to-hex need (e.g. displaying a truncated hash in a future 'copy hash' debug action) will likely re-copy this same format! loop a third time rather than call a shared `to_hex(bytes: &[u8]) -> String` in vbuff-types.
197. **Row-index-to-Clip two-step resolution chain (filtered[i] -> clip_by_id[id]) reimplemented separately in render.rs and input.rs rather than one shared resolver** `[idea]` 🟢 `[low]` - crates/vbuff-gui/src/render.rs's render_panel (lines 70-83) resolves each visible row by indexing `filtered.get(row)` to get a ClipId, then `clip_by_id.get(id)` to get the Clip - a two-step index-then-id-lookup chain performed inline in the ScrollArea closure. crates/vbuff-gui/src/input.rs's handle_keys performs the identical first step for quick-pick number keys: `filtered.get(n)` to get an id (input.rs:48), then relies on the caller (actions.rs's Paste handler) to do a second, separate `clips.iter().find` by that id later. Both call sites reimplement 'resolve a UI-visible row/slot number to an actual Clip' via the same `filtered: &[ClipId]` intermediate rather than a single `fn resolve(&self, filtered: &[ClipId], clip_by_id: &HashMap<ClipId,&Clip>, index: usize) -> Option<&Clip>` helper that both rendering and key-handling could share. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-gui/src/render.rs:74-79 vs crates/vbuff-gui/src/input.rs:48._
198. **Lock-then-destructure-a-subset-of-AppState pattern repeated at three call sites with three different subsets, none sharing an accessor** `[improvement]` 🟢 `[low]` - crates/vbuff-gui/src/app.rs's update() (lines 108-112) takes the state lock once and destructures `(s.clips.clone(), s.paused, show, s.revision)` inline. This ad hoc tuple-destructure-under-lock pattern is the same shape as src/gui.rs's tray sync block (gui.rs:102-105, `let s = shared.lock().unwrap(); t.sync_state(s.paused, s.clips.len());`) and src/actions.rs's clip lookup (actions.rs:63-66, `let s = shared.lock().unwrap(); s.clips.iter().find(...)`) - three separate call sites each independently deciding which subset of AppState's fields to read out from under the same Mutex, rather than a single `AppState::snapshot(&self) -> StateSnapshot` (or narrower per-need accessor methods) that centralizes what 'a consistent read of shared state' means. This matters because app.rs's version clones the entire clip Vec every frame while the other two call sites prove that most callers only need `paused` or a single clip - a shared accessor would make the cheap partial-read path the obvious default instead of full-clone being the only pattern anyone copies from. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-gui/src/app.rs:108-112 vs src/gui.rs:102-105 vs src/actions.rs:63-66 - three independently-written lock-then-destructure blocks over the same AppState._
199. **Enigo key press/click/release triple with guaranteed-release-on-error has no reusable name, so a second synthesized key chord would duplicate it** `[idea]` 🟢 `[low]` - crates/vbuff-platform/src/paste.rs's EnigoPaste::paste (lines 38-47) manually sequences press/click/release with a comment explaining 'always release the modifier even if the click failed' and three separate `.map_err(...)` calls. This 'guarded modifier chord' pattern (press, do the thing, always release even on error, then propagate the first error) is exactly the kind of logic that would need to be duplicated verbatim if a second synthesized chord is ever added (e.g. a future manual capture-on-demand hotkey, or a copy-as-plain-text chord), since nothing here is factored into a reusable `fn with_modifier_held(enigo, modifier, action: impl FnOnce(&mut Enigo) -> Result<()>) -> Result<()>` that guarantees the release-on-error behavior for any future chord instead of re-deriving it by hand.
200. **Bool-to-SQL-int coercion (`as i64`) repeated inline at every write site instead of relying on rusqlite's built-in bool ToSql** `[improvement]` 🟢 `[low]` - crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs casts Rust bools to SQLite integers inline at four separate call sites: insert's `clip.pinned as i64, clip.favorite as i64` (lines 116-117), set_pinned's `pinned as i64` (line 147), set_favorite's `favorite as i64` (line 156), and the corresponding read-side inverse `row.get::<_, i64>(8)? != 0` / `row.get::<_, i64>(9)? != 0` in row.rs (row.rs:33-34). Since rusqlite's `params!` macro requires a `ToSql`-implementing type and `bool` already implements `ToSql` directly (storing as 0/1 automatically), the manual `as i64` casts are a hand-rolled reimplementation of a conversion the driver already provides for free, done differently (and asymmetrically - write side casts to i64, read side reads i64 then compares to 0) at four call sites that would all silently need to change together if the storage representation of booleans ever became TEXT ('true'/'false') or the column type changed. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:116-117,147,156 (write-side `as i64` casts) vs crates/vbuff-store/src/row.rs:33-34 (read-side `!= 0` decode)._
201. **Epoch-millis-to-DateTime-with-fallback idiom duplicated between row.rs and ClipId::timestamp** `[idea]` 🟢 `[low]` - crates/vbuff-store/src/row.rs's raw_to_clip decodes stored millis via `chrono::DateTime::from_timestamp_millis(raw.created_at).unwrap_or_else(chrono::Utc::now)` then `unwrap_or(created_at)` for updated_at (row.rs:48-50), while crates/vbuff-types/src/lib.rs's ClipId::timestamp does the same `DateTime::from_timestamp_millis(ms as i64).unwrap_or_else(Utc::now)` (lib.rs:46-49) for the ULID-embedded timestamp. Both are 'decode an epoch-millis integer to a DateTime, falling back to now() on an out-of-range value' - the same idiom with the same fallback policy, written twice in two different crates rather than exposed as one `fn millis_to_datetime(ms: i64) -> DateTime<Utc>` in vbuff-types that row.rs (which already depends on vbuff-types) could import instead of re-deriving the unwrap_or_else fallback shape.
202. **Config's save() and Store's open_default() both duplicate the 'ensure parent dir exists' two-step without sharing it** `[improvement]` 🟢 `[low]` - src/config.rs's Config::save (lines 72-80) does `path.parent()` -> `create_dir_all` -> write, and crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs's Store::open_default (lines 38-44) does the identical `path.parent()` -> `create_dir_all` -> then opens the DB at that path. Both are 'given a target file path, make sure its parent directory tree exists before touching the file,' written independently in two crates with two different error types (`anyhow::Error` in config.rs vs `StoreError::Io` in lib.rs) wrapping the same `std::fs::create_dir_all` call. A shared `fn ensure_parent_dir(path: &Path) -> std::io::Result<()>` in a common location (or even duplicated-but-named consistently) would remove the need to re-derive 'call parent(), then create_dir_all on it, handling the None-parent case' independently in both crates. _Evidence: src/config.rs:74-76 vs crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:40-42._
203. **thumbnail.rs hand-types the RGBA MIME prefix string instead of importing and using the RGBA_MIME_PREFIX constant, unlike clipboard.rs's correct usage of the same constant** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - vbuff_types::Flavor::is_image (lib.rs:194-196, `self.mime.starts_with("image/")`) is the canonical image-flavor check, correctly reused by classify.rs's detect_kind (classify.rs:16). crates/vbuff-platform/src/clipboard.rs correctly uses the exported constant: `use vbuff_types::{..., RGBA_MIME_PREFIX, ...}` (clipboard.rs:11) then `f.mime.starts_with(RGBA_MIME_PREFIX)` (clipboard.rs:75). But crates/vbuff-gui/src/thumbnail.rs's build_thumbnail does not import `RGBA_MIME_PREFIX` at all - its `use vbuff_types::{Body, Clip, Flavor, parse_rgba_dims}` (thumbnail.rs:11) omits it, and the function instead re-checks `flavor.mime.starts_with("image/x-vbuff-rgba")` as a hand-typed literal string (thumbnail.rs:56). rgba.rs's own doc comment states the format 'lives here once instead of being duplicated in each crate' specifically to prevent this, yet thumbnail.rs types out the prefix string by hand instead of using the already-exported constant - a future change to the MIME prefix string would silently miss this call site while clipboard.rs stayed correct. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-gui/src/thumbnail.rs:11,56 (imports `parse_rgba_dims` but not `RGBA_MIME_PREFIX`, then hand-types `"image/x-vbuff-rgba"` as a literal) vs crates/vbuff-platform/src/clipboard.rs:11,75 (imports and correctly uses `RGBA_MIME_PREFIX`)._
204. **Root binary's Cargo.toml declares `image.workspace = true` for a dependency it never uses directly, duplicating the dependency edge vbuff-gui's manifest already owns** `[idea]` 🟢 `[low]` - The root Cargo.toml's `[dependencies]` section declares `image.workspace = true` (root Cargo.toml:84) for the `vbuff` binary crate, while crates/vbuff-gui/Cargo.toml (the actual consumer of the `image` crate, per thumbnail.rs's `image::load_from_memory` call) independently also declares `image.workspace = true` in its own manifest. A grep across `src/` finds no direct `image::` usage anywhere outside crates/vbuff-gui/src/thumbnail.rs, meaning the root manifest's `image.workspace = true` line is a duplicate declaration of a dependency edge that vbuff-gui's own manifest already expresses correctly (and which reaches the binary transitively through the `vbuff-gui.workspace = true` dependency already listed). Removing the redundant root-level line would leave one place, not two, declaring 'the binary depends on the image codec crate.' _Evidence: root Cargo.toml:84 declares `image.workspace = true` for the `vbuff` binary crate, but `grep -rn image:: src/` finds no direct use of the `image` crate outside crates/vbuff-gui/src/thumbnail.rs._
205. **Square-vec2-from-THUMBNAIL_SIZE construction duplicated between color.rs's swatch and render.rs's thumbnail image sizing** `[idea]` 🟢 `[low]` - crates/vbuff-gui/src/color.rs's draw_color_swatch builds `egui::vec2(size, size)` where `size = crate::theme::THUMBNAIL_SIZE` (color.rs:8-9), and crates/vbuff-gui/src/render.rs's render_row independently builds `egui::vec2(THUMBNAIL_SIZE, THUMBNAIL_SIZE)` for the image thumbnail (render.rs:142) - the same 'square vec2 from the shared THUMBNAIL_SIZE constant' construction written twice a few files apart. A `theme::thumbnail_square() -> egui::Vec2` helper would remove the need for both the color swatch and the image thumbnail to separately remember that the row's icon slot is meant to always be square. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-gui/src/color.rs:8-9 vs crates/vbuff-gui/src/render.rs:142._
206. **Fully-qualified `std::collections::HashSet<_>` typed four times inline in one test instead of a single top-of-module `use`** `[idea]` 🟢 `[low]` - crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs's enforce_cap_matches_pure_eviction_policy test (lines 328-362) writes out `std::collections::HashSet<_>` fully-qualified four separate times inline (lines 346, 352, 354, 355) rather than adding a single `use std::collections::HashSet;` to the test module the way every other multi-use-of-a-collection module in this codebase does (e.g. crates/vbuff-gui/src/thumbnail.rs:9 imports `use std::collections::{HashMap, HashSet};` once at the top). This is a small in-file duplication (the same fully-qualified path typed four times) that a one-line import would collapse, and is inconsistent with this codebase's own established convention of importing collection types once at module scope. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:346,352,354,355 (four inline `std::collections::HashSet<_>` uses in one test) vs the codebase's own convention of a top-of-module `use std::collections::{HashMap, HashSet};` seen in crates/vbuff-gui/src/thumbnail.rs:9._
207. **macOS-vs-other-OS default is independently branched with #[cfg(target_os = "macos")] in two crates for two conceptually related settings** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - src/config.rs's default_hotkey() (lines 44-53) and crates/vbuff-platform/src/lib.rs's paste_modifier() (lines 35-43) both independently write the identical `#[cfg(target_os = "macos")] { <mac value> } #[cfg(not(target_os = "macos"))] { <other value> }` branch shape to decide a macOS-vs-everyone-else default: one picks `"Cmd+Shift+V"` vs `"Ctrl+Shift+V"` for the hotkey string, the other picks `Modifier::Meta` vs `Modifier::Control` for the paste-keystroke modifier - the same underlying 'is this macOS' platform question, answered by two separately-written `cfg` blocks in two different crates rather than one shared `fn is_macos_like() -> bool` or a single `PlatformDefaults` struct. Since both settings describe conceptually the same 'what does Cmd/Ctrl mean on this OS' policy (the hotkey's Cmd/Ctrl prefix and the paste modifier are meant to agree), a third OS-conditional default added later (e.g. a macOS-specific menu-bar-icon glyph) is likely to re-derive this same cfg-branch shape a third time instead of consulting a single source of truth for 'what is this platform's primary modifier.' _Evidence: src/config.rs:44-53 (default_hotkey, `#[cfg(target_os = "macos")]` picks "Cmd+Shift+V" vs "Ctrl+Shift+V") vs crates/vbuff-platform/src/lib.rs:35-43 (paste_modifier, the identical cfg shape picks Modifier::Meta vs Modifier::Control)._

---

## Capture fidelity & platform parity (additional, beyond the first 10)

208. **No positioning logic exists anywhere for the popup window** `[problem]` 🟠 `[high]` - src/gui.rs's ViewportBuilder in run_gui() (lines 28-34) sets title/inner_size/decorations/transparent/always_on_top/visible but never calls with_position, and there is no reference to monitor, cursor position, or DPI anywhere in vbuff-gui or the binary. The popup relies entirely on whatever position winit/the OS picks at window creation (typically screen center or a remembered position), with no logic to appear near the cursor, near the tray icon, or on the currently active monitor. _Evidence: src/gui.rs run_gui(): egui::ViewportBuilder::default().with_title("vbuff").with_inner_size([520.0,600.0]).with_decorations(false).with_transparent(true).with_always_on_top().with_visible(false) - no .with_position() call anywhere in the file; grep for monitor|dpi|scale_factor|screen|position|cursor across crates/vbuff-gui/src and src returns nothing relevant except an unrelated comment about badge-column x-alignment at render.rs:124._
209. **On multi-monitor setups the popup can appear on a monitor the user isn't looking at** `[problem]` 🟠 `[high]` - PopupApp::show() (crates/vbuff-gui/src/app.rs, lines 74-82) only sends ViewportCommand::Visible(true) and ViewportCommand::Focus; it never sends a position command or queries which monitor the cursor/focused window is on. Combined with the missing with_position() at window-creation time, the popup opens wherever the window already sits regardless of which monitor the user is actively working on or where their cursor/tray click was when the hotkey fired. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-gui/src/app.rs PopupApp::show(): `ctx.send_viewport_cmd(ViewportCommand::Visible(true)); ctx.send_viewport_cmd(ViewportCommand::Focus);` is the entire body - no ViewportCommand::OuterPosition or monitor query anywhere in the file._
210. **Tray-triggered show also has no position-near-tray-icon behavior** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - src/gui.rs's TrayAction::Show handler (line 110) calls shared.lock().unwrap().request_show(), which routes to the same PopupApp::show() with no positional argument. Unlike most menu-bar/tray clipboard managers, which anchor the popup under the clicked tray icon, vbuff's tray-triggered popup and hotkey-triggered popup are visually indistinguishable in placement because neither path ever knows or uses the tray icon's screen coordinates. _Evidence: src/gui.rs: `crate::tray::TrayAction::Show => { shared.lock().unwrap().request_show(); }` (line 110) - no coordinate is captured from the tray click event; src/tray.rs Tray::poll() only drains MenuEvent::receiver(), never a click-position event._
211. **tray_icon's click-position event is never consumed, only the menu event** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - src/tray.rs's Tray::poll() (lines 77-93) only drains MenuEvent::receiver(); tray-icon also exposes a TrayIconEvent receiver (left-click, right-click, double-click, carrying the icon's screen rect/cursor position) that is never read anywhere in the crate. This means a left-click directly on the tray icon (as opposed to opening the menu and picking "Show vbuff") does nothing, and the icon's screen rect - which would be needed for any future popup-near-tray-icon anchoring - is never available to the rest of the app. _Evidence: src/tray.rs Tray::poll(): `while let Ok(event) = MenuEvent::receiver().try_recv() { ... }` is the only event source drained in the file; no TrayIconEvent::receiver() call exists anywhere in src/tray.rs or elsewhere in src/._
212. **No DPI-awareness handling for the fixed 520x600 popup on mixed-DPI multi-monitor setups** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - The viewport's inner_size is a hardcoded [520.0, 600.0] logical-pixel constant in src/gui.rs (line 30) with no code reading egui::Context::pixels_per_point or reacting to a scale-factor change when the window is dragged/reopened on a different-DPI monitor than it was created on. On a mixed-DPI multi-monitor rig (e.g. a 1x external display next to a 2x laptop panel), nothing in the codebase tests or guards the popup's rendered size or clipping behavior against a scale-factor change. _Evidence: src/gui.rs: `.with_inner_size([520.0, 600.0])` is the only sizing call; grep for pixels_per_point|scale_factor across crates/vbuff-gui and src returns no matches._
213. **Paste-back write path has no HTML/RTF branch, so rich-text flavors can never round-trip even if a future backend captures them** `[improvement]` 🟡 `[medium]` - Distinct from the missing HTML/RTF capture itself (already tracked in code-audit-top-50 #15): ArboardClipboard::write() (crates/vbuff-platform/src/clipboard.rs, lines 59-92) can also never write back an HTML/RTF flavor even if one somehow entered a Clip's flavor list - the fallback chain is text -> RGBA image -> PlatformError::Empty, with no branch for text/html or text/rtf mimes. When vbuff eventually gains a native capture backend that stores HTML/RTF flavors, paste-back of those clips will still silently downgrade to plain text (if a sibling text/plain flavor exists) or fail outright, because the write path was never extended in step with capture. Track this as a required companion change to any future HTML/RTF capture work, not an independent fix. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-platform/src/clipboard.rs write(): checks `f.is_text()`, then the RGBA-prefixed mime, then returns `Err(PlatformError::Empty)` - no branch for text/html or text/rtf mimes exists anywhere in the function._
214. **Image round-trip is always lossy raw-RGBA, discarding the source encoding on every capture, not just on paste** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - ArboardClipboard::write() reconstructs an image purely from an image/x-vbuff-rgba;width=W;height=H flavor via arboard's set_image. Because ArboardClipboard::read() only ever produces the RGBA flavor (never an inline PNG/JPEG passthrough flavor), and thumbnail.rs's build_thumbnail() separately supports decoding PNG/JPEG/BMP source bytes for display, any image clip is round-tripped exclusively as decoded, uncompressed RGBA - so a copied JPEG or paletted/animated image loses its original encoding and any format-specific metadata on the very first capture, independent of the single-flavor-per-copy limitation already tracked as code-audit-top-50 #14. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-platform/src/clipboard.rs read(): only ever constructs `Flavor::inline(rgba_mime(...), img.bytes...)`, no PNG/JPEG passthrough flavor is stored; write(): only looks for a flavor whose mime starts_with(RGBA_MIME_PREFIX), no alternate-encoding flavor is ever considered._
215. **No GIF, WebP, or TIFF thumbnail decoding despite the image crate dependency being able to support them** `[idea]` 🟢 `[low]` - Cargo.toml's image dependency is pinned to default-features = false, features = ["png", "jpeg", "bmp"] (line 40), and crates/vbuff-gui/src/thumbnail.rs's build_thumbnail() calls image::load_from_memory(bytes) generically, so any GIF/WebP/TIFF image copied from a browser (a common source, since web pages frequently serve WebP or animated GIF images to the clipboard on copy) fails to decode and build_thumbnail() returns None silently - the row falls back to no thumbnail with no user-visible distinction from a corrupt image. Enabling the gif and webp image-crate features (already available upstream, just not turned on) would close a real, common capture-fidelity gap without touching any platform code.
216. **No macOS tray icon template-mode support, so the icon will look wrong in dark menu-bar mode and with non-default accent colors** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - src/tray.rs's build_icon() (lines 97-112) constructs a fixed two-tone blue-on-navy 32x32 RGBA bitmap and passes it directly to TrayIconBuilder::with_icon() with no call to any template/is_template API. macOS menu-bar icons are conventionally monochrome "template images" (NSImage.isTemplate = true) so the OS can auto-invert them for dark/light menu bar and apply the system tint; a full-color blue square will look inconsistent with every other menu-bar icon on macOS. Windows/Linux tray icons are unaffected by this convention, so this is a macOS-specific parity gap, not a cross-platform one. _Evidence: src/tray.rs build_icon(): hardcodes RGBA bytes [0x20,0x40,0x80,0xff] (border) and [0x3a,0x6e,0xd0,0xff] (fill) unconditionally for all platforms; no #[cfg(target_os = "macos")] branch exists in tray.rs, and tray-icon's macOS template-icon API is never invoked._
217. **The tray icon has no platform-conditional variant despite tray-icon conventions differing across OSes** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - src/tray.rs has zero cfg(target_os) blocks, even though Windows notification-area icons, macOS menu-bar icons, and Linux StatusNotifierItem/AppIndicator icons have different expected sizes/formats/conventions (Windows commonly wants a multi-resolution .ico, GNOME/KDE SNI implementations render SVG or larger PNGs better than a tiny raw 32x32 RGBA blob). vbuff ships one code path for all three with no platform tuning at all, unlike every other cross-platform concern in the codebase that does branch on target_os for analogous concerns. _Evidence: `grep -n 'cfg(' src/tray.rs` returns no matches at all; contrast crates/vbuff-store/src/paths.rs (cfg(target_os = "macos")/cfg(target_os = "windows") for data-dir resolution) and src/config.rs's default_hotkey() (cfg(target_os = "macos") for the default combo), both of which do branch on target_os for their analogous OS-specific concern._
218. **No autostart-on-login registration exists on any platform, and no config field or dependency for it either** `[problem]` 🟠 `[high]` - There is no launchd plist writer, no Windows registry Run-key or Startup-folder shortcut writer, and no XDG autostart .desktop file writer anywhere in the tree. Config (src/config.rs) has no autostart/launch_at_login boolean field, and no external crate like auto-launch is a Cargo.toml dependency. A user who wants vbuff running after reboot must manually configure OS-level autostart themselves; there is no in-app way to request or verify it on any of the three target platforms. _Evidence: Cargo.toml lists no autostart/auto-launch crate under [dependencies] or [workspace.dependencies]; grep for autostart|launchd|LaunchAgent|HKEY_CURRENT_USER\\Run|xdg.*autostart|\.desktop across crates and src returns no matches anywhere in the codebase; src/config.rs's Config struct (lines 12-28) has no such field._
219. **Quit from the tray calls std::process::exit(0) on the same tick as the close command, skipping graceful window/tray teardown** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - src/gui.rs's TrayAction::Quit handler (lines 124-127) sends ViewportCommand::Close and then immediately calls std::process::exit(0), without waiting for the viewport-close event to run any Drop logic on the SQLite connection or the tray icon handle. On Windows in particular, an abrupt process::exit can leave the tray icon visually stuck in the notification area until the shell notices the process died (a well-known Shell_NotifyIcon quirk), which this code path does nothing to avoid. _Evidence: src/gui.rs: `crate::tray::TrayAction::Quit => { ctx.send_viewport_cmd(egui::ViewportCommand::Close); std::process::exit(0); }` (lines 124-127) - exit(0) runs unconditionally on the same event-loop tick as the close command, before eframe/winit can process the close and drop window/tray resources._
220. **key_to_code in the hotkey parser has no mapping for function keys, arrow keys, or common punctuation, silently limiting configurable hotkeys** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - crates/vbuff-platform/src/hotkey.rs's key_to_code() (lines 75-120) match arm only covers A-Z, 0-9, Space, Enter/Return, and Tab; any other key name (F1-F12, arrow keys, comma/period/slash, numpad keys, Escape, Backspace/Delete) falls through to `_ => return None`, which propagates up through combo_to_hotkey as PlatformError::BadCombo. Since Config::hotkey (src/config.rs) is user-editable TOML with no validation UI, a user who sets e.g. hotkey = "Cmd+F1" (a plausible clipboard-manager shortcut choice) gets a config that fails registration at startup with only a tracing::warn! log line and a silently-inert hotkey. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-platform/src/hotkey.rs key_to_code(): match arm lists only KeyA..KeyZ, Digit0..Digit9, Space, Enter, Tab, then `_ => return None`; src/main.rs's hotkey registration: `Err(e) => { tracing::warn!("failed to register hotkey {:?}: {e}", config.hotkey); None }` (lines 84-87) with no further user-facing surface._
221. **parse_combo silently accepts multiple main-key tokens and keeps only the last one** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - crates/vbuff-platform/src/hotkey.rs's parse_combo() (lines 127-147) iterates s.split('+') and for every token that doesn't match a known modifier keyword, unconditionally overwrites `key = Some(token.to_string())` with no check that a main key hasn't already been set. A malformed config value like hotkey = "Cmd+V+X" (e.g. from manual TOML editing) silently resolves to X as the main key with Cmd, discarding V with no warning at parse time - the malformed intent is masked rather than rejected. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-platform/src/hotkey.rs parse_combo(): `_ => key = Some(token.to_string())` (line 142) inside the `for raw in s.split('+')` loop has no `if key.is_some() { return Err(...) }` guard before the assignment._
222. **paste_modifier() hardcodes a two-way macOS/not-macOS split with no explicit per-target decision for future platforms** `[improvement]` 🟢 `[low]` - crates/vbuff-platform/src/lib.rs's paste_modifier() is #[cfg(target_os = "macos")] Modifier::Meta vs #[cfg(not(target_os = "macos"))] Modifier::Control, meaning any future compile target that isn't literally macOS (a hypothetical BSD build, or a Linux desktop environment with an unusual paste convention) is silently folded into the Windows/Linux-X11 assumption with no per-target review. This is a minor, currently-correct simplification, but the two-way split will need explicit auditing (not just a recompile) if vbuff ever targets a fourth platform, since the not(macos) catch-all masks the absence of a real decision for the new target.
223. **detect_kind's File/uri-list branch is unreachable dead code because arboard never surfaces file-list flavors** `[problem]` 🟠 `[high]` - crates/vbuff-core/src/classify.rs's detect_kind() (lines 20-29) explicitly checks for mime == "text/uri-list" || mime.contains("file-url") || mime.contains("Filenames") || mime == "application/x-file-list" and would correctly classify a captured file-list flavor as ContentKind::File - but ArboardClipboard::read() never produces any flavor with those MIME strings, since arboard's public API has no file-list accessor at all. The File content-kind branch is therefore fully unreachable in production: copying files in Finder/Explorer/a file manager and pasting into vbuff either falls through to the image branch (if the file manager also puts a thumbnail on the clipboard) or captures nothing, with no code path ever exercising ContentKind::File outside its own unit tests. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-core/src/classify.rs detect_kind(): the file-MIME for-loop over mime == "text/uri-list" || mime.contains("file-url") || mime.contains("Filenames") || mime == "application/x-file-list" (lines 20-29); crates/vbuff-platform/src/clipboard.rs ArboardClipboard::read(): only ever pushes a text/plain;charset=utf-8 flavor or an image/x-vbuff-rgba flavor, never anything matching those four MIME predicates._
224. **detect_kind's Rtf/Html branches are equally unreachable dead classification logic, a distinct gap from the missing capture code itself** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - detect_kind() has dedicated branches for mime.contains("html") -> ContentKind::Html and mime.contains("rtf") -> ContentKind::Rtf (lines 42-49), both gated behind if plain.is_none(). Since ArboardClipboard::read() never emits a text/html or text/rtf flavor, these two branches - plus their ContentKind label/icon entries in vbuff-types and the unit test html_only_falls_back_to_html - are exercised only by hand-constructed test Flavor vectors, never by anything the running app can actually produce. Unlike the File/uri-list branch (a separate finding above), this one flags that the downstream classification machinery for HTML/RTF already exists and is fully wired up, yet can never fire in the shipped binary - the fix belongs entirely on the capture side (code-audit-top-50 #15), not here. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-core/src/classify.rs detect_kind(): `if mime.contains("html") { return ContentKind::Html; } if mime.contains("rtf") { return ContentKind::Rtf; }` inside `if plain.is_none()` (lines 42-49); the only callers constructing flavors with those mimes are the crate's own #[cfg(test)] module (e.g. html_only_falls_back_to_html), not any capture path._
225. **No Wayland-vs-X11 session detection exists anywhere, so vbuff cannot even know it is running degraded on GNOME-Wayland** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - Distinct from the already-tracked missing Wayland fallback capture path (code-audit-top-50 #18/#19): there is no code anywhere that inspects XDG_SESSION_TYPE/WAYLAND_DISPLAY or otherwise distinguishes an X11 session from a Wayland session at runtime, for logging or diagnostic purposes. Since ArboardClipboard is used identically regardless of session type, vbuff has no way to log or surface whether it is running under GNOME-Wayland versus X11 at all - a support report of "clipboard capture works sometimes" from a GNOME-Wayland user is indistinguishable in the logs from an X11 user's report of the same symptom, independent of whether a fallback capture path ever gets built. _Evidence: grep for XDG_SESSION_TYPE|WAYLAND_DISPLAY across crates/vbuff-platform/src, crates/vbuff-core/src, and src returns no runtime session-detection code; ArboardClipboard::new()/read()/write() in clipboard.rs contain no cfg or runtime branch of any kind for session type, and no tracing call anywhere logs the session type at startup._
226. **Capture-thread's if flavors.is_empty() image-read guard drops the image whenever a copy simultaneously offers text and an image** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - ArboardClipboard::read() only attempts self.clipboard.get_image() if flavors.is_empty() after the text branch - meaning any clipboard offering both text/plain and an image flavor simultaneously (common: copying an image in a browser often also populates a text/plain flavor with the image's alt text or source URL) captures only the text and permanently discards the image data. This is a stronger, more specific claim than the general multi-flavor loss already tracked in code-audit-top-50 #14: this item is specifically about the text-vs-image priority ordering being a one-way street that drops image bytes even when the image is arguably the primary content the user intended to copy, and the in-code comment justifying it ("avoid spurious image reads") does not address the data-loss cost when both flavors are legitimately present. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-platform/src/clipboard.rs ArboardClipboard::read() (lines 44-51): `if flavors.is_empty() && let Ok(img) = self.clipboard.get_image() { ... }` - the image branch is unreachable whenever the text branch above it already pushed a flavor._
227. **No X11 clipboard-manager selection-ownership handoff exists, so clips vanish the instant the source app exits, worse than the documented poll-miss gap** `[problem]` 🟠 `[high]` - architecture.md (line 519) explicitly documents that X11 selection data "lives in the owning app and vanishes when it quits" unless a real clipboard manager takes CLIPBOARD ownership and re-serves TARGETS/data on SelectionRequest - and names this exact "owner-dies problem" as the reason arboard "cannot serve here." arboard, as used in ArboardClipboard, never takes or holds selection ownership; it only reads the current owner's data on each poll tick. On X11, if a user copies text and then quits the source app before vbuff's poll thread's next tick happens to catch it, the clip is unrecoverable from the OS clipboard entirely - a distinct, more severe failure mode than the already-tracked rapid-copy poll-miss (code-audit-top-50 #12), since that item is about losing an overwritten intermediate copy, while this one is about losing data that the OS itself no longer has anywhere to serve from. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-platform/src/clipboard.rs ArboardClipboard has no selection-ownership acquisition of any kind; architecture.md line 519: "X11 selection data lives in the owning app and vanishes when it quits. A real manager must take CLIPBOARD ownership and re-serve TARGETS/data on SelectionRequest so content survives the source closing. This is why arboard cannot serve here" - yet clipboard.rs is arboard end-to-end with no XSetSelectionOwner-equivalent call anywhere in the crate._
228. **write()'s RGBA reconstruction has no bounds check that bytes.len() matches w * h * 4, unlike the thumbnail loader's equivalent guard** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - ArboardClipboard::write() parses (w, h) via parse_rgba_dims(&flavor.mime) and then constructs ImageData { width: w, height: h, bytes: Cow::Borrowed(bytes) } directly, passing it to self.clipboard.set_image(image) with no check that bytes.len() == w * h * 4. Contrast crates/vbuff-gui/src/thumbnail.rs's build_thumbnail(), which explicitly guards `if w == 0 || h == 0 || bytes.len() < w * h * 4 { return None; }` before calling egui::ColorImage::from_rgba_unmultiplied. If a corrupted or truncated RGBA flavor ever reaches write() (e.g. from a future spilled-body read that under-reads the file, or a hand-edited DB row), the underlying OS clipboard API receives a width/height that doesn't match the buffer length, unchecked at this FFI boundary even though the read-side thumbnail path already treats this exact data shape as worth guarding. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-platform/src/clipboard.rs write() (lines 73-89): `let (w, h) = parse_rgba_dims(&flavor.mime)...; let image = ImageData { width: w, height: h, bytes: Cow::Borrowed(bytes) }; return self.clipboard.set_image(image)...` - no length-vs-dimensions assertion anywhere in this function; crates/vbuff-gui/src/thumbnail.rs build_thumbnail() line 58 has the analogous guard vbuff-platform lacks._
229. **No handling for macOS NSPasteboard promised/deferred-data pasteboard items (e.g. Finder drag-to-clipboard)** `[idea]` 🟢 `[low]` - macOS apps (Finder drag-to-clipboard, Preview, many creative apps) frequently place a promise on the pasteboard rather than eager data - the actual bytes are only produced when a receiver calls back into the source app. arboard's synchronous get_image()/get_text() calls have no way to satisfy or wait on a promise callback, so any macOS copy using this pattern reads back empty or stale data with no explicit error - ArboardClipboard::read() simply produces zero flavors for that copy, indistinguishable in the logs from an ordinary empty-clipboard poll tick. Worth flagging explicitly for a native macOS NSPasteboard backend design, since arboard's abstraction has no hook for it and a caller can't currently distinguish "nothing was copied" from "something was copied but is a promise this reader can't fulfill."
230. **No plan for KDE Klipper-specific exclusion markers beyond the generic x-kde-passwordManagerHint already flagged** `[idea]` 🟢 `[low]` - Beyond the already-flagged generic concealed-hint gap (code-audit-top-50 #3) and architecture.md's own x-kde-passwordManagerHint convention (lines 510/522/884), KDE's own Klipper clipboard manager honors additional KDE-specific exclusion configuration (e.g. per-app and per-window-title exclude patterns configured in Klipper's own settings) that a vbuff user migrating from Klipper would expect an equivalent for. A future Linux/KDE-aware backend should treat matching Klipper's existing user-configured exclusion behavior as a distinct compatibility surface from the generic freedesktop.org concealed-type check, since a naive "just check x-kde-passwordManagerHint" implementation leaves KDE users with a narrower exclusion feature set than the tool they are switching from.
231. **No plan to honor the legacy Windows Clipboard Viewer Ignore format name distinct from the two DWORD flags already cited in the audit** `[idea]` 🟢 `[low]` - architecture.md names three Windows sensitivity signals to honor (line 510): ExcludeClipboardContentFromMonitorProcessing, CanIncludeInClipboardHistory, and separately "Treat Clipboard Viewer Ignore similarly" - a legacy pre-Windows-10 convention some older enterprise password managers still set. code-audit-top-50's item #3 only names the first two; a future native Windows backend should not stop at those two and skip the third, since some still-deployed enterprise password managers (particularly older, non-UWP ones) only set the legacy Clipboard Viewer Ignore format and not the newer DWORD flags.
232. **source_app has a text-shortening path but no companion icon-resolution concept, even though it is already rendered in the popup's meta line** `[idea]` 🟢 `[low]` - ClipMeta::source_app (crates/vbuff-types/src/lib.rs) is a bare Option<String> holding "bundle id / exe / WM_CLASS" per its doc comment, and render.rs already renders it via short_app_name() (crates/vbuff-gui/src/view.rs), which turns e.g. com.apple.Safari into the readable text label Safari - so the current design is not a raw-string display, but it is text-only. There is no companion concept anywhere in the type system for resolving source_app into an icon (e.g. macOS NSWorkspace bundle-id-to-icon lookup, Windows SHGetFileInfo exe-icon extraction, Linux .desktop-file lookup by WM_CLASS). Even once source_app population is fixed (code-audit-top-50 #16), a future icon badge next to the shortened app name would need a new resolution layer added, since CapturedClipboard (traits.rs) and ClipMeta have no icon field, only source_app: Option<String> and its text shortener - worth scoping now since bundle-id-to-icon resolution differs completely per platform.
233. **EnigoPaste is constructed once at GUI startup and never retried, so an Accessibility grant mid-session requires a full app restart** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - src/gui.rs's run_gui() calls `let mut paste_backend = EnigoPaste::new().ok();` (line 42) exactly once before entering the event loop; if this returns None (e.g. because macOS Accessibility permission wasn't yet granted at launch), paste_backend stays None for the remainder of the process, and there is no retry/recheck logic anywhere in the update closure. A user who grants Accessibility permission mid-session (the natural flow: launch app, get denied, go to System Settings, grant it, come back) still has paste-back permanently disabled until they quit and relaunch vbuff, with nothing in the UI telling them a restart is required - the only signal is the one-time tracing::warn! log line at startup. _Evidence: src/gui.rs run_gui(): `let mut paste_backend = EnigoPaste::new().ok(); if paste_backend.is_none() { tracing::warn!("paste backend unavailable; paste-back disabled"); }` (lines 42-45) runs once before eframe::run_simple_native; inside the per-frame closure, paste_backend is only ever read via `if let Some(backend) = &mut paste_backend` (line 141), never reconstructed or retried._
234. **Paste keystroke uses Key::Unicode('v') instead of a physical/raw keycode, risking wrong-key synthesis on non-QWERTY layouts** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - EnigoPaste::paste() (crates/vbuff-platform/src/paste.rs, line 41) sends Key::Unicode('v') with the platform modifier held. enigo's Unicode key variant synthesizes the character 'v' via layout-independent Unicode input on some backends, but standard OS paste shortcuts are conventionally bound to the physical key position (macOS pins Cmd+V/C/X to physical key codes, not layout-mapped characters). Using Key::Unicode('v') instead of a raw platform keycode risks synthesizing a paste keystroke that behaves differently from a physical V-key press on layouts where 'v' as a literal Unicode character requires a dead-key/AltGr sequence, or where the receiving app distinguishes Unicode-input from physical-keycode input. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-platform/src/paste.rs EnigoPaste::paste(): `let click = self.enigo.key(Key::Unicode('v'), Direction::Click);` (line 41) - no layout-aware or raw-keycode alternative is used or considered anywhere in the file._
235. **No fallback path exists if both the hotkey and the tray icon fail to initialize, leaving the popup permanently unreachable** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - src/main.rs's hotkey registration failure path (lines 84-87) only logs via tracing::warn! and continues with hotkey_id = None. Separately, src/gui.rs's tray creation failure path (lines 77-81, `tray = crate::tray::Tray::new().ok(); if tray.is_none() { tracing::warn!("tray icon unavailable"); }`) also only logs. If both fail simultaneously on a locked-down desktop with no StatusNotifierItem host and a compositor that rejects global hotkey grabs, there is no remaining way for the user to ever open the popup: the window starts with .with_visible(false) and nothing in the codebase provides a CLI flag, startup dialog, or any other summon path in that scenario. _Evidence: src/main.rs: hotkey failure -> `tracing::warn!(...); None` only (lines 84-87); src/gui.rs: tray failure -> `tracing::warn!("tray icon unavailable")` only (lines 79-81); ViewportBuilder in src/gui.rs sets .with_visible(false) (line 34) with no other summon path - grep confirms no CLI arg parsing (std::env::args, clap, or any Parser) exists anywhere in src/main.rs._
236. **Default hotkey Ctrl+Shift+V collides with common app-level "paste without formatting" bindings, with no conflict check at all** `[idea]` 🟢 `[low]` - src/config.rs's default_hotkey() (lines 44-53) picks Cmd+Shift+V on macOS and Ctrl+Shift+V elsewhere with no runtime check for conflicts. Ctrl+Shift+V is a very common "paste without formatting" binding already claimed by many editors/browsers/IDEs (VS Code, Chrome extensions, LibreOffice, JetBrains IDEs) on Windows/Linux; global_hotkey's register() will still succeed at the OS level (global hotkeys and app-level shortcuts are different mechanisms), but the practical UX is that pressing the intended vbuff hotkey while focus is in one of those apps can trigger the app's own paste-without-formatting instead of (or in addition to) vbuff's popup, depending on OS-level global-hotkey precedence - worth a documented known-conflict note or an in-app first-run collision check, since nothing currently surfaces this before a user hits it by accident.
237. **No design accounting for macOS Universal Clipboard (Handoff) pushing content with no local originating app** `[idea]` 🟢 `[low]` - macOS's Handoff feature (Universal Clipboard) can push clipboard content from a paired iPhone/iPad into the Mac's pasteboard, indistinguishable at the arboard/get_text level from a local copy - but with a source_app (once populated per code-audit-top-50 #16 and future native work) that would need special handling, since frontmost-app resolution on macOS at the moment of a Handoff-triggered change would report whatever app happens to be frontmost locally, not the actual originating iOS app, silently mislabeling the clip's source. architecture.md's existing Universal Clipboard mentions (lines 1159, 1237) are about echo-loop suppression and OS-history leakage, not about this source-app mislabeling angle, so this is a genuinely separate design note for the eventual native macOS backend and source-app attribution work - not a bug in the current arboard-only implementation, which has no source_app at all yet, but a real fidelity gap the polling-based changeCount design doesn't currently account for.

---

## Storage, schema & search (additional, beyond the first 8)

238. **WAL + NORMAL synchronous is pure overhead for a single-connection, mutex-serialized process** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - `Store::from_connection` (crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:59-60) sets `journal_mode=WAL` and `synchronous=NORMAL`. WAL exists to let readers and a writer proceed concurrently across multiple connections/processes; `src/main.rs` opens exactly one `Connection` wrapped in a single `Arc<Mutex<Store>>`, and every access is already serialized in-process by that mutex. The module doc comment (lib.rs:3, "runs in WAL mode") implies a concurrency benefit that does not exist here since there is no second connection to benefit from it, and `synchronous=NORMAL` with WAL means a hard power-loss can lose the last few committed transactions that would survive under `synchronous=FULL`. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:3, 59-60._
239. **`foreign_keys = ON` pragma is set against a schema with zero foreign keys** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - `from_connection` (lib.rs:61) turns on `PRAGMA foreign_keys = ON`, but `schema::migrate` (schema.rs:19-39) defines a single `clips` table with no `FOREIGN KEY`/`REFERENCES` clause anywhere in the codebase (grep confirms zero hits in schema.rs). The pragma is inert today; it reads as a placeholder for a normalized `item`/`flavor` schema that schema.rs's own module doc comment mentions as a future direction, but nothing currently exercises it. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:61; crates/vbuff-store/src/schema.rs:1-43 (no FOREIGN KEY/REFERENCES anywhere)._
240. **No `busy_timeout` is configured, so any external lock contention surfaces as an immediate SQLITE_BUSY error** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - Neither `from_connection` (lib.rs:58-64) nor any other code in the crate calls `conn.busy_timeout(...)` or sets `PRAGMA busy_timeout` (grep of the whole crate returns nothing). rusqlite's default busy handler returns `SQLITE_BUSY` immediately on the first lock conflict. Because the WAL sidecar files sit in a user-writable data directory, anything that briefly opens the same `history.db` file (a backup tool, an antivirus scanner, a second accidental vbuff launch given audit item #41's missing single-instance guard) will make the next `Store` call fail outright instead of retrying for even a few hundred milliseconds. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:58-64 (no busy_timeout call anywhere in the crate)._
241. **Migration runner has no schema-version ceiling check, so a downgrade silently runs against a newer database** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - `schema::migrate` (schema.rs:16-43) only checks `if version < 1`; it never checks whether the on-disk `user_version` is *greater* than `SCHEMA_VERSION`. If a user runs a newer vbuff build (which bumps `SCHEMA_VERSION` and adds columns), then downgrades to an older binary, `migrate` sees `version >= 1`, skips all migration logic, and the old binary starts running `SELECT`/`INSERT` statements against a table shape it doesn't know about - any newly added NOT NULL column without a default would make every `INSERT` in `Store::insert` fail with a generic `StoreError::Sqlite`, not a clear 'database is from a newer version' message. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/schema.rs:16-18 (only `if version < 1`, no `version > SCHEMA_VERSION` branch)._
242. **Migration's `CREATE TABLE`/index batch and the `user_version` bump are two separate statements, not one atomic unit** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - `schema::migrate`'s `conn.execute_batch(...)` (schema.rs:19-39) creates the table and three indexes as one implicit transaction, but the `pragma_update` for `user_version` (schema.rs:40) is a distinct statement issued after that batch already committed. If the process is killed between the batch commit and the pragma_update (e.g. an OS-level SIGKILL during first launch), the next launch finds `version < 1` again and re-runs `CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS`/`CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS`, which happens to be harmless only because of the `IF NOT EXISTS` guards, not because of a deliberate all-or-nothing migration transaction wrapping both statements. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/schema.rs:19-40._
243. **`insert`'s dedup SELECT and the fallback INSERT are two separate statements with no transaction boundary between them** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - `Store::insert` (lib.rs:71-121) runs `SELECT id FROM clips WHERE content_hash = ?1` (lib.rs:77-82) and only falls through to `INSERT` (lib.rs:99-119) if that returns `None`. Nothing in the `Store` API wraps this SELECT-then-INSERT pair in a `BEGIN`/`COMMIT`; the single-writer guarantee comes entirely from `main.rs` funneling every call through one `Arc<Mutex<Store>>`, an invariant the store itself neither enforces nor documents. If `Store` ever gained a second caller on a different connection (a future background task, a CLI companion tool), a race between the SELECT and INSERT would hit the `UNIQUE INDEX idx_clips_hash` (schema.rs:35) and surface as an opaque `rusqlite::Error` via `StoreError::Sqlite` instead of being handled as a dedup case. This is distinct from audit item #37 (insert+enforce_cap across main.rs not being one transaction): this is the SELECT/INSERT pair *inside* `insert` itself. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:71-121; unique index at crates/vbuff-store/src/schema.rs:35._
244. **Dedup UPDATE only bumps `updated_at`/`seq`; it never refreshes `source_app` from the re-copied clip** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - On a dedup hit, `Store::insert` (lib.rs:84-93) runs `UPDATE clips SET updated_at = ?1, seq = (SELECT COALESCE(MAX(seq), 0) + 1 FROM clips) WHERE id = ?2` and returns early, discarding the newly-passed `clip` argument entirely. `flavors_json`/`preview` are computed later at lib.rs:95-97 but only used on the non-dedup insert path. Because dedup keys off `content_hash` (a hash of flavor bytes), the flavor bytes are identical between the two calls by construction, but `source_app` is not part of that hash - so re-copying the exact same text from a different application leaves the original row's `source_app` stale forever, silently misattributing where the most recent copy came from. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:84-93 vs 95-97 (flavors_json/preview computed but unused on the dedup branch that returns early)._
245. **`idx_clips_pinned` partial index's `WHERE pinned = 1` predicate is never matched by any query the store issues** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - `schema.rs:37` creates `CREATE INDEX ... idx_clips_pinned ON clips(updated_at DESC) WHERE pinned = 1`, a partial index intended to speed up pinned-row lookups. But `list` (lib.rs:124-136) orders by `pinned DESC, updated_at DESC, seq DESC` over the whole table rather than filtering `WHERE pinned = 1`, and `enforce_cap`'s inner SELECT (lib.rs:207-217) filters `WHERE pinned = 0 AND favorite = 0` - the exact opposite predicate. No query anywhere in lib.rs issues a bare `WHERE pinned = 1` that this partial index could serve, so it adds write-amplification on every pin/unpin and insert with no matching read benefit. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/schema.rs:37; crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:124-136, 201-219 (no query filters on pinned=1 alone)._
246. **`idx_clips_updated` index column order does not match `list`'s actual ORDER BY, so it cannot fully satisfy the sort without a temp b-tree** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - `schema.rs:36` defines `idx_clips_updated ON clips(updated_at DESC, seq DESC)`, but `Store::list`'s query (lib.rs:130) orders by `pinned DESC, updated_at DESC, seq DESC` - three columns, with `pinned` leading and absent from the index entirely. SQLite can only use an index to avoid re-sorting if the leading ORDER BY column matches the index's leading column (or isn't part of the ORDER BY at all); here `pinned` leads the sort but isn't in the index, so SQLite must materialize and sort the whole result set for every `list()`/`load_recent()` call rather than walking the index in order. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/schema.rs:36; crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:124-136 (ORDER BY pinned DESC, updated_at DESC, seq DESC)._
247. **No `CHECK` constraint on `kind`, so `row::kind_from_int`'s catch-all silently reinterprets any out-of-range integer as `ContentKind::Other` instead of surfacing corruption** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - `schema.rs:26` declares `kind INTEGER NOT NULL` with no `CHECK (kind BETWEEN 0 AND 8)`. `row::kind_from_int` (row.rs:93-103) maps unrecognized values to `ContentKind::Other` via its `_ =>` catch-all arm (row.rs:103) instead of surfacing a `StoreError::Corrupt` the way `raw_to_clip` does for a bad ULID (row.rs:40) or a malformed `content_hash` (row.rs:42-47) in that same function. A future schema bump that adds a `ContentKind` variant without a matching migration, or accidental data corruption, is masked as 'Other' instead of being caught as corrupt data the way every other malformed-row case in `raw_to_clip` is handled. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/schema.rs:26; crates/vbuff-store/src/row.rs:93-103 vs 39-47 (inconsistent corruption handling within the same conceptual read path)._
248. **`content_hash` BLOB column has no length CHECK, so a wrong-length value only fails at read time, not write time** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - `schema.rs:24` declares `content_hash BLOB NOT NULL` with no `CHECK(length(content_hash) = 32)`. `row::raw_to_clip` (row.rs:42-47) does check the length on the way out and returns `StoreError::Corrupt`, but nothing stops a 31- or 33-byte value from being written in the first place (e.g. via a future direct `UPDATE`, a buggy migration, or manual DB surgery) - the failure is deferred from write time, where it would be cheap to reject with a constraint, to every subsequent `list()`/read call touching that row. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/schema.rs:24; crates/vbuff-store/src/row.rs:42-47._
249. **`enforce_cap`'s row-count read and the eviction DELETE are two separate autocommit statements keyed on a count that can go stale between them** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - `Store::enforce_cap` (lib.rs:201-219) calls `self.count()` (lib.rs:202, a full `SELECT COUNT(*)`), computes `overflow` in Rust (lib.rs:206), then issues a separate `DELETE ... LIMIT ?1` (lib.rs:207-217) keyed on that now-stale count. Nothing in `Store` wraps these two statements in an explicit `BEGIN`/`COMMIT`; today's single-mutex call pattern in `main.rs` happens to make this safe, but that is an invariant enforced by the caller, not by `enforce_cap` itself. This is distinct from the `insert` SELECT/INSERT race above and from audit item #37 (which is about `insert` and `enforce_cap` not being one transaction across the `main.rs` call site) - this is the count-then-DELETE race purely inside `enforce_cap`. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:201-219 (two sequential auto-commit statements, no explicit transaction)._
250. **`preview` column is cached once at insert time and never refreshed on the dedup path, so it can drift from `Clip::preview`'s own truncation logic over time** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - `Store::insert` computes `let preview = clip.preview(512);` once (lib.rs:97) and stores it only on the non-dedup INSERT path (lib.rs:115); the dedup-hit branch (lib.rs:84-93) never touches the `preview` column. If `Clip::preview`'s output changes in a later release (e.g. different whitespace-collapsing or truncation logic in vbuff-types/src/lib.rs:270-282), old rows keep whatever preview text was cached under the old logic, and there is no migration in schema.rs that recomputes `preview` for existing rows - so rows inserted before and after such a change can show previews generated by two different versions of the same logic. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:97, 115, 84-93; crates/vbuff-types/src/lib.rs:270-282 (preview() logic that could change); no migration recomputes preview._
251. **`byte_size` is stored verbatim from the caller-supplied `clip.meta.byte_size` and can silently disagree with the actual JSON-encoded `flavors` blob size** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - `lib.rs:113` stores `clip.meta.byte_size as i64` - a value computed outside this crate from raw flavor bytes - while the `flavors` column actually stored is the JSON-array-of-numbers encoding from `serde_clip::flavors_to_json` (serde_clip.rs:13-15), which the module's own doc comment (serde_clip.rs:3-6) says is bulkier than the raw bytes (per code-audit-top-50.md #25, roughly 3-5x for images). Nothing in `vbuff-store` cross-checks that `byte_size` reflects on-disk cost; any future code that sums `byte_size` across rows to show the user 'history uses N MB' would undercount actual SQLite file growth with no way to detect the drift from inside this crate. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:96-97, 113; crates/vbuff-store/src/serde_clip.rs:1-6, 13-15._
252. **`clear()`'s `DELETE FROM clips WHERE pinned = 0` also deletes favorited-but-unpinned clips, contradicting `enforce_cap`'s own exemption rule for favorites** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - `Store::clear` (lib.rs:171-175) only exempts `pinned = 1` rows. But `enforce_cap` (lib.rs:201-219) exempts `pinned = 0 AND favorite = 0` from eviction - i.e. treats `favorite` as equally protective as `pinned`. A clip marked `favorite = true` but not `pinned` survives automatic cap eviction yet is destroyed by a manual 'Clear History' action, an inconsistent definition of 'protected' between the two deletion paths on the same struct. Neither the `pin_delete_clear` test (lib.rs:280-296) nor `enforce_cap_matches_pure_eviction_policy` (lib.rs:328-363) exercises a favorited-but-unpinned clip against `clear()`, so this divergence has no test coverage on either side. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:171-175 vs 201-219 (differing protection predicates for the same 'favorite' flag)._
253. **No test exercises `set_pinned`/`set_favorite`/`delete` against a nonexistent `ClipId`** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - `Store::set_pinned` (lib.rs:144-150), `set_favorite` (lib.rs:152-159), and `delete` (lib.rs:161-168) all run an `UPDATE`/`DELETE ... WHERE id = ?` and return `Ok(())` unconditionally, without checking `execute`'s returned affected-row count. None of the unit tests in lib.rs's `#[cfg(test)] mod tests` or `tests/integration.rs` call any of these three methods with a `ClipId` that was never inserted, so there is no coverage proving these are intentionally no-ops on a miss rather than a bug - a caller cannot distinguish 'the clip didn't exist' from 'the update succeeded' by the return value alone. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:144-168 (Result<()> return, no rows_affected check); no not-found case in the test module or tests/integration.rs._
254. **Integration tests never simulate an unclean shutdown to verify WAL recovery on reopen** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - `tests/integration.rs`'s `persists_across_reopen` (lines 27-44) closes the `Store` cleanly (drops it, letting `Connection`'s `Drop` run its normal WAL checkpoint) before reopening. `wal_files_are_created` (integration.rs:74-83) only asserts the `-wal` sidecar exists after an insert, never simulates copying the `.db`+`-wal`+`-shm` trio to a fresh directory and reopening without a clean close - the actual scenario WAL mode is meant to survive. There is no test proving data written just before an unclean process kill (the realistic vbuff crash/force-quit scenario) is actually recoverable on next launch. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/tests/integration.rs:27-44, 74-83 (no unclean-shutdown / mid-WAL reopen scenario)._
255. **No test inserts a clip with an empty `flavors` vec, though the schema, serde helper, and `Clip::preview` all implicitly allow it** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - `schema.rs`'s `clips` table has no constraint requiring at least one flavor, `serde_clip::flavors_to_json` (serde_clip.rs:13-15) happily serializes an empty `Vec<Flavor>` as `"[]"`, and `Clip::preview` (vbuff-types/src/lib.rs:277-280) has a `None`-flavor fallback branch (`"[empty]"`) implying this state is anticipated. No test in `vbuff-store`'s unit tests or `tests/integration.rs` inserts and round-trips a zero-flavor clip to confirm `row::raw_to_clip` and content-hash-based dedup behave sanely - e.g. do two different zero-flavor clips collide on the same `content_hash` and dedup into one row unexpectedly? _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/serde_clip.rs:13-15; crates/vbuff-types/src/lib.rs:276-280; no empty-flavors test anywhere in crates/vbuff-store._
256. **No dedicated test covers `enforce_cap(0)`'s 'evict everything except protected clips' boundary** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - `enforce_cap(0)` (lib.rs:201-219) is only exercised indirectly, via `enforce_cap_matches_pure_eviction_policy`'s parametrized `max_history` list which does include `0usize` (lib.rs:331) - but that test only checks that the SQL and pure-Rust implementations evict the *same set* as each other, not that `enforce_cap(0)` correctly leaves pinned/favorite clips behind while evicting everything else, including clips inserted moments earlier. There is no dedicated, readable test asserting `enforce_cap(0)`'s specific 'wipe everything except protected clips' behavior the way `pin_delete_clear` (lib.rs:280-296) does for `clear()`. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:201-219, 328-363 (0 only appears inside the cross-check loop; no standalone zero-cap test)._
257. **`enforce_cap`'s docstring claims the implementations are 'kept honest' with each other, but the cross-check test only verifies evicted-set membership, not tie-break ordering** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - The doc comment on `enforce_cap` (lib.rs:191-200) says the two implementations are 'kept honest against each other' by `enforce_cap_matches_pure_eviction_policy`, and that test (lib.rs:328-363) does compare the evicted *set* of ids via `HashSet`. But SQL's `DELETE ... LIMIT ?1` with `ORDER BY updated_at ASC, seq ASC` and Rust's `evict()` (vbuff-core/src/eviction.rs) could break additional hidden ties differently if the two sorts aren't using the exact same composite key - the test's own doc comment (lib.rs:320-326) already admits same-millisecond ties are an 'accepted limit' it deliberately avoids via `sleep(2ms)` between inserts, meaning the actual guarantee is narrower than the docstring's wording implies to a reader who doesn't also read the test's caveats. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:191-200 vs 320-363 (docstring overstates what the cross-check test actually proves, and the test avoids the untested case by construction)._
258. **`paths::dirs_data_dir` silently returns `None` on a Linux/BSD target lacking both `XDG_DATA_HOME` and `HOME`, with no fallback to a relative or temp directory** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - `dirs_data_dir` (paths.rs:14-41), on the non-macOS unix branch (paths.rs:28-36), returns `None` if neither `XDG_DATA_HOME` nor `HOME` is set - a real scenario for minimal containers, systemd services with a stripped environment, or sandboxed launchers. `default_db_path` (paths.rs:8-11) maps that to `StoreError::NoDataDir`, and `Store::open_default` (lib.rs:38-44) propagates it with no fallback path (e.g. next to the executable, or a temp directory), so vbuff simply cannot start persistence at all in that environment beyond the bare error string. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/paths.rs:14-41; crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:38-44 (open_default propagates NoDataDir with no fallback)._
259. **`preview TEXT NOT NULL DEFAULT ''` in the schema is dead schema; the only INSERT in the codebase always supplies an explicit value** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - `schema.rs:31` declares `preview TEXT NOT NULL DEFAULT ''`, but the only INSERT in the codebase (`Store::insert`, lib.rs:99-119) always supplies an explicit `?9` bound to `clip.preview(512)` (lib.rs:97, 115) - there is no code path anywhere that inserts a `clips` row without specifying `preview`, so the column default can never actually apply. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/schema.rs:31; crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:99-119 (preview always explicitly bound)._
260. **No test proves `list()`'s three-key ORDER BY is correct when many rows tie on `updated_at` within the same millisecond** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - `list`'s query (lib.rs:124-136) sorts `pinned DESC, updated_at DESC, seq DESC`, relying on `seq` to break ties within the same millisecond - the same mechanism `enforce_cap_matches_pure_eviction_policy`'s own doc comment (lib.rs:320-326) calls out as necessary and deliberately spaces inserts by `sleep(2ms)` to avoid exercising. No test in the unit test module inserts several clips in a tight loop *without* that spacing and then asserts `list()` returns them in insertion order via `seq` alone - the only test that inserts many clips quickly (`insert_and_list`, lib.rs:249-261) only checks the two most recent, not a same-millisecond tie set. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:124-136, 249-261, 320-363 (only the cross-check test approaches this territory, and it deliberately avoids same-millisecond ties via sleep(2ms))._
261. **`kind_to_int`/`kind_from_int` is a hand-maintained parallel enum mapping with no round-trip exhaustiveness test tying it to `ContentKind`'s variant count** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - `row.rs:79-103` hand-maps each `ContentKind` variant to a fixed integer twice (to-int and from-int). `kind_to_int` is exhaustive by the compiler (a forgotten arm fails to build), but `kind_from_int`'s catch-all (`_ => ContentKind::Other`, row.rs:103) means a newly added `ContentKind` variant that someone forgets to add to `kind_from_int`'s match compiles silently and misdecodes that new variant back as `Other` forever. No test in the crate iterates all `ContentKind` variants through a round-trip `kind_to_int`/`kind_from_int` to catch this class of drift. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/row.rs:79-103 (kind_to_int exhaustive-by-compiler, kind_from_int has a catch-all masking future drift; no round-trip test)._
262. **`StoreError::Corrupt` has one free-text variant covering two structurally different failures, so callers can't react differently without string-matching** `[improvement]` 🟢 `[low]` - `error.rs:24-26` defines a single `Corrupt(String)` variant, and it is constructed with two different hardcoded messages across three call sites: 'bad ulid in db' (row.rs:40 and lib.rs:92) and 'content_hash not 32 bytes' (row.rs:46). A caller that wants to react differently - e.g. a corrupt ULID might be recoverable by regenerating an id and re-keying the row, while a corrupt hash blob might warrant discarding the row entirely - has to string-match `StoreError::Corrupt`'s inner `String`, which is fragile against future wording changes to any of those three `.into()` calls. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/error.rs:24-26; crates/vbuff-store/src/row.rs:40,46; crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:92._
263. **`Store` never runs `PRAGMA integrity_check`/`quick_check` on startup, so a corrupted history.db fails opaquely deep inside the first query instead of at open time** `[improvement]` 🟡 `[medium]` - `Store::open`/`open_default` (lib.rs:38-50) go straight from `Connection::open` to `schema::migrate` with no sanity check on the file's integrity. A partially-written or disk-corrupted `history.db` surfaces its first symptom as a cryptic `rusqlite::Error` from whatever query the GUI happens to run first (typically `load_recent` at startup), rather than a clear 'your clip history database is corrupt, starting fresh at path X' message the user could act on. A `PRAGMA quick_check` right after opening, gated behind a flag so it doesn't slow down every launch, would turn an inscrutable runtime failure into an actionable one. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:38-64 (open path has no integrity_check/quick_check call)._
264. **No backup/export path exists for the SQLite file itself, so a user cannot safely snapshot history.db while vbuff is running** `[idea]` 🟢 `[low]` - Because the store runs in WAL mode, naively `cp`-ing `history.db` while vbuff is open (something a user might try before an OS reinstall) can produce an inconsistent snapshot unless the `-wal` and `-shm` sidecar files are also copied atomically, which most users won't know to do. `Store` could expose a `backup_to(path: &Path)` using SQLite's Online Backup API (`rusqlite::backup`) so `main.rs` or a future settings pane can offer a one-click 'Export history.db' that is guaranteed consistent regardless of WAL state, instead of leaving users to manually locate and copy three files correctly. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs (no backup/export method exists anywhere in the public Store API)._
265. **No index (or covering strategy) supports a future prefix search without a full table scan, beyond the missing FTS5 table the audit already flags** `[idea]` 🟡 `[medium]` - code-audit-top-50.md #21 already flags that no FTS5 table exists. Beyond that: even the currently-shipped indexes (`idx_clips_hash`, `idx_clips_updated`, `idx_clips_pinned`) give SQLite nothing to use for a `preview LIKE '%term%'`-style scan, since a leading wildcard can never use a B-tree index. If FTS5 is deferred further, a cheaper interim step is a plain B-tree index on `preview` restricted to prefix queries (`preview LIKE 'term%'` with no leading wildcard), which at least accelerates the common 'jump to what I typed at the start' case without the schema churn of adding a virtual FTS5 table. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/schema.rs:35-37 (existing indexes, none usable for a leading-wildcard LIKE scan)._
