266. **Consider storing `content_hash` as hex TEXT with a length CHECK instead of BLOB, trading 32 bytes of storage for direct debuggability via the sqlite3 CLI** `[idea]` 🟢 `[low]` - Today `content_hash` is a raw 32-byte `BLOB` (schema.rs:24), so any ad hoc `sqlite3 history.db 'SELECT content_hash FROM clips'` a developer runs while debugging dedup issues prints unreadable binary garbage, forcing a detour through `Clip::content_hash_hex()` in application code just to eyeball a value. `vbuff-types` already exposes `content_hash_hex()` (vbuff-types/src/lib.rs:285-291) for exactly this purpose in-app; storing the hex string directly (with a `CHECK(length = 64)` and the same `UNIQUE` index) would make the raw `.db` file directly inspectable at the minor cost of ~32 extra bytes per row and one hex-encode/decode step per row. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/schema.rs:24; crates/vbuff-types/src/lib.rs:285-291._
267. **Add a `Store::vacuum()`/`incremental_vacuum` story for a table that only ever grows-then-shrinks via row deletion, since SQLite does not reclaim freed pages by default** `[idea]` 🟡 `[medium]` - `schema.rs`'s `CREATE TABLE` never sets `PRAGMA auto_vacuum` (SQLite defaults to `NONE`), and `clear`/`clear_all`/`delete`/`enforce_cap` (lib.rs:161-219) all delete rows without reclaiming freed pages back to the filesystem - deleted pages go onto SQLite's internal freelist and are reused for future inserts, but the `.db` file itself never shrinks. For a clipboard history that churns through thousands of image/text blobs over months (the bulky JSON-array-of-numbers image encoding from serde_clip.rs compounds this per code-audit #25), the on-disk file can grow to a high-water mark and stay there indefinitely with no user-facing 'compact database' action and no scheduled `PRAGMA incremental_vacuum` anywhere in the codebase. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/schema.rs (no PRAGMA auto_vacuum set anywhere); crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:161-219 (delete paths, no vacuum call anywhere in the crate)._
268. **`Store` has no method to fetch a single clip by id, forcing every future caller that needs one row to scan `list()`'s results or hand-roll a new query** `[idea]` 🟢 `[low]` - Every read path in `lib.rs` returns a `Vec<Clip>` (`list`, `load_recent`) - there is no `get(&self, id: ClipId) -> Result<Option<Clip>>` analogous to the single-id write methods `set_pinned`/`set_favorite`/`delete` (lib.rs:144-168). A future 'view full text' expand action or large-preview side pane feature needing one clip's full flavor bytes by id has to either linear-scan an already-fetched `Vec<Clip>` in memory or write a new one-off `conn.query_row` outside the existing row-mapping helpers (`row::row_to_clip`/`raw_to_clip`), which the schema/row split is otherwise well-positioned to support directly. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs (public API surface has no get-by-id method; see the full impl block, lines 35-220)._
269. **`enforce_cap`'s inner SELECT filters/sorts on a column combination not covered by any existing index, forcing a scan-and-sort on every capture** `[improvement]` 🟢 `[low]` - The inner SELECT in `enforce_cap` (lib.rs:209-214) filters `WHERE pinned = 0 AND favorite = 0` then orders `updated_at ASC, seq ASC`. None of the three indexes in schema.rs (`idx_clips_hash` on content_hash, `idx_clips_updated` on `(updated_at DESC, seq DESC)`, `idx_clips_pinned` partial on `pinned = 1`) match this filter+sort combination - `idx_clips_updated` is even sorted in the opposite direction (DESC) from what this query needs (ASC), and neither index includes `favorite` at all - so SQLite must scan and sort the non-pinned/non-favorite subset from scratch every time the row cap is enforced, which per the module's own doc comment happens after every insert. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:201-219; crates/vbuff-store/src/schema.rs:35-37 (no index covers pinned=0 AND favorite=0 ORDER BY updated_at ASC)._
270. **`count()` runs a full `SELECT COUNT(*)` scan on every single capture as part of `enforce_cap`, adding an avoidable query to the hot path** `[improvement]` 🟢 `[low]` - `enforce_cap` (lib.rs:201-206) starts with `let total = self.count()?;`, and `count()` itself (lib.rs:184-189) runs `SELECT COUNT(*) FROM clips` with no covering index. Because enforce_cap runs after every insert, a single capture already costs one query for the dedup SELECT in `insert`, one for `count` in `enforce_cap`, plus the INSERT/UPDATE and DELETE - a running counter maintained transactionally alongside insert/delete could avoid the COUNT(*) scan entirely for what is fundamentally bookkeeping. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:184-189, 201-206._
271. **Schema comment calling `seq` the 'definitive recency tiebreaker' documents a storage-internal value with no note that it must never leak into a future export/import or sync format** `[improvement]` 🟢 `[low]` - `schema.rs:22` documents `seq` as the 'definitive recency tiebreaker,' and `Store::insert`'s dedup path (lib.rs:87-90) actively depends on `seq`'s autoincrement monotonicity for the 'float to top even within the same millisecond' behavior - a reasonable design for a single local file. But nothing in the crate flags `seq` as storage-internal/non-portable: if a future 'merge two vbuff histories' or 'sync across machines' feature ever serializes `Clip` rows including some notion of order, `seq` must never leak into that representation, since two independently autoincrementing databases have no comparable `seq` values across files. Worth a doc note now, before any export/import code is written, given `Clip` itself deliberately has no `seq` field to stay storage-agnostic (per lib.rs:320-326's own comment). _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/schema.rs:22; crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:87-90, 320-326._
272. **`open_in_memory()` is a fully public, non-cfg-gated function documented only as 'useful for tests' with nothing preventing accidental production use** `[improvement]` 🟢 `[low]` - `Store::open_in_memory` (lib.rs:52-56) is a public associated function with no `#[cfg(any(test, feature = "test-utils"))]` gate or other scoping out of the crate's production API surface. A future refactor of `main.rs` (or a new binary added to the workspace) could call `Store::open_in_memory()` by mistake - e.g. as a quick 'let me just get it compiling' placeholder during a larger change - and ship a build that silently discards all clip history on every restart with no compiler or clippy signal that this was meant as a test-only helper. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:52-56 (pub fn, not cfg-gated, doc comment says 'useful for tests' but nothing enforces that)._

---

## Concurrency & robustness (additional, beyond the first 12)

273. **Capture-thread insert/enforce_cap/load loop has no backoff or retry limit when Store writes start failing** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - src/capture.rs's insert block (`let store = store.lock().unwrap(); if let Err(e) = store.insert(&clip) { tracing::warn!(...); continue; } let _ = store.enforce_cap(...); store.load_recent(GUI_LIMIT).ok()`) runs every poll tick (default 300ms). If insert starts failing (disk full, WAL corruption, permission loss), the code only warns and continues -- no backoff, retry counter, or circuit breaker, so the thread spins acquiring/releasing the mutex at the full poll rate forever while every write silently fails. Distinct from audit item 33 (clipboard *read* errors discarded): this is store-*write* errors after a successful read. _Evidence: src/capture.rs, insert block inside `spawn_capture_thread`'s loop: `if let Err(e) = store.insert(&clip) { tracing::warn!("insert failed: {e}"); continue; }` with no retry state carried across iterations._
274. **capture.rs stamps last_hash as seen before the insert result is known, so a failed store write can never be retried on an identical re-copy** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - In `spawn_capture_thread`'s loop, `last_hash = Some(hash);` executes unconditionally right after the capture-gate checks, several statements before the `store.lock()`/`store.insert(&clip)` block that can fail. If that insert then fails (disk full, corruption -- see the sibling backoff finding), the dedup gate at the top of the next iteration (`if last_hash == Some(hash) { continue; }`) will suppress the *exact same content* on every subsequent poll, even if the user copies it again, because `last_hash` was already advanced regardless of whether the write succeeded. The only way to recover is to copy something else first (to change `last_hash`) and then re-copy the failed content -- a non-obvious, undocumented recovery step for silent data loss. _Evidence: src/capture.rs: `last_hash = Some(hash);` executes before the `let refreshed = { let store = store.lock().unwrap(); if let Err(e) = store.insert(&clip) { ... continue; } ... };` block that can fail._
275. **gui.rs takes two separate shared.lock() calls per frame for hotkey-show and tray-sync instead of one combined critical section** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - src/gui.rs locks `shared` once to call `s.request_show()` when a hotkey event fires, then locks `shared` again immediately after just to read `s.paused`/`s.clips.len()` for `t.sync_state(...)`. This runs on every eframe frame (every ~100ms while hidden via the ticker thread, every frame while visible), so the same mutex is acquired and released twice per frame for logically adjacent reads/writes that could share one critical section. Not a correctness bug by itself, but it doubles contention against the capture thread's own lock on every tick, distinct from audit item 29 (clips.clone() cost) since this is about lock *count*, not payload size. _Evidence: src/gui.rs: the hotkey-poll block's `let mut s = shared.lock().unwrap(); s.request_show();` and the immediately following tray-sync block's `let s = shared.lock().unwrap(); t.sync_state(s.paused, s.clips.len());`, two independent lock acquisitions in the same closure invocation._
276. **PopupApp::update's initial state snapshot lock is held across a full Vec<Clip> clone plus three field reads, serializing against the capture thread and action handlers for longer than necessary** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - `PopupApp::update` does `let mut s = self.state.lock().unwrap(); let show = std::mem::take(&mut s.show_requested); (s.clips.clone(), s.paused, show, s.revision)` all inside one lock scope. The clone of the entire clip Vec (already flagged distinctly in audit item 29 for its per-frame repaint cost) additionally means the lock is held for the duration of that clone, not just a pointer/Arc bump -- so while the popup is open and cloning potentially large image byte buffers, the capture thread's `shared.lock().unwrap()` in capture.rs and the tray/action handlers' `shared.lock()` calls in gui.rs/actions.rs all block behind it for the clone's duration on every single frame. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-gui/src/app.rs, `PopupApp::update`'s first block: `let (clips, paused, show_requested, revision) = { let mut s = self.state.lock().unwrap(); let show = std::mem::take(&mut s.show_requested); (s.clips.clone(), s.paused, show, s.revision) };`._
277. **store-then-shared nested locking in actions.rs's mutation handlers has no documented ordering discipline, and the pattern differs from capture.rs's sequential (non-nested) acquisition** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - Every mutating `UiAction` handler in src/actions.rs (`SetPinned`, `Delete`, `ClearAll`) and gui.rs's tray `ClearHistory` handler hold the `store` MutexGuard open across a call to `refresh_snapshot(&store, shared)`, which itself locks `shared` -- a genuine nested acquisition, `store` then `shared`, while both guards are live simultaneously. capture.rs, by contrast, drops its `store` guard (block-scoped) before separately acquiring `shared` -- sequential, never nested. Both patterns happen to agree on ordering today, but nothing (no wrapper type, no debug_assert, no doc comment) stops a future call site from acquiring `shared` first and `store` second while holding both, which is exactly the precondition for an ABA deadlock the moment two threads hit reversed orders concurrently. _Evidence: src/actions.rs: `if let Ok(store) = store.lock() { let _ = store.set_pinned(id, pinned); refresh_snapshot(&store, shared); }` (store guard still in scope when refresh_snapshot locks shared) versus src/capture.rs's block-scoped `store.lock()` that closes before `shared.lock()` runs._
278. **copy_latest_clip reads `shared`, drops the lock, then writes to the OS clipboard, so the read-then-act is not atomic against a concurrent Delete** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - `copy_latest_clip` locks `shared`, clones `s.clips.first()`, drops the lock, then calls `ArboardClipboard::new()` and `cb.write(...)` outside the lock. Between the clone and the write, another thread (the capture thread inserting a new clip, or a UiAction::Delete from the popup) can mutate `shared.clips` and even have the store delete that exact clip out from under it. The written-to-clipboard content can therefore reference a clip that no longer exists in the store, silently desyncing 'what's on the OS clipboard' from 'what vbuff considers current' with no reconciliation. _Evidence: src/actions.rs: `pub(crate) fn copy_latest_clip(shared: &SharedState) { let clip = { let s = shared.lock().unwrap(); s.clips.first().cloned() }; ... if let Ok(mut cb) = ArboardClipboard::new() ... cb.write(&clip.flavors) ... }`, the write happens after the lock is released._
279. **UiAction::Paste's clipboard write races the capture thread's thread-local last_hash, risking the paste-back clip being immediately re-captured as a spurious insert cycle** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - actions.rs's Paste handler writes the picked clip to the OS clipboard via `cb.write(&clip.flavors)` with no coordination with the capture thread's `last_hash` state in capture.rs (already noted generically in audit item 44 as missing self-write suppression). Because `last_hash` is thread-local, the very next poll tick after a Paste only avoids re-inserting if the capture thread's cached `last_hash` already equals the pasted content's hash (e.g. it was the most recently captured clip); if `last_hash` currently differs -- the first poll after a fresh capture-thread restart, or another clip was captured in between the original copy and the paste -- the poll runs a full insert+enforce_cap+load_recent cycle purely to re-insert content vbuff itself just wrote, competing with the GUI thread for the `store` lock at exactly the moment a paste is being sequenced. _Evidence: src/actions.rs's `UiAction::Paste` arm (`cb.write(&clip.flavors)`) versus src/capture.rs's `last_hash` (thread-local to the capture loop, never seeded from or checked against recent GUI-thread writes)._
280. **Tray Quit calls std::process::exit(0) while `store` or `shared` may be locked on another thread, skipping all Drop/flush guarantees** `[problem]` 🟠 `[high]` - src/gui.rs's `TrayAction::Quit` arm calls `ctx.send_viewport_cmd(egui::ViewportCommand::Close)` immediately followed by `std::process::exit(0)`. `std::process::exit` terminates the process immediately without unwinding or running destructors on any other thread, including the capture thread, which may be mid-way through holding `store.lock()` in capture.rs (e.g. between `store.insert` and `store.enforce_cap`, or mid-way through a SQLite write). If SQLite is mid-transaction or mid-WAL-checkpoint when the process is killed this way, the design gives no guarantee beyond WAL replay on next open, since there's no coordinated shutdown, no join on the capture thread, and no explicit lock-then-release by the quit handler to ensure no write is in flight. _Evidence: src/gui.rs: `crate::tray::TrayAction::Quit => { ctx.send_viewport_cmd(egui::ViewportCommand::Close); std::process::exit(0); }` with no join/shutdown coordination with the capture thread spawned in src/capture.rs._
281. **The ticker thread spawned inside the eframe closure is leaked with no shutdown handle, masked today only by Quit's hard process::exit** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - src/gui.rs spawns a detached `std::thread::spawn` ticker loop (`loop { sleep(100ms); ctx.request_repaint(); }`) with `ticker_started` only gating re-spawning it; no `JoinHandle` is ever stored or joined. Since Quit calls `std::process::exit(0)` (see separate finding) the leak is currently masked by hard process termination, but if any future code path replaced the exit with a graceful `eframe::run_simple_native` return, this thread has no way to be told to stop and would keep calling `ctx.request_repaint()` on a `Context` whose underlying window has already been torn down. _Evidence: src/gui.rs: `if !ticker_started { ticker_started = true; let ctx = ctx.clone(); std::thread::spawn(move || { loop { std::thread::sleep(Duration::from_millis(100)); ctx.request_repaint(); } }); }`, no JoinHandle or shutdown channel._
282. **PendingPaste is a single-slot Option with last-write-wins semantics, so two Paste actions drained in the same frame silently drop the first** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - gui.rs's `pending_paste: Option<PendingPaste>` is a single-slot `Option`, and actions.rs's `UiAction::Paste` arm unconditionally does `*pending_paste = Some(PendingPaste { at: ... })`, overwriting any already-pending paste. Because `popup.take_actions()` drains the whole queue each frame and the popup's quick-pick keys (input.rs's Cmd/Ctrl+1..9 loop) can push multiple `UiAction::Paste` entries from a single input batch (Enter plus a quick-pick key registering in the same frame), two Paste actions processed in the same `for action in popup.take_actions()` loop in gui.rs will write clip A to the clipboard, then immediately overwrite it with clip B's write and reschedule the 120ms timer -- the paste that actually fires is whichever ran last, with no error and no indication the first was dropped. _Evidence: src/gui.rs: `let mut pending_paste: Option<PendingPaste> = None;` combined with src/actions.rs's `UiAction::Paste` arm doing `*pending_paste = Some(PendingPaste { at: Instant::now() + Duration::from_millis(120) });` unconditionally, and crates/vbuff-gui/src/input.rs's Enter handler plus its Cmd/Ctrl+1..9 quick-pick loop, both of which can push `UiAction::Paste` in the same `ctx.input` closure call._
283. **AtomicBool `paused` and `shared.lock().paused` are two independent copies of the same boolean that can transiently disagree** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - `toggle_pause` does `paused.store(now, Ordering::Relaxed); shared.lock().unwrap().paused = now;` as two separate, non-atomic operations. Between the `AtomicBool` store and the `Mutex<AppState>.paused` assignment, the capture thread's `paused.load(Ordering::Relaxed)` can observe the new value while the GUI's `s.paused` (read by `PopupApp::update` and rendered via `render_panel`'s `paused` parameter) still shows the old value for one more frame, or vice versa. The UI can therefore show 'Pause capture' for a tick after capture has actually already resumed (or the reverse) -- a dual-source-of-truth desync distinct from audit item 31/32 (lock-poisoning/error-handling, not this specific state split). _Evidence: src/actions.rs: `pub(crate) fn toggle_pause(paused: &Arc<AtomicBool>, shared: &SharedState) { let now = !paused.load(Ordering::Relaxed); paused.store(now, Ordering::Relaxed); shared.lock().unwrap().paused = now; ... }`; consumers at src/capture.rs (`paused.load(Ordering::Relaxed)`) and crates/vbuff-gui/src/app.rs / render.rs (`s.paused` read out of the Mutex)._
284. **Store is a bare rusqlite::Connection with no internal Send+Sync guard or documented single-threaded precondition beyond the caller's external Arc<Mutex<_>>** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs defines `pub struct Store { conn: Connection }` with no internal synchronization; every guarantee that `Store` is only ever touched from one thread at a time comes entirely from the `Arc<Mutex<Store>>` wrapper constructed in src/main.rs, external to the type. Nothing in `vbuff-store`'s public API (`open`, `open_default`, `open_in_memory`) documents or enforces this precondition. rusqlite's `Connection` is `Send` but not `Sync`, so a future caller that shares a bare `Store` across threads without the `Mutex` (e.g. wrapping it in a plain `Arc<Store>`, which compiles because nothing in the crate asserts otherwise) would silently corrupt the SQLite connection state under concurrent access with no compile-time or runtime signal from `Store` itself. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs: `pub struct Store { conn: Connection }` has no doc comment or marker asserting single-threaded/lock-required use; the mutex discipline lives entirely in src/main.rs's `let store = Arc::new(Mutex::new(store));`, outside the crate._
285. **capture.rs drops the store lock before acquiring the shared lock, opening a lost-update window against actions.rs's own store-then-shared refresh sequence** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - capture.rs locks `store`, does insert+enforce_cap+load_recent, drops the store lock at the end of that block, and only then locks `shared` to call `s.set_clips(clips)`. Between dropping the store lock and acquiring the shared lock, a concurrent `UiAction::Delete`/`SetPinned`/`ClearAll` handled by actions.rs (which locks `store`, mutates, then calls `refresh_snapshot` while still holding it, itself locking `shared`) can interleave, so the `clips` vector the capture thread is about to write into `shared` can be a snapshot taken *before* the concurrent delete/pin was applied, overwriting the GUI-thread's more recent `refresh_snapshot` write with stale data purely due to scheduling order. _Evidence: src/capture.rs (store lock dropped at the closing brace of the insert block, `shared` locked afterward in a separate statement) versus src/actions.rs's `SetPinned`/`Delete`/`ClearAll` arms and `refresh_snapshot` (same two-lock, non-atomic pattern from the GUI-thread side)._
286. **GlobalHotkeyBackend::unregister on shutdown is only reached via the normal eframe::run_simple_native return path, which Quit's std::process::exit bypasses entirely** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - src/gui.rs does `if let Some(id) = hotkey_id { let _ = hotkey_backend.unregister(id); }` only after `eframe::run_simple_native(...)` returns normally. Since `TrayAction::Quit` calls `std::process::exit(0)` directly from inside the update closure, this cleanup code is dead on that path -- the global hotkey registration is left in whatever state the OS leaves it in on abrupt process death rather than being explicitly released. Distinct from audit item 41 (no single-instance guard): this is about an already-running instance failing to release its own hotkey on the one exit path the app actually exposes to the user (the tray Quit item). _Evidence: src/gui.rs: `std::process::exit(0)` inside the Quit arm versus the post-loop `if let Some(id) = hotkey_id { let _ = hotkey_backend.unregister(id); }`, unreachable from that Quit path._
287. **N mutating UiActions drained in one frame each independently re-lock store and shared and re-run a full load_recent(1000) query instead of coalescing into one refresh after the batch** `[improvement]` 🟢 `[low]` - Each call to `refresh_snapshot` in src/actions.rs independently re-locks `store` to call `load_recent(GUI_LIMIT)` (1000-row `ORDER BY pinned DESC, updated_at DESC, seq DESC LIMIT` query) and then re-locks `shared` to call `set_clips`. If a user's single frame produces multiple mutating actions -- structurally possible since `popup.take_actions()` drains the whole per-frame action queue in one loop in gui.rs -- N mutations in that frame cause N full `load_recent` queries instead of coalescing to a single refresh after the last mutation in the batch. Worth batching the drained-action loop to defer `refresh_snapshot` until after all actions in the frame's batch are applied. _Evidence: src/gui.rs: `for action in popup.take_actions() { handle_action(action, &store, &shared, &paused, &mut pending_paste, ctx); }` combined with src/actions.rs's `SetPinned`/`Delete`/`ClearAll` arms each independently calling `refresh_snapshot(&store, shared)`._
288. **No watchdog or liveness check on the capture thread from the GUI thread; a silently-dead thread leaves the tray/popup fully unaware** `[problem]` 🟠 `[high]` - `spawn_capture_thread` is fired with `std::thread::spawn` and its `JoinHandle` is discarded -- src/main.rs never binds the return value. If the closure panics anywhere in the loop (e.g. a `.unwrap()` on a poisoned `store` lock after some other panic already poisoned it), the thread dies silently: no message reaches the app's `tracing` output or any UI surface, `paused` and `shared` are simply never touched again, and the GUI has no mechanism (heartbeat timestamp, dead-man's switch, or JoinHandle poll) to detect this and show the 'capture stopped' state audit item 45 already flags as generically missing. The concurrency-specific gap is that there isn't even a JoinHandle retained to `is_finished()`-poll from the eframe loop, so recovering this signal isn't possible without a code change. _Evidence: src/main.rs: `spawn_capture_thread(Arc::clone(&store), Arc::clone(&shared), Arc::clone(&paused), config.clone());` (return value discarded) and src/capture.rs's `std::thread::spawn(move || { ... })` with no panic hook or handle retention._
289. **Config is cloned once at startup into the capture thread with no shared/live-update path, so a future hot-reload would silently diverge between the two owners** `[idea]` 🟢 `[low]` - src/main.rs passes `config.clone()` by value into `spawn_capture_thread`, which closes over that owned copy for the entire process lifetime (referenced for `poll_interval_ms`, `skip_whitespace_only`, `is_excluded`, `max_history` inside the loop). The main thread's own `config` binding (used only during startup for the hotkey combo) is a second, independent copy. If config hot-reload is ever added (audit item 43 flags its absence as a gap), the natural fix of re-reading `Config::load_or_create()` on a SIGHUP/file-watch would update neither copy unless a new `Arc<Mutex<Config>>` (or `arc-swap`) is threaded through both the capture thread and the GUI/tray paths that reference `Config` fields today as plain owned values -- worth designing the shared-config primitive now, before hot-reload ships, so the eventual change does not require re-plumbing every `Config` field access. _Evidence: src/main.rs: `spawn_capture_thread(..., config.clone())` and the separate `config.hotkey`/`parse_combo(&config.hotkey)` read further down in the same function; src/capture.rs's loop closes over `config` by value (`config.poll_interval_ms`, `config.is_excluded`, `config.max_history`, `config.skip_whitespace_only`)._
290. **actions.rs's Delete/SetPinned/ClearAll handlers silently swallow a poisoned `store` lock while the `refresh_snapshot` they call one line later unwraps `shared` unconditionally, in the same call chain** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - actions.rs's mutating arms guard the `store` lock with `if let Ok(store) = store.lock()` (matching audit item 32's pattern of silently swallowing poison on `store`), but the `refresh_snapshot` helper they call does `shared.lock().unwrap()` unconditionally. So on this exact call path, a poisoned `store` mutex is handled gracefully (no-op, no crash) while a poisoned `shared` mutex one line later in the same function call still panics -- a more specific, code-level inconsistency than audit item 32 (which contrasts capture.rs's unwrap vs. main.rs's if-let across *different call sites*); this one shows the inconsistency *within a single function's own call graph*, store tolerant, shared not, in the same statement sequence. _Evidence: src/actions.rs: `if let Ok(store) = store.lock() { let _ = store.set_pinned(id, pinned); refresh_snapshot(&store, shared); }` calling `pub(crate) fn refresh_snapshot(store: &Store, shared: &SharedState) { if let Ok(clips) = store.load_recent(GUI_LIMIT) { shared.lock().unwrap().set_clips(clips); } }`._
291. **capture.rs's last_hash dedup state is thread-local and reset to None on every process start, so a restart immediately after a crash bumps the currently-clipboarded item's updated_at as if freshly copied** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - capture.rs initializes `let mut last_hash: Option<[u8; 32]> = None;` fresh in every call to `spawn_capture_thread`, which only ever runs once per process. There is no persistence of the last-seen hash across restarts (e.g. into the store or a small state file), so if vbuff crashes and is relaunched (or is restarted by a supervisor) while the clipboard still holds the same content it held at crash time, the first poll tick after restart treats it as a brand-new change (since `last_hash == Some(hash)` can never be true on a fresh `None`), triggering an insert. Content-hash dedup in `Store::insert` will still just bump the existing row's `updated_at` rather than truly duplicating it, so this is not data corruption, but the row's `updated_at` gets bumped to 'now' on every restart even when the user copied nothing new, silently jumping the item to the top of history. _Evidence: src/capture.rs: `let mut last_hash: Option<[u8; 32]> = None;` (fresh on every spawn) and the `if last_hash == Some(hash) { continue; }` gate, combined with crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs's `insert` dedup path (`UPDATE clips SET updated_at = ?1, seq = ... WHERE id = ?2`) which bumps `updated_at` on any matching insert._
292. **No timeout on Mutex::lock anywhere -- a hung SQLite call inside the store lock blocks the capture thread, the GUI thread, and the tray thread indefinitely with no diagnostic** `[improvement]` 🟡 `[medium]` - Every `store.lock()` call site (capture.rs, actions.rs's three mutating arms, gui.rs's ClearHistory arm) uses the blocking `std::sync::Mutex::lock()` with no timeout variant; a grep across src/*.rs and crates/vbuff-store confirms no `try_lock` call exists anywhere in the workspace. If a single SQLite call inside the lock scope stalls (e.g. `history.db` living on a network-mounted or FUSE data directory, or OS-level file-lock contention with another process touching the same file), every other thread that subsequently calls `store.lock()` -- the capture thread every poll tick, and the GUI thread on every popup action -- blocks indefinitely with the UI simply appearing frozen (Delete/Pin/ClearAll clicks stop responding), no timeout, no error surfaced, and no 'store unresponsive' indicator. Stronger and more specific than audit item 45's generic 'no visible degradation indicator': this is the specific missing fallback for a hang, not a fast failure. _Evidence: grep across src/*.rs and crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs shows every lock site uses `.lock()`; no `try_lock`, no lock-timeout wrapper, no watchdog thread anywhere in the workspace._
293. **AppState derives Default with all-empty/zero fields, a second, independently-maintained construction path from the hand-built literal main.rs actually uses at startup** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - crates/vbuff-gui/src/state.rs derives `#[derive(Default)]` on `AppState`, but the only construction path exercised today (src/main.rs) builds `AppState { clips: recent, paused: false, show_requested: false, revision: 0 }` by hand with the store-hydrated `recent` list. Nothing ties the two together or tests that they diverge as expected; a future call site (a test harness, or a refactor that swaps the manual struct literal for `AppState::default()` to reduce boilerplate) could silently start the GUI with an empty history even though the store has data, since `Default` and the 'real' constructor are two independently-maintained code paths for the same type with no single source of truth. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-gui/src/state.rs: `#[derive(Default)] pub struct AppState { pub clips: Vec<Clip>, pub paused: bool, pub show_requested: bool, pub revision: u64 }` versus src/main.rs's hand-built `AppState { clips: recent, paused: false, show_requested: false, revision: 0 }`._
294. **UiAction::Paste's clipboard write and viewport-hide fire before the paste actually executes, with no check that OS focus has actually left vbuff's window before the 120ms timer fires** `[idea]` 🟢 `[low]` - actions.rs sends the hide command and sets `*pending_paste` in the same statement block, non-atomically with respect to the OS window manager's own async focus-transfer. Nothing enforces that the OS has actually returned focus to the previously-focused app before the fixed 120ms timer in `PendingPaste` fires the keystroke (already flagged generically as audit item 40's 'unverified 120ms guess'), and there's no mechanism reusing the same focused-check the popup already computes for its own hide-on-blur logic (`ctx.input(|i| i.viewport().focused...)` in `PopupApp::update`) to gate the paste-firing path in src/gui.rs on focus having actually left first -- a concrete, implementable improvement distinct from just 'the delay might be wrong': there is a signal already computed elsewhere in this same codebase that could gate the fire instead of blind timing. _Evidence: src/actions.rs's `UiAction::Paste` arm (`ctx.send_viewport_cmd(egui::ViewportCommand::Visible(false)); *pending_paste = Some(PendingPaste { at: Instant::now() + Duration::from_millis(120) });`) versus crates/vbuff-gui/src/app.rs's `let focused = ctx.input(|i| i.viewport().focused.unwrap_or(true));`, computed for hide-on-blur but unused by the paste-firing path in src/gui.rs._
295. **Two-phase insert-dedup-then-enforce_cap sequence is not wrapped in a SQLite transaction, and the in-process Mutex<Store> provides zero protection against a second vbuff process interleaving the same statements** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - Building on but distinct from audit item 37 (which flags insert/enforce_cap as not one transaction): the concurrency-specific angle is that `Arc<Mutex<Store>>` only provides mutual exclusion *within this process*; it does nothing for a second `vbuff` process (audit item 41 already flags the missing single-instance guard) opening the same `history.db` file concurrently. Two processes each holding their own in-process `Mutex<Store>` guard can interleave `insert`'s dedup-check-then-update with the other process's `enforce_cap`'s count-then-delete at the SQLite level, since neither reads happen inside an explicit `BEGIN IMMEDIATE` transaction -- WAL mode allows concurrent readers plus one writer, but these multi-statement non-transactional sequences are exactly the classic TOCTOU pattern (count, then delete based on a stale count) that a second process's own concurrent DELETE/INSERT can invalidate mid-sequence, which the in-process Mutex cannot address. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs: `insert`'s dedup check-then-`UPDATE`/`INSERT` (no `BEGIN`) and `enforce_cap`'s `count()` followed by a separate `DELETE ... LIMIT ?1` (no `BEGIN`), combined with the absence of any single-instance guard in src/main.rs that would make the in-process Mutex actually sufficient._
296. **eframe's request_repaint_after(100ms) and the separate ticker thread's unconditional request_repaint() every 100ms are two independently-timed, uncoordinated wake sources for the same event loop** `[improvement]` 🟢 `[low]` - src/gui.rs spawns a ticker thread sleeping exactly 100ms and calling `ctx.request_repaint()` unconditionally, while the update closure itself also calls `ctx.request_repaint_after(Duration::from_millis(100))` on every frame. Under normal conditions these roughly double the wake frequency (both firing near-100ms marks but not synchronized), and if the GUI thread is ever briefly delayed (e.g. by the `s.clips.clone()` cost flagged in audit item 29 while the popup is visible), the ticker thread's independent OS-thread timer continues firing at its own pace regardless, so the two mechanisms can drift apart over a long-running session with no single source of truth for wake cadence -- worth consolidating to one timing source (the ticker thread alone, since it is what actually keeps the loop alive while hidden) rather than keeping both. _Evidence: src/gui.rs: the ticker thread's `loop { std::thread::sleep(Duration::from_millis(100)); ctx.request_repaint(); }` and the update closure's own `ctx.request_repaint_after(Duration::from_millis(100));`, called every frame from inside the same closure the ticker also wakes._
297. **A scheduled PendingPaste can be silently dropped if TrayAction::Quit is processed earlier in the same frame's closure invocation** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - gui.rs's pending-paste check (`if let Some(p) = &pending_paste { if Instant::now() >= p.at { ... backend.paste() ... } }`) runs unconditionally in the closure on every frame, which is correct in intent, but the tray-poll block that can process `TrayAction::Quit` runs *earlier* in the same closure body, before the popup/pending-paste block. Because `TrayAction::Quit`'s handler calls `std::process::exit(0)` immediately, a Quit click processed in the same frame (or any frame after a Paste was scheduled but before its 120ms elapses) permanently drops the scheduled paste with the user never seeing the keystroke land and no warning that it was lost -- a real, orderable race between two pieces of state (`pending_paste` and the quit signal) mutated in the same closure invocation but never cross-checked against each other. _Evidence: src/gui.rs: the tray-poll block containing `crate::tray::TrayAction::Quit => { ctx.send_viewport_cmd(egui::ViewportCommand::Close); std::process::exit(0); }` runs before the later `if let Some(p) = &pending_paste { if Instant::now() >= p.at { ... } }` block in the same closure body, so `exit(0)` never lets the later block run._
298. **ArboardClipboard::new() is called fresh on every UiAction::Paste and every tray CopyLatest, opening a new native clipboard handle on the GUI thread while the capture thread holds its own long-lived handle open concurrently** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - `copy_latest_clip` and the `UiAction::Paste` arm both call `ArboardClipboard::new()` inline, creating a brand-new native clipboard connection on the GUI thread, while `spawn_capture_thread` holds its own separate long-lived `ArboardClipboard` open for the entire process lifetime on a different thread. On Windows, `OpenClipboard`/`CloseClipboard` is a genuine system-wide exclusive lock; `arboard` opens and closes around each individual read/write call rather than holding it open persistently, so a coincidental overlap between the capture thread's poll-driven `clipboard.read()` and the GUI thread's action-driven `ArboardClipboard::new()` + `cb.write(...)` can transiently fail either side depending on timing. Distinct from audit item 39 (a design-consistency complaint about reuse vs. fresh handles): this finding is about the actual cross-thread contention for the underlying OS clipboard resource that results from two independently-timed handles being open on two different threads at once. _Evidence: src/actions.rs: `copy_latest_clip`'s `ArboardClipboard::new()` and the `UiAction::Paste` arm's `ArboardClipboard::new()`, both GUI-thread, versus src/capture.rs's single long-lived `let mut clipboard = ArboardClipboard::new()...` held for the thread's lifetime and read via `clipboard.read()` every poll tick._
299. **EnigoPaste::paste() leaves the modifier key stuck down at the OS level if the initial key-press call itself errors, since the '?' short-circuits before the release statement** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - `EnigoPaste::paste()` does `self.enigo.key(modifier_key, Direction::Press).map_err(...)?;` as its first synthesized action, then separately synthesizes the 'v' click and the modifier release, with a comment noting the release runs 'even if the v click failed.' That guarantee only holds for a *click* failure -- if the `Press` call on the first line itself returns an `Err` (a transient enigo/OS input-injection failure, plausible on a Wayland session with restricted synthetic-input permissions, or right after an Accessibility-permission revocation), the `?` propagates immediately and the function returns before the release statement is ever reached, leaving the modifier key (Cmd/Ctrl) held down at the OS level with no code path to un-stick it -- silently breaking every subsequent real keystroke the user makes as a modifier-chord until they manually tap the key. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-platform/src/paste.rs: `self.enigo.key(modifier_key, Direction::Press).map_err(|e| PlatformError::Paste(e.to_string()))?;` precedes the `let click = ...; let release = self.enigo.key(modifier_key, Direction::Release);` pair by several statements, so the `?` on the press line returns before `release` is ever computed._
300. **config.rs's is_excluded re-lowercases the input and every exclusion-list entry on every call, with no precomputed lowercased cache built at config-load time** `[improvement]` 🟢 `[low]` - capture.rs calls `config.is_excluded(app)` on the capture-gate path whenever `captured.source_app` is `Some` (currently always `None` per audit item 4, but the branch logic still executes every tick). `Config::is_excluded` allocates a new lowercased `String` for the input plus one more per exclusion-list entry on every single call (`self.excluded_apps.iter().any(|e| !e.is_empty() && lower.contains(&e.to_lowercase()))`), with no pre-lowercased cache built once at `Config::load_or_create` time. Not a concurrency bug, but it sits on the same hot path analyzed for lock granularity elsewhere in this list, and since `Config` is a plain owned value with no interior mutability, precomputing lowercased exclusion entries once would be a straightforward, lock-free improvement. _Evidence: src/capture.rs: `if let Some(app) = &captured.source_app && config.is_excluded(app) { ... }` inside the poll loop, and src/config.rs: `pub fn is_excluded(&self, source_app: &str) -> bool { let lower = source_app.to_lowercase(); self.excluded_apps.iter().any(|e| !e.is_empty() && lower.contains(&e.to_lowercase())) }`, re-lowercasing every entry on every call._
301. **handle_action's UiAction::Delete/SetPinned/ClearAll arms all guard the store lock with if let Ok but the popup's own single-threaded egui rendering means a poisoned shared lock from any other panic site still takes down the whole update closure on the very next frame** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - PopupApp::update's very first statement every frame is `let mut s = self.state.lock().unwrap();` -- an unconditional unwrap on `shared`, unguarded by any `if let Ok`. Because this runs unconditionally at the top of every single frame regardless of which UiAction (if any) was just processed, any prior panic anywhere in the process that poisoned `shared` (including, for instance, a panic inside the capture thread's own `shared.lock().unwrap()` call in capture.rs) guarantees the very next popup frame panics too, tearing down the eframe event loop entirely -- unlike the store-side handlers elsewhere in the codebase that at least degrade to a no-op via `if let Ok(store) = store.lock()`, there is no equivalent guard anywhere on the `shared` mutex's most frequently hit call site. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-gui/src/app.rs: `let (clips, paused, show_requested, revision) = { let mut s = self.state.lock().unwrap(); ... };` as the first statement of `PopupApp::update`, run unconditionally every frame with no `if let Ok` guard anywhere on this call site._

---

## Error handling & observability

302. **Pin/delete/clear results silently discarded in the primary action handler** `[problem]` 🟠 `[high]` - src/actions.rs handle_action(): `let _ = store.set_pinned(id, pinned);` (line 82), `let _ = store.delete(id);` (line 88), and `let _ = store.clear();` (line 94) all throw away the `Result<(), StoreError>` with zero logging. If the SQLite write fails (locked file, disk full, corrupt row), the user clicks Delete/Pin/Clear-all, sees nothing happen or stale data, and no trace/log line exists anywhere to diagnose it. Distinct from audit #32, which is about lock-poisoning on the outer `store.lock()`, not the inner call's own Result. _Evidence: src/actions.rs:82,88,94._
303. **refresh_snapshot swallows load_recent failures with no signal** `[problem]` 🟠 `[high]` - `pub(crate) fn refresh_snapshot(store: &Store, shared: &SharedState) { if let Ok(clips) = store.load_recent(GUI_LIMIT) { shared.lock().unwrap().set_clips(clips); } }` - on any `Result::Err` the function is a silent no-op: the GUI keeps showing the pre-mutation snapshot with no log line and no revision bump, so a user who just deleted a clip may still see it listed with no indication the reload failed. _Evidence: src/actions.rs:108-112._
304. **Tray's ClearHistory handler duplicates the un-logged clear-then-refresh pattern independently** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - src/gui.rs's tray poll loop reimplements `if let Ok(store) = store.lock() { let _ = store.clear(); refresh_snapshot(&store, &shared); }` inline instead of calling `crate::actions::handle_action(UiAction::ClearAll, ...)`, so any future logging/telemetry added to the popup's ClearAll path (were the first finding above fixed) would not apply here - two independently drifting copies of the same error-swallowing sequence. _Evidence: src/gui.rs:115-120._
305. **Corrupt stored timestamps are silently replaced with 'now' instead of surfaced** `[problem]` 🟠 `[high]` - `row::raw_to_clip` does `chrono::DateTime::from_timestamp_millis(raw.created_at).unwrap_or_else(chrono::Utc::now)` and `.unwrap_or(created_at)` for `updated_at`. A corrupt or out-of-range millisecond value in the DB (bit flip, manual edit, future schema bug) is silently reinterpreted as 'captured right now' with no `StoreError::Corrupt` and no log - the clip silently jumps to the top of the recency-sorted list every time it's loaded, masking the corruption as fresh activity instead of surfacing it. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/row.rs:48-50._
306. **Two independent ULID-parse-error sites discard the real ulid::DecodeError** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - Both `Store::insert`'s dedup path (`ClipId::parse(&id_str).map_err(|_| StoreError::Corrupt("bad ulid in db".into()))`) and `row::raw_to_clip` (`ClipId::parse(&raw.id).map_err(|_| StoreError::Corrupt("bad ulid in db".into()))`) throw away the actual `ulid::DecodeError` (which encodes whether the string was too short, too long, or had invalid base32 characters) behind an identical hardcoded string, so the log/error message can never distinguish the failure modes or even show the offending id value. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:91-92; crates/vbuff-store/src/row.rs:40._
307. **clipboard.get_text() error and legitimate empty text are indistinguishable on the read side** `[problem]` 🟠 `[high]` - `ArboardClipboard::read()`'s text branch is `match self.clipboard.get_text() { Ok(text) if !text.is_empty() => {...}, _ => {} }`. The wildcard `_` arm matches both `Err(e)` (permission denied, unsupported clipboard format, X11 selection-owner-gone) and `Ok("")` identically - a genuine OS-level read failure never reaches a log line anywhere in the call chain (the caller in capture.rs only sees an empty flavor list, not the underlying error). _Evidence: crates/vbuff-platform/src/clipboard.rs:34-42._
308. **Image read failure in ArboardClipboard::read() is unlogged** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - `if flavors.is_empty() && let Ok(img) = self.clipboard.get_image() { ... }` uses `let Ok` to only proceed on success; any `Err` (no image on clipboard vs. a real decode/backend failure) is dropped on the floor with no `tracing::debug!`/`warn!` anywhere, unlike the text branch's caller-side warns for write failures - read-side image errors have zero observability. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-platform/src/clipboard.rs:46-48._
309. **enforce_cap failures inside the capture thread are silently dropped** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - `let _ = store.enforce_cap(config.max_history);` in the capture thread discards the `Result<usize, StoreError>` entirely - unlike the adjacent `store.insert` call three lines above which does `tracing::warn!("insert failed: {e}")`, a failure to evict old clips (e.g. a locked DB file) produces zero log output, so `max_history` can be silently violated indefinitely with no way to tell from the logs. _Evidence: src/capture.rs:94._
310. **A permanently failing store.insert silently drops that clip forever with no counter** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - In the capture loop, `last_hash` is updated to the new content's hash (line 74) before `store.insert` is attempted (line 90). If `insert` then fails (e.g. transient disk-full), the code logs one `warn!` and `continue`s - but because `last_hash` already reflects this content, an identical re-copy of the same clipboard content on the next poll is treated as 'unchanged' and skipped before ever reaching `insert` again, so the clip is lost permanently with a single easily-missed warn line and no retry/backoff/counter. _Evidence: src/capture.rs:74,90-93._
311. **EnigoPaste::new().ok() discards the specific PlatformError::Paste reason at startup** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - `let mut paste_backend = EnigoPaste::new().ok(); if paste_backend.is_none() { tracing::warn!("paste backend unavailable; paste-back disabled"); }` throws away the actual `PlatformError::Paste(String)` (which on macOS carries the OS-level reason, e.g. missing Accessibility permission vs. no display server) and replaces it with one hardcoded string - the log can never tell an operator why paste-back is unavailable, only that it is. _Evidence: src/gui.rs:42-45._
312. **Tray construction failure discards the underlying tray_icon error entirely** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - `tray = crate::tray::Tray::new().ok(); if tray.is_none() { tracing::warn!("tray icon unavailable"); }` drops whatever `anyhow::Error` `Tray::new()` returned (menu-append failure, icon-build failure, OS tray API failure) - the `anyhow::Result<Self>` return type on `Tray::new` is clearly designed to carry a real cause chain, but the caller never reads it. _Evidence: src/gui.rs:78-82._
313. **Hotkey unregister-on-exit failure is fully silent, unlike register's warn** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - `let _ = hotkey_backend.unregister(id);` at shutdown swallows the `Result` with no logging at all, while the corresponding `register` call earlier in main.rs explicitly does `tracing::warn!("failed to register hotkey {:?}: {e}", config.hotkey)` on failure - the asymmetry means a leaked OS-level hotkey registration (which can block the next launch of vbuff from registering the same combo) leaves no trace in the logs to explain a subsequent 'hotkey unavailable' report. _Evidence: src/gui.rs:154-156; src/main.rs:84-85._
314. **Every tracing::warn!/error! call uses string interpolation instead of structured error fields** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - All ten `tracing::warn!`/`error!` call sites that carry an error value (src/capture.rs:31,91; src/actions.rs:46,72; src/gui.rs:44,80,144; src/main.rs:85) format the error via `{e}` inside the message string rather than as a structured field (`error = %e` or `error = ?e`). None of them are queryable/filterable by error type or value in a structured-log sink (JSON output, log aggregators), and none preserve `std::error::Error::source()` chains from the underlying `anyhow`/`thiserror` errors - main.rs's own `.context(...)` chains built with `anyhow::Context` are never actually surfaced beyond the top-level message once logged this way. _Evidence: src/capture.rs:31,91; src/actions.rs:46,72; src/gui.rs:44,80,144; src/main.rs:85._
315. **RUST_LOG parse errors silently fall back to "info" with no indication to the user** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - `init_tracing()` does `EnvFilter::try_from_default_env().unwrap_or_else(|_| EnvFilter::new("info"))` - if a user sets a malformed `RUST_LOG` value (typo'd target name, bad directive syntax), the error from `try_from_default_env` is discarded and tracing silently falls back to the default filter with zero output anywhere (not even to stderr before the subscriber is installed) telling the user their filter was rejected. _Evidence: src/main.rs:94,96._
316. **Corrupt config.toml crashes the whole app at startup instead of falling back to defaults** `[problem]` 🟠 `[high]` - `Config::load_or_create()`'s existing-file branch does `let cfg: Config = toml::from_str(&text)?;` with no fallback - a config.toml that fails to parse (hand-edited typo, partial write from a crash mid-save) propagates straight through main()'s `.context("loading config")?` and aborts the entire process before any GUI/tray/capture starts, with no distinct error message telling the user 'your config file is corrupt' versus any other startup failure category, and no automatic recovery to defaults the way the missing-file branch already has. _Evidence: src/config.rs:58-64._
317. **Corrupt image bytes in a stored clip render as a generic icon with no log anywhere** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - `build_thumbnail`'s encoded-image branch does `let img = image::load_from_memory(bytes).ok()?;` - if the stored bytes are truncated or the format is unsupported, the function returns `None` and the row silently falls back to `clip.meta.kind.icon()`, indistinguishable in the UI (and in the logs, since nothing is logged) from a clip that legitimately has no image flavor at all. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-gui/src/thumbnail.rs:63._
318. **parse_hex_color silently rejects 4-digit #rgba hex that classify.rs's is_color_hex already accepted** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - `vbuff_core::classify::is_color_hex` accepts hex payload lengths `3 | 4 | 6 | 8` (the `4` covers CSS `#rgba` shorthand), so a clip copied as `#f80c` is classified `ContentKind::Color`. But `vbuff_gui::color::parse_hex_color`'s `match hex.len() { 3 => ..., 6 => ..., 8 => ..., _ => None }` has no arm for length 4, so it falls into `_ => None`. `draw_color_swatch` then does `parse_hex_color(text).unwrap_or(Color32::GRAY)`, silently rendering a plain gray square for a value the app itself just classified as a color, with no log anywhere flagging the mismatch between the two independently-written hex parsers. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-core/src/classify.rs:103 vs crates/vbuff-gui/src/color.rs:13-30 and :6._
319. **content_hash_from_flavors silently treats a Spilled body's blob_ref string as hash input instead of its bytes** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - `content_hash_from_flavors` does `Body::Spilled { blob_ref, .. } => blob_ref.as_bytes().to_vec()` - this hashes the UTF-8 bytes of the blob_ref string itself (e.g. the literal characters of a hex digest) rather than decoding it back into the 32 raw digest bytes it represents. Since nothing in the codebase ever constructs a `Body::Spilled` (per audit #20), this path is currently untested and unexercised, so if a future spill implementation is added the dedup hash for spilled clips would be wrong from day one with no test or log to catch the mismatch against the inline-hash equivalent. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-core/src/hash.rs:48-52._
320. **Config::save() write failure during first-run creation has no distinguishing context** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - `Config::save()`'s `std::fs::write(&path, text)?` propagates a bare `io::Error` through anyhow's `?` with no `.context(...)` call anywhere in the function, unlike main()'s other startup calls which all wrap failures with `.context("opening store")`/`.context("loading config")` etc. - a disk-full or permission-denied failure while writing the very first config.toml on a fresh install surfaces only as a raw `io::Error` Display string with no indication it happened during config save specifically. _Evidence: src/config.rs:72-80._
321. **toggle_pause has no error path at all for a poisoned shared-state lock, unlike every other shared.lock() call site** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - `toggle_pause` does `shared.lock().unwrap().paused = now;` - a bare `.unwrap()` with no fallback, consistent with most of the codebase's `Mutex::lock().unwrap()` pattern (already flagged generally by audit #31), but notably this is the only mutation site for the pause flag reachable from both the popup keybind and the tray menu, so a poisoned lock here (from an earlier panic anywhere else holding `shared`) means Pause/Resume becomes permanently unusable from both UI entry points simultaneously with the panic's origin lost by the time the user notices. _Evidence: src/actions.rs:26._
322. **StoreError::Io is not #[from]-derived, creating an inconsistent conversion story with the rest of StoreError's variants** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - `StoreError::Sqlite` and `StoreError::Json` both derive `#[from]` so `?` converts automatically, but `StoreError::Io(#[source] std::io::Error)` deliberately omits `#[from]`, forcing every io error site to spell out `.map_err(StoreError::Io)` by hand (currently only `Store::open_default`'s `std::fs::create_dir_all` call). If a future edit adds another `std::io::Error`-producing call anywhere in this crate and someone reaches for `?` out of habit (since every other error type here supports it), it will fail to compile rather than silently misbehave - a latent trap in the crate's own error-conversion consistency, not a runtime bug yet. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/error.rs:13-14; crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:41._
323. **copy_latest_clip and Paste's UiAction handler duplicate the identical write-then-warn pattern with no shared helper** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - `copy_latest_clip` (tray-only) and the `UiAction::Paste` branch of `handle_action` both independently write `if let Ok(mut cb) = ArboardClipboard::new() && let Err(e) = cb.write(&clip.flavors) { tracing::warn!("...failed: {e}"); }` with only the log message text differing - a `ClipboardBackend::new()` failure (the clipboard handle itself couldn't be opened, e.g. another process holds an exclusive X11 selection lock) is silently absorbed by the outer `if let Ok` in both places with no log line at all, only the inner `write` failure is logged; the two copies can drift independently since there is no shared function. _Evidence: src/actions.rs:43-47,69-73._
324. **No tracing span exists anywhere for the capture-poll loop or a single poll iteration** `[idea]` 🟢 `[low]` - `spawn_capture_thread`'s `loop { ... }` in src/capture.rs never opens a `tracing::span!`/`#[instrument]` around a poll iteration, so every `warn!`/`error!` emitted inside it (insert failed, clipboard backend unavailable) appears as a flat, context-free log line with no correlation id tying repeated failures on the same clip attempt together, and no way to compute poll-loop latency or failure rate from the log stream alone without also parsing timestamps by hand. _Evidence: src/capture.rs:22-103 (no span/instrument anywhere in this file)._
325. **No counters/metrics exist for capture successes, capture failures, or evictions - only ad hoc log lines** `[idea]` 🟢 `[low]` - Nothing in the codebase increments any counter (no `metrics` crate, no `AtomicU64` counters) for clips captured, clips skipped by the capture gate, insert failures, or clips evicted by `enforce_cap` - the only observability is the scattered `tracing::info!/warn!/error!` calls already inventoried above. A user experiencing 'my history feels incomplete' has no `vbuff --stats`/tray tooltip/log summary to consult; they would have to grep raw logs and manually count warn lines to estimate a capture-failure rate. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-core, crates/vbuff-store, src/capture.rs - no counter/metric type anywhere in the workspace._
326. **insert()'s dedup UPDATE and the fallback INSERT share no transaction, so a crash between them can leave the dedup decision stale with no rollback signal** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - `Store::insert` first runs a `SELECT id FROM clips WHERE content_hash = ?1`, then conditionally either an `UPDATE ... SET updated_at, seq` or an `INSERT`, as separate autocommit statements with no `conn.transaction()` wrapper anywhere in the function (grep confirms zero occurrences of `transaction`/`BEGIN`/`savepoint` in the file). If the process is killed between the SELECT and the UPDATE/INSERT (e.g. by the OS during a forced-quit while the capture thread is mid-poll), the dedup decision made against the SELECT's snapshot can go stale with no error raised at all - a narrower, distinct claim from audit #37 (which was about `insert`+`enforce_cap` across two separate call sites) since this is entirely inside `insert` itself, between its own SELECT and its own write. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:71-121 (no transaction wrapper anywhere in the file)._
327. **schema::migrate()'s PRAGMA user_version read has no validation that it succeeded meaningfully** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - `let version: i64 = conn.query_row("PRAGMA user_version", [], |row| row.get(0))?;` trusts whatever integer SQLite returns with no sanity check (e.g. a `version` greater than `SCHEMA_VERSION`, which would happen if a newer vbuff build downgraded to an older binary against the same DB file) - the `if version < 1` check only handles the upgrade case; a `version > SCHEMA_VERSION` silently does nothing (no error, no log), so an old binary opening a newer DB proceeds as if the schema matched, with no warning that its hardcoded SQL (e.g. the `INSERT INTO clips (...) VALUES (...)`) may not match the actual on-disk columns. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/schema.rs:16-17._
328. **Nothing ever logs the matched hash or surviving ClipId when insert()'s dedup branch bumps an existing row** `[idea]` 🟢 `[low]` - `Clip::content_hash_hex` exists specifically to render the dedup key for diagnostics (defined at vbuff-types/src/lib.rs:285), but nothing in `Store::insert`'s dedup branch (crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:75-93) ever calls it or logs the matched hash/ClipId when a duplicate is detected and bumped - a user asking 'why did my two different-looking copies merge into one history entry' (e.g. copying the same text with trailing whitespace differences that got trimmed upstream) has no debug-level trace showing which hash matched or which row absorbed the update. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:75-93 vs crates/vbuff-types/src/lib.rs:285 (content_hash_hex defined but never called in vbuff-store)._
329. **PendingPaste's paste-backend Err is logged but the pending-paste state is unconditionally cleared, discarding the chance to distinguish transient vs. permanent failure** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - In run_gui's frame loop, `if let Some(backend) = &mut paste_backend && let Err(e) = backend.paste() { tracing::warn!("paste-back failed: {e}"); } pending_paste = None;` unconditionally sets `pending_paste = None` regardless of whether `paste()` succeeded or failed - there is no retry, no escalating log level for repeated failures, and no distinction in the log between 'the modifier press failed' vs 'the release failed' even though `EnigoPaste::paste()` internally has three separate `.map_err` call sites (press, click, release) that all funnel into the same `PlatformError::Paste(String)` shape - that detail is flattened into one string by the time it reaches this warn. _Evidence: src/gui.rs:139-150; crates/vbuff-platform/src/paste.rs:24,40,45-46._
330. **GlobalHotkeyBackend::unregister silently no-ops when the id was never registered, with no log distinguishing 'already gone' from 'success'** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - `fn unregister(&mut self, id: u32) -> Result<()> { if let Some(hotkey) = self.registered.remove(&id) { ... } Ok(()) }` returns `Ok(())` identically whether the id was found and successfully unregistered from the OS, or was never in the `registered` map at all (e.g. called twice, or called with a stale id after `register` failed and returned `None` upstream) - a caller has no way to tell 'this hotkey was already gone' from 'this hotkey was just cleanly removed' from the return value or any log line. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-platform/src/hotkey.rs:45-52._
331. **key_to_code's exhaustive match returning None for unsupported keys produces a generic BadCombo string with no list of what IS supported** `[improvement]` 🟢 `[low]` - `parse_combo`'s eventual `PlatformError::BadCombo(format!("unknown key {:?}", combo.key))` (surfaced via `key_to_code` returning `None` in `combo_to_hotkey`) tells the user which key string failed but never enumerates the actually-supported key set (A-Z, 0-9, Space, Enter/Return, Tab) anywhere in the error message - a user who configures `hotkey = "Cmd+Shift+F13"` in config.toml gets 'unknown key "F13"' with no hint that function keys aren't supported at all, forcing a source read to discover the limitation. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-platform/src/hotkey.rs:66-67,75-120._
332. **is_excluded's substring match has no logging when a capture is actually gated out, making the exclusion feature unverifiable even once wired up** `[improvement]` 🟢 `[low]` - `Config::is_excluded` returns a plain `bool` with no side channel, and its one call site in the (currently dead, per audit #4) capture-gate path in src/capture.rs does `if let Some(app) = &captured.source_app && config.is_excluded(app) { last_hash = Some(hash); continue; }` with no `tracing::debug!`/`info!` announcing 'skipped capture from {app}: matched exclusion rule {rule}' - even once #4's dead-code bug is fixed and `source_app` is populated, a user who configured an exclusion would have zero way to confirm from the logs that it is actually firing versus their copy simply never having reached the poll. _Evidence: src/capture.rs:67-72; src/config.rs:83-88._
333. **No warning or error is ever logged when the capture-gate whitespace-only skip fires, unlike every other skip/continue branch's sibling paths** `[improvement]` 🟢 `[low]` - The `config.skip_whitespace_only && text.trim().is_empty()` branch in the capture loop silently `continue`s with `last_hash` updated but no `tracing::debug!` call, so a user who copies what looks like visible content (e.g. a cell full of only tab characters from a spreadsheet) but gets nothing captured has no debug-level breadcrumb anywhere distinguishing 'gated by the whitespace-only rule' from 'capture is broken' - the only way to find out is reading source or flipping the config off and back on to compare. _Evidence: src/capture.rs:60-66._
334. **PlatformError::Empty and a genuine OS write failure are logged through the identical warn! text at both clipboard-write call sites** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - `ArboardClipboard::write` returns `Err(PlatformError::Empty)` (`crates/vbuff-platform/src/clipboard.rs:91`) when a clip's flavor set has no text flavor and no RGBA-prefixed image flavor to write - a benign 'nothing paste-able on this clip' condition, distinct in kind from `PlatformError::Clipboard(String)` (an actual OS-level set_text/set_image failure). Both `copy_latest_clip` and the `Paste` handler in src/actions.rs funnel every `Err(e)` from `cb.write(...)` through the same `tracing::warn!("...failed: {e}")` call, so the log text for 'this clip literally cannot be written to any clipboard format' and 'the OS refused the write' is indistinguishable without inspecting the Display impl's wording by eye. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-platform/src/clipboard.rs:59-91; src/actions.rs:43-47,69-73._
335. **set_pinned/set_favorite/delete return Ok(()) even when zero rows matched the given ClipId, discarding rusqlite's affected-row count** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - `Store::set_pinned`, `set_favorite`, and `delete` each call `self.conn.execute("UPDATE ..."/"DELETE ...", params![...])?` and immediately return `Ok(())`, ignoring the `usize` rows-affected value `rusqlite::Connection::execute` returns. A GUI action racing against `enforce_cap` evicting the same clip (or a double-click sending the same Delete action twice) silently reports success on a no-op UPDATE/DELETE that touched zero rows - the `Result<(), StoreError>` type gives callers no way to distinguish 'the clip was actually pinned/deleted' from 'no clip with that id existed,' unlike audit item #1 above which is about callers discarding a `Result` that would at least carry a real `StoreError` on failure; here the `Result` itself carries no such signal even when checked. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:144-168._

---

## Performance & resource use

336. **filtered() re-runs a full search+collect pass every frame the popup is open, with no change gating** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - PopupApp::filtered calls vbuff_core::search(clips, &self.query) unconditionally from update() every call, even when neither `clips` nor `query` changed since the previous frame. search() itself heap-allocates a lowercased copy of the query and, per clip, builds a fresh searchable_text() String plus another to_lowercase() over the whole haystack, then collects a Vec<SearchResult> that filtered() immediately re-collects into a second Vec<ClipId>. Because gui.rs's event loop calls ctx.request_repaint_after(100ms) unconditionally and PopupApp::update also calls ctx.request_repaint() while visible, this is two full re-allocating passes over the clip list on every repaint, not just on keystrokes. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-gui/src/app.rs fn filtered: `let results: Vec<SearchResult<'_>> = search(clips, &self.query); results.into_iter().map(|r| r.clip.id).collect()`, called unconditionally from update()'s step 3 every frame._
337. **search() allocates a fresh String per clip via searchable_text() on every non-empty-query keystroke** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - filter::search short-circuits to pinned-then-recency only when the query is empty; the instant the user types one character, every clip pays for score_clip -> searchable_text(clip), which builds a Vec<String>, pushes a full clone of primary_text() (the clip's entire text, potentially large for pasted code/log dumps), pushes the source_app clone and kind label, joins them into a new String, then lowercases that into a third allocation. For a large history with multi-KB clips this is several MB of throwaway allocation on every keystroke. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-core/src/filter.rs fn searchable_text: `let mut parts: Vec<String> = Vec::new(); ... parts.join(" ")`, and fn score_clip: `let haystack = searchable_text(clip).to_lowercase();`._
338. **clip_by_id HashMap is rebuilt from scratch every frame regardless of whether clips changed** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - PopupApp::update builds `clip_by_id: HashMap<ClipId, &Clip> = clips.iter().map(|c| (c.id, c)).collect()` unconditionally on every call, right after cloning the whole clip Vec out of the mutex. This means a fresh hash-map allocation and N insertions (with a Ulid hash cost each) every frame the popup is visible, purely to look up the handful of rows show_rows actually renders that frame. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-gui/src/app.rs update(): `let clip_by_id: HashMap<ClipId, &Clip> = clips.iter().map(|c| (c.id, c)).collect();` runs every frame with no revision-based gating, right before render_panel._
339. **live_ids HashSet<String> rebuild allocates a String per clip on every revision bump instead of using the already-Copy ClipId** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - PopupApp::update's revision-change branch builds `live_ids: HashSet<String> = clips.iter().map(|c| c.id.to_string_repr()).collect()` purely to call thumbnails.retain_only(&live_ids). ClipId::to_string_repr() heap-allocates a 26-byte Crockford base32 String per clip; since ClipId is already Copy + Hash + Eq, this could be a HashSet<ClipId> with zero string allocation. It runs only on revision change, but every capture-thread insert bumps the revision, so an active clipboard reallocates the whole set repeatedly through a session. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-gui/src/app.rs: `let live_ids: HashSet<String> = clips.iter().map(|c| c.id.to_string_repr()).collect();` feeding ThumbnailCache::retain_only, versus ClipId being Copy+Hash+Eq (crates/vbuff-types/src/lib.rs)._
340. **ThumbnailCache is keyed by String instead of the already-Copy ClipId, adding an allocation to every lookup including cache hits** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - ThumbnailCache::cache is HashMap<String, Option<TextureHandle>>, and get_or_build computes `let key = clip.id.to_string_repr();` on every call, i.e. every visible row every frame, before even checking the cache. The common case (cache hit) still pays for a fresh 26-byte String allocation and a String hash just to do the lookup. HashMap<ClipId, Option<TextureHandle>> would make the hit path allocation-free. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-gui/src/thumbnail.rs: `cache: HashMap<String, Option<egui::TextureHandle>>` and `let key = clip.id.to_string_repr();` executed unconditionally at the top of get_or_build before self.cache.get(&key)._
341. **Image thumbnails are decoded and uploaded to the GPU at full source resolution before being fit to a 40x40 draw box** `[problem]` 🟠 `[high]` - build_thumbnail decodes the encoded image with image::load_from_memory(bytes), converts to_rgba8() at native resolution, and calls ctx.load_texture with the full-size ColorImage; only later does render_row's egui::Image::from_texture(&tex).fit_to_exact_size(size) scale it down for display. A single 4K screenshot copy (3840x2160) becomes a roughly 33 MB RGBA8 GPU texture cached forever for a 40x40 on-screen thumbnail, instead of being downsampled to something like 64x64 before upload. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-gui/src/thumbnail.rs fn build_thumbnail: `let img = image::load_from_memory(bytes).ok()?; let rgba = img.to_rgba8();` builds ColorImage at (rgba.width(), rgba.height()) with no resize step; crates/vbuff-gui/src/render.rs render_row calls `.fit_to_exact_size(size)` only at draw time._
342. **Raw-RGBA thumbnail path also uploads the full captured clipboard image resolution as a GPU texture with no downscale** `[problem]` 🟠 `[high]` - The image/x-vbuff-rgba branch of build_thumbnail builds `egui::ColorImage::from_rgba_unmultiplied([w, h], &bytes[..w*h*4])` directly from the captured dimensions with no downscale, the same issue as the encoded-image path but for the raw-RGBA capture format arboard produces for a screenshot copy. A full-screen screenshot (e.g. 5120x2880 on a 5K display) becomes a roughly 59 MB texture per thumbnail. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-gui/src/thumbnail.rs: `egui::ColorImage::from_rgba_unmultiplied([w, h], &bytes[..w * h * 4])` for the image/x-vbuff-rgba branch, no resize before ctx.load_texture._
343. **PopupApp::update clones the full clip Vec out of the lock every ~100ms even while the popup window is hidden, not just while visible** `[problem]` 🟠 `[high]` - PopupApp::update takes the lock and does `s.clips.clone()` unconditionally as its very first step, before the `if !self.visible { return; }` early-out a few lines later. Because gui.rs's run_simple_native closure calls `ctx.request_repaint_after(Duration::from_millis(100))` unconditionally every frame (plus a dedicated background ticker thread that also calls ctx.request_repaint() every 100ms specifically to keep the loop alive while the window is hidden), popup.update() - and therefore this clone - runs roughly 10 times a second for the entire process lifetime, including all the time the popup is not shown at all, not merely while it is on-screen. Clip derives Clone with no Arc-wrapped bytes anywhere in Body::Inline(Vec<u8>), so this duplicates every flavor's bytes (including any inline images) on each of those background wakeups. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-gui/src/app.rs update(): `let (clips, paused, show_requested, revision) = { let mut s = self.state.lock().unwrap(); ...; (s.clips.clone(), ...) };` runs before the `if !self.visible { return; }` check; src/gui.rs: `ctx.request_repaint_after(Duration::from_millis(100));` unconditional every closure call, plus the ticker thread's own `ctx.request_repaint()` every 100ms specifically so update() keeps running while the window is hidden._
344. **content_hash_hex() builds its hex string with a per-byte format! call instead of a direct hex encoder** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - Clip::content_hash_hex loops over the 32-byte hash and calls `s.push_str(&format!("{b:02x}"))` per byte. format! goes through the full Display/fmt machinery and allocates a temporary String for every one of the 32 bytes before pushing into the pre-sized output buffer, when a lookup-table or write! into the existing String would do it with zero extra allocations. Not currently hot (grep shows no non-test caller), but it is the kind of helper that becomes hot the moment content-hash display or search-by-hash ships. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-types/src/lib.rs fn content_hash_hex: `for b in &self.content_hash { s.push_str(&format!("{b:02x}")); }` - 32 format! allocations for a 64-char output._
345. **Capture thread builds the full Clip (kind detection, byte-size sum, and metadata) before every insert, even on the common dedup-bump path where all of it is discarded** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - spawn_capture_thread always runs detect_kind(&captured.flavors) (up to three/four sequential passes over the flavor slice doing MIME string comparisons), sums byte_size across all flavors, and stamps ClipMeta::now() before calling store.insert(&clip). Store::insert's dedup branch (content_hash already exists, e.g. after a delete+re-copy of identical text) only bumps updated_at/seq in SQL and returns early - it never reads clip.kind, clip.meta.byte_size, or clip.meta itself, and never touches clip.preview(512) either, since that computation sits after the dedup early return. So on the capture thread's fairly common re-copy path, detect_kind's flavor walk and the byte_size sum are wasted work whose result is silently thrown away. _Evidence: src/capture.rs: `let kind = detect_kind(&captured.flavors); let byte_size: u64 = captured.flavors.iter().map(|f| f.body.byte_size()).sum(); let clip = Clip { ... };` computed unconditionally before store.insert(&clip); crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs Store::insert's `if let Some(id_str) = existing { ...; return ...; }` branch runs before `clip.preview(512)` and never reads kind/byte_size/meta._
346. **enforce_cap runs a full-table COUNT(*) on every single capture-thread insert cycle** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - Store::count() issues `SELECT COUNT(*) FROM clips` with no WHERE clause, and Store::enforce_cap calls count() first thing on every call. spawn_capture_thread calls store.enforce_cap(config.max_history) after every successful insert, i.e. on every distinct clipboard change detected, potentially every poll interval under active copying. SQLite can serve COUNT(*) cheaply via an index scan, but this is still an unconditional full logical scan of the clips table's primary index on every insert instead of maintaining a running counter or only checking the cap every K inserts. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs Store::count(): `self.conn.query_row("SELECT COUNT(*) FROM clips", [], ...)`; Store::enforce_cap calls `let total = self.count()?;` first; src/capture.rs calls `let _ = store.enforce_cap(config.max_history);` after every insert._
347. **load_recent(GUI_LIMIT) reloads and JSON-deserializes up to 1000 full clip rows after every single capture-thread insert** `[problem]` 🟠 `[high]` - After every new clip insert, spawn_capture_thread calls store.load_recent(GUI_LIMIT) (GUI_LIMIT = 1000, src/constants.rs), which runs Store::list -> SELECT ... FROM clips ORDER BY ... LIMIT 1000, then row::collect_clips deserializes the flavors JSON TEXT column for every one of up to 1000 rows, including any inline images. One clipboard copy triggers a full re-fetch and full-history JSON deserialization of the entire working set, then a second full Vec<Clip> move into AppState via set_clips, purely to add one new row to the front of the in-memory list. _Evidence: src/capture.rs: `let refreshed = { ...; store.load_recent(GUI_LIMIT).ok() }; if let Some(clips) = refreshed { ...; s.set_clips(clips); }`; crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs Store::list/load_recent select and JSON-decode up to `limit` full rows unconditionally rather than prepending the just-inserted clip in memory._
