348. **refresh_snapshot after Pin/Delete/ClearAll re-fetches and re-deserializes the entire GUI_LIMIT-sized history for a single-row mutation** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - actions::refresh_snapshot is called after SetPinned, Delete, and ClearAll and unconditionally does store.load_recent(GUI_LIMIT), a full up-to-1000-row SELECT plus JSON-flavor-decode round trip, to reflect a change that for Pin/Delete touched exactly one row. Deleting or pinning a single clip re-parses the JSON flavors blob (including any inline images) for up to 999 unrelated clips just to redraw the list. _Evidence: src/actions.rs fn refresh_snapshot: `if let Ok(clips) = store.load_recent(GUI_LIMIT) { shared.lock().unwrap().set_clips(clips); }`, invoked from the UiAction::SetPinned/Delete/ClearAll arms of handle_action for a single-row DB mutation._
349. **Flavor byte payloads round-trip through serde_json's per-byte number encoding on every load, not just every insert** `[problem]` 🟠 `[high]` - serde_clip::flavors_from_json calls serde_json::from_str::<Vec<Flavor>>, and because Body::Inline(Vec<u8>) has no custom (de)serializer, serde_json parses each byte as a separate JSON number token (comma, digits, whitespace) - for an inline PNG/RGBA payload this means per-byte integer parsing across potentially megabytes of image data, on every load_recent call (every capture-thread insert, and every Pin/Delete/ClearAll refresh). This is a decode-side CPU cost distinct from the already-flagged encode-side disk-bulk issue; it has not been called out on its own. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/serde_clip.rs: `pub fn flavors_from_json(json: &str) -> Result<Vec<Flavor>> { Ok(serde_json::from_str(json)?) }` with Body::Inline(Vec<u8>) using serde's default Vec<u8> impl (per-element JSON numbers), invoked once per row for every one of up to 1000 rows in every load_recent call (crates/vbuff-store/src/row.rs raw_to_clip)._
350. **Store::list's SELECT decodes the full flavors JSON blob for rows the GUI will never render beyond the visible scroll window** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - Store::list's SELECT includes the flavors column (the full JSON-encoded byte payload set) for all `limit` rows, even though the popup's ScrollArea::show_rows only renders the handful of rows currently scrolled into view. Every other clip's image bytes get deserialized into memory purely to sit in the AppState Vec, never touched until scrolled to. A lazy/paginated load (select id/preview/kind eagerly, fetch flavors on demand) would avoid materializing image bytes for off-screen history. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs Store::list SELECT includes `flavors` unconditionally for the full LIMIT; crates/vbuff-gui/src/render.rs render_panel iterates only `row_range` from `egui::ScrollArea::vertical().show_rows(ui, ROW_HEIGHT, total, ...)`, a small visible subset of `total`._
351. **search()'s sort_by comparator re-derefs clip.pinned and score through a pointer chase on every comparison instead of a precomputed key** `[improvement]` 🟢 `[low]` - vbuff_core::filter::search's `results.sort_by(|a, b| b.clip.pinned.cmp(&a.clip.pinned).then_with(|| b.score.cmp(&a.score)))` dereferences a.clip/b.clip (a pointer indirection to the original Clip) on every comparator call during the O(n log n) sort. Since `pinned` and `score` are already known per SearchResult, precomputing a (bool, i64) sort key once per element (sort_by_cached_key or a decorate-sort-undecorate pass) would turn each comparison into two integer compares with no pointer chase - worth doing since this runs on every keystroke per the filtered()/search() findings above. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-core/src/filter.rs: `results.sort_by(|a, b| b.clip.pinned.cmp(&a.clip.pinned).then_with(|| b.score.cmp(&a.score)));` dereferences `.clip` per comparison instead of sorting on a precomputed key._
352. **is_url lowercases the entire input string just to check a handful of fixed-length scheme prefixes** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - classify::is_url does `let lower = s.to_ascii_lowercase();` unconditionally, even though the scheme prefixes are all ASCII and a case-insensitive prefix check (eq_ignore_ascii_case per candidate scheme) would avoid allocating. is_url is called from detect_text_kind on every captured clip's primary text in the capture thread's hot path, so a large pasted document classified as plain text gets fully lowercased just to check 4-8 byte scheme prefixes at the start. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-core/src/classify.rs fn is_url: `let lower = s.to_ascii_lowercase(); ... if SCHEMES.iter().any(|p| lower.starts_with(p))`, invoked from detect_text_kind on every capture via detect_kind._
353. **looks_like_code always materializes a Vec<&str> of every line before checking the strong-token short-circuit that alone would resolve most inputs** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - classify::looks_like_code immediately does `let lines: Vec<&str> = s.lines().collect();` before checking has_strong, a substring scan that alone would settle most cases. This materializes a full line-index Vec for potentially large multi-KB/MB text clips (a pasted log file or config) even when `if has_strong { return true; }` on the next few lines would make the line Vec unnecessary. Checking has_strong first, and only collecting lines if that is inconclusive, would skip the allocation on the common path. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-core/src/classify.rs fn looks_like_code: `let lines: Vec<&str> = s.lines().collect();` built before `has_strong` is checked, even though the very next `if has_strong { return true; }` can already resolve the call without the Vec._
354. **filtered() discards the &Clip and score that search() already computed, forcing render_panel to re-look them up through a second freshly built HashMap** `[improvement]` 🟢 `[low]` - filtered() does `search(clips, &self.query).into_iter().map(|r| r.clip.id).collect()`, throwing away the score field and the &Clip borrow vbuff_core::search computed, and render_panel then immediately looks the id back up via clip_by_id (a separate HashMap built fresh every frame, see the clip_by_id finding above). A search() variant, or a SearchResult-returning path threaded straight into rendering, would avoid the round-trip of borrow -> id -> re-lookup through a freshly built map every frame. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-gui/src/app.rs fn filtered: `results.into_iter().map(|r| r.clip.id).collect()` discards `r.clip`/`r.score`; crates/vbuff-gui/src/render.rs render_panel's `clip_by_id.get(id)` re-fetches the same &Clip via a separate HashMap built in app.rs update()._
355. **AppState::set_clips replaces the whole Vec<Clip> on every capture-thread insert instead of prepending in place** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - AppState::set_clips does `self.clips = clips;`, a full move-assignment of a freshly loaded up-to-1000-item Vec<Clip> over the old one, on every capture-thread poll that inserts a new clip. This drops the previous Vec's allocation (and the up-to-999 unrelated clips' Body::Inline byte buffers, deallocated) and takes ownership of the newly loaded, freshly JSON-decoded one. Since only one clip actually changed (floated to the front), this discards and reallocates hundreds of unrelated clips' worth of Flavor/Vec<u8> heap storage on every single new clip captured, rather than mutating the existing Vec in place. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-gui/src/state.rs fn set_clips: `pub fn set_clips(&mut self, clips: Vec<Clip>) { self.clips = clips; self.revision = self.revision.wrapping_add(1); }`, called with the full store.load_recent(GUI_LIMIT) result on every capture (src/capture.rs) instead of an in-place prepend._
356. **ClipId::to_string_repr() is used as an in-memory lookup key in several GUI-side hot paths where a Copy ClipId would do** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - DB-boundary call sites (Store::insert/set_pinned/set_favorite/delete's params![id.to_string_repr()], row::raw_to_clip's ClipId::parse) need the string form for SQLite parameter binding, but the GUI-side uses (ThumbnailCache's cache key, live_ids's HashSet<String>, per the findings above) needlessly repeat the same string conversion in-process, where ClipId's existing Copy+Hash+Eq impl would do. Consolidating the DB-boundary string conversion away from in-memory GUI code paths would remove several of the allocations flagged above at their root cause. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-types/src/lib.rs `pub fn to_string_repr(&self) -> String { self.0.to_string() }` called from crates/vbuff-gui/src/app.rs (live_ids) and crates/vbuff-gui/src/thumbnail.rs (cache key) alike, with no Copy-based fast path for those in-memory-only call sites._
357. **detect_kind walks the flavors slice in three or four separate sequential passes instead of a single classifying loop** `[improvement]` 🟢 `[low]` - classify::detect_kind does three sequential `for f in flavors` loops (image check, file-mime check, then a find_map for the plain-text flavor) plus a fourth conditional loop for html/rtf. For a clip with today's 1-2 flavors this is negligible, but architecture.md's target design captures 'all flavors of a single copy atomically' (multiple simultaneous flavors per copy per audit item #14); once capture fidelity improves, this function will scan a larger flavor set 3-4x instead of classifying in one early-exit pass. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-core/src/classify.rs fn detect_kind: three/four sequential `for f in flavors` / `.find_map` passes over the same slice rather than a single classifying loop._
358. **content_hash_from_flavors clones every flavor's mime and bytes into an owned Vec before hashing, instead of borrowing directly from the input slice** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - hash::content_hash_from_flavors builds `owned: Vec<(String, Vec<u8>)>` by doing `Body::Inline(b) => b.clone()` and `f.mime.clone()` for every flavor, then builds a second Vec<CanonicalFlavor> borrowing from `owned`, before finally hashing. This is a full duplicate copy of every inline flavor's bytes (including image payloads) purely to satisfy CanonicalFlavor<'a>'s borrow lifetime, when CanonicalFlavor references could be constructed directly against `flavors`'s existing Body::Inline slices without the intermediate owned Vec clone. This runs on every capture-thread poll that detects a change. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-core/src/hash.rs fn content_hash_from_flavors: `let bytes = match &f.body { Body::Inline(b) => b.clone(), ... }; owned.push((f.mime.clone(), bytes));` clones both mime and bytes before hashing, called from src/capture.rs on every poll with new content._
359. **Capture thread hashes the full flavor bytes on every poll tick even when clipboard content is unchanged, instead of gating on a cheap OS change counter** `[idea]` 🟡 `[medium]` - spawn_capture_thread reads the clipboard, then unconditionally computes content_hash_from_flavors(&captured.flavors) (a BLAKE3 hash over every byte of every flavor, including images) on every poll tick, then compares against last_hash to decide if anything changed - meaning a multi-MB image sitting unchanged on the clipboard gets fully re-hashed every poll_interval_ms (sub-second by default) for as long as it remains there, purely to conclude 'nothing changed.' macOS exposes NSPasteboard.changeCount (an integer bumped only on actual writes) and Windows/X11 have analogous sequence numbers; gating the read+hash behind a cheap change-counter check would skip the hash entirely on the common no-op poll. _Evidence: src/capture.rs: `let captured = match clipboard.read() { ... }; let hash = content_hash_from_flavors(&captured.flavors); if last_hash == Some(hash) { continue; }` re-reads and re-hashes full flavor bytes every `interval` tick regardless of whether the clipboard changed, with no cheaper pre-check._
360. **ThumbnailCache::get_or_build clones the Option<TextureHandle> on every cache hit, re-fetched every frame for every visible thumbnail row** `[improvement]` 🟢 `[low]` - get_or_build does `if let Some(cached) = self.cache.get(&key) { return cached.clone(); }`. TextureHandle's clone is Arc-backed and cheap by itself, but combined with the String key allocation flagged above, every visible thumbnail row pays for a String allocation plus hash-map lookup plus Option clone on every single frame just to fetch an already-cached handle, when the handle could be resolved once per revision bump and cached directly in row-render state instead of re-queried every frame. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-gui/src/thumbnail.rs: `if let Some(cached) = self.cache.get(&key) { return cached.clone(); }` executed for every visible image row on every frame from render_row's `self.thumbnails.get_or_build(ctx, clip)` call._
361. **egui::TextureOptions::LINEAR with no mipmap generation forces full-resolution GPU sampling for a tiny draw target** `[idea]` 🟢 `[low]` - build_thumbnail always loads textures with egui::TextureOptions::LINEAR (bilinear, no mipmaps). Combined with the full-resolution-upload issue flagged above, drawing a large source texture at a tiny 40x40 destination size with only bilinear (not trilinear/mipmapped) filtering means the GPU samples from the full-resolution mip level every frame the row is visible - both a bandwidth and an aliasing-quality cost that pre-downscaling would also fix as a side effect. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-gui/src/thumbnail.rs: `ctx.load_texture(key, color_image, egui::TextureOptions::LINEAR)` with color_image built at full source resolution, not the eventual THUMBNAIL_SIZE=40.0 (crates/vbuff-gui/src/theme.rs) draw size._
362. **Store::list's three-column ORDER BY has no covering index, forcing SQLite to sort in memory on every load** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - The schema defines `idx_clips_updated ON clips(updated_at DESC, seq DESC)` and a separate partial `idx_clips_pinned ON clips(updated_at DESC) WHERE pinned = 1`, but Store::list's actual query orders by `pinned DESC, updated_at DESC, seq DESC`. No single index covers `pinned` as its leading column together with `updated_at`/`seq`, so SQLite's planner cannot satisfy the full ORDER BY from an index scan alone and must materialize and sort, on every load_recent call, i.e. every capture-thread insert and every Pin/Delete/ClearAll refresh. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/schema.rs: `CREATE INDEX idx_clips_updated ON clips(updated_at DESC, seq DESC); CREATE INDEX idx_clips_pinned ON clips(updated_at DESC) WHERE pinned = 1;` versus crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs Store::list's `ORDER BY pinned DESC, updated_at DESC, seq DESC` - no index has `pinned` as a leading non-partial column alongside updated_at/seq._
363. **UiAction::Paste's handler does an O(n) linear scan plus a full Clip clone even though the popup already had the exact &Clip in hand at click time** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - UiAction::Paste's handler does `s.clips.iter().find(|c| c.id == id).cloned()`, an O(n) scan over the full clip Vec plus a full deep-clone of the matched Clip (including any inline image bytes) just to get its flavors for a clipboard write, when render_row already had the exact &Clip reference at the moment the user clicked or pressed Enter. Threading the clip's flavors (or a cheap Arc<Clip>) through the UiAction::Paste payload instead of re-deriving it via a linear scan and clone would remove both costs. _Evidence: src/actions.rs UiAction::Paste arm: `let clip = { let s = shared.lock().unwrap(); s.clips.iter().find(|c| c.id == id).cloned() };` O(n) find plus full Clip clone (including Vec<u8> image bytes), triggered from a UI action that already had the &Clip reference at click time (crates/vbuff-gui/src/render.rs render_row)._
364. **copy_latest_clip clones the entire first Clip out of shared state just to reach its .flavors field** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - copy_latest_clip (tray-only) does `s.clips.first().cloned()`, cloning the entire first Clip (id, meta, all flavor bytes) just to pass `&clip.flavors` to ArboardClipboard::write a few lines later. For a large pinned or most-recent image clip this duplicates the image bytes in memory for the duration of the call for no reason beyond satisfying the borrow checker across the lock scope; cloning only `clip.flavors` (or writing before releasing the lock) would avoid duplicating the id/meta and any bytes not actually needed. _Evidence: src/actions.rs fn copy_latest_clip: `let clip = { let s = shared.lock().unwrap(); s.clips.first().cloned() }; ... cb.write(&clip.flavors)` clones the whole Clip (all fields) to use only the `.flavors` field._
365. **eviction::evict fully sorts every unprotected candidate even when overflow is tiny relative to the candidate pool** `[improvement]` 🟢 `[low]` - vbuff_core::eviction::evict collects all unprotected clips into `candidates: Vec<&Clip>` and fully sorts them by updated_at, then only ever consumes the first `overflow` entries. When overflow is small relative to the candidate pool (evicting 1-2 clips out of a near-full unprotected pool because the cap was just exceeded by one new insert), an O(n log n) full sort does far more comparison work than a partial selection (select_nth_unstable_by or a size-`overflow` min-heap) needs. Currently unreachable from the shipped binary (main.rs calls Store::enforce_cap's SQL version instead, per the existing audit's item #24), but the pure function itself is what unit tests exercise and would become the hot path if the binary is ever switched over to it. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-core/src/eviction.rs fn evict: `let mut candidates: Vec<&Clip> = clips.iter().filter(|c| !is_protected(c)).collect(); candidates.sort_by_key(|a| a.meta.updated_at);` full sort of the whole unprotected pool regardless of how small `overflow` is._
366. **enforce_cap's DELETE subquery filters pinned/favorite outside any index, preventing a fully covering-index scan straight to the oldest unprotected rows** `[improvement]` 🟢 `[low]` - enforce_cap's DELETE statement uses `WHERE id IN (SELECT id FROM clips WHERE pinned=0 AND favorite=0 ORDER BY updated_at ASC, seq ASC LIMIT ?1)`. SQLite can use idx_clips_updated to avoid a full sort here, but the `pinned=0 AND favorite=0` filter is not part of that index, so the planner must still filter every unprotected row via the index scan rather than jumping straight to the oldest `overflow` unprotected rows. A composite index on (pinned, favorite, updated_at) would let this query use a fully covering index instead. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs Store::enforce_cap SQL: `SELECT id FROM clips WHERE pinned = 0 AND favorite = 0 ORDER BY updated_at ASC, seq ASC LIMIT ?1` against crates/vbuff-store/src/schema.rs indexes, none of which lead with (pinned, favorite)._
367. **render_row builds and joins a Vec<String> meta line from scratch for every visible row on every frame instead of a reused buffer** `[improvement]` 🟢 `[low]` - render_row builds `let mut meta = vec![clip.meta.kind.label().to_string()];`, allocating a Vec<String> and an owned copy of a &'static str, then conditionally pushes short_app_name(app) and relative_time(...) (each their own allocation), and finally `meta.join(" · ")` allocates a fourth String - all repeated for every visible row on every frame, since the popup keeps repainting. None of these need to be owned Strings up front; the meta line could be written directly into one reused String buffer instead of a Vec<String> that is immediately joined and discarded. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-gui/src/render.rs render_row: `let mut meta = vec![clip.meta.kind.label().to_string()]; if let Some(app) = &clip.meta.source_app { meta.push(short_app_name(app)); } meta.push(relative_time(clip.meta.updated_at, Utc::now())); ui.small(meta.join(" · "));` - four-plus String allocations per visible row per frame for mostly static or short-lived display text._
368. **relative_time() and short_app_name() are recomputed from scratch every frame for every visible row instead of being cached per clip** `[improvement]` 🟢 `[low]` - Because render_row runs every frame for the visible rows, relative_time(clip.meta.updated_at, Utc::now()) and short_app_name(app), each allocating a String, are recomputed on every repaint even though relative_time's bucketed output ('3m', '2h', etc.) only changes at most once a minute and short_app_name's output never changes for a given clip at all. Caching short_app_name's result in ClipMeta (or a per-row cache keyed by clip id) and only recomputing relative_time on a coarser cadence would cut most of this allocation. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-gui/src/view.rs relative_time/short_app_name both allocate (format!/to_string), called unconditionally from crates/vbuff-gui/src/render.rs render_row on every frame the row is visible, with no memoization._
369. **render_row recomputes clip.preview(80) every frame for every visible row instead of caching the truncated text** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - render_row calls `let preview = clip.preview(80);` every frame for every visible row. Clip::preview does `text.split_whitespace().collect::<Vec<_>>().join(" ")` (allocating a Vec<&str> and a new String) followed by truncate_chars's own `.chars().count()` plus potential `.take().collect()` - a non-trivial string-processing pass over the full clip text, repeated every frame for every visible row, when the store already caches an analogous 512-char preview column in SQLite that could instead be precomputed once per clip and cached on the in-memory Clip or a side table. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-gui/src/render.rs render_row: `let preview = clip.preview(80);` every frame; crates/vbuff-types/src/lib.rs Clip::preview: `text.split_whitespace().collect::<Vec<_>>().join(" ")` then truncate_chars, re-run from scratch every frame with no caching despite being pure over immutable clip data._
370. **Every render_row call rebuilds the quick-pick badge string even for rows past QUICK_PICK_SLOTS where it renders as empty** `[improvement]` 🟢 `[low]` - render_row computes `let badge = if row < QUICK_PICK_SLOTS { (row + 1).to_string() } else { String::new() };` for every visible row on every frame. For the badge digits (1-9), `.to_string()` allocates a fresh single-character String each frame purely to hand it to `RichText::new(badge)`, when the badge set is fixed per QUICK_PICK_SLOTS and could be precomputed once into a small static/lazy array of &'static str (or written into a small stack buffer) instead of re-formatted every repaint for every one of the first QUICK_PICK_SLOTS rows. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-gui/src/render.rs render_row: `let badge = if row < QUICK_PICK_SLOTS { (row + 1).to_string() } else { String::new() }; ui.add_sized(..., egui::Label::new(RichText::new(badge)...))` recomputed every frame for every visible row._

---

## Testing & CI gaps

371. **No CI workflow exists anywhere, so nothing enforces cargo fmt/clippy/test on PRs beyond README prose** `[problem]` 🟠 `[high]` - There is no `.github/workflows/` directory, no `.gitlab-ci.yml`, no `Makefile`, and no other CI config file anywhere in the repository root or subdirectories. README's 'before opening a pull request' checklist (fmt/clippy/test) is unenforced guidance; a contributor can push code that fails to build, is unformatted, or has failing tests and nothing blocks it. This is distinct from item #36 in code-audit-top-50.md (which only notes the absence) in that it also has no cross-platform matrix, meaning even if a workflow were added tomorrow, Windows/Linux-specific compile breakage (e.g. the platform `#[cfg]` branches in `crates/vbuff-store/src/paths.rs` or `src/config.rs`) would still ship undetected on macOS-only CI. _Evidence: `find . -iname "*.yml" -o -iname "*.yaml"` (excluding target/) returns zero matches; `find . -iname "ci*"` likewise returns nothing anywhere in the repo._
372. **The three platform-specific branches of `vbuff-store::paths::dirs_data_dir` can only ever compile-test one arm per CI runner, and have zero tests today regardless** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - `dirs_data_dir()` in `crates/vbuff-store/src/paths.rs` has `#[cfg(target_os = "macos")]`, `#[cfg(target_os = "windows")]`, and `#[cfg(all(unix, not(target_os = "macos")))]` arms that resolve the database directory differently (Application Support vs APPDATA vs XDG_DATA_HOME/.local/share). None of the three arms has a single test today; even a `#[test]` guarded by the same `#[cfg]` verifying the join of `HOME`/`XDG_DATA_HOME`/`APPDATA` env vars into the expected path would catch a typo in the `.join("vbuff").join("history.db")` chain in `default_db_path`, but no such test exists for any arm. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/paths.rs (41-line file): lines 18-36 hold the three cfg-gated branches inside `dirs_data_dir`; `grep -n "cfg(test)" crates/vbuff-store/src/paths.rs` returns nothing._
373. **The capture-gate rules (whitespace-skip, exclusion, hash-dedup) are inlined in the poll-loop closure, so they cannot be unit tested at all** `[problem]` 🟠 `[high]` - `spawn_capture_thread` in src/capture.rs hardcodes the whitespace-skip check, the `config.is_excluded` check, and the `last_hash == Some(hash)` dedup comparison directly inside the `loop { ... }` block that also does the real clipboard I/O and store I/O. There is no extracted pure function like `fn should_capture(captured: &CapturedClipboard, last_hash: Option<[u8;32]>, config: &Config) -> CaptureDecision` that a `#[test]` could call without spinning a thread, opening a real clipboard, or touching a Mutex. Every one of these gating rules is therefore only exercised by manually copying things while running the full binary. _Evidence: src/capture.rs: the hash-dedup comparison is at lines 54-57, the whitespace-only skip at lines 60-66, and the exclusion check at lines 67-72, all directly inside the `loop` body of `spawn_capture_thread`; `grep -n "cfg(test)" src/capture.rs` returns nothing._
374. **`src/actions.rs`'s `handle_action` dispatcher has zero tests despite being the sole translator from every GUI action to a store/clipboard side effect** `[problem]` 🟠 `[high]` - `handle_action` in src/actions.rs (lines 51-105) is the single chokepoint through which `UiAction::Paste/SetPinned/Delete/ClearAll/TogglePause/Hide` become store mutations, clipboard writes, and paste scheduling. None of its six match arms is covered by a test; a regression that, say, swapped the `Delete`/`ClearAll` bodies, or stopped calling `refresh_snapshot` after `SetPinned`, would only surface as a UI bug report. Because `Store::open_in_memory()` already exists and `SharedState`/`AppState` are plain `Arc<Mutex<..>>` wrappers, this dispatcher is straightforward to test headlessly (accept that `ArboardClipboard::new()` will typically fail/no-op in a headless test sandbox and assert on the store/state side effects instead) but nothing does so today. _Evidence: src/actions.rs lines 51-105 (`handle_action`); `grep -n "cfg(test)" src/actions.rs` returns nothing, and no other file references `handle_action` from a test context._
375. **`Config::is_excluded`'s only test never runs on Windows/Linux CI because there is no CI, so its cross-platform casefold assumption is unverified** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - `is_excluded` in src/config.rs asserts case-insensitive substring matching via `str::to_lowercase()`, which is locale-independent for ASCII app identifiers but subtly wrong for non-ASCII bundle ids/exe names containing e.g. Turkish 'İ' (Rust's `to_lowercase` is Unicode-aware, not the simple ASCII fold a reader would assume from the doc comment). No test exercises a non-ASCII source-app string, and because there is no CI matrix at all (see the CI-absence item), this was never going to be caught by a platform difference either. _Evidence: src/config.rs line 84 (`let lower = source_app.to_lowercase();` inside `is_excluded`, not `to_ascii_lowercase`); the only test, `exclusion_matches_substring` (lines 111-121), uses exclusively ASCII strings._
376. **`combo_to_hotkey`'s modifier-bitflag mapping has zero direct tests** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - `hotkey.rs` unit-tests `parse_combo` (string-to-`KeyCombo`) and `key_to_code`, but never calls `combo_to_hotkey` itself, which is the function that actually maps `&[Modifier]` into `global_hotkey::hotkey::Modifiers` bitflags via the `mods |= match m {...}` loop. A bug that mapped `Modifier::Alt` to `Modifiers::SHIFT` (an easy copy-paste error in that four-arm match) would pass every existing test since none inspects the resulting `Modifiers` value, only the pre-conversion `KeyCombo`. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-platform/src/hotkey.rs lines 56-69 (`combo_to_hotkey`) is never referenced by name in the `#[cfg(test)] mod tests` block at lines 149-179, which only calls `parse_combo` and `key_to_code`._
377. **`ThumbnailCache::get_or_build`/`build_thumbnail` RGBA boundary conditions have no tests** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - `build_thumbnail` in crates/vbuff-gui/src/thumbnail.rs has explicit bounds-checking logic (`if w == 0 || h == 0 || bytes.len() < w * h * 4 { return None; }`) guarding a raw slice index `&bytes[..w * h * 4]` that would panic on an underflow/overflow if the guard were ever weakened, plus a separate PNG/JPEG/BMP decode path via `image::load_from_memory`. Neither path is exercised by any test: no test constructs a `Flavor` with an `image/x-vbuff-rgba` mime whose declared dimensions exceed its byte buffer (the exact case the guard exists for), and no test feeds a truncated/corrupt PNG through the `image::load_from_memory(bytes).ok()?` fallback. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-gui/src/thumbnail.rs lines 50-70 (`build_thumbnail`); `grep -n "cfg(test)" crates/vbuff-gui/src/thumbnail.rs` returns nothing._
378. **`PopupApp`'s selection-clamping and focus-loss-hide state machine in app.rs has no tests despite being pure enough to drive with a fake `SharedState`** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - `PopupApp::update` contains non-trivial state transitions - resetting `selected` to 0 on revision change and pruning thumbnails (lines 121-126), the 250ms focus-loss grace period before auto-hiding (lines 133-143), and clamping `selected` to `total - 1` when the filtered list shrinks (lines 148-152) - all guarded only by manual testing. Because `PopupApp::new` takes a plain `SharedState` and the selection-clamp math does not require an egui frame to evaluate on its own, at minimum that clamp logic could be extracted and unit tested; today it cannot be tested at all short of a full eframe harness. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-gui/src/app.rs (169-line file) lines 121-152 inside `PopupApp::update`; `grep -n "cfg(test)" crates/vbuff-gui/src/app.rs` returns nothing._
379. **`handle_keys`'s arrow-navigation and quick-pick dispatch in input.rs is untested** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - `handle_keys` computes `self.selected = (self.selected + 1).min(total - 1)` for ArrowDown and `self.selected.saturating_sub(1)` for ArrowUp, and separately maps `Cmd/Ctrl+1..9` to `UiAction::Paste(filtered[n])` via a `QUICK_PICK_KEYS` array. Off-by-one errors here (e.g. quick-pick key Num1 mapping to `filtered[1]` instead of `filtered[0]`) would silently paste the wrong clip and are exactly the kind of bug arrow-key/number-key tests exist to catch, but egui's `ctx.input(|i| ...)` closure makes this function require a live `egui::Context` and cannot currently be called from a plain `#[test]` without constructing one via `egui::Context::default()` and feeding synthetic `RawInput` - which nothing in the repo does. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-gui/src/input.rs lines 15-55 (`handle_keys`); `grep -n "cfg(test)" crates/vbuff-gui/src/input.rs` returns nothing, and no other file in vbuff-gui constructs an `egui::Context` for headless input simulation._
380. **No test drives `PopupApp` through a full show -> type-to-filter -> select -> paste cycle end-to-end within the GUI crate** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - Every existing vbuff-gui test (color.rs, view.rs) tests a leaf pure function in isolation. There is no integration-style test inside vbuff-gui itself that constructs a `SharedState` with seeded clips, calls `PopupApp::new`, drives `update()` across a couple of synthetic frames via egui's offline `Context::run`, and asserts the resulting `take_actions()` queue matches what a user's keypresses should have produced. Because `eframe::App::update` is the one integration point where `input.rs`, `render.rs`, `thumbnail.rs`, and `state.rs` all compose, a bug in how they interact (e.g. `take_actions` draining before `render_panel` pushes its own click-triggered actions) would not be caught by any of the current leaf-function tests. _Evidence: grep across crates/vbuff-gui/src/*.rs for `Context::run` or `egui::Context::default()` returns no matches; the only `#[cfg(test)]` blocks in vbuff-gui are in color.rs (parse_hex_color) and view.rs (relative_time/short_app_name), both pure-function-only._
381. **`vbuff-store::row::raw_to_clip`'s corruption-detection branches (`StoreError::Corrupt`) are never exercised by a test** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - `raw_to_clip` returns `StoreError::Corrupt("bad ulid in db")` when `ClipId::parse` fails and `StoreError::Corrupt("content_hash not 32 bytes")` when the stored BLOB isn't exactly 32 bytes. Both branches exist specifically to handle a hand-edited or externally-corrupted database file, which is a realistic failure mode for a SQLite file a user might poke at with a DB browser, yet no test ever constructs a `RawRow` with a malformed `id` string or a `content_hash` of the wrong length to confirm the error (rather than a panic or silent misread) is what actually happens. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/row.rs lines 40 and 46 (`StoreError::Corrupt` construction sites in `raw_to_clip`); no test file in vbuff-store references `raw_to_clip` directly or seeds a corrupt row._
382. **`Store::from_connection`'s three `pragma_update` calls (WAL, synchronous, foreign_keys) are asserted nowhere** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - `from_connection` (crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs lines 58-64) sets `journal_mode=WAL`, `synchronous=NORMAL`, and `foreign_keys=ON` before running migrations. Only the WAL setting is indirectly checked (`wal_files_are_created` in the integration test asserts a `-wal` sidecar file exists), but nothing asserts `PRAGMA synchronous` or `PRAGMA foreign_keys` actually took effect - a regression that dropped the `synchronous` pragma (silently reverting to SQLite's slower default, or the reverse: accidentally setting `OFF` and risking corruption on crash) would pass every existing test. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs lines 58-64 (`from_connection`); crates/vbuff-store/tests/integration.rs's `wal_files_are_created` (lines 74-83) only checks the WAL file's existence via `dir.path().join("history.db-wal")`, never queries back `PRAGMA synchronous` or `PRAGMA foreign_keys`._
383. **`schema::migrate`'s idempotency (calling it twice, or opening a DB already at `user_version = 1`) is never tested** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - `migrate` reads `PRAGMA user_version` and only runs the `CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS` batch `if version < 1`. This is the exact code path exercised every time an existing user upgrades vbuff and reopens their history.db, but the test suite only ever opens fresh in-memory or fresh temp-file databases (`Store::open_in_memory()`, `tempfile::tempdir()`), so `migrate` always runs its `version < 1` branch for the first time. No test opens a `Store`, closes it, and reopens the same path a second time to confirm `migrate` is a no-op (and does not error) the second time around, and no test pre-sets `user_version` to a future/unknown value (e.g. 2) to confirm the store fails predictably rather than silently misreading a newer schema. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/schema.rs lines 16-43 (`migrate`, `SCHEMA_VERSION: i64 = 1` at line 13); crates/vbuff-store/tests/integration.rs's `persists_across_reopen` (lines 27-44) reopens the store but never asserts anything about `migrate`'s behavior or `PRAGMA user_version` specifically, and no test sets `user_version` to a non-zero/non-one value before opening._
384. **No migration forward-compat test exists for a hypothetical `SCHEMA_VERSION` bump, so the very first real migration this project writes will be untested by construction** `[idea]` 🟡 `[medium]` - Add a test fixture (a checked-in, versioned `.db` file, or a SQL script building one) representing a `user_version = 1` database with a handful of rows, and a test that opens it through `Store::open` after bumping `SCHEMA_VERSION` to 2 with a real `ALTER TABLE`/data-migration step, asserting old rows survive and new columns get sane defaults. Because `schema::migrate` is currently a single `if version < 1` block, there is no established pattern in the codebase for writing the *next* migration safely (e.g. whether to chain `if version < 2 { ... }` after the existing block, and whether that chain is itself tested) - this should be decided and demonstrated with a real test before the first schema change ships, not after. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/schema.rs's `migrate` function is single-version (`SCHEMA_VERSION: i64 = 1` at line 13, one `if version < 1` branch); no `docs/` file (the repo's docs/ directory holds only code-audit-top-50.md, ideas-top-300.md, mistakes-top-500.md, and similar) or test establishes what a second migration step should look like._
385. **vbuff-core has zero property-based tests despite owning the pure hash/eviction/search/classify logic that is the most natural fit for them in the whole workspace** `[idea]` 🟡 `[medium]` - Add `proptest` as a vbuff-core dev-dependency and write properties like: `content_hash_from_flavors` is invariant under any permutation of the input flavor slice (currently only spot-checked with a 2-element fixed case in `flavor_order_does_not_matter`); `evict` (crates/vbuff-core/src/eviction.rs) never returns an id belonging to a pinned clip for any randomly generated `Vec<Clip>`/`EvictionPolicy` pair (currently only 5 hand-picked scenarios: `under_cap_evicts_nothing`, `evicts_oldest_first`, `never_evicts_pinned`, `all_pinned_evicts_nothing`, and the recency-bump test); and `search`'s output is always a subset of its input clip ids for any query string, with pinned clips always sorted before unpinned ones regardless of score (the sort comparator in `filter.rs`'s `search` does `b.clip.pinned.cmp(&a.clip.pinned).then_with(...)`). These are exactly the kind of invariants proptest shrinking is good at finding minimal counterexamples for, and vbuff-core's total lack of I/O dependencies makes it the cheapest place in the workspace to add this. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-core/Cargo.toml dev-dependencies list only `ulid` and `chrono` (no `proptest`/`quickcheck`); workspace-wide grep for `proptest`/`quickcheck` across the root and all five crates' Cargo.toml files returns no matches._
386. **No fuzz target exists for `flavors_from_json`, the one function that deserializes attacker-adjacent bytes (a hand-edited SQLite row) into a live `Vec<Flavor>`** `[idea]` 🟡 `[medium]` - Set up a `cargo-fuzz` target (or a `proptest`-driven arbitrary-bytes harness) feeding random/mutated byte strings into `serde_clip::flavors_from_json`, asserting it only ever returns `Ok` or a `StoreError` variant, never panics. This is the store's only JSON deserialization entry point and the one place vbuff parses bytes it did not itself just serialize (a user could hand-edit history.db's `flavors` TEXT column with a SQLite browser, or a future sync feature could pull rows from another device), yet the only test is a same-process roundtrip that can never exercise malformed input. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/serde_clip.rs's only test, `roundtrip` (lines 27-36), calls `flavors_to_json` then `flavors_from_json` on its own output; there is no `fuzz/` directory anywhere in the repository and no dependency on `cargo-fuzz`/`arbitrary` in any Cargo.toml._
387. **No golden-vector test fixes the on-disk JSON shape of a serialized `Flavor`/`Clip`, so a serde attribute change could silently break every existing user's history.db without any test failing** `[idea]` 🟠 `[high]` - Add a small set of checked-in JSON fixture files (e.g. `crates/vbuff-store/tests/fixtures/flavor_v1.json`) captured from the current `Body`/`Flavor` serde output, and a test that deserializes each fixture and asserts specific field values. Today, `serde_clip`'s only test round-trips through the crate's own current serializer, so if someone renamed a `Flavor` field, changed `Body`'s enum representation, or reordered enum variants in a way that shifts the untagged default representation, that same-process roundtrip test would still pass even though every real user's `history.db` `flavors` column would fail to deserialize on the next launch. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/serde_clip.rs lines 27-36 (the only test round-trips through its own serializer); `vbuff_types::Body` (line 132) and `Flavor` (line 171) derive plain `Serialize, Deserialize` with no explicit `#[serde(...)]` stability attributes, so their wire format is whatever serde's default derive currently produces, unpinned by any fixture._
388. **No benchmark or perf-regression test exists for `Store::insert`/`enforce_cap`/`load_recent` despite the capture thread running them on every single clipboard poll** `[idea]` 🟡 `[medium]` - Add a `benches/` directory (Criterion or a simple timed harness run manually or in future CI on a fixed runner) that measures `Store::insert` + `enforce_cap` + `load_recent(GUI_LIMIT)` latency against a pre-seeded database of, say, 500/1000/5000 clips, matching the real `GUI_LIMIT` (1000, src/constants.rs) and `config.max_history` (default 500, src/config.rs) values. `spawn_capture_thread` in src/capture.rs runs this exact insert -> enforce_cap -> load_recent sequence synchronously on every poll tick (default 300ms interval); a query-plan regression (e.g. a future migration dropping the `idx_clips_updated` index) would silently make every poll tick slower with nothing in the test suite ever measuring it, only a user noticing CPU/latency creep after the fact. _Evidence: src/capture.rs lines 88-96 (the `store.insert` -> `enforce_cap` -> `load_recent(GUI_LIMIT)` sequence run on every poll); no `benches/` directory exists anywhere in the workspace and no `criterion` dependency exists in any Cargo.toml._
389. **No cross-crate integration test exercises the actual capture-to-render pipeline (vbuff-platform capture -> vbuff-core classify/hash -> vbuff-store insert -> vbuff-gui search/render) as one flow** `[idea]` 🟠 `[high]` - The only integration-style test in the workspace, crates/vbuff-store/tests/integration.rs, is scoped to `Store` in isolation: its `make_clip` helper constructs a `Clip` literal directly rather than going through `vbuff_platform::CapturedClipboard` + `vbuff_core::detect_kind` the way src/capture.rs actually builds one on every real poll. Add a workspace-level integration test (e.g. a new `tests/` directory at the repo root, or in a currently-nonexistent `vbuff-app` lib target extracted from `src/`) that takes a `CapturedClipboard` literal, runs it through the same `detect_kind` -> `content_hash_from_flavors` -> `Clip` construction -> `Store::insert` -> `vbuff_core::search` chain `spawn_capture_thread` and `PopupApp` use, and asserts the final searchable/rendered state - this is the only way to catch a mismatch at any of those module boundaries (e.g. a `ContentKind::Color` clip never being searchable because `searchable_text` in filter.rs doesn't special-case swatch clips). _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/tests/integration.rs's `make_clip` helper (lines 7-25) constructs a `Clip` directly rather than going through `CapturedClipboard`/`detect_kind`; grepping the whole workspace for `CapturedClipboard` or `detect_kind` shows neither is ever referenced from any `tests/` file, only from crates/vbuff-platform/src/*.rs and crates/vbuff-core/src/classify.rs's own unit tests._
390. **`main.rs`'s startup wiring (`main()` itself) has no smoke test verifying it doesn't panic on a fresh machine with no prior config/store** `[idea]` 🟢 `[low]` - There is no test - not even an ignored one requiring manual invocation - that runs `Config::load_or_create()` followed by `Store::open_default()` against a temp `HOME`/`XDG_CONFIG_HOME`/`XDG_DATA_HOME` to confirm first-run works end-to-end without a pre-existing config.toml or history.db. Because both `load_or_create` and `open_default` create their parent directories and default files on demand, this is testable by setting env vars to a `tempdir()` before calling them, but nothing in the repo does so; a change that broke first-run (e.g. `config_path()`'s `dirs::config_dir()` call failing silently in a way that isn't surfaced until a user actually installs the app fresh) would not be caught pre-release. _Evidence: src/config.rs's `load_or_create` (lines 58-69) and `config_path` (lines 92-96) call `dirs::config_dir()` directly with no test seam to redirect it; src/main.rs's `main()` (lines 44-91) is entirely untested and has no `#[cfg(test)]` block anywhere in the file._
391. **No test verifies `list`/`load_recent` behavior against a truly empty (zero-row, just-created) store, the exact state every new user starts in** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - `store.load_recent(GUI_LIMIT)` is called both at startup (main.rs) and after every capture-thread insert (src/capture.rs) and every action (`actions::refresh_snapshot`), always requesting `GUI_LIMIT` (1000) clips. Every existing test in vbuff-store's own `#[cfg(test)]` block and in tests/integration.rs calls `list`/`load_recent` only after inserting at least one clip first; none calls it against a brand-new store with zero rows to confirm it returns an empty `Vec` rather than erroring - a realistic gap since it does work correctly today via a plain SQL `LIMIT` clause, but that behavior is asserted nowhere. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs's `insert_and_list` test (lines 250-261) always inserts 2 clips before calling `list`; crates/vbuff-store/tests/integration.rs's tests likewise always insert first; grepping both files for a `list`/`load_recent` call against a store with zero prior inserts finds none._
392. **`ThumbnailCache::retain_only`'s pruning-on-revision-change wiring in `PopupApp` is untested as an interaction, even though the cache is pruned in principle** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - `PopupApp::update` computes `live_ids` from the current `clips` snapshot and calls `self.thumbnails.retain_only(&live_ids)` only inside the `if revision != self.last_revision` branch (app.rs lines 121-126). There is no test proving that a texture built for a clip which is later deleted (revision bumps, clip disappears from `clips`) is actually evicted from the cache's `HashMap` on the very next `update()` call - `retain_only` itself is a trivial one-line `HashMap::retain` that doesn't need isolated testing, but the *trigger* condition (does `PopupApp` reliably call it exactly when clips change, not more or less often) is exactly the kind of wiring bug that a leaf-function test of `retain_only` alone cannot catch, and neither app.rs nor thumbnail.rs has any test today. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-gui/src/app.rs lines 121-126 (revision-gated `retain_only` call inside `PopupApp::update`); `grep -n "cfg(test)" crates/vbuff-gui/src/app.rs crates/vbuff-gui/src/thumbnail.rs` returns nothing in either file._
393. **No test exists for `Store::set_favorite`, the sibling of the well-tested `set_pinned`** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - `set_pinned` is exercised by `pin_delete_clear` and indirectly by `enforce_cap_matches_pure_eviction_policy`, but `set_favorite` (line 153) - which `vbuff_core::eviction` treats as a separate concept from `pinned` - has no test anywhere calling it. A regression in `set_favorite`'s SQL (e.g. a copy-paste of `set_pinned` that forgot to change the column name and silently updated `pinned` instead) would pass the entire existing suite since `favorite` is never asserted on after being set. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs's `set_favorite` (line 153); grep for `set_favorite` across all `#[cfg(test)]` blocks in lib.rs and across crates/vbuff-store/tests/integration.rs returns zero matches outside the function definition itself._
394. **No test exists for `Store::clear_all` (as opposed to the pinned-preserving `clear`), and it has no caller anywhere in the shipped binary either** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - `clear_all` (line 178) deletes every row unconditionally including pinned ones, the destructive counterpart to the already-tested `clear` (pinned-preserving, tested via `pin_delete_clear`). It is currently unreferenced by any test, and unreferenced by the shipped binary too: grep across src/*.rs shows `clear_all` is never called from actions.rs, tray.rs, gui.rs, or capture.rs - only `clear` is wired to the UI's 'Clear all' action and the tray's 'Clear history' item. This is a distinct condition from the already-logged dead-code items in code-audit-top-50.md (#22/#24, which concern search/eviction duplication) since it is an untested destructive data-loss operation with no caller and no test guarding its one obvious future use case (a 'factory reset' button). _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs's `clear_all` (line 178); `grep -rn clear_all src/` returns no matches in any src/*.rs file, and no `#[cfg(test)]` block anywhere references `clear_all`._
395. **`ContentKind::icon()`/`label()`'s exhaustive match arms are untested, so a wrong (as opposed to missing) mapping would silently ship** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - `ContentKind` has 9 variants, each mapped to an emoji icon and a text label via two separate `match` blocks in vbuff-types/src/lib.rs. Neither `icon()` (lines 96-108) nor `label()` (lines 111-123) has a single test asserting even one variant's output; because both matches are already exhaustive (no `_ =>` fallback), Rust's compiler already prevents a *missing* arm, but a *wrong* one (e.g. `ContentKind::File` accidentally returning the `Rtf` icon due to a copy-paste in the match block) would never be caught since nothing asserts the icon/label pairing. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-types/src/lib.rs lines 96-123 (`icon`/`label`); the `#[cfg(test)] mod tests` block in the same file (lines 306-336) tests only `ClipId::roundtrips`, `preview_collapses_whitespace`, and `truncate_adds_ellipsis`, never `ContentKind::icon`/`label`._
396. **`vbuff_core::classify::is_color_hex` accepts 4-character hex strings but `vbuff_gui::color::parse_hex_color` doesn't, and no test in either crate catches the resulting classify/render mismatch** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - `is_color_hex` accepts `rest.len()` of 3, 4, 6, or 8 (the CSS `#rgba` shorthand), so a 4-digit hex clip like `#f80a` gets classified as `ContentKind::Color`. But `parse_hex_color`'s `match hex.len()` only handles 3, 6, and 8 - there is no `4 =>` arm - so that same clip falls through to `_ => None` in `draw_color_swatch`, which then renders `Color32::GRAY` instead of the actual color via `unwrap_or(Color32::GRAY)`. Neither `classify.rs`'s `detects_colors` test nor `color.rs`'s `parses_short_hex`/`parses_long_hex`/`rejects_bad_hex` tests use a 4-character hex string, so this classify/render mismatch has zero test coverage in either direction. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-core/src/classify.rs line 103 (`matches!(rest.len(), 3 | 4 | 6 | 8)`) vs crates/vbuff-gui/src/color.rs lines 17-32 (`match hex.len() { 3 => .., 6 => .., 8 => .., _ => None }`, no `4` arm); classify.rs's `detects_colors` test (lines 173-180) and color.rs's tests (lines 39-58) both omit any 4-digit input._
397. **No test harness exists to run the popup GUI in a headless/off-screen mode for rendering smoke tests, and no such infrastructure is planned anywhere in the docs** `[idea]` 🟡 `[medium]` - eframe/egui supports being driven without a real window via `egui::Context::run(raw_input, |ctx| { ... })` for pure-logic frame simulation, which does not require GPU/display access and would work in a future headless CI runner. Introduce a small test helper in vbuff-gui (e.g. a `#[cfg(test)] fn test_ctx() -> egui::Context` plus a way to feed synthetic `egui::RawInput` key events) so that `render_panel`, `handle_keys`, and `PopupApp::update`'s branching logic can be smoke-tested for 'does it panic / does it produce the expected action queue' without needing an actual OS window - today the only way to exercise any of that code is running the full `vbuff` binary interactively. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-gui/Cargo.toml declares `eframe`/`egui` under `[dependencies]` but has no `[dev-dependencies]` section at all; no file in vbuff-gui constructs an `egui::Context` for testing purposes (grep for `Context::run`/`Context::default()` across crates/vbuff-gui/src/*.rs finds nothing)._
398. **No automation verifies `cargo build --locked`/`cargo test --locked` succeed, which matters more for a project with zero CI to catch dependency drift** `[idea]` 🟢 `[low]` - Once any CI is added, run it with `cargo build --locked --workspace` and `cargo test --locked --workspace` rather than plain `cargo build`/`cargo test`, so an accidental `Cargo.lock` edit (or an out-of-date lockfile after a manual `Cargo.toml` version bump) fails fast instead of silently resolving a different dependency tree on the next contributor's machine than what was last tested. This is a process gap that only becomes fully visible once CI exists, but is worth deciding upfront rather than defaulting to unlocked builds. _Evidence: No CI configuration exists to specify `--locked` or not (see the CI-absence item); `Cargo.lock` is present at the repository root but no automation currently verifies it matches `Cargo.toml` on every change._
399. **No test verifies `--no-default-features` (i.e. building without the `tray` feature) actually compiles and runs, despite Cargo.toml explicitly documenting it as a supported configuration** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - Cargo.toml's `[features]` section comment says the tray integration 'is enabled by default; if it ever proves troublesome to build/run on a given platform it can be disabled with `--no-default-features`', explicitly inviting users to build without it. But every `#[cfg(feature = "tray")]` branch - the `mod tray` import in main.rs, `copy_latest_clip` in actions.rs, and the `tray: Option<Tray>` field plus tray-event-polling block in gui.rs - is only ever compiled and tested in the default (tray-enabled) configuration. No test command or script anywhere in the repo runs `cargo build --no-default-features` or `cargo test --no-default-features`, so a change that broke the non-tray build (e.g. an unguarded reference to a tray type leaking outside its `#[cfg]` block) would only be discovered by a user who explicitly opts out. _Evidence: Cargo.toml lines 66-70 (`[features]` section: the `--no-default-features` comment and `default = ["tray"]`); `#[cfg(feature = "tray")]` gates appear at src/main.rs line 28, src/actions.rs line 35, and src/gui.rs lines 17, 49, 75, 100; grep across the repo for `no-default-features` finds only the Cargo.toml comment itself, never an actual invocation in any script or config._
400. **No test exercises `Config::load_or_create` against a config.toml with a field deliberately omitted, to confirm forward/backward-compat of the TOML schema** `[idea]` 🟡 `[medium]` - `Config` derives `#[serde(default)]` at the struct level (src/config.rs line 13), meaning a config.toml missing a newly added field (e.g. a future `incognito: bool`) should deserialize fine, filling in the missing field with `Default::default()`'s value for that field. This specific behavior - does a partial/old config.toml on disk from a prior vbuff version load without error and fill in new fields with sane defaults - is never tested. The only test, `default_roundtrips_through_toml`, always serializes a *complete* `Config::default()` first and round-trips it, so it can never expose a `#[serde(default)]` misconfiguration on an individual field or a case where a field lacks its own `#[serde(default = ...)]` when one is later needed. _Evidence: src/config.rs line 13 (`#[serde(default)]` on `struct Config`); the only test, `default_roundtrips_through_toml` (lines 102-109), builds `Config::default()`, serializes it, and deserializes the complete output - it never hand-writes a partial TOML string missing a field and calls `load_or_create` or `toml::from_str` on it._
401. **No test verifies `Config::load_or_create` against a config.toml with an invalid/unparseable value produces a clear error rather than panicking somewhere in the chain** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - `load_or_create` propagates `toml::from_str` errors via `?` straight into `anyhow::Result` (src/config.rs line 62), wrapped only by main.rs's generic `.context("loading config")`. No test writes a syntactically-invalid or type-mismatched config.toml (e.g. `poll_interval_ms = "not a number"`) to a temp path and asserts `load_or_create` returns an `Err` rather than panicking - the only existing config test round-trips a valid, freshly-generated `Config` and never touches the file-I/O path at all. _Evidence: src/config.rs lines 58-69 (`load_or_create`'s `toml::from_str(&text)?` at line 62); the sole test in the file, `default_roundtrips_through_toml` (lines 102-109), never writes an invalid TOML string to disk or calls `load_or_create`, only `toml::to_string_pretty`/`toml::from_str` directly._
402. **`EnigoPaste::paste`'s modifier-release-on-failure guarantee (the comment 'Always release the modifier even if the v click failed') has no test proving it** `[idea]` 🟢 `[low]` - The comment on `EnigoPaste::paste` (paste.rs line 42) explicitly calls out a safety property: the modifier key is released even if the `v` keystroke fails, to avoid leaving a stuck Cmd/Ctrl key held down system-wide - a genuinely bad failure mode for a background clipboard tool. Since `enigo::Enigo` talks to real OS input APIs with no mockable seam (code-audit-top-50.md item #34 already notes vbuff-platform has no mock backends at all), this specific safety property - that `release` at line 43 runs unconditionally regardless of `click`'s `Result`, with both errors only propagated after both calls execute (lines 45-46) - can currently only be verified by reading the source, not by any automated check; a future refactor (e.g. adding an early `?` on the `click` line) could silently remove this guarantee and no test would fail. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-platform/src/paste.rs lines 38-47 (`click`/`release` both computed unconditionally before either `?`-propagates); the file has no `#[cfg(test)]` block at all._
403. **No test asserts `Flavor::is_text()`'s bare-`"text"` special case is ever reachable, since nothing in the codebase constructs a flavor with that literal mime** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - `is_text` checks `self.mime.starts_with("text/") || self.mime == "text"`. Every flavor constructed anywhere in the workspace (clipboard.rs's `"text/plain;charset=utf-8"`, test helpers' `"text/plain"`) uses a full `text/...` MIME type; the bare `"text"` literal branch is dead in practice and untested, so it is unclear whether it is intentional forward-compat for some future backend or a leftover from an earlier representation. No test exercises `Flavor::inline("text", ...)` to confirm `is_text()` returns true for it, and no test in vbuff-types' `#[cfg(test)]` block (lines 306-336) exercises `is_text`/`is_image` at all. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-types/src/lib.rs line 190 (`self.mime == "text"` branch in `is_text`); grepping the whole workspace for the bare literal `"text"` finds only this one occurrence (the check itself), never a construction site._
404. **`enforce_cap_matches_pure_eviction_policy` sleeps for real time in a loop with no `#[ignore]`/fast-path convention, and the pattern will compound as slower tests (proptest, fixtures) get added** `[idea]` 🟢 `[low]` - `enforce_cap_matches_pure_eviction_policy` in crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs calls `std::thread::sleep(Duration::from_millis(2))` inside a `for i in 0..10` loop, itself repeated for `max_history` in `[0, 1, 3, 5, 10]` - roughly 100ms of real sleep time for this one test. As the test suite grows (property tests, fixture-based golden tests, etc. per other items here), a project with no CI and no test-tagging convention (`#[ignore]` for slow tests, a nextest profile, or a documented `slow`/`fast` split) will make contributors reach for `cargo test -- --skip` ad hoc rather than a documented fast path, discouraging frequent local test runs. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs lines 327-363 (`enforce_cap_matches_pure_eviction_policy`), specifically line 338's `std::thread::sleep(std::time::Duration::from_millis(2))` inside the nested loops (10 iterations x 5 policy values); no `#[ignore]` attribute, cargo alias, or nextest config exists anywhere in the repo to separate this from instant unit tests._
405. **`vbuff-gui`'s `Cargo.toml` has no `[dev-dependencies]` section at all despite having six existing `#[cfg(test)]` tests, so there is no established place for the next test-only dependency** `[idea]` 🟢 `[low]` - Both other crates with tests (vbuff-core, vbuff-store) declare an explicit `[dev-dependencies]` section separating test-only deps from runtime deps (vbuff-core's holds `ulid`/`chrono`, vbuff-store's holds `tempfile`); vbuff-gui's existing tests get away with having none because they only exercise `egui::Color32` and `chrono`, both already runtime dependencies. This works today but sets no precedent for adding a genuinely test-only dependency (e.g. `proptest`, or a headless-eframe test helper per the earlier item) - the next contributor adding a test dependency to vbuff-gui has no existing pattern in this specific crate to follow, unlike vbuff-core/vbuff-store. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-gui/Cargo.toml (full file read) has a `[dependencies]` section only, no `[dev-dependencies]` section, despite crates/vbuff-gui/src/color.rs and view.rs each containing `#[cfg(test)] mod tests` blocks._

---

## Rust idiom & code quality

406. **content_hash_from_flavors clones every inline byte buffer just to re-borrow it** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - crates/vbuff-core/src/hash.rs:44-62, content_hash_from_flavors(). For each flavor it does `Body::Inline(b) => b.clone()` (line 49) and `f.mime.clone()` (line 52) into an owned Vec<(String, Vec<u8>)>, then immediately builds `CanonicalFlavor { mime: mime.as_str(), bytes: bytes.as_slice() }` from that owned Vec and never mutates or moves it further. Since `owned` and its borrows never outlive this function, the clones exist only to satisfy a self-referential-looking pattern that isn't actually necessary: the loop can push `CanonicalFlavor { mime: &f.mime, bytes: b }` directly for the Inline case (borrowing `flavors` itself), and only allocate (via `blob_ref.as_bytes()`, no clone needed either) for the Spilled case. This runs on every single capture (called from src/capture.rs:54), so it duplicates the full byte content of every clipboard payload for no reason other than sidestepping a lifetime that doesn't need sidestepping. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-core/src/hash.rs:49 `Body::Inline(b) => b.clone()` and :52 `owned.push((f.mime.clone(), bytes))`, called from src/capture.rs:54 `content_hash_from_flavors(&captured.flavors)`._
407. **27 public fallible functions have no `# Errors` doc section** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - `cargo clippy -- -W clippy::pedantic` flags 27 missing_errors_doc warnings across the workspace (verified by running it), e.g. Store::open_default/open/open_in_memory/insert/list/load_recent/set_pinned/set_favorite/delete/clear/clear_all/count/enforce_cap (crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs), ArboardClipboard::new/read/write (crates/vbuff-platform/src/clipboard.rs:23,30,59), GlobalHotkeyBackend::register/unregister (crates/vbuff-platform/src/hotkey.rs), EnigoPaste::new/paste (crates/vbuff-platform/src/paste.rs), and Config::load_or_create/save/config_path (src/config.rs). None of the doc comments enumerate which `StoreError`/`PlatformError`/`anyhow::Error` variants a caller should expect, so a caller has to read the implementation to know what `match`/`?` handling is safe. _Evidence: clippy::pedantic missing_errors_doc (27 hits, verified via `cargo clippy --workspace --all-features -- -W clippy::pedantic`), e.g. crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:201 `pub fn enforce_cap`, crates/vbuff-platform/src/clipboard.rs:23 `pub fn new`._
408. **31 public constructor/getter-style functions are missing #[must_use]** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - clippy::pedantic's must_use_candidate fires 31 times (verified by running clippy) across vbuff-types, vbuff-core, and vbuff-platform for functions like `ContentKind::icon`/`label` (crates/vbuff-types/src/lib.rs:96,111), `Body::byte_size`/`inline_bytes` (lib.rs:142,150), `Clip::content_hash_hex` (lib.rs:285), `vbuff_core::eviction::evict` (crates/vbuff-core/src/eviction.rs:38), `vbuff_core::filter::search` (crates/vbuff-core/src/filter.rs:23), and `content_hash`/`content_hash_from_flavors` (crates/vbuff-core/src/hash.rs:25,44). Because these are pure query/constructor functions with no side effect, a caller who calls one and discards the result silently does nothing useful, and nothing warns them - the opposite of what these types are for. _Evidence: clippy::pedantic must_use_candidate (31 hits, verified via `cargo clippy --workspace --all-features -- -W clippy::pedantic`), e.g. crates/vbuff-types/src/lib.rs:96 `pub fn icon`, crates/vbuff-core/src/hash.rs:25 `pub fn content_hash`._
409. **content_hash_hex builds a 64-char string via a `push_str(&format!(...))` loop instead of `write!`** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - crates/vbuff-types/src/lib.rs:285-291, Clip::content_hash_hex(). The loop `for b in &self.content_hash { s.push_str(&format!("{b:02x}")); }` allocates a fresh temporary String on every one of the 32 iterations just to immediately copy it into `s` and drop it. `use std::fmt::Write as _;` plus `write!(s, "{b:02x}").unwrap();` (or `core::fmt::Write`, infallible on String) writes directly into the pre-sized buffer with zero extra allocations - clippy::pedantic's format_push_string flags exactly this pattern (confirmed by running clippy). _Evidence: crates/vbuff-types/src/lib.rs:288 `s.push_str(&format!("{b:02x}"));` inside a `for b in &self.content_hash` loop; clippy::pedantic format_push_string confirmed at this exact line._
410. **Six bool-to-i64 casts in Store use `as i64` instead of `i64::from`** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:116,117,147,156 all write `<bool-expr> as i64` (e.g. `clip.pinned as i64`, `favorite as i64`) to convert a bool into the integer SQLite param. `bool -> i64` is a lossless, infallible widening that `From`/`Into` already implements, so clippy::pedantic's cast_lossless suggests `i64::from(clip.pinned)` etc (confirmed by running clippy, 4 cast_lossless hits at exactly these lines). Using `as` here silences the same lint category that also (correctly) flags the truncating/wrapping casts elsewhere in this file (e.g. line 113's `byte_size as i64`, line 216's `overflow as i64`), so the file mixes 'this cast is fine' and 'this cast may lose data' under one identical-looking syntax with no way to tell them apart at the call site. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:116 `clip.pinned as i64`, :117 `clip.favorite as i64`, :147 `pinned as i64`, :156 `favorite as i64` - clippy::pedantic cast_lossless confirmed at all four lines._
411. **Store::count truncates/sign-loses i64 -> usize with a bare `as` cast and no bounds check** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:184-189, Store::count(). `let n: i64 = ...; Ok(n as usize)` silently wraps if SQLite's COUNT(*) somehow returns a negative value (impossible in practice, but not enforced by the type system) and truncates on 32-bit targets. `usize::try_from(n).map_err(...)` (or `.unwrap_or(0)` with a documented invariant comment) would make the assumption explicit instead of relying on `as` to paper over it - clippy::pedantic's cast_possible_truncation and cast_sign_loss both flag line 188 exactly (confirmed by running clippy). _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:184-188 `let n: i64 = self.conn.query_row("SELECT COUNT(*) FROM clips", ...)?; Ok(n as usize)`; clippy::pedantic cast_possible_truncation and cast_sign_loss both confirmed at line 188._
412. **enforce_cap does an unchecked usize -> i64 cast on an attacker/user-controlled overflow count** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:206-217, Store::enforce_cap(). `overflow = total - max_history` (a usize) is passed to SQL as `params![overflow as i64]` (line 216). On a 64-bit target a `usize` value above `i64::MAX` would wrap to a negative `LIMIT`, which SQLite treats as 'no limit' - turning a cap-enforcement call into a full-table delete. That value is unreachable in today's usage (clip counts are always small), but the cast is still an `as` with no `try_from`/bounds assertion - clippy::pedantic's cast_possible_wrap confirms this exact line by running clippy. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:216 `params![overflow as i64]` inside enforce_cap; clippy::pedantic cast_possible_wrap confirmed at this line._
413. **handle_action takes UiAction by value across match arms that never need ownership of the enum itself** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - src/actions.rs:51-58, handle_action(action: UiAction, ...). `UiAction` derives `Clone, Debug, PartialEq, Eq` (crates/vbuff-gui/src/state.rs:40-41) and every arm either destructures out `Copy` payloads (`ClipId`, `bool`) or drops the variant entirely (`Hide`, `ClearAll`, `TogglePause`), so nothing in the function needs to own the enum itself. Taking `&UiAction` and matching on `*action`/by-reference pattern would let the single call site (src/gui.rs:135, iterating `popup.take_actions()`) avoid moving an already-owned `Vec<UiAction>` element into the call just to hand it off. _Evidence: src/actions.rs:52 `action: UiAction,` parameter of handle_action; crates/vbuff-gui/src/state.rs:40 `#[derive(Clone, Debug, PartialEq, Eq)] pub enum UiAction`; called from src/gui.rs:135 with an owned action from `popup.take_actions()`._
414. **spawn_capture_thread's clipboard-read match can be a `let...else`** `[improvement]` 🟢 `[low]` - src/capture.rs:46-49 writes `let captured = match clipboard.read() { Ok(c) => c, Err(_) => continue };` purely to unwrap the Ok arm and fall through on Err - the textbook shape `let...else` (stabilized well before this codebase's edition 2024) replaces. `let Ok(captured) = clipboard.read() else { continue };` says the same thing in one line and reads as 'bind or bail' instead of a match whose Err arm exists only to control flow. clippy::pedantic's manual_let_else confirms this exact site by running clippy. _Evidence: src/capture.rs:46-49 `let captured = match clipboard.read() { Ok(c) => c, Err(_) => continue };`; clippy::pedantic manual_let_else confirmed at this location._
415. **PopupApp::update's grace-period check uses `.map(...).unwrap_or(true)` instead of `map_or`** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - crates/vbuff-gui/src/app.rs:135-138: `self.shown_at.map(|t| t.elapsed().as_millis() > 250).unwrap_or(true)` allocates an intermediate `Option<bool>` only to immediately collapse it. `self.shown_at.map_or(true, |t| t.elapsed().as_millis() > 250)` is the direct one-call replacement clippy::pedantic's map_unwrap_or lint proposes here (confirmed by running clippy at this exact line), and reads as a single 'default vs. compute' decision rather than two chained combinators. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-gui/src/app.rs:135-138 `let grace_elapsed = self.shown_at.map(|t| t.elapsed().as_millis() > 250).unwrap_or(true);`; clippy::pedantic map_unwrap_or confirmed at line 135._
416. **gui.rs's closure parameter is bound as `_frame` yet still read at the call site** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - src/gui.rs:62 declares the eframe update closure as `move |ctx, _frame|`, signaling 'unused', but line 133 then does `popup.update(ctx, _frame);`, actually reading the underscore-prefixed binding. clippy::pedantic's used_underscore_binding flags this exact pair of sites (confirmed by running clippy): the leading underscore is a lie about the binding's use, and a reader skimming the closure signature would reasonably assume `_frame` is dead and skip checking how it flows into `popup.update`. Rename the parameter to `frame` to avoid the false 'unused' signal. _Evidence: src/gui.rs:62 `move |ctx, _frame| {` and src/gui.rs:133 `popup.update(ctx, _frame);`; clippy::pedantic used_underscore_binding confirmed, binding defined at gui.rs:62:80 and used at gui.rs:133:27._
417. **build_icon's two `N as u32` casts have no truncation guard even though N is a local const** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - src/tray.rs:98-111: `const N: usize = 32;` then `tray_icon::Icon::from_rgba(rgba, N as u32, N as u32)`. Because `N` is a fixed local constant this can never actually truncate, but clippy::pedantic's cast_possible_truncation still flags both casts at line 111 (confirmed by running clippy, two separate warnings for the two `N as u32` occurrences) since the compiler cannot see that invariant through the `as`. `u32::try_from(N).expect(...)` or simply declaring `const N: u32 = 32;` and deriving the `usize` needed for indexing via `N as usize` (a widening, always-safe cast) the other direction removes the ambiguity in the direction that actually matters. _Evidence: src/tray.rs:111 `tray_icon::Icon::from_rgba(rgba, N as u32, N as u32).expect("valid icon")`, with `const N: usize = 32;` at src/tray.rs:98; clippy::pedantic cast_possible_truncation confirmed twice at line 111 (columns 38 and 48)._
418. **is_url's SCHEMES const is declared mid-function after other statements** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - crates/vbuff-core/src/classify.rs:78-95, is_url(). The `const SCHEMES: &[&str] = &[...]` declaration sits at line 84, after the early-return `if s.split_whitespace().count() != 1 { return false; }` (line 80-82) and the `let lower = ...` binding (line 83). Since Rust items are hoisted to the top of their enclosing scope regardless of where they're written, placing a `const` after statements reads as though it depends on `lower`/earlier control flow when it does not; clippy::pedantic's items_after_statements flags this specifically because it misleads readers about evaluation order. Moving `SCHEMES` to the top of the function (or to module scope, since it is used only here but is otherwise a plain data table) removes the false ordering signal. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-core/src/classify.rs:84-86 `const SCHEMES: &[&str] = &[...]` declared after the count-check (line 80-82) and `lower` binding (line 83) inside is_url._
419. **parse_combo's last match arm omits the trailing semicolon Rust's own formatter would add** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - crates/vbuff-platform/src/hotkey.rs:139-141: the final match arm `"cmd" | "command" | "super" | "meta" | "win" | "windows" => { modifiers.push(Modifier::Meta) }` omits the semicolon after `modifiers.push(...)`, making that block's tail expression (`()` from `Vec::push`) implicitly returned instead of explicitly discarded like every other arm in the same match (which are all single-expression `=>` arms with no block). clippy::pedantic's semicolon_if_nothing_returned flags the inconsistency; adding the `;` matches the surrounding arms and avoids a stray non-`()`-looking tail expression in a match whose arms are all meant to be statements. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-platform/src/hotkey.rs:139-141, the `"cmd" | ... | "windows" => { modifiers.push(Modifier::Meta) }` arm inside parse_combo, missing a `;` present implicitly on every sibling single-expression arm._
420. **12 doc comments name types/env-vars without backtick-fencing, tripping doc_markdown** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - clippy::pedantic's doc_markdown fires 12 times for bare identifiers in doc comments that should be code-fenced (verified by running clippy), e.g. `crates/vbuff-types/src/lib.rs:83` ('CF_HDROP' and 'NSFilenames' both unfenced, two separate warnings), `crates/vbuff-types/src/lib.rs:219` ('WM_CLASS'), `crates/vbuff-platform/src/hotkey.rs:18` ('HotKey'), `crates/vbuff-store/src/error.rs:8` ('SQLite'), `crates/vbuff-store/src/row.rs:1,21,22` (six warnings across 'SQLite rows', 'content_hash', 'kind', 'created_at', 'byte_size', 'source_app'), and `src/main.rs:93` ('RUST_LOG', which is unfenced even though the adjacent word `` `info` `` on the same line already is). This is a real (if minor) documentation-generation quality issue: rustdoc renders these as plain prose, so identifiers like `RUST_LOG`/`HotKey`/`WM_CLASS` look like ordinary words instead of the identifiers they are. _Evidence: clippy::pedantic doc_markdown (12 hits, verified via `cargo clippy --workspace --all-features -- -W clippy::pedantic`), e.g. crates/vbuff-types/src/lib.rs:83:45 and :83:56 (CF_HDROP, NSFilenames), src/main.rs:93:44 (RUST_LOG unfenced despite `info` being fenced on the same line)._
421. **parse_hex_color's local `bytes` closure shadows the outer parameter name pattern used nowhere else in the crate** `[improvement]` 🟢 `[low]` - crates/vbuff-gui/src/color.rs:14-32, parse_hex_color(). The closure `let bytes = |i: usize, len: usize| u8::from_str_radix(&hex[i..i + len], 16).ok();` is named `bytes` (plural, suggesting a byte buffer) but actually returns a single `Option<u8>` per call - it is a 'parse this hex pair' helper, not a byte collection. A name like `hex_byte` or `parse_pair` would match what it does and avoid the reader momentarily expecting `bytes(0, 2)` to return a slice given the name's plural, buffer-like connotation elsewhere in the same crate (e.g. `Body::Inline(Vec<u8>)` bytes are always plural-named because they are actual buffers). _Evidence: crates/vbuff-gui/src/color.rs:16 `let bytes = |i: usize, len: usize| u8::from_str_radix(&hex[i..i + len], 16).ok();` returning a single `Option<u8>`, used as `bytes(0, 2)?` at line 24._
422. **Tray stores five MenuId fields plus three MenuItem fields that are never read together, doubling the struct's surface for the same five menu entries** `[improvement]` 🟢 `[low]` - src/tray.rs:16-26, struct Tray. Each menu entry needs both its `MenuId` (to match incoming `MenuEvent`s in `poll()`) and, for three of them, the `MenuItem` handle itself (to call `.set_text()`/`.set_enabled()` in `sync_state()`). Because `MenuItem::id()` already returns a `&MenuId` (used at construction time, src/tray.rs:54-58, via `.id().clone()`), the five separate `*_id: MenuId` fields are a stored, cloned copy of data the corresponding `MenuItem` already owns. Keeping only `show: MenuItem, copy_latest: MenuItem, clear_history: MenuItem, pause: MenuItem, quit: MenuItem` and calling `.id()` inside `poll()` instead would drop 5 fields and 5 `.clone()` calls at construction with no loss of capability. _Evidence: src/tray.rs:18-26 five `*_id: MenuId` fields plus three separate `MenuItem` fields (`copy_latest`, `clear_history`, `pause`) on the same struct, populated by five `.id().clone()` calls at src/tray.rs:54-58._
423. **short_app_name's bundle-id branch condition reads as three unrelated checks rather than one 'looks like a bundle id' predicate** `[improvement]` 🟢 `[low]` - crates/vbuff-gui/src/view.rs:42-53, short_app_name(). The condition `if source.contains('.') && !source.contains('/') && let Some(last) = source.rsplit('.').next()` mixes a boolean guard with a let-chain binding in one `if`, so the reader has to parse 'has a dot AND has no slash AND (incidentally) the rsplit succeeds' as a single unit even though the third clause can only ever be `Some` (rsplit on a string containing '.' always yields at least one component) - it exists purely to obtain `last`, not as a real condition.
