Splitting into `let looks_like_bundle_id = source.contains('.') && !source.contains('/'); if looks_like_bundle_id { let last = source.rsplit('.').next().unwrap_or(source); ... }` would separate the actual classification logic from the infallible extraction, and give the classification a name instead of leaving it anonymous in the `if`. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-gui/src/view.rs:44-47 `if source.contains('.') && !source.contains('/') && let Some(last) = source.rsplit('.').next() { return last.to_string(); }`._
424. **kind_to_int/kind_from_int hand-roll a bidirectional enum<->i64 mapping instead of deriving it** `[improvement]` 🟢 `[low]` - crates/vbuff-store/src/row.rs:79-105. `kind_to_int` and `kind_from_int` are two manually-written, order-dependent match statements that must be kept in sync by hand every time `ContentKind` (crates/vbuff-types/src/lib.rs:72-92) gains, loses, or reorders a variant - nothing enforces that the discriminants line up, and a new variant added to `ContentKind` without touching both match arms here would silently fall through `kind_from_int`'s `_ => ContentKind::Other` catch-all instead of failing to compile. Since `ContentKind` already derives nothing that fixes its discriminants, adding `#[repr(i64)]` plus explicit `= N` discriminants on `ContentKind` and using `kind as i64` / a `TryFrom<i64>` derive (or the `num_enum` crate's `IntoPrimitive`/`TryFromPrimitive`) would make the mapping a single source of truth instead of two hand-maintained tables that can drift silently. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/row.rs:79-91 kind_to_int and :93-105 kind_from_int, two independent match statements over the same 9 ContentKind variants defined in crates/vbuff-types/src/lib.rs:72-92._
425. **looks_like_code's strong_tokens array mixes trailing-space and bare-symbol tokens with no shared invariant, inviting substring false-positives** `[improvement]` 🟢 `[low]` - crates/vbuff-core/src/classify.rs:113-132. `strong_tokens` mixes word-boundary-safe entries like `"fn "`/`"def "` (trailing space prevents matching inside a longer identifier) with bare symbol tokens like `"->"`/`"::"`/`"</"` that have no such guard, and the check is `s.contains(t)` over the whole un-split string rather than per-line/per-token matching. A prose sentence containing a literal `"->"` arrow-drawn-in-ASCII (e.g. a changelog line 'renamed foo->bar') or a `::` used as an emoticon/separator in ordinary text would classify as Code purely from `has_strong`, with no length or context requirement the way the trailing-space tokens implicitly get. Splitting the list into 'word tokens' (checked with a word-boundary-aware helper) and 'structural symbols' (kept as-is, since `->`/`::`/`</`/`/>` are already fairly code-specific) would document the actual precision assumption instead of leaving it implicit in which strings happen to have a trailing space. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-core/src/classify.rs:114-131 strong_tokens array mixing `"fn "` (space-guarded) with `"->"`, `"::"` (unguarded), checked via `s.contains(t)` at line 132._
426. **ArboardClipboard::read's text-arm `match` only needs an `if let`, not a full match with a discarded catch-all** `[improvement]` 🟢 `[low]` - crates/vbuff-platform/src/clipboard.rs:34-42. `match self.clipboard.get_text() { Ok(text) if !text.is_empty() => { ... } _ => {} }` is a two-armed match where the second arm is a bare `_ => {}` no-op - exactly the shape `if let Ok(text) = self.clipboard.get_text() { if !text.is_empty() { flavors.push(...); } }` (or a single `if let Ok(text) = ... && !text.is_empty()` let-chain, already used two lines later at clipboard.rs:46-48 for the image-flavor branch, and in src/capture.rs) expresses more directly. Given the file already uses a let-chain for the image branch, the text branch reads as an inconsistency in style rather than a deliberate choice. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-platform/src/clipboard.rs:34-42 `match self.clipboard.get_text() { Ok(text) if !text.is_empty() => {...}, _ => {} }`, versus the let-chain used two lines later at clipboard.rs:46-48 for the image flavor._
427. **PendingPaste is a one-field struct wrapping a single Instant with no behavior of its own** `[improvement]` 🟢 `[low]` - src/actions.rs:17-20: `pub(crate) struct PendingPaste { pub(crate) at: Instant }`. The struct exists solely to give a name to a bare `Instant`; every use site (src/actions.rs:75-77, src/gui.rs:52,139-149) just reads `.at` straight back out, with no invariant, method, or additional field the wrapper enforces or will plausibly grow (the doc comment on the struct already describes the entire behavior in one sentence). `Option<Instant>` directly as the `pending_paste` field/parameter type would remove a layer of indirection with zero loss of clarity, since the variable name `pending_paste` already carries the semantic meaning the struct name repeats. _Evidence: src/actions.rs:17-20 `pub(crate) struct PendingPaste { pub(crate) at: Instant }`, only ever constructed at src/actions.rs:75-77 and read via `.at` at src/gui.rs:140._
428. **Config::is_excluded recomputes `e.to_lowercase()` inside the `.any()` closure on every call instead of normalizing once** `[improvement]` 🟢 `[low]` - src/config.rs:83-88, Config::is_excluded(). `self.excluded_apps.iter().any(|e| !e.is_empty() && lower.contains(&e.to_lowercase()))` allocates a fresh lowercased `String` for every entry in `excluded_apps` on every single call, even though `excluded_apps` is config data that changes only when the user edits settings, not per capture. Note that today this function's only call site in src/capture.rs:68 is behind `if let Some(app) = &captured.source_app`, and `ArboardClipboard::read` (crates/vbuff-platform/src/clipboard.rs:55) hardcodes `source_app: None`, so the closure never actually runs yet; the moment a real backend populates `source_app` (needed to fix the dead-code gap already tracked as item #4 in docs/code-audit-top-50.md), this becomes a per-poll allocation. Normalizing `excluded_apps` to lowercase once (e.g. at config-load time, or via a cached `Vec<String>` built alongside `excluded_apps`) would turn that future O(n) per-poll allocation into a one-time cost, and is cheap to do now before the hot path goes live. _Evidence: src/config.rs:85-87 `self.excluded_apps.iter().any(|e| !e.is_empty() && lower.contains(&e.to_lowercase()))`, guarded at its only call site by src/capture.rs:67-68 `if let Some(app) = &captured.source_app`, and crates/vbuff-platform/src/clipboard.rs:55 `source_app: None` (always None today)._
429. **spawn_capture_thread computes byte_size with a `.map(...).sum()` that allocates no intermediate but still walks the flavor list twice with detect_kind** `[improvement]` 🟢 `[low]` - src/capture.rs:76-77: `let kind = detect_kind(&captured.flavors); let byte_size: u64 = captured.flavors.iter().map(|f| f.body.byte_size()).sum();` walks `captured.flavors` twice per capture: once inside `detect_kind` (crates/vbuff-core/src/classify.rs:13-57, itself already two passes over `flavors` for the MIME-signal loop and the file-signal loop) and again for the byte-size sum. For the MVP's typical 1-2 flavor case this is not a hot-path concern, but `detect_kind` could return `(ContentKind, u64)` or the byte-size sum could be folded into a single pass alongside classification, since both are already O(flavors) traversals of the same slice computed back-to-back with no branching dependency between them. _Evidence: src/capture.rs:76-77, detect_kind(&captured.flavors) followed immediately by a separate `.iter().map(...).sum()` pass over the same captured.flavors._
430. **detect_kind's file-flavor MIME check uses `.contains("file-url")`/`.contains("Filenames")` substring matching instead of exact/prefix matching** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - crates/vbuff-core/src/classify.rs:20-29: `mime.contains("file-url")` and `mime.contains("Filenames")` will match any MIME string that happens to contain those substrings anywhere, not just the intended platform constants (macOS `NSFilenamesPboardType`, a hypothetical `*/file-url` type). A flavor mime string like `application/x-my-custom-filenames-format` (unrelated to the actual file-list flavor) would be misclassified as `ContentKind::File` purely from the substring match. Since the surrounding checks in the same function use exact equality (`mime == "text/uri-list"`, `mime == "application/x-file-list"`), the two `.contains(...)` calls are the odd ones out and should either be exact matches against the specific platform constant strings or a documented prefix check, not an unbounded substring search. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-core/src/classify.rs:22-26 `mime.contains("file-url") || mime.contains("Filenames")` mixed with exact `mime == "text/uri-list"` in the same `if`._
431. **raw_to_clip's `content_hash.len() == 32` check silently accepts any wrong length as a Corrupt error but never includes the actual observed length** `[improvement]` 🟢 `[low]` - crates/vbuff-store/src/row.rs:39-47, raw_to_clip(). The length check `if raw.content_hash.len() == 32 { content_hash.copy_from_slice(...) } else { return Err(...) }` is correct, but the whole function discards the *actual* observed length in the error message (`StoreError::Corrupt("content_hash not 32 bytes".into())` at line 46) rather than including `raw.content_hash.len()`, which would materially help debugging a genuinely corrupt row (e.g. distinguishing a 0-byte NULL-coalesced column from a 16-byte truncated one). A one-line `format!("content_hash not 32 bytes (got {})", raw.content_hash.len())` costs nothing and turns an opaque corruption report into an actionable one. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/row.rs:43-47 `if raw.content_hash.len() == 32 { ... } else { return Err(StoreError::Corrupt("content_hash not 32 bytes".into())); }` - error message drops the actual observed length._
432. **ThumbnailCache keys its HashMap by `String` (ClipId::to_string_repr) instead of the already-Copy, already-Hash ClipId** `[improvement]` 🟢 `[low]` - crates/vbuff-gui/src/thumbnail.rs:16, `cache: HashMap<String, Option<egui::TextureHandle>>`, keyed via `clip.id.to_string_repr()` (line 28) and pruned via `HashSet<String>` of `clips.iter().map(|c| c.id.to_string_repr())` (crates/vbuff-gui/src/app.rs:124). `ClipId` already derives `Clone, Copy, PartialEq, Eq, Hash` (crates/vbuff-types/src/lib.rs:26), so it is a drop-in `HashMap`/`HashSet` key with no allocation, but both the cache and its `retain_only` set instead allocate a fresh 26-character `String` per clip per revision bump just to use as a lookup key. Switching to `HashMap<ClipId, Option<TextureHandle>>` / `HashSet<ClipId>` removes one String allocation per clip on every revision change (i.e. every capture and every store mutation while the popup is open) with no behavior change. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-gui/src/thumbnail.rs:16 `cache: HashMap<String, Option<egui::TextureHandle>>` keyed by `clip.id.to_string_repr()` at line 28, and crates/vbuff-gui/src/app.rs:124 building a parallel `HashSet<String>` of the same stringified ids for pruning._
433. **GlobalHotkeyBackend::unregister looks up by u32 id in a HashMap but the underlying HotKey already carries its own id, duplicating the key** `[improvement]` 🟢 `[low]` - crates/vbuff-platform/src/hotkey.rs:16-52. `registered: HashMap<u32, HotKey>` stores each `HotKey` keyed by `hotkey.id()` (line 41), but `HotKey` already exposes `.id()` as a method (used at line 40 to obtain the very key it's stored under), so the map key is entirely derivable from its own value. A `Vec<HotKey>` searched by `.iter().position(|h| h.id() == id)` would be equivalent in behavior for the tiny (single-hotkey, in this MVP) registration set and avoid storing the id twice (once as the map key, once inside the `HotKey` itself), though the `HashMap` does pay for itself if the registration count grows past a handful - worth a comment either way since it's not obvious which regime this is optimized for. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-platform/src/hotkey.rs:19 `registered: HashMap<u32, HotKey>`, populated at line 40-41 `let id = hotkey.id(); self.registered.insert(id, hotkey);` - the key is derived from a method already callable on the stored value._
434. **Store::insert's dedup branch discards the original ULID parse error via `.map_err(|_| ...)`** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:91-92: `ClipId::parse(&id_str).map_err(|_| StoreError::Corrupt("bad ulid in db".into()))` discards the `ulid::DecodeError` entirely, so a genuinely corrupt id string in the `clips.id` column produces an error message that says only 'bad ulid in db' with no indication of what the actual malformed value was or why parsing failed (bad length? bad Crockford base32 char?). The identical pattern repeats in crates/vbuff-store/src/row.rs:40. Interpolating `id_str` (or the underlying `ulid::DecodeError`'s `Display`) into the `Corrupt` message would make a rare-but-real production DB corruption bug actually diagnosable from the error string alone instead of requiring a debugger session. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:91-92 `ClipId::parse(&id_str).map_err(|_| StoreError::Corrupt("bad ulid in db".into()))` and the identical pattern at crates/vbuff-store/src/row.rs:40._
435. **PopupApp::filtered rebuilds a Vec<ClipId> from vbuff_core::search's SearchResult<'_> every frame even for an unchanged query** `[improvement]` 🟢 `[low]` - crates/vbuff-gui/src/app.rs:91-94 and its call site at app.rs:146: `filtered(&self.query)` is invoked unconditionally on every `update()` call while the popup is visible (i.e. every frame egui repaints, which per `ctx.request_repaint()` at app.rs:167 is continuous), running the full `vbuff_core::search` case-insensitive substring scan and rank-sort over the entire clip list even when neither `self.query` nor `clips` changed since the last frame. Caching the last `(query, revision)` pair alongside the resulting `Vec<ClipId>` and only recomputing when either changes would turn an O(clips log clips) full rescan-and-resort into a no-op on the (overwhelmingly common) frame where nothing changed but the cursor still blinks. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-gui/src/app.rs:91-94 fn filtered() calling vbuff_core::search unconditionally, invoked every frame at app.rs:146 inside update() which requests continuous repaint at app.rs:167._
436. **Tray::poll drains MenuEvent::receiver() with an if/else-if chain instead of a match on the MenuId** `[improvement]` 🟢 `[low]` - src/tray.rs:77-93, Tray::poll(). The event-to-action mapping is five sequential `if event.id == self.X_id { ... } else if ...` comparisons against `MenuId` (which is `PartialEq` but not an enum, so a real `match` isn't directly possible) - functionally fine, but it means adding a sixth menu item requires remembering to extend this exact chain in the exact right place, with no exhaustiveness check from the compiler the way a match over a closed enum would give. Since `TrayAction` itself is a closed enum one line above (src/tray.rs:7-13), an intermediate lookup table (`Vec<(MenuId, TrayAction)>` built once in `new()` and searched here) would let this loop become data-driven and self-documenting instead of five copy-pasted branches that must stay in lockstep with the five id fields flagged separately in this review. _Evidence: src/tray.rs:80-90, five `if event.id == self.show_id {...} else if event.id == self.copy_latest_id {...} else if ...` branches with no exhaustiveness enforcement._
437. **score_clip does two usize-to-i64 casts on subtraction paths that clippy flags as potentially wrapping** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - crates/vbuff-core/src/filter.rs:54-76, score_clip(). Both `score -= pos as i64;` (line 60, `pos` from `haystack.find(q)`) and `score -= (haystack.len() / 64) as i64;` (line 73) cast a `usize` to `i64` with a bare `as` inside a search-ranking hot path that runs once per clip per keystroke. In practice `pos`/`haystack.len()` are bounded by realistic clipboard-content sizes and never approach `i64::MAX`, but the cast still silences clippy::pedantic's cast_possible_wrap at both lines (confirmed by running clippy) with no `try_from`/bounds comment explaining why it's safe here - the same pattern already flagged elsewhere in the store layer (e.g. `enforce_cap`'s `overflow as i64`) but not yet noted in `vbuff-core`. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-core/src/filter.rs:60 `score -= pos as i64;` and :73 `score -= (haystack.len() / 64) as i64;`; clippy::pedantic cast_possible_wrap confirmed at both lines._

---

## Configuration & policy UX

438. **config.paste_modifier field is fully dead; nothing ever reads it** `[problem]` 🟠 `[high]` - Config::paste_modifier is documented as "cmd" or "ctrl", empty = OS default (src/config.rs:21-22), and Config::default() sets it to String::new() (config.rs:36). But crates/vbuff-platform/src/paste.rs's EnigoPaste::paste() (line 31) calls the free function vbuff_platform::paste_modifier() (lib.rs:35-44), a #[cfg(target_os)] compile-time OS switch that takes no arguments and never looks at Config at all. A user who edits paste_modifier in config.toml sees zero effect on which modifier is synthesized; the field is a name collision with an unrelated function, not a working setting. _Evidence: src/config.rs:21-22,36; crates/vbuff-platform/src/paste.rs:31; crates/vbuff-platform/src/lib.rs:35-44._
439. **Malformed config.toml crashes the whole app at startup with a raw TOML parser error** `[problem]` 🟠 `[high]` - Config::load_or_create() (config.rs:58-69) calls toml::from_str(&text)? with no fallback: any syntax error, wrong type (e.g. a quoted string where max_history expects an integer), or unknown structure propagates straight out of main() via the `?` in main.rs:47 (`.context("loading config")?`), so main() returns Err and the process exits with only a terminal-printed anyhow chain - no popup, no tray, no indication to a GUI-only user of what to fix or where the file lives. _Evidence: src/config.rs:58-69; src/main.rs:47._
440. **No range/sanity validation on any numeric config field after parsing** `[problem]` 🟠 `[high]` - Once TOML parsing succeeds, Config has zero semantic validation: poll_interval_ms and max_history accept any u64/usize the deserializer produces, including 0. There is no Config::validate() method anywhere in config.rs, and load_or_create() returns the parsed struct unchecked. A hand-edited `poll_interval_ms = 0` or `max_history = 0` is accepted as valid and only produces effects deep inside capture.rs/vbuff-store (see related items below), not a clear config-time error. _Evidence: src/config.rs:12-28,58-69 (no validate/sanity-check method exists)._
441. **max_history = 0 silently deletes every clip on every capture and every startup** `[problem]` 🟠 `[high]` - main.rs:52-54 calls store.enforce_cap(config.max_history) unconditionally at startup, and capture.rs:94 calls it again after every single insert. Store::enforce_cap (crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:201-219) computes `overflow = total - max_history`; with max_history = 0, overflow == total, so the DELETE removes every unpinned/unfavorited row immediately. A user who sets max_history = 0 thinking "no limit" or mistypes an empty value gets a clipboard manager that discards history as fast as it's captured, with no warning that 0 means "keep nothing" rather than "unlimited". _Evidence: src/main.rs:52-54; src/capture.rs:94; crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:201-219._
442. **poll_interval_ms is silently clamped to a 50ms floor with no feedback that the configured value was overridden** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - spawn_capture_thread computes `Duration::from_millis(config.poll_interval_ms.max(50))` (capture.rs:37). If a user sets poll_interval_ms = 0 or 10 in config.toml expecting near-instant capture, the thread silently runs at 50ms instead with no log line, no tray indicator, and no note in config.toml (which still shows the user's original small number) - the effective and stored values permanently diverge. _Evidence: src/capture.rs:37._
443. **max_history has no configured or documented upper bound, so an impractically large value grows the SQLite file with zero warning** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - max_history (config.rs:20) accepts any usize with no ceiling check anywhere in config.rs or main.rs. A user is free to set max_history = 1_000_000 and the store will happily try to hold that many rows (subject only to disk space), since enforce_cap only ever trims down to max_history and never flags the value as impractical before or after it's saved. _Evidence: src/config.rs:20; crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:201-219 (enforce_cap has no upper-bound check)._
444. **Invalid hotkey strings are only ever discovered at hotkey registration, not at config load/save time** `[problem]` 🟠 `[high]` - Config::load_or_create() performs no validation of the hotkey field (config.rs:58-69); a syntactically-valid-TOML-but-garbage string like `hotkey = ""` or `hotkey = "Cmd+Shift"` (no key, only modifiers) loads successfully. The failure only surfaces later in main(), where parse_combo(&config.hotkey) (main.rs:80-81) returns Err, and that Err is turned into a hard `.with_context(...)?` that aborts main() entirely (unlike the softer handling given to an actual registration conflict at main.rs:82-88, which just logs a warning and continues with hotkey_id = None). So a bad hotkey *string* kills the whole app, while a hotkey *conflict* with another app degrades gracefully - the two failure modes for "the hotkey doesn't work" have inconsistent severities for no principled reason. _Evidence: src/main.rs:80-88; crates/vbuff-platform/src/hotkey.rs:127-147 (parse_combo returns PlatformError::BadCombo on empty/no-key input)._
445. **parse_combo silently accepts unknown/typo'd modifier tokens as the main key instead of rejecting them, and keeps only the last one on multi-token typos** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - parse_combo's match arm (hotkey.rs:135-143) treats any token that isn't a recognized modifier keyword as `key = Some(token)` via the `_ =>` fallback - there is no validation that a non-modifier token is a single recognized key, and the assignment inside the `for` loop overwrites `key` on every non-modifier token seen. So `hotkey = "Cmd+Shft+V"` (typo: Shft instead of Shift) parses with `key` first set to "Shft" and then overwritten to "V" - accidentally correct here - but `hotkey = "Cmd+Shift+V+X"` silently keeps only "X" as the final key, discarding "V" with no indication the earlier token was dropped. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-platform/src/hotkey.rs:127-147._
446. **key_to_code's small allowlist means many technically-valid hotkey strings fail with an opaque "unknown key" error and no listed alternative** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - key_to_code (hotkey.rs:75-120) only recognizes A-Z, 0-9, Space, Enter/Return, and Tab - no function keys, punctuation, or arrow keys. A user who edits config.toml to set `hotkey = "Cmd+Shift+F1"` or `hotkey = "Cmd+,"` (a common "open preferences" pattern) gets `PlatformError::BadCombo("unknown key \"F1\"")` propagated as a fatal main() error (main.rs:80-81) with no in-app list of what keys are actually supported - the only place that list exists is this match arm in the source. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-platform/src/hotkey.rs:75-120; src/main.rs:80-81._
447. **No settings UI exists anywhere in the GUI, tray, or CLI; every config knob requires manually editing and saving config.toml while the app is closed** `[problem]` 🟠 `[high]` - A search across crates/vbuff-gui/src/*.rs, src/tray.rs, src/gui.rs, and src/actions.rs for "config"/"settings" finds zero hits outside config.rs itself and its one construction site in main.rs - there is no Settings window, no tray submenu item for hotkey/poll-interval/max-history/exclusions, and no in-popup way to view or change any Config field. Combined with the lack of config re-save after startup (see below), a user's only path to changing any policy value is: find `<config_dir>/vbuff/config.toml` themselves (undocumented in any UI), hand-edit TOML syntax correctly, and fully restart the app - there's no discoverability signal in-app that config.toml even exists. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-gui/src/*.rs; src/tray.rs; src/gui.rs; src/actions.rs (grep for config/settings returns no hits outside config.rs and main.rs's construction site)._
448. **config_path() silently varies per-OS with no in-app disclosure of where the file was created or loaded from** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - config_path() (config.rs:92-96) resolves to `dirs::config_dir()/vbuff/config.toml`, a different absolute path on macOS (~/Library/Application Support), Windows (%APPDATA%), and Linux (~/.config or $XDG_CONFIG_HOME) - correct behavior, but main.rs never logs or displays this resolved path: the startup info log at main.rs:48 logs only `config.hotkey` and `config.poll_interval_ms`, never the path itself, so a user troubleshooting "my settings aren't taking effect" has to guess or consult README rather than being told by the running app. _Evidence: src/config.rs:92-96; src/main.rs:47-48 (info log omits the resolved config path)._
449. **dirs::config_dir() returning None is only surfaced as a generic anyhow string, not a targeted error message telling the user what to fix** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - config_path() (config.rs:93-95) maps a `None` from dirs::config_dir() (which can happen on minimal/misconfigured Linux setups lacking both $XDG_CONFIG_HOME and $HOME) to `anyhow::anyhow!("could not determine config directory")`. This bubbles through load_or_create -> main() -> `.context("loading config")?` as a generic two-line error with no suggestion (e.g. "set XDG_CONFIG_HOME" or "set HOME") - a user on an unusual environment gets no actionable next step, just the app refusing to start. _Evidence: src/config.rs:92-96; src/main.rs:47._
450. **Config::save() has no atomic-write protection; a crash or power loss mid-write can corrupt config.toml and brick the next startup** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - Config::save() (config.rs:72-80) calls std::fs::write(&path, text) directly, which truncates the existing config.toml in place before writing the new content. If the process is killed (OOM, forced quit, power loss) between truncation and the write completing, the file is left partially written or empty. On the next launch, load_or_create() sees `path.exists()` is true, attempts `toml::from_str` on the truncated/garbage content, and - per the malformed-TOML finding above - hard-fails main() with no automatic fallback to defaults or backup, unlike a write-temp-then-rename pattern which would leave the last-good file intact. _Evidence: src/config.rs:72-80._
451. **Config::save() is only ever called from load_or_create() on first run; there is no code path anywhere that re-saves an updated Config during the process lifetime** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - A search for `.save()` on a Config value across src/*.rs shows the only call site is inside load_or_create() itself (config.rs:66), when the file doesn't yet exist. There is no in-app mutation of Config after startup (consistent with no settings UI existing at all), meaning even if a settings UI were added later, the persistence half (writing back to disk) has never been exercised outside the fresh-install path - save()'s directory-creation and TOML-serialization logic for an *update* scenario is currently only unit-tested via round-trip in isolation (config.rs:102-109), never via an actual re-save flow. _Evidence: src/config.rs:66,72-80 (only call site in the whole binary); config.rs:102-109 (only exercised via isolated round-trip test)._
452. **excluded_apps default is a comment-only Vec::new() with no shipped starter list, and no in-app way to discover the feature exists at all** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - Distinct from the audit doc's dead-at-runtime finding (source_app is always None): even once source_app population is fixed, there is no onboarding surface, TOML comment example, or tray menu entry that tells a user this field exists or how to populate it (e.g. `excluded_apps = ["1password", "keychain"]`). The only place the field's existence and matching semantics are documented is the Rust doc-comment in config.rs:23-24 and the unit test in config.rs:112-121 - neither of which a non-developer end user will ever see, since toml::to_string_pretty does not carry Rust doc comments into the generated file. _Evidence: src/config.rs:23-25,37,72-80 (save() writes via toml::to_string_pretty, which drops doc comments); no README/onboarding/tray reference to excluded_apps outside config.rs._
453. **skip_whitespace_only is a fixed boolean with no severity levels and no per-source override, silently dropping intentional whitespace-only copies (e.g. a single space or tab used as a spacer)** `[improvement]` 🟢 `[low]` - Config::skip_whitespace_only (config.rs:27) is all-or-nothing: capture.rs:60-66 skips any text where `text.trim().is_empty()` when the flag is true, with no way to distinguish "accidentally copied nothing" from "deliberately copied a tab character to use as a spreadsheet-paste separator". Add either a length threshold (e.g. only skip if trimmed length is 0 AND raw length is small, so a long whitespace run like an indented code block still gets captured) or drop the setting to a per-source-app override list alongside excluded_apps. _Evidence: src/config.rs:27; src/capture.rs:60-66._
454. **No config schema version field, so a future breaking change to Config's shape has no migration path and will silently reset user settings to defaults via #[serde(default)]** `[improvement]` 🟡 `[medium]` - Config derives #[serde(default)] at the struct level (config.rs:13), which means adding, renaming, or retyping a field in a future release causes serde to silently fall back to Default::default() for any field it can't match by name/type in an old config.toml, rather than erroring. Without a `schema_version: u32` field checked explicitly in load_or_create(), a user upgrading vbuff after a field rename (e.g. renaming poll_interval_ms to capture_interval_ms) would have their configured value silently discarded with no log line, no migration, and no way to tell the difference between "defaulted because missing" and "defaulted because renamed". _Evidence: src/config.rs:12-13,58-69 (no version field, no migration logic)._
455. **hotkey and paste_modifier are both free-form strings with no enum/validated type, so the same logical value can be spelled multiple incompatible ways with no canonicalization on save** `[improvement]` 🟢 `[low]` - hotkey (config.rs:16) and paste_modifier (config.rs:22) are plain String fields. parse_combo (hotkey.rs:135-143) accepts many synonyms for the same modifier (ctrl/control, cmd/command/super/meta/win) but Config::save() never rewrites config.toml to a canonical spelling after a successful load - so a user who types `hotkey = "windows+shift+v"` keeps that exact string on disk forever, with no visible confirmation of which modifier vbuff actually resolved it to. Consider a validated newtype (parse-on-deserialize with serde, or a canonicalize-then-rewrite step in load_or_create) so config.toml always reflects the interpreted value, not just the raw typed one. _Evidence: src/config.rs:16,22; crates/vbuff-platform/src/hotkey.rs:135-143._
456. **No way to configure per-flavor or per-kind capture policy (e.g. "never capture images", "never capture from clipboard when size > N") - Config only has one global skip_whitespace_only gate** `[improvement]` 🟡 `[medium]` - capture.rs's capture-gate section (lines 59-72) applies exactly two policies: whitespace-only text skip and app-name exclusion. There is no config field to disable image capture entirely (useful for users who never want screenshots persisted), no per-kind size ceiling, and no way to say "only capture text, ignore everything else" - all policy surface in Config is either whitespace-related or app-identity-related, with no content-kind axis at all despite vbuff_core::detect_kind already classifying Text/Image/etc. at capture time (capture.rs:76). _Evidence: src/config.rs:12-28 (no kind-based field); src/capture.rs:59-76._
457. **No dry-run/validate subcommand or flag to check a config.toml before committing to it, forcing trial-and-error via full app restarts** `[improvement]` 🟢 `[low]` - main.rs has no CLI argument parsing at all (no `clap`/`argh`/std::env::args() branch beyond running the GUI directly) - there's no `vbuff --check-config` or `vbuff --validate-config <path>` path that would let a user confirm their hand-edited hotkey string and numeric fields parse and validate before killing and relaunching the whole tray app to find out it now refuses to start (see the malformed-TOML and bad-hotkey findings above). _Evidence: src/main.rs:1-98 (no argument parsing / subcommand dispatch of any kind)._
458. **Config is captured by value into the capture thread's closure with no shared/interior-mutable cell; the tray Pause/Resume toggle is the only runtime-mutable policy knob that actually exists** `[improvement]` 🟡 `[medium]` - spawn_capture_thread takes `config: Config` by value and moves it into the closure (capture.rs:21-26, 37); it is a fully owned snapshot with no Arc<Mutex<_>> or watch channel, so nothing outside that thread can ever change poll_interval_ms, max_history, skip_whitespace_only, or excluded_apps for the running process's capture loop - only the separate `paused: Arc<AtomicBool>` is mutable at runtime (main.rs:67, wired to the tray Pause/Resume action). If/when a settings UI is added, it will need a structural change (Arc<Mutex<Config>> or a watch channel) rather than being able to reuse the existing plumbing. _Evidence: src/capture.rs:21-26,37; src/main.rs:59-67 (paused is the only Arc-shared, mutable-at-runtime policy value)._
459. **No config field or mechanism to disable the global hotkey entirely (e.g. for users who only want tray-click access), forcing every user through register()/parse_combo() even if they never intend to use a hotkey** `[improvement]` 🟢 `[low]` - main.rs unconditionally attempts `parse_combo(&config.hotkey)` and `hotkey_backend.register(&combo)` (main.rs:80-88) for every startup; there is no `hotkey_enabled: bool` or empty-string-means-disabled convention in Config, so a user who wants zero global hotkey (relying solely on the tray icon's Show action) has no supported way to express that - they'd have to supply some string that happens to fail parse_combo and rely on the warn-and-continue path (main.rs:82-88) as an unintended workaround, which is not documented as a supported use case anywhere. _Evidence: src/config.rs:16 (no enabled/disabled toggle); src/main.rs:79-88._
460. **poll_interval_ms has no documented recommended range or trade-off explanation anywhere a user editing config.toml would see it** `[improvement]` 🟢 `[low]` - The only prose describing poll_interval_ms is the one-line doc-comment "Clipboard poll interval in milliseconds." (config.rs:17) - there's no guidance in the generated config.toml (toml::to_string_pretty doesn't preserve Rust doc comments as TOML comments) about the CPU/battery trade-off of a low value, or that values below 50ms are silently clamped (per the earlier finding). A user hand-editing the file sees a bare `poll_interval_ms = 300` with no inline explanation of safe bounds. _Evidence: src/config.rs:17-18,34; toml::to_string_pretty output does not carry Rust doc comments into the written file._
461. **Config has no field for controlling which clip kinds are eligible for the max_history cap independently (e.g. keep more text than images) - eviction treats all kinds identically regardless of size** `[idea]` 🟢 `[low]` - Store::enforce_cap (crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:201-219) evicts strictly by `updated_at ASC, seq ASC` across all rows regardless of kind or byte size, and Config's only quantity knob is the single flat max_history count. A config-level policy like `max_history_images` separate from `max_history_text`, or a `max_total_bytes` budget instead of (or alongside) a raw count, would let users keep e.g. 2000 small text clips but only 50 multi-MB images without one kind starving the other's retention window. _Evidence: src/config.rs:20 (single flat max_history); crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:201-219 (kind-agnostic eviction order)._
462. **No config-level way to pin the app's own popup window class/process from ever appearing in its own captured history (self-capture guard), leaving that entirely to the inert excluded_apps mechanism** `[idea]` 🟢 `[low]` - Even conceptually, there's no dedicated `exclude_self: bool` (default true) field distinct from the general excluded_apps list - copying text out of vbuff's own popup (e.g. selecting and Cmd+C-ing a preview row) would, once source-app population ships, need an explicit self-identifier in Config rather than relying on the user to know and type vbuff's own bundle id/process name into excluded_apps. _Evidence: src/config.rs:23-25 (no dedicated self-exclusion flag; only the general-purpose excluded_apps list exists)._
463. **main.rs enforces the history cap before the GUI ever hydrates or shows the user which items are about to be discarded** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - main.rs runs `store.enforce_cap(config.max_history)` (line 52-54) BEFORE `store.load_recent(GUI_LIMIT)` (line 55) hydrates the GUI snapshot. If a user lowers max_history between runs (e.g. from 500 to 50), the very next startup permanently deletes the now-over-cap older rows before the popup ever shows or the user confirms which items are about to be discarded - there is no "you are about to lose N items because max_history dropped, continue?" confirmation path, silent or otherwise. This is a distinct ordering/UX problem from max_history = 0's data-loss severity above; it applies to any downward change in the value, not just zero. _Evidence: src/main.rs:47-56._
464. **Two independent modifier vocabularies exist (hotkey parser's Meta/Control/Alt/Shift vs paste_modifier's OS-only Meta/Control) with no shared validation, so a config claiming paste_modifier = "alt" or "shift" would be accepted by TOML with no rejection if the field were ever wired up** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - Config::paste_modifier is an unconstrained String (config.rs:22) that (per the dead-field finding above) is never read at all - but even setting that aside, there's no validation restricting it to just "cmd"/"ctrl" as the doc-comment claims; `paste_modifier = "alt"` or `paste_modifier = "banana"` would pass TOML parsing and Config's Deserialize with no error, silently accepted as a nonsensical value with no enum-level guard (unlike hotkey's KeyCombo, which at least gets exercised through parse_combo's validation, even if paste_modifier never does). _Evidence: src/config.rs:21-22 (String, not an enum, no serde validation attribute or custom Deserialize impl)._
465. **No config field or mechanism for restricting which clip kinds trigger the global hotkey's auto-show behavior or filtering the popup's default view by kind - Config only gates capture, never presentation** `[idea]` 🟢 `[low]` - Every field in Config (hotkey, poll_interval_ms, max_history, paste_modifier, excluded_apps, skip_whitespace_only) governs either capture-thread behavior or the paste backend; none govern how the popup presents history by default (e.g. "default filter to text only", "hide images by default", "sort by frequency instead of recency"). As GUI features grow, presentation policy will likely need its own config section, and right now there's no established convention (e.g. a nested `[popup]` TOML table) for where such settings would live. _Evidence: src/config.rs:12-28 (all six fields are capture- or paste-scoped; none are presentation-scoped)._
466. **load_or_create writes a freshly created default config.toml to disk before the rest of startup has verified the store or hotkey backend can even initialize, so a first-run failure elsewhere still leaves a written config file with no marker that it was never validated by a working session** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - Config::load_or_create() (config.rs:58-69) calls cfg.save() immediately when the file doesn't exist, before main() has attempted Store::open_default() (main.rs:51) or GlobalHotkeyBackend::new() (main.rs:79). If either of those subsequently fails on a genuinely first run (e.g. a locked/permission-denied DB path or an unsupported hotkey backend), the user is left with a config.toml on disk from a run that never actually succeeded, with no marker distinguishing "this config was validated by a working session" from "this config was written but the app immediately crashed after." _Evidence: src/config.rs:64-67; src/main.rs:47,51-56,79 (save happens before store/hotkey initialization is attempted)._
467. **No environment-variable override mechanism for any config field, forcing every override (including one-off debugging) through the on-disk TOML file at the fixed OS-specific config_dir path** `[improvement]` 🟢 `[low]` - Unlike init_tracing() which respects RUST_LOG (main.rs:96), Config::load_or_create() has no equivalent VBUFF_* environment-variable override layer (e.g. VBUFF_CONFIG_PATH to point at an alternate file, or VBUFF_POLL_INTERVAL_MS for quick one-off testing). Every config change, including temporary ones for debugging a specific poll-interval or hotkey issue, requires editing the real config.toml at the real OS path and restarting, with no lightweight override for a single run. _Evidence: src/config.rs:56-69 (no env var lookups anywhere in the module); src/main.rs:94-98 (contrast with init_tracing's RUST_LOG support)._
468. **Config's default_hotkey() only special-cases macOS; Windows and Linux both silently share "Ctrl+Shift+V" with no per-OS differentiation for conflicts common on those platforms** `[improvement]` 🟢 `[low]` - default_hotkey() (config.rs:44-53) has exactly two branches: macOS gets "Cmd+Shift+V", and #[cfg(not(target_os = "macos"))] (i.e. every other target, Windows AND all Linux variants alike) gets "Ctrl+Shift+V" - a combo that collides with common browser/editor "paste and match style" or "reopen closed tab" type bindings on some Linux desktop environments and with some Windows password-manager defaults. There's no Windows-specific or per-desktop-environment default that accounts for these known collisions, unlike the OS-aware split that already exists for macOS. _Evidence: src/config.rs:44-53._
469. **Config derives Debug at the struct level with no field-level redaction, so a future broadened logging call would dump excluded_apps and paste_modifier verbatim into logs** `[idea]` 🟢 `[low]` - main.rs:48 currently logs only `config.hotkey` and `config.poll_interval_ms` explicitly via `tracing::info!(?config.hotkey, config.poll_interval_ms, ...)`, which is narrowly scoped and not itself a bug today. But Config derives `Debug` (config.rs:12) with no field-level redaction, so a very natural future change - `tracing::info!(?config, ...)` for a broader debug line - would dump excluded_apps and paste_modifier verbatim into logs with no guard against it; excluded_apps entries are exactly the kind of app-identity data a privacy-focused tool should treat carefully in its own logs. _Evidence: src/config.rs:12 (`#[derive(Clone, Debug, ...)]` with no field redaction); src/main.rs:48 (current call is narrowly scoped but the struct-level Debug derive invites a broader one later)._
470. **No config-level way to require confirmation or a grace period before excluded_apps changes take effect, so a typo'd broad pattern silently starts dropping clips on the very next poll** `[idea]` 🟢 `[low]` - Because Config is loaded once at startup and excluded_apps has no config-time preview or logging of what it matches (is_excluded, config.rs:83-88, is a pure boolean predicate with no tracing call on either branch), a user who hand-edits config.toml to add an overly broad exclusion pattern gets no feedback loop at all: the next capture-thread poll (capture.rs:67-72) silently starts discarding matching clips with nothing in the logs to show a match occurred, let alone which pattern caused it. _Evidence: src/config.rs:83-88 (is_excluded has no logging on match or non-match); src/capture.rs:67-72 (exclusion check has no tracing call)._

---

## Visual & interaction design (the GUI, evaluated with a designer's eye)

471. **Selected-row highlight is a flat, square-cornered fill with no border** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - In render.rs render_row, the only visual difference for the selected row is `ui.visuals().selection.bg_fill` passed to `egui::Frame::new().fill(bg)` with no `.corner_radius()` and no `.stroke()` call anywhere in the file. Every other surface in the popup (search box, buttons) uses egui's default rounded widget corners, so the one row that most needs a strong, intentional focus indicator is the only rectangle in the whole popup with hard 90-degree corners butted against the panel edges - it reads like a rendering glitch rather than a deliberate selection state. Fix: give the selection frame a corner_radius matching egui's default widget rounding and add a 1px stroke in the accent color so keyboard selection is unmistakable at a glance, not just a color swap. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-gui/src/render.rs:118 - `let frame = egui::Frame::new().fill(bg).inner_margin(SPACING_SM);` with no corner_radius/stroke call anywhere in the file._
472. **Selected-row fill has no inset - it touches the scroll area's left/right edges** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - `egui::Frame::new().fill(bg).inner_margin(SPACING_SM)` sets only inner_margin (padding for the row's own content); it never adds outer margin or reduces the frame width relative to the panel, so the colored selection rectangle spans edge-to-edge inside the CentralPanel, visually fusing with the window border on both sides. A selection highlight that bleeds into the chrome looks unfinished next to any list UI with a card-like inset (even 4px of horizontal margin) that lets the panel background show as a frame around the highlight. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-gui/src/render.rs:118 - frame built with `inner_margin(SPACING_SM)` only, no horizontal outer margin/width reduction, inside `egui::CentralPanel::default()` (render.rs:29) which itself uses egui's default (unset) panel margins._
473. **No hover state on unselected rows** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - render_row only branches background fill on `selected` (render.rs:112-116); there is no `.hovered()` check anywhere in render.rs that lightens/tints a row under the mouse. Combined with the fact the preview label is the only clickable sub-element (`Sense::click()` is attached to that Label alone), a mouse user gets zero visual feedback that a row is interactive until they notice the cursor change over the preview text specifically - the badge, icon/thumbnail, meta line, and action-button columns give no hover affordance at all. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-gui/src/render.rs:112-116 (only conditional background is `if selected {...} else {Color32::TRANSPARENT}`, no hovered() check) and render.rs:151-155 (`Sense::click()` attached only to the preview Label)._
474. **Delete and pin buttons are unlabeled emoji glyphs with no text fallback** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - The row's trailing actions render as bare emoji (a trash-bin glyph for delete, a pushpin/round-pin glyph for pin) inside `ui.small_button(...)`, relying entirely on emoji rendering plus a hover tooltip for meaning. Emoji glyph shapes vary substantially by platform font (Windows Segoe UI Emoji renders these differently from macOS Apple Color Emoji, or shows a missing-glyph tofu box on a minimal Linux install with no color-emoji font installed), so on some Linux setups these buttons could show as empty boxes with no visible affordance beyond the hover tooltip. Fix: pair each emoji with a 1-2 letter or short-word fallback label so button meaning doesn't depend entirely on emoji-font availability. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-gui/src/render.rs:175-180 - `ui.small_button("🗑")` for delete and `let pin_icon = if clip.pinned {"📌"} else {"📍"};` fed straight into `ui.small_button(pin_icon)`, with only `.on_hover_text(...)` as a fallback, no visible text label._
475. **Kind icon and row-action icons are drawn from unrelated emoji families with mismatched visual weight** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - `ContentKind::icon()` returns nine pictograph emoji (one per content kind) rendered at `ICON_FONT_SIZE` (20.0) in the thumbnail column, while the row actions use a completely different pair of emoji glyphs at the default small_button glyph size. None of these are drawn from a single icon set, so stroke weight, corner style, and visual density differ per icon - a document icon next to a trash-bin icon look like they came from two different apps because they did (different Unicode emoji design eras/styles even within one system emoji font). Fix: adopt one small consistent icon set (a bundled SVG/font icon pack rendered via egui's image/font-glyph support) for both kind icons and action icons so weight and style match. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-types/src/lib.rs:96-108 (ContentKind::icon returns nine distinct emoji glyphs) vs crates/vbuff-gui/src/render.rs:175,178 (two more distinct emoji glyphs for delete/pin) - two visually unrelated emoji sets used side by side in the same row._
476. **Popup shows and hides with a hard cut - no fade/scale transition on visibility toggle** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - `show()` and `hide()` in app.rs do nothing but flip `ViewportCommand::Visible(true/false)` (plus Focus on show); there is no opacity ramp and not a single `animate_` call anywhere in the crate. A global-hotkey summon popup that snaps fully opaque into existence and vanishes instantly reads as jarring/unpolished compared to virtually every competing clipboard-history popup, which all use a short fade or slide. Fix: drive the window's alpha via `clear_color`'s alpha channel (already customizable there) ramped over roughly 100-150ms using `ctx.animate_bool_with_time`, keyed off `visible`, before actually flipping `ViewportCommand::Visible(false)` so the fade is visible instead of the window disappearing on frame 1. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-gui/src/app.rs:74-88 - `show()` and `hide()` call only `ctx.send_viewport_cmd(ViewportCommand::Visible(...))`/`Focus`; grep for `animate_` across the vbuff-gui crate returns no results._
477. **Row selection changes (arrow keys, quick-pick) have no scroll-into-view guarantee** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - `handle_keys` in input.rs updates `self.selected` on ArrowDown/ArrowUp/quick-pick, but render_panel's `ScrollArea::vertical().show_rows(...)` never calls `scroll_to_cursor()` or `scroll_to_rect()` for the newly selected row. If the user presses ArrowDown repeatedly with more rows than fit on screen, the highlighted row can move below the visible viewport with no auto-scroll, leaving the user staring at a list where nothing appears selected even though a row is still receiving Enter/quick-pick actions off-screen. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-gui/src/input.rs:21-26 (selection index changes on ArrowDown/ArrowUp) and crates/vbuff-gui/src/render.rs:70-83 (`ScrollArea::vertical().show_rows` with no `scroll_to_*` call anywhere in render.rs, confirmed by grep across the crate)._
478. **Search box has no leading search icon or trailing clear button, and Esc doesn't clear the query first** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - The header's `egui::TextEdit::singleline(&mut self.query).hint_text(hint).desired_width(f32::INFINITY)` is a bare text field with no leading magnifying-glass glyph and no trailing 'x' to clear the query. Once a user types a filter, the only way to clear it is to select-all and delete manually - Escape is bound exclusively to hiding the whole popup, not to clearing the query first. Every comparable quick-launcher/palette UI (Spotlight, Alfred, VS Code command palette) pairs the input with both affordances and a two-stage Esc (clear, then dismiss); their absence here makes the search state feel like a dead end once populated. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-gui/src/render.rs:37-39 - TextEdit has hint_text only, no leading icon widget and no clear button; crates/vbuff-gui/src/input.rs:18-20 binds `Key::Escape` unconditionally to `UiAction::Hide` with no query-clearing branch._
479. **'N items' counter and Clear all / Pause buttons sit in the same visual row with no separation from the search box above** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - The status row (`ui.horizontal` containing the item count plus right-aligned Clear all/Pause buttons) is placed directly under the search box's `ui.horizontal` with no `ui.add_space()` between them - the single `ui.separator()` call comes only after both rows, not between them. The two rows read as one merged block; there's no breathing room to signal 'primary input' vs 'secondary status/controls' as distinct tiers, undercutting the type/spacing hierarchy a 3-tier header (search -> status -> list) should have. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-gui/src/render.rs:31-62 - search-box horizontal (31-48) is immediately followed by the status horizontal (50-61) with no `ui.add_space` call between them in source; the one `ui.separator()` (line 62) comes only after both._
480. **Empty state's copy nudge is generic and never mentions the actual configured hotkey** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - render_empty_state's zero-history copy is the static string 'Copy something and it will show up here.' - it never surfaces the user's actual configured show-popup hotkey, even though `config.rs` loads `Config.hotkey` at startup and `main.rs` logs it. `PopupApp` carries no hotkey-string field for render.rs to reference, so a brand-new user who dismissed the popup and reopened it via tray has no idea what key combo to press next time - the one first-run onboarding moment wastes it on a generic statement instead of a concrete, actionable hint. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-gui/src/render.rs:90-101 (render_empty_state) - hardcoded literal string with no interpolation of a hotkey value; src/config.rs:16 defines `pub hotkey: String` on `Config`, but `PopupApp`'s fields (crates/vbuff-gui/src/app.rs:25-50) hold no hotkey string at all._
481. **Empty-state illustration is entirely absent - only two lines of text at a fixed 24px top offset** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - render_empty_state adds `ui.add_space(24.0)` then two label calls with no icon, glyph, or illustration above the 'No clips yet' / 'No matches' text. A 520x600 popup with the entire body reduced to two centered lines of text and nothing else reads as an unfinished screen rather than a deliberately designed empty state; even a single large glyph or mark above the heading would anchor the eye and signal 'this is the whole screen, not a loading glitch'. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-gui/src/render.rs:90-101 - render_empty_state body is exactly `ui.add_space(24.0)` + `ui.vertical_centered` with two label/small calls, no icon/image widget anywhere in the function._
482. **Quick-pick digit badges (1-9) use plain low-contrast text with no keycap-style container** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - The quick-pick badge is drawn as `RichText::new(badge).weak().monospace()` inside a 14px-wide sized label (`QUICK_PICK_BADGE_WIDTH = 14.0` in theme.rs). `.weak()` intentionally lowers contrast, which is reasonable for a secondary affordance, but there's no visual container (no rounded-rect chip or border) distinguishing 'this is a keyboard shortcut' from 'this is a row index label' - at a glance a plain low-contrast digit reads as metadata (like a line number), not as an actionable Cmd/Ctrl+N hint, so the feature is easy to miss entirely on first use. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-gui/src/render.rs:125-133 and crates/vbuff-gui/src/theme.rs:26-31 (QUICK_PICK_BADGE_WIDTH = 14.0) - badge rendered as plain weak monospace text via `ui.add_sized`, no Frame/stroke/rounded-rect keycap styling._
483. **Row height (52px) is a single fixed constant with no taller variant for image/color rows** `[improvement]` 🟢 `[low]` - ROW_HEIGHT is a single constant (theme.rs, 52.0) used uniformly for every ContentKind via `show_rows(ui, ROW_HEIGHT, total, ...)`, even though an Image clip renders a 40x40 thumbnail plus two lines of text in the same 52px band as a plain single-line Text clip. Add a taller row variant (or let show_rows take per-kind heights) so image/color rows get enough vertical room for the thumbnail to breathe with margin above/below instead of being vertically cropped-tight against SPACING_SM padding on all sides. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-gui/src/theme.rs:16 (single `ROW_HEIGHT=52.0` constant) and crates/vbuff-gui/src/render.rs:72 (`show_rows` called with that one constant for every row regardless of `clip.meta.kind`)._
484. **Preview text truncates at a hardcoded 80-character budget regardless of available panel width** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - render_row calls `clip.preview(80)` unconditionally before egui's own `.truncate()` is applied to the Label - the character budget is a fixed number, not derived from the popup's actual 520px width or the runtime panel size. Nothing in `src/gui.rs`'s ViewportBuilder chain calls `with_resizable(false)` or sets a min size, so the window is resizable by the OS/WM by default; if it's ever resized narrower, rows either waste space with an untruncated blank tail or get double-truncated (once by the 80-char cut, once by egui's ellipsis), producing an arbitrary, non-responsive line length that doesn't adapt to actual layout. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-gui/src/render.rs:150 - `let preview = clip.preview(80);` is a fixed literal, followed by `.truncate()` at lines 151-155; src/gui.rs:28-34's ViewportBuilder chain has `with_inner_size`/`with_decorations`/`with_transparent`/`with_always_on_top` but no `with_resizable`/`with_min_inner_size` call._
485. **Meta line concatenates kind/app/time with a middle-dot but never truncates independently from the preview line above it** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - The meta line builds `meta.join(" · ")` from kind label, optional short_app_name, and relative_time, and passes it straight to `ui.small(...)` with no `.truncate()` call - unlike the preview Label two lines above it, which explicitly chains `.truncate()`. A clip with a long source-app name can push the meta line wider than the row, causing egui to either wrap it onto a second line (breaking the fixed ROW_HEIGHT budget and visually colliding with the next row) or overflow the panel width outright. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-gui/src/render.rs:163-170 - `ui.small(meta.join(" · "))` has no `.truncate()`/wrap control, contrasted with the preview Label at lines 151-155 which explicitly calls `.truncate()`._
486. **short_app_name has no length cap, feeding directly into the untruncated meta line** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - `short_app_name` for a bundle-id-style source containing dots returns the raw last dotted component with no length cap, and for anything not matching either the bundle-id or path heuristics it falls through to returning the entire input string unmodified. Paired with the meta line having no truncate() (previous finding), a malformed or unusually long `source_app` string set by any future platform backend renders as an unbounded-width line with zero defensive width handling anywhere in the render path. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-gui/src/view.rs:42-53 - short_app_name's final `let last = source.rsplit([...]).next().unwrap_or(source); last.strip_suffix(".app").unwrap_or(last).to_string()` has no length clamp, and the bundle-id branch (lines 44-49) returns `last.to_string()` uncapped._
487. **Search box hint text is the only paused-capture cue, and it disappears the moment the user types** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - The only visible cue that capture is paused is the search box's placeholder text switching to 'Search (capture PAUSED)…' - placeholder/hint text in egui renders in the same low-contrast gray as any empty-field hint and disappears the instant the user types a single character, at which point there is no persistent paused indicator anywhere else in the popup (no banner, no colored dot, no icon). A user who pauses capture, opens the popup, and starts typing a search loses the only paused signal that existed, and could mistake 'no new clips appearing' for a bug rather than the pause they set themselves. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-gui/src/render.rs:32-39 - `let hint = if paused {"Search (capture PAUSED)…"} else {"Search…"};` is passed only to `.hint_text(hint)`; no other paused-state rendering exists anywhere in render.rs._
488. **'Clear all' has no confirmation step despite being a destructive, irreversible bulk action** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - The status row's 'Clear all' small_button immediately pushes `UiAction::ClearAll` on click with no modal, no hold-to-confirm, no undo toast - a single misclick on a small_button-sized target sitting directly beside the equally small Pause/Resume button wipes all non-pinned/non-favorite history at once. Given the row is laid out right_to_left with Pause immediately adjacent, the two visually near-identical small buttons sitting side by side raise real risk of hitting the wrong one, with zero recovery path once clicked. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-gui/src/render.rs:52-59 - `if ui.small_button("Clear all").clicked() { self.actions.push_back(UiAction::ClearAll); }` fires the action directly with no confirmation UI, positioned immediately next to `ui.small_button(pause_label)` in the same right_to_left layout._
489. **Delete button has no confirmation either, and sits directly beside the Pin toggle in the same tight cluster** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - Per-row Delete fires `UiAction::Delete(clip.id)` immediately on click, with Pin rendered right next to it in the same right_to_left horizontal. Both are small_button-sized emoji glyphs at the far edge of a 52px-tall row, so a slightly imprecise click aimed at 'pin this' can land on 'delete this' instead, permanently removing a clip with no undo. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-gui/src/render.rs:174-184 - Delete and pin small_buttons are adjacent in one `right_to_left` `ui.with_layout` block, both firing their action synchronously on `.clicked()`._
490. **Pin icon uses two different emoji for on/off state instead of one glyph with a fill/outline or color change** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - The pin icon swaps between a pushpin emoji and a round-pin/location-marker emoji to indicate pinned vs unpinned. These are two semantically different pictographs (one reads as 'thumbtack', the other as 'map location marker') rather than a filled/outlined pair of the same icon, so the on/off state distinction depends on the user recognizing a subtle glyph-shape swap rather than an obvious visual toggle (color, fill, rotation) - a common source of 'wait, is this pinned or not?' confusion. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-gui/src/render.rs:178 - `let pin_icon = if clip.pinned { "📌" } else { "📍" };` swaps between two distinct emoji glyphs rather than one glyph with a state-driven fill/color change._
491. **Color-swatch clips render a flat filled rectangle with no border, indistinguishable from empty space at the dark end of the color space** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - `draw_color_swatch` paints `ui.painter().rect_filled(rect, 4.0, color)` with no stroke around the swatch. A copied near-black color (e.g. `#0a0a0a`) or a color close to the popup's own dark-theme background renders as a swatch nearly invisible against its own row background, with no outline to separate 'this is a color chip' from 'this is empty space'. Every serious color-picker UI (macOS color panel swatches, Figma's color chips) outlines swatches precisely because flat-fill-only breaks down at the extremes of the color space. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-gui/src/color.rs:6-11 - `ui.painter().rect_filled(rect, 4.0, color);` is the only paint call; no `rect_stroke` or border call anywhere in `draw_color_swatch`._
492. **Invalid/unparseable color clip text falls back to a flat gray swatch with no visual signal that parsing failed** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - `draw_color_swatch` does `parse_hex_color(text).unwrap_or(Color32::GRAY)` - if a clip was classified `ContentKind::Color` but its text doesn't parse as `#rgb`/`#rrggbb`/`#rrggbbaa` (e.g. an `rgb(...)` or `hsl(...)` string), the swatch silently renders as a generic mid-gray square identical to what a genuinely gray color clip would produce. The user has no way to distinguish 'this clip actually is gray' from 'vbuff failed to parse this as a color', which is a misleading, not just missing, signal. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-gui/src/color.rs:7,14-32 - `parse_hex_color` only handles hex forms (len 3/6/8) and returns `None` for anything else; `draw_color_swatch`'s `.unwrap_or(Color32::GRAY)` renders a real-color-looking swatch instead of an error/placeholder state for the `None` case._
493. **Thumbnail/icon column has no fixed-size container for the fallback glyph, so it doesn't line up with the 40x40 image/color slot** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - THUMBNAIL_SIZE (40.0) sizes both the image thumbnail and the color swatch to a 40x40 square, but the non-image/non-color fallback path renders `RichText::new(icon).size(ICON_FONT_SIZE)` where ICON_FONT_SIZE is only 20.0, with no fixed-size container around it - so Text/Url/Code/File/Rtf/Html/Other rows show a small emoji glyph roughly half the visual footprint of an Image or Color row's swatch, sitting in a variable-width slot rather than a consistent 40x40 box. This breaks the column alignment the QUICK_PICK_BADGE_WIDTH comment explicitly says the layout cares about: every row's icon/thumbnail column ends up a different visual size even though consistent alignment was the stated intent. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-gui/src/theme.rs:18-22 (THUMBNAIL_SIZE=40.0 vs ICON_FONT_SIZE=20.0) and crates/vbuff-gui/src/render.rs:144-146 - the icon-glyph branch (`ui.label(RichText::new(...).size(ICON_FONT_SIZE))`) is not wrapped in any `add_sized`/`allocate_exact_size` call, unlike the badge column at lines 130-133 which explicitly uses `add_sized` for alignment._
494. **No visual grouping/separator between rows - adjacent unselected rows have zero border, divider, or alternating tint** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - render_row's Frame has `fill(Color32::TRANSPARENT)` for every unselected row with no bottom-border stroke, no alternating-row background tint, and the ScrollArea itself never draws separators between rows. In a dense 52px-per-row list showing many items at once, rows visually run together into one undifferentiated block of text with no rhythm marking where one clip ends and the next begins, other than the raw vertical gap from row padding - a design choice at odds with virtually every list-based popup UI (mail clients, file pickers) that use at least a hairline divider or subtle zebra striping to aid scanning. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-gui/src/render.rs:112-118 - unselected background is always `Color32::TRANSPARENT` with no stroke/border, and no `ui.separator()` or divider call exists anywhere inside the `show_rows` closure (lines 72-83)._
495. **Tray icon is a single hardcoded 32x32 solid-blue square with no template/monochrome variant for macOS menu bar conventions** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - `build_icon()` in tray.rs generates one fixed bitmap: a solid blue fill with a darker blue 2px border, used unconditionally via `TrayIconBuilder::new().with_icon(icon)` with no `.with_icon_as_template(true)` call (which the vendored `tray-icon` 0.24 crate genuinely exposes) and no alternate rendering for macOS. macOS menu-bar icons are expected to be monochrome 'template images' that automatically invert for the system's light/dark menu bar and selection highlight; a solid saturated blue square instead sits as a jarring colored blob among neighboring monochrome menu-bar icons and will look out of place when the user switches the menu bar between light and dark. _Evidence: src/tray.rs:45-50 (`TrayIconBuilder::new()...with_icon(icon).build()?` with no template-image flag) and src/tray.rs:97-112 (`build_icon()` hardcodes RGBA bytes for a bordered solid-color square, no platform branch); `with_icon_as_template` confirmed present on `TrayIconBuilder` in the vendored tray-icon 0.24.1 crate source._
496. **Tray icon is a plain filled square with no shape, letterform, or clipboard glyph baked in** `[improvement]` 🟢 `[low]` - build_icon() procedurally draws a bordered solid-color square with no shape, letterform, or clipboard glyph in the pixel data - at the 16-22px menu-bar/notification-area render size most OSes scale a 32x32 source to, this is indistinguishable from any other placeholder app's default icon. Replace it with a simple recognizable glyph (a clipboard silhouette, or a letter mark) rasterized at build time, or load a bundled PNG/ICO asset instead of procedurally generating raw RGBA bytes at runtime, so the tray icon reads as vbuff rather than as an arbitrary blue swatch a user could confuse with an unrelated app. _Evidence: src/tray.rs:97-112 - build_icon()'s entire pixel-generation loop only tests `x < 2 || y < 2 || x >= N-2 || y >= N-2` for a border vs fill color; there is no glyph, letterform, or shape drawn beyond that flat border/fill split._
497. **Tray menu items for Copy latest clip / Clear history are disabled with no explanation shown to the user** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - `sync_state` sets `self.copy_latest.set_enabled(clip_count > 0)` and `self.clear_history.set_enabled(clip_count > 0)` so both items gray out when history is empty, but `MenuItem::new(...)` is constructed in `Tray::new()` with no tooltip/help text set anywhere in the file. A first-time user with an empty history who opens the tray sees two grayed-out items with zero explanation, which reads as broken menu items rather than an empty-state-appropriate disabled control. _Evidence: src/tray.rs:32-36 (`MenuItem::new("Copy latest clip", false, None)` / `MenuItem::new("Clear history", false, None)` - no tooltip call anywhere in the file) and src/tray.rs:66-74 (`sync_state` toggles enabled state with no accompanying explanatory text)._
498. **Popup window has no drop shadow or border definition despite being borderless/transparent and always-on-top** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - `ViewportBuilder::default().with_decorations(false).with_transparent(true).with_always_on_top()` removes OS window chrome entirely, and `clear_color` returns fully transparent `[0.0, 0.0, 0.0, 0.0]` with a comment that 'egui draws its own panel' - but `CentralPanel::default()`'s Frame is never customized with a shadow or stroke anywhere in render.rs. A borderless always-on-top popup floating over arbitrary desktop content (which can be any color/pattern) with no shadow or outline to separate it from whatever is behind it will visually blend into busy backgrounds, especially on Linux/X11 compositors without native shadow support for undecorated windows. _Evidence: src/gui.rs:28-34 (`with_decorations(false)`, `with_transparent(true)`) and crates/vbuff-gui/src/app.rs:98-101 (`clear_color` fully transparent) combined with render.rs:29 (`egui::CentralPanel::default().show(...)` - the default Frame, never customized with shadow/stroke anywhere in the crate, confirmed by grep)._
499. **Popup has a fixed 520x600 size with no minimum-size guard against accidental resize** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - `ViewportBuilder::default().with_inner_size([520.0, 600.0])` sets a one-time initial size with no `with_min_inner_size` call anywhere in gui.rs, and nothing in app.rs reads back or persists a resized viewport dimension across hotkey show/hide cycles or process restarts. If the OS/WM allows resizing an undecorated always-on-top window (platform-dependent but not prevented here), the user has no way to intentionally resize for a larger/smaller history view in a controlled way, and any accidental resize is lost (reset to 520x600) on next launch with no guard against shrinking to an unusably tiny size. _Evidence: src/gui.rs:28-34 - ViewportBuilder chain has `with_inner_size` but no `with_min_inner_size`/`with_resizable` call anywhere in the file._
500. **No visual weight difference between the primary preview text and the meta line beyond font size - both use the default full-contrast text color** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - The preview Label uses `RichText::new(preview).strong()` (bold weight, full-contrast default color) while the meta line uses `ui.small(...)`, which only changes size, not color - egui's `.small()` helper does not automatically dim text the way `.weak()` does. So the secondary metadata line (kind, app, time) renders at the same high-contrast foreground color as body text elsewhere, just smaller, rather than being visually deprioritized via a muted color the way a real type hierarchy (primary/secondary/tertiary) would use; only the quick-pick badge explicitly uses `.weak()` elsewhere in the same file, showing the inconsistency is a choice gap rather than a technical limitation. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-gui/src/render.rs:151-155 (preview: `.strong()`, no color override) vs render.rs:163-170 (meta: `ui.small(meta.join(" · "))`, no `.weak()`/color call) - contrasted with render.rs:132 where `.weak()` IS used for the quick-pick badge._
501. **Search box's focus styling relies entirely on egui's stock defaults with no accent treatment tuned for the transparent, chrome-less window** `[improvement]` 🟢 `[low]` - render_panel's TextEdit is built as a bare `egui::TextEdit::singleline(...)` with hint_text and desired_width only - the crate never calls `ctx.style_mut()`/`ctx.set_visuals()` anywhere, so whatever the OS/theme's default egui focus-ring color happens to be is the only focus indicator, with no consideration of whether that default is visible enough against the popup's fully transparent CentralPanel background versus egui's normal assumption of an opaque host window. _Evidence: Grepping crates/vbuff-gui/src for `visuals`/`set_style`/`Style::default` returns only render.rs:113 (`ui.visuals().selection.bg_fill`, a read) and app.rs:98 (`clear_color`'s unrelated parameter name) - no `ctx.set_visuals(...)`/`ctx.style_mut(...)` call exists anywhere to tune focus-ring or accent styling for the transparent window._
502. **small_button hit targets (Clear all, Pause/Resume, Delete, Pin) shrink already-tight click targets with no minimum-size override** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - Every interactive button in the popup - header controls and per-row actions - uses `ui.small_button(...)`, egui's explicitly reduced-padding button variant, with no minimum-size override applied anywhere. Combined with the fact per-row Delete/Pin sit inside a 52px-tall row alongside a preview label, meta line, and thumbnail column all competing for the same horizontal band, the actual clickable area for each action button is small relative to both the row height and to comfortable mouse-precision targets, compounding the earlier finding about accidental delete/clear clicks. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-gui/src/render.rs:53,57,175,180 - all four buttons in the file use `ui.small_button(...)`; no `ui.add_sized(...)` or min-size override wraps any of them (contrast with the badge label at line 130 which does use `add_sized` for a different reason)._
503. **No UI scaling/zoom control and no font-size customization anywhere in the popup** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - Every text size in the popup (ICON_FONT_SIZE, the preview's default label size, `.small()` for meta, `.monospace()` for the badge) is a hardcoded literal or an egui style default; nothing in vbuff-gui or the app wiring calls `ctx.set_pixels_per_point`, reads a zoom/scale factor from config, or exposes a font-size setting. A visually dense 52px-row popup with fixed-size emoji thumbnails and 20px icon glyphs cannot be scaled up for low-vision users or scaled down to fit more history on a small display without an OS-level accessibility zoom workaround, since nothing in the app itself is scale-aware. _Evidence: Grepping crates/vbuff-gui/src and src for `pixels_per_point`, `zoom`, and `Font` returns no scaling-control code; theme.rs's ICON_FONT_SIZE/ROW_HEIGHT/THUMBNAIL_SIZE constants (theme.rs:16-22) are the only size definitions in the crate and none are read from a config or adjustable setting._
504. **The `favorite` flag is fully wired in storage and eviction but has zero UI surface - no way to see, set, or distinguish it from `pinned`** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - `Clip.favorite: bool` has a real SQLite column, a dedicated `Store::set_favorite` method, and is checked alongside `pinned` in eviction protection (`is_protected`) and the cap-enforcement SQL - but `vbuff-gui`'s `UiAction` enum has no `SetFavorite` variant, `render.rs` never reads `clip.favorite` anywhere, and there is no button, icon, or visual state anywhere in the popup for it. A user (or any future automation) that sets `favorite = true` via the store API gets a clip that is silently protected from eviction with no visible indicator distinguishing it from an ordinary unpinned clip in the popup - the flag is a dead affordance from the GUI's perspective. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-types/src/lib.rs:252-253 (`pub favorite: bool` on Clip) and crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:152-157 (`set_favorite`) and crates/vbuff-core/src/eviction.rs:26 (`clip.pinned || clip.favorite` in `is_protected`) vs. crates/vbuff-gui/src/state.rs (UiAction has Paste/SetPinned/Delete/ClearAll/TogglePause/Hide only, no favorite variant) and crates/vbuff-gui/src/render.rs (no reference to `clip.favorite` anywhere in the file, confirmed by grep)._
