## Documentation consistency (additional, beyond the first 5)

505. **docs/mistakes-top-500.md's own intro contradicts its filename and title: 638 items, not 500** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - The file is named mistakes-top-500.md and its H1 (line 1) is '# vbuff - Top 500 Things Competitors Do Badly (and how vbuff fixes them)', but its own blockquote intro (line 3) says '**638** concrete anti-patterns, bugs and failures', and the last numbered entry (line 720) is '638. **Ownership transfer / acquisition...**'. The '500' in the filename/title was never updated after the catalog grew past 500, so the file's own title is self-contradicting before any cross-referencing document even quotes it. _Evidence: docs/mistakes-top-500.md line 1 ('Top 500 Things Competitors Do Badly') vs line 3 ('**638** concrete anti-patterns') vs line 720 (item '638. Ownership transfer / acquisition...'). Verified by reading the file directly._
506. **docs/features-top-500.md's own intro contradicts its filename and title: 640 items, not 500** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - Same pattern as mistakes-top-500.md: the file (line 1) is titled '# vbuff - Top 500 Clipboard Manager Features' but its own intro (line 3) says 'A catalog of **640** concrete features', and the last item (line 722) is '640. **AI-suggested recipients and channels**'. README.md and recommendation.md both correctly cite '640' in prose, which only makes the mismatched filename/H1 more conspicuous - a reader who trusts the filename alone will believe there are 500 entries. _Evidence: docs/features-top-500.md line 1 ('Top 500 Clipboard Manager Features') vs line 3 ('catalog of **640** concrete features') vs line 722 (item '640.'). Verified by reading the file directly._
507. **architecture.md and recommendation.md both cite docs/problems-improvements-top-500.md by name as an existing artifact, but the file does not exist in the repo** `[problem]` 🟠 `[high]` - architecture.md's 'Current module map' section says 'docs/problems-improvements-top-500.md catalogs the specific SOLID/DRY violations this addressed' (line 207, repeated line 286) and recommendation.md's section 6 also cites it by name (line 246: 'see architecture.md's "Current module map" section and docs/problems-improvements-top-500.md'), both describing it as an already-written artifact backing specific claims (the parse_rgba_dims dedup, the ClipMeta::updated_at fix). `ls docs/` confirms no such file exists anywhere in the repo, and a repo-wide grep for the string finds only these three citing lines. Any reader who greps for it hits a dead reference for a document both files treat as already authoritative. _Evidence: grep for 'problems-improvements-top-500' across the repo returns only architecture.md:207, architecture.md:286, and recommendation.md:246; `ls docs/` lists code-audit-top-50.md, competitive-analysis.md, competitor-extras.md, competitor-research.md, features-top-500.md, ideas-301-400.md, ideas-top-300.md, mistakes-top-500.md, pain-points.md - no problems-improvements file._
508. **docs/pain-points.md is cited as a grounding source in recommendation.md's own prose but omitted from README's and architecture.md's document-index lists** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - recommendation.md's header sourcing note (line 7) explicitly grounds 'competitor mistakes and differentiators' in 'docs/mistakes-top-500.md, docs/pain-points.md, and the 122-item docs/competitor-extras.md', and section 3's intro (line 105) repeats the citation; recommendation.md's own 'Related documents' list (line 280) correctly includes it too. But README.md's 'Documentation' list (lines 222-231) and architecture.md's 'Related documents' list (lines 1140-1147) both enumerate every other docs/*.md file (competitive-analysis, competitor-extras, features-top-500, ideas-top-300, ideas-301-400, mistakes-top-500, code-audit-top-50) except pain-points.md. A reader following README's or architecture.md's own index will never discover the file recommendation.md leans on for its Theme A-E competitor evidence. _Evidence: recommendation.md line 7 and line 105 cite docs/pain-points.md, and recommendation.md's own Related-documents list at line 280 includes it; README.md's Documentation section (lines 222-231) and architecture.md's Related-documents section (lines 1140-1147) both omit it entirely._

The target-state crate name in the docs does not match the crate actually chosen and shipped. _Evidence: architecture.md line 808 ('directories::ProjectDirs') and line 966 (dependency table row); Cargo.toml lines 49/88 list `dirs = "6"` / `dirs.workspace = true`, with no `directories` entry anywhere; crates/vbuff-store/src/paths.rs's own comment says it avoids a `dirs` dependency by hand-rolling path resolution._

521. **architecture.md's ideas-backlog section header and recommendation.md's companion header both restate the same 1-113/114-197/198-300/301-400 split inline rather than pointing to one canonical scope table** `[improvement]` 🟢 `[low]` - architecture.md's engineering-ideas section says '> Items 1-113 of a 400-idea backlog' (line 1154) and cross-links the other three ranges; recommendation.md's product-ideas section says '> Items 114-197 of a 400-idea backlog' (line 286) and does the same; docs/ideas-top-300.md and docs/ideas-301-400.md's own opening lines repeat the identical four-way split again. This is internally consistent today, not a contradiction, but the four-way duplication (two ranges inline in architecture.md/recommendation.md, two ranges as standalone docs/ files, each restating all four ranges in its own header) means updating the total count in the future requires touching four files' header prose in lockstep with no single canonical place stating 'the backlog has exactly 400 ideas, split 1-113/114-197/198-300/301-400.' A short table in README's Documentation section enumerating the four ranges next to their file links would remove the duplication risk and give one place to update if the backlog grows past 400. _Evidence: architecture.md line 1154, recommendation.md line 286, docs/ideas-top-300.md line 3, docs/ideas-301-400.md line 3 - four separate headers each independently restating the same 1-113/114-197/198-300/301-400 split with no single source of truth._
522. **README's platform-support caveat and architecture.md's storage-target caveat use inconsistent styles for badging the same kind of not-yet-built claim, making the badging convention itself undocumented** `[idea]` 🟢 `[low]` - Across the doc set, 'not yet built' claims are marked three different ways with no stated convention anywhere: README's platform table uses a blockquote disclaimer paragraph before the table ('Target design, not current state'); README's feature-highlights bullets use inline bold '**target**' tags with parenthetical audit citations; architecture.md's top-of-file disclaimer uses a single blockquote covering the whole document. Nothing in any of the four top-level docs states which convention applies where, so a reader cannot tell from formatting alone whether a given claim in a new section they haven't read yet will be caveated by a preceding blockquote, an inline tag, or nothing. Adding one line to README's or architecture.md's own front matter naming the convention ('Claims are marked **target** inline, or caveated by a blockquote immediately above the relevant table/section') would make the shipped-vs-target signal itself consistent and easier to trust across the whole doc set, not just within any single section. _Evidence: README.md line 21-24 uses a blockquote-before-table pattern for the platform table; README.md lines 49-53 use inline '**target**' tags per bullet; architecture.md lines 5-11 use one whole-document blockquote; no document states which convention governs which section._
523. ~~**recommendation.md's 'Related documents' list includes docs/pain-points.md but omits README.md itself, while architecture.md's equivalent list does include README.md - the two documents' own self-referential-omission conventions differ with no stated rule**~~ `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` **[FIXED]** - recommendation.md's 'Related documents' now opens with a `README.md` entry too, matching architecture.md's convention. Original finding: - architecture.md's 'Related documents' section (lines 1140-1147) opens with `README.md - project overview, build & usage` as its first entry. recommendation.md's 'Related documents' section (lines 271-280) never lists README.md at all, starting instead with architecture.md and plan.md. Both sections otherwise serve the identical purpose (an index of sibling documents), and README.md's own Documentation list (lines 222-231) never lists itself either - consistent with recommendation.md's omission but inconsistent with architecture.md's inclusion. There is no stated convention for whether a document's own index should list README.md, so the three top-level docs disagree on it in a way that is easy to miss and easy to get wrong again the next time one of these lists is edited. _Evidence: architecture.md's Related-documents list (line 1140) opens with an entry for README.md; recommendation.md's Related-documents list (lines 271-280) has no entry for README.md anywhere; README.md's own Documentation list (lines 222-231) also omits itself, matching recommendation.md's convention but not architecture.md's._

---

## Dependencies, supply chain & future extensibility

524. **No rust-version (MSRV) field anywhere in the workspace** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - Grep of the root Cargo.toml and every crate Cargo.toml turns up no `rust-version` key, and `edition = "2024"` plus `resolver = "3"` (root Cargo.toml lines 7-3) already require a very recent toolchain (edition 2024 stabilized in Rust 1.85). Nothing pins or documents the floor, so a contributor on an older stable toolchain gets an opaque edition/resolver parse error instead of a clear MSRV message, and there is no CI matrix (confirmed absent, see audit #36) to catch a regression if a future dependency bump silently raises the real floor further. _Evidence: Cargo.toml:1-9 (`edition = "2024"`, `resolver = "3"`, no `rust-version` key in `[workspace.package]`); same absence repeated in all five crates/*/Cargo.toml files._
525. **The `tray` feature transitively drags in the entire GTK3 stack on Linux** `[problem]` 🟠 `[high]` - Cargo.lock resolves `gtk 0.18.2`, `gdk 0.18.2`, `cairo-rs 0.18.5`, `gio 0.18.4`, and `glib 0.18.5` as dependencies of `libappindicator`/`muda`, which `tray-icon` (root Cargo.toml:45, enabled by default via the `tray` feature at line 69-70) pulls in on Linux. None of these are named anywhere in vbuff's own Cargo.toml files, so a contributor auditing `cargo tree` for what the binary links against will not find them by searching the manifests; they only appear by resolving `tray-icon`'s own Linux-specific dependency tree. This is a heavyweight, easy-to-miss native dependency (GTK3 + its C toolchain requirement) hiding behind a Rust feature flag that's on by default. _Evidence: Cargo.lock: `gtk 0.18.2` (line 1330) depends on `cairo-rs`; `libappindicator 0.9.0`/`muda 0.19.3` depend on `gtk`; root Cargo.toml:69-70 makes `tray` a default feature._
526. **44 crates resolve to two or more distinct major/minor versions simultaneously** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - Parsing Cargo.lock shows 44 crate names with duplicate version entries (verified programmatically), including security-relevant ones: `getrandom` at 0.2.17/0.3.4/0.4.3 (three copies), `rand`/`rand_core` at two majors each, `syn` at 1.0.109/2.0.118, `thiserror`/`thiserror-impl` at 1.0.69/2.0.18 despite the workspace itself pinning `thiserror = "2"` (root Cargo.toml:51), and `windows-sys` at four different versions (0.52/0.59/0.60/0.61). Every duplicate is extra compiled code, extra binary size, and an extra thing `cargo update`/`cargo audit` has to reconcile; a fix in one `getrandom` line does nothing for the other two copies still linked in. _Evidence: Cargo.lock (parsed programmatically, 442 `[[package]]` blocks): exactly 44 crate names with >1 version, e.g. `getrandom` ['0.2.17','0.3.4','0.4.3'], `thiserror` ['1.0.69','2.0.18'] (lines 3142,3151), `windows-sys` ['0.52.0','0.59.0','0.60.2','0.61.2'] (lines 4074-4103)._
527. **`egui_extras` is a declared dependency of `vbuff-gui` with zero references in its source** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - `crates/vbuff-gui/Cargo.toml:13` declares `egui_extras.workspace = true` (which itself pulls the `image` feature per the workspace table, root Cargo.toml:39), but grepping every `.rs` file under `crates/vbuff-gui/src/` (thumbnail.rs, color.rs, render.rs, lib.rs, theme.rs, state.rs, input.rs, app.rs, view.rs) for `egui_extras` finds zero matches - it is never imported or used anywhere. It compiles a whole extra crate (and its own transitive deps) into every build for no runtime benefit. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-gui/Cargo.toml:13 (`egui_extras.workspace = true`); `grep -rn egui_extras crates/vbuff-gui/src/*.rs` returns no matches in any of the nine source files._
528. **`image` crate's png/jpeg/bmp decoders are compiled in but structurally unreachable from any capture path** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - The workspace pins `image = { version = "0.25", features = ["png", "jpeg", "bmp"] }` (Cargo.toml:40) and `thumbnail.rs:63` calls `image::load_from_memory(bytes)` for the branch its own doc comment (lines 47-49) describes as handling 'encoded images (PNG/JPEG/BMP)'. But `ArboardClipboard::read()` (`crates/vbuff-platform/src/clipboard.rs:30-57`) only ever produces the custom `image/x-vbuff-rgba;...` mime via `rgba_mime()` (line 49) - there is no code path anywhere in the workspace that stores a `Flavor` with mime `image/png`, `image/jpeg`, or `image/bmp`. The three decoder features are dead weight today: compiled in, linked, but the branch that would use them is unreachable until a future capture backend actually writes encoded-image flavors. _Evidence: Cargo.toml:40 (`features = ["png", "jpeg", "bmp"]`); crates/vbuff-gui/src/thumbnail.rs:56-64 (branches on `image/x-vbuff-rgba` prefix, else falls through to `image::load_from_memory`); crates/vbuff-platform/src/clipboard.rs:44-51 (only ever produces the rgba mime, never png/jpeg/bmp)._
529. **No `cargo-deny`/`cargo-audit` config or CI step exists for license or advisory scanning** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - There is no `deny.toml`, `.cargo/audit.toml`, or any workflow file in the repository (confirmed by directory listing and by audit #36's independent finding that no `.github/workflows` exists at all). With 442 resolved packages across a dependency graph that includes GTK bindings, Windows FFI crates, and multiple crypto-adjacent RNG crates, there is currently no automated gate that would catch a newly-published RUSTSEC advisory or an incompatible license landing via a transitive bump - `cargo update` today is a purely manual, unaudited action. _Evidence: `ls` of the repo root and `crates/*` shows no `deny.toml` or `audit.toml`; combined with the already-documented absence of `.github/workflows` (code-audit-top-50.md #36), there is no scan step of any kind wired into the project._
530. **`serde_json` is a hard, non-optional dependency of `vbuff-store` purely for the flavor-blob encoding** `[improvement]` 🟡 `[medium]` - `crates/vbuff-store/Cargo.toml:13` pins `serde_json.workspace = true` unconditionally, and it exists solely to serialize `Vec<Flavor>` as a JSON blob column (per audit #25's finding that this encoding is 3-5x bulkier than raw bytes). When that encoding is eventually replaced with a binary format (bincode/postcard/a custom framed layout) to fix #25, `serde_json` should become removable from `vbuff-store` entirely rather than lingering as a legacy dependency nobody remembers to delete - worth tracking as a two-step change (swap encoding, then drop the dependency) rather than a single migration that leaves the old crate wired in 'just in case'.
531. **`vbuff-core`'s trait-free design blocks a clean seam for a future `vbuff-sync` conflict-resolution policy** `[improvement]` 🟡 `[medium]` - `crates/vbuff-core/src/lib.rs` exposes free functions (`detect_kind`, `evict`, `search`, `content_hash`) with no trait boundary at all - fine for a single-writer MVP, but architecture.md's target crate list has `vbuff-sync` performing 'record-level' conflict-resolving replication (architecture.md:1125) that will need to call into the same eviction/dedup policy `vbuff-core` already owns, but with a merge-aware variant (e.g. 'this clip exists locally with `updated_at` T1 and remotely with T2, which wins'). Since `evict()` and dedup are plain functions rather than an injectable `RetentionPolicy`/`ConflictPolicy` trait, `vbuff-sync` will either have to duplicate `vbuff-core`'s logic or `vbuff-core` will need a breaking API redesign at that point rather than an additive one.
532. **`Store` has no notification/event hook, so `vbuff-daemon`'s planned `StoreEvent::Inserted` fan-out has nowhere to attach** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - architecture.md:65 shows the target pipeline flowing store inserts through a `StoreEvent::Inserted` channel toward `vbuff-sync`. The actual `Store` in `crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs` has no observer/event/channel mechanism at all - `insert()` (line 71) just writes a row and returns `Result<ClipId>`; the only way today's code learns about a new clip is the capture thread manually re-querying `load_recent()` after every insert (`src/capture.rs:88-100`). Adding `vbuff-sync` later means either retrofitting an event-emission point into `Store::insert` (a change to a crate three other crates already depend on) or having `vbuff-sync` poll the DB independently, duplicating the capture thread's own polling pattern. _Evidence: architecture.md:65 (`StoreEvent::Inserted ────┼──► vbuff-sync`); crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:71 (`Store::insert` returns `Result<ClipId>` with no event/callback parameter); src/capture.rs:88-100 (capture thread manually calls `load_recent` after every insert instead of receiving an event)._
533. **`ClipId`'s ULID is generated from wall-clock time with no monotonic/node-id guard, which will collide under multi-device sync** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - `ClipId::new()` (`crates/vbuff-types/src/lib.rs:31-33`) calls `Ulid::new()`, which seeds the ULID's 80 random bits from the OS RNG on each call with no per-process monotonic counter and no device/node discriminator. vbuff-types' own doc comment (lines 24-25) explicitly justifies ULIDs as 'friendly to future sync (no central coordinator needed to allocate ids)', but two independent devices generating ids within the same millisecond have only the 80 random bits (not a device id) to avoid collision, and nothing in this crate reserves node-id bits the way sync-oriented ULID/UUID schemes (e.g. UUIDv7 with a node suffix) typically do. This is exactly the kind of on-disk id-format decision recommendation.md item 196 flags as needing a pre-sync data-contract freeze - and today's `ClipId` format has not been designed with that freeze in mind. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-types/src/lib.rs:22-33 (doc comment claims sync-friendliness; `ClipId::new()` calls `Ulid::new()` with no node/device discriminator argument)._
534. **No workspace-level `[workspace.lints]` table exists to enforce consistent clippy/rustc lint levels across the five crates plus the root binary** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - Cargo.toml's `[workspace]` section has no `[workspace.lints]` table, and none of the six `Cargo.toml` files (root plus five crates) reference `lints.workspace = true`. Today that just means clippy runs at its default level everywhere, but as the crate count grows toward the planned `vbuff-cli`/`vbuff-ipc`/`vbuff-daemon`/`vbuff-sync` split, each new crate will need someone to remember to opt into the same lint bar by hand rather than inheriting it automatically - there is no single place today that would let a future contributor add `unsafe_code = "forbid"` or `missing_docs = "warn"` once and have it apply everywhere. _Evidence: Cargo.toml (full file, no `[workspace.lints]` table); none of crates/{vbuff-types,vbuff-core,vbuff-store,vbuff-platform,vbuff-gui}/Cargo.toml reference `lints.workspace`._
535. **`vbuff-platform`'s traits are synchronous and blocking, which will not compose with an async `vbuff-ipc` server without a bridging layer** `[improvement]` 🟡 `[medium]` - `ClipboardBackend::read`/`write`, `HotkeyBackend::register`/`unregister`, and `PasteBackend::paste` (`crates/vbuff-platform/src/traits.rs:49-75`) are all plain synchronous `&mut self` methods called from a dedicated OS thread (`src/capture.rs:27` spawns a whole thread just to own the blocking poll loop). architecture.md's target `vbuff-ipc` is a 'framed protocol... client + server' - the conventional Rust implementation of a socket server that also needs to react to clipboard/hotkey events is async (tokio/async-std), and today's traits give no `async fn` variant or channel-based alternative. Whoever builds `vbuff-daemon` will need to either wrap every one of these trait calls in `spawn_blocking`-style adapters or redesign the trait signatures at that point - worth deciding now whether the traits stay sync-only (with the daemon explicitly bridging) or gain an async variant, since it changes every existing implementor (`ArboardClipboard`, `GlobalHotkeyBackend`, `EnigoPaste`).
536. **No feature flag exists to build `vbuff-store`/`vbuff-core` without the GUI/platform stack, yet the root binary is the only integration point** `[improvement]` 🟡 `[medium]` - The planned `vbuff-cli` (README.md:124, 'pure IPC client') will not need `vbuff-gui`, `eframe`, `egui`, `arboard`, `global-hotkey`, or `tray-icon` at all - it only needs to speak the future `vbuff-ipc` protocol. Right now there is no crate that exposes 'just the store + core logic' as an installable, GUI-free target: the root `vbuff` binary's Cargo.toml links every GUI/platform dependency unconditionally except `tray-icon` (which alone has a feature gate). When `vbuff-cli` is added as a sixth workspace member, it will import `vbuff-store`/`vbuff-core`/`vbuff-types` directly (fine, those are already GUI-free) but there is currently no precedent or documented convention in this workspace for how a leaf binary crate should selectively depend on the shared crates without also picking up transitive GUI weight - worth setting that precedent with the `tray` feature's already-established `dep:` pattern before a second and third binary crate need to make the same choice independently.
537. **`vbuff-types`' `RGBA_MIME_PREFIX`/`parse_rgba_dims` embed a vbuff-specific, unversioned wire format directly in the shared types crate** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - `crates/vbuff-types/src/rgba.rs` (re-exported at lib.rs:20) defines `image/x-vbuff-rgba;width=N;height=M` as a string-encoded custom mime that both `vbuff-platform` (writer, clipboard.rs:49) and `vbuff-gui` (reader, thumbnail.rs:56) parse by string-matching a prefix and splitting on `;`/`=`. This mime string is also what gets serialized into the SQLite `clips` table via `serde_clip.rs` (per audit #25), meaning it is already an on-disk data format. There is no version marker in the mime string itself (e.g. no `v1` component), so if the RGBA encoding ever needs to change (e.g. adding a stride or color-space field), old rows in an existing user's database become ambiguous with new rows - and this is exactly the kind of format recommendation.md item 196 says should be frozen deliberately before sync/CLI consumers attach, yet it already has three independent consumers (platform writer, GUI reader, store's JSON blob) with no format version anywhere in it. _Evidence: crates/vbuff-types/src/rgba.rs (defines the `image/x-vbuff-rgba;width=...;height=...` mime, re-exported vbuff-types/src/lib.rs:20); crates/vbuff-platform/src/clipboard.rs:49 (producer, via `rgba_mime`); crates/vbuff-gui/src/thumbnail.rs:56 (consumer, matches on the mime prefix) - no version field in the format._
538. **`chrono`'s `serde` feature is enabled workspace-wide even though `vbuff-platform` doesn't depend on `chrono` at all and `vbuff-core` only uses it in dev-dependencies** `[improvement]` 🟢 `[low]` - The workspace table pins `chrono = { version = "0.4", features = ["serde"] }` (Cargo.toml:26) as a single shared definition. `crates/vbuff-platform/Cargo.toml` has no `chrono` line at all, and `vbuff-core`'s only `chrono` reference is under `[dev-dependencies]` (crates/vbuff-core/Cargo.toml:15), not `[dependencies]`. That's a minor case of the workspace-dependencies table applying one feature set globally regardless of which crates actually need serde support for `chrono` types - harmless today, but as more crates join the workspace (`vbuff-sync` in particular will have its own serialization needs for wire types), it's worth deciding whether workspace-level dependency definitions carry a fixed feature set for every consumer or whether each crate should declare its own `chrono = { workspace = true, features = [...] }` overrides. _Evidence: Cargo.toml:26 (`chrono = { version = "0.4", features = ["serde"] }`); crates/vbuff-platform/Cargo.toml (no `chrono` entry anywhere); crates/vbuff-core/Cargo.toml:15 (`chrono.workspace = true` listed only under `[dev-dependencies]`, not `[dependencies]`)._
539. **`enigo` 0.6 is pinned as a plain version with no documented rationale or fallback, unlike the `tray` feature's own justification comment** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - Compare root Cargo.toml:66-67 ('if it ever proves troublesome to build/run on a given platform it can be disabled') - the `tray` feature has an explicit fallback comment - against `enigo.workspace = true` (`crates/vbuff-platform/Cargo.toml:12`), which has no comment anywhere explaining what happens if `enigo`'s synthetic-keystroke approach fails on a given platform (e.g. it needs Accessibility permission on macOS and can be blocked entirely by some Wayland compositors' security model). There is no feature flag to disable paste-back the way there is for tray, so a platform where `enigo` genuinely cannot function has no escape hatch and no documented decision trail for why this crate over alternatives (e.g. platform-native `SendInput`/`CGEventPost`/`XTestFakeKeyEvent` calls). _Evidence: Cargo.toml:66-70 (tray feature has an explanatory comment and an off-switch); crates/vbuff-platform/Cargo.toml:12 (`enigo.workspace = true`, no comment, no feature gate) - asymmetric treatment of two similarly OS-fragile dependencies._
540. **`ulid`'s `serde` feature is a workspace-wide pin but `ClipId`'s `Serialize`/`Deserialize` impls are hand-derived on a newtype wrapper, which may not match a future wire schema** `[improvement]` 🟢 `[low]` - `ulid = { version = "1.2", features = ["serde"] }` (Cargo.toml:24) enables `Ulid`'s own serde support, but `ClipId` (crates/vbuff-types/src/lib.rs:26-27) wraps `Ulid` in a tuple struct and derives `Serialize`/`Deserialize` on the wrapper via `#[derive(... Serialize, Deserialize)]`, which serializes with serde's default newtype handling rather than necessarily matching whatever wire representation a future `vbuff-ipc`/`vbuff-sync` JSON or binary schema expects. Worth deciding intentionally now - before external consumers (CLI JSON output, sync wire format) depend on the exact shape - whether `ClipId` should implement `Serialize`/`Deserialize` manually to guarantee a bare-string wire form.
541. **No `[workspace.metadata]` or per-crate `categories`/`keywords`/`readme`/`publish` fields exist, blocking a future crates.io publish of `vbuff-types`/`vbuff-core` and leaving the binary crate publishable by accident** `[improvement]` 🟢 `[low]` - All five crates set `license.workspace = true` (satisfying crates.io's license requirement) but none set `categories`, `keywords`, `readme`, or `documentation` fields, and the root `[package]` has no `publish` field either (confirmed absent workspace-wide), so it defaults to publishable, which is probably not intended for a `[[bin]]`-only crate. If `vbuff-core` or `vbuff-types` are ever useful standalone (e.g. another Rust clipboard tool wants vbuff's dedup/eviction policy), there is no metadata scaffolding in place today, and the root binary crate has no explicit `publish = false` guard against an accidental `cargo publish` of the whole workspace. _Evidence: Cargo.toml root `[package]` block (no `publish` field anywhere in the file); crates/*/Cargo.toml (none set `categories`, `keywords`, `readme`, or `documentation`; confirmed via grep across all six manifests)._
542. **`blake3` is duplicated as a direct dependency of the root binary even though the binary never calls `blake3::` directly** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - Root Cargo.toml:92 declares `blake3.workspace = true` as a direct dependency of the `vbuff` binary, and `vbuff-core` also depends on it directly (crates/vbuff-core/Cargo.toml:10) and re-exports `content_hash`/`content_hash_from_flavors` (crates/vbuff-core/src/lib.rs:19). Grepping `src/*.rs` for `blake3::` finds zero matches - `src/capture.rs:11,54` goes exclusively through `vbuff_core::content_hash_from_flavors`. The root binary's own `blake3` line is dead weight: it compiles the crate into the binary's own dependency graph a second time for no call site, and it is one more line that has to be kept in sync with `vbuff-core`'s own `blake3` version pin across two separate `Cargo.toml` files instead of one. _Evidence: Cargo.toml:92 (`blake3.workspace = true` under `[dependencies]` for the `vbuff` binary); crates/vbuff-core/Cargo.toml:10 (`blake3.workspace = true`); `grep -rn 'blake3::' src/*.rs` returns no matches, confirming the root binary never calls it directly and only reaches hashing via `vbuff_core::content_hash_from_flavors` (src/capture.rs:11,54)._
543. **`GlobalHotkeyBackend` and `ArboardClipboard` are constructed directly by binary-crate code (`main.rs`, `capture.rs`) rather than behind a factory the future daemon can substitute** `[improvement]` 🟡 `[medium]` - `src/main.rs:79` calls `GlobalHotkeyBackend::new()` directly, and `src/capture.rs:28` calls `ArboardClipboard::new()` directly - both are concrete-type constructions in the binary crate, not resolved through any factory/registry that could later choose between a cross-platform fallback (`arboard`/`global-hotkey`) and a native per-OS backend (the architecture.md-described XFIXES/wlr-data-control/AddClipboardFormatListener backends). When `vbuff-daemon` eventually needs to pick a backend at runtime (e.g. based on a Wayland-compositor capability probe), that selection logic has nowhere to live today except by editing `main.rs`/`capture.rs` directly, since there is no `Backend::detect() -> Box<dyn ClipboardBackend>`-style entry point in `vbuff-platform` for callers to use instead of naming the concrete struct. _Evidence: src/main.rs:79 (`GlobalHotkeyBackend::new().context(...)`); src/capture.rs:28 (`ArboardClipboard::new()` inside `match`) - both concrete-type constructions with no factory seam in `vbuff-platform`._
544. **`vbuff-store`'s `Store` type owns a single non-`Sync` `rusqlite::Connection` with no pooling story, which conflicts with a future multi-consumer daemon** `[improvement]` 🟡 `[medium]` - `crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:31-33` defines `Store { conn: Connection }` as a single owned connection wrapped externally in `Arc<Mutex<Store>>` by the binary (`src/main.rs:56`). That's adequate for one capture thread plus one GUI thread today, but `vbuff-ipc`'s server will likely need to service multiple concurrent CLI/GUI/sync clients querying the store at once; `rusqlite::Connection` is not `Sync`, so the `Arc<Mutex<>>` pattern already in use will serialize every read behind one lock indefinitely unless `vbuff-store` grows a connection-pool or `r2d2`-style API before the daemon needs concurrent readers. Nothing in the crate today signals this is a known future constraint (no doc comment, no `TODO`, no pooling abstraction started). _Evidence: crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs:31-33 (`pub struct Store { conn: Connection }`); src/main.rs:56 (`let store = Arc::new(Mutex::new(store));`) - single connection, no pooling type anywhere in the crate._
545. **No integration-test crate or `tests/` directory exists at the workspace root to pin cross-crate contracts before a `vbuff-ipc` wire format is added** `[improvement]` 🟢 `[low]` - Every existing test lives inside `#[cfg(test)] mod tests` blocks within each crate's own `src/`. There is no workspace-level `tests/` directory (checked: none exists at the repo root or under `crates/*/tests/`) exercising cross-crate behavior end-to-end (e.g. 'insert via vbuff-store, read back through vbuff-core::search, confirm the same Clip round-trips'). Before `vbuff-ipc` introduces a serialized wire format that has to stay compatible with whatever `vbuff-store`/`vbuff-types` produce, an integration-test harness that pins these cross-crate contracts (golden-file JSON snapshots of a `Clip`, for instance) would catch a breaking change at the boundary; today nothing would fail if `vbuff-types::Clip`'s serde shape changed incompatibly, since no test asserts a stable serialized form.
546. **`Cargo.lock` is 4528 lines / 442 packages for a five-crate MVP with a single native GUI backend, and nothing tracks or budgets that growth** `[idea]` 🟢 `[low]` - As `vbuff-cli`, `vbuff-ipc`, `vbuff-daemon`, and `vbuff-sync` are added, each will bring its own dependency tree (an async runtime for the IPC server, `ring`/`rustls`/`x25519`/`chacha20poly1305` for sync per recommendation.md's own architecture note, mDNS discovery libraries). Nothing today establishes a lockfile-size or duplicate-version budget as a project norm (e.g. a CI check that fails if `cargo tree -d` reports more duplicate crate versions than a checked-in baseline), so the 44-crate duplication already present (see the dedicated duplicate-versions item above) has no mechanism to keep it from silently doubling again with each new crate the architecture calls for. _Evidence: `wc -l Cargo.lock` = 4528; `grep -c '^\[\[package\]\]' Cargo.lock` = 442 (verified counts)._
547. **`arboard`'s resolved dependency tree shows no Wayland-native crate at all, meaning Linux clipboard access likely runs through XWayland rather than `wlr-data-control`** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - The workspace pins `arboard = "3.6"` (Cargo.toml:43) with no `features = [...]` list, so it builds with arboard's default feature set. Cargo.lock's resolved dependency list for `arboard 3.6.1` is `clipboard-win`, `image`, `log`, three `objc2*` crates, `parking_lot`, `percent-encoding`, `windows-sys`, and `x11rb` - no wayland-client, smithay-client-toolkit, or any other Wayland crate appears anywhere in arboard's own dependency block. The only Wayland-clipboard-capable crate resolved anywhere in the lockfile is `smithay-clipboard`, and tracing its reverse dependency shows it comes in via `egui-winit` (the GUI toolkit's own text-widget clipboard support), not via `arboard`. That is consistent with arboard falling back to X11/XWayland-compatibility clipboard access on Linux rather than native `wlr-data-control`, which compounds audit #17/#19's finding that there is no native Wayland capture backend at all. _Evidence: Cargo.toml:43 (`arboard = "3.6"`, no `features` array); Cargo.lock lines 90-107 (`arboard 3.6.1` dependencies list `x11rb` but no wayland crate); Cargo.lock (`smithay-clipboard` is a dependency of `egui-winit`, not of `arboard`, per the resolved dependency graph)._
548. **`rusqlite`'s `bundled` feature statically compiles SQLite from source on every build, with no documented fallback to a system-linked SQLite for downstream packagers** `[improvement]` 🟢 `[low]` - `rusqlite = { version = "0.37", features = ["bundled"] }` (Cargo.toml:29) is the only feature configuration; there is no alternate feature set or build-time switch (e.g. a `system-sqlite` cargo feature on the `vbuff-store` crate itself) for distro packagers who want to link against the OS-provided SQLite for CVE-patch-tracking or binary-size reasons. That's a reasonable default for an MVP (bundled avoids version-skew bugs), but as the project matures toward distro packaging (Homebrew/AUR/apt), not having even a documented escape hatch on the `vbuff-store` crate means every packager who wants system SQLite has to fork the manifest rather than flip a feature.
549. **No `deny(unsafe_code)` or audited `unsafe` inventory exists despite `enigo`, `arboard`, and `tray-icon` all wrapping platform FFI** `[improvement]` 🟢 `[low]` - vbuff's own crates appear to contain no `unsafe` blocks (consistent with the pure-logic design of `vbuff-core`/`vbuff-types`), but nothing enforces that going forward - there is no `#![forbid(unsafe_code)]` in any `lib.rs`/`main.rs` (checked: `crates/vbuff-core/src/lib.rs`, `crates/vbuff-types/src/lib.rs`, `crates/vbuff-store/src/lib.rs`, `crates/vbuff-platform/src/lib.rs`, `crates/vbuff-gui/src/lib.rs`, `src/main.rs` - none contain a `forbid`/`deny` attribute for `unsafe_code`). As the workspace grows toward native per-OS backends (architecture.md's planned XFIXES/AddClipboardFormatListener/wlr-data-control code, which will likely need raw FFI), it would be worth locking down the crates that should stay pure-safe (`vbuff-types`, `vbuff-core`) now, before a native backend crate's `unsafe` needs get intermingled with logic that should remain audit-simple.
550. **`vbuff-gui`'s `AppState`/`SharedState` types live in the GUI crate, but a headless `vbuff-daemon` will need the same shared-state shape without linking `egui`/`eframe`** `[problem]` 🟡 `[medium]` - `SharedState` (used by `src/capture.rs:12` as `vbuff_gui::SharedState`, and `AppState` constructed in `src/main.rs:35,59`) is defined inside the `vbuff-gui` crate, which depends on `eframe`, `egui`, `egui_extras`, and `image` (crates/vbuff-gui/Cargo.toml, `[dependencies]` block). The capture thread - which has nothing to do with rendering - already has to link the entire egui/eframe dependency tree today just to update `SharedState.clips`/`revision`. When `vbuff-daemon` is split out as a headless background process (README.md:121, 'Background wiring... as the model splits out'), it will inherit this same problem: the state type the capture logic needs to mutate is defined in a crate whose entire reason to exist is a windowed GUI toolkit, so either `vbuff-daemon` links `eframe` for no rendering purpose or `AppState`/`SharedState` need to move to a GUI-free crate (`vbuff-core` or a new `vbuff-app-state`) before the daemon split happens. _Evidence: src/capture.rs:12 (`use vbuff_gui::SharedState;`); crates/vbuff-gui/Cargo.toml `[dependencies]` (depends on eframe/egui/egui_extras/image just to define the shared state struct that the non-GUI capture thread also needs)._
551. **`tracing-subscriber`'s `env-filter` feature is enabled workspace-wide but only the root binary ever calls `EnvFilter`/`fmt().init()`** `[improvement]` 🟢 `[low]` - `tracing-subscriber = { version = "0.3", features = ["env-filter"] }` (Cargo.toml:53) is a workspace dependency, but only `src/main.rs:94-98` (`init_tracing`) actually constructs a subscriber; none of the five library crates depend on `tracing-subscriber` at all (they only take `tracing.workspace = true` for the emit-side macros, e.g. crates/vbuff-platform/Cargo.toml, crates/vbuff-store/Cargo.toml). That's correct layering (only the binary should install a subscriber), but it means `tracing-subscriber` doesn't need to be in the shared `[workspace.dependencies]` table at all - it could be a direct, binary-only dependency, which would make it obvious at a glance (without opening every crate's Cargo.toml) that it's a leaf-only concern rather than something every future crate (`vbuff-cli`, `vbuff-daemon`) is expected to also pull in from the shared table. _Evidence: Cargo.toml:53 (`tracing-subscriber = { version = "0.3", features = ["env-filter"] }` in `[workspace.dependencies]`); src/main.rs:94-98 (`fn init_tracing()` - the only call site of `EnvFilter`/`tracing_subscriber::fmt()` in the whole workspace)._
552. **`anyhow` is used for the root binary's error handling while every library crate uses `thiserror`, with no adapter path documented for how a future `vbuff-cli`/`vbuff-ipc` should propagate errors across the process boundary** `[improvement]` 🟢 `[low]` - `src/main.rs`/`src/config.rs` use `anyhow::Result`/`anyhow::Context` throughout (e.g. main.rs:34,44), while every library crate (`vbuff-store::StoreError`, `vbuff-platform::PlatformError`) defines its own `thiserror`-based enum. That split is a defensible, common pattern (binaries use anyhow, libraries use typed errors), but once `vbuff-ipc` needs to serialize an error back to a `vbuff-cli` client over the wire, an `anyhow::Error` (opaque, not `Serialize`) cannot cross that boundary the way `StoreError`/`PlatformError` could if they derived `Serialize`. Neither `StoreError` nor `PlatformError` derives `Serialize` today (both derive only `Debug, Error`), so even the typed-error side of the boundary isn't yet wire-ready; worth deciding the IPC error-wire-format story before those two enums grow further and need a breaking change to add serialization. _Evidence: src/main.rs:34,44 (anyhow::Context usage throughout); crates/vbuff-store/src/error.rs:6 and crates/vbuff-platform/src/error.rs:6 (`#[derive(Debug, Error)]` on both `StoreError`/`PlatformError`, neither derives Serialize)._
553. **The workspace has no `[workspace.metadata.release]` or version-bump tooling, yet six-plus crates will need coordinated version bumps once published as separate binaries** `[idea]` 🟢 `[low]` - Every crate currently pins `version.workspace = true` (e.g. crates/vbuff-core/Cargo.toml:3) against the single `[workspace.package] version = "0.1.0"` (Cargo.toml:6), so today a version bump is a one-line edit. Once `vbuff-cli` ships as an installable binary users `cargo install` directly, its version number becomes user-visible and potentially decoupled from the GUI binary's release cadence (a CLI bugfix release shouldn't force a GUI point release and vice versa). No tooling (`cargo-release`, `cargo-workspaces`, or even a documented convention in README/architecture.md) addresses whether the workspace intends lock-step versioning forever or per-crate versioning once multiple binaries exist - worth deciding before `vbuff-cli` ships its first release, since retrofitting independent versioning after users depend on a shared version number is a harder migration.
554. **`dirs` crate (not `directories`) is used for path resolution, diverging from architecture.md's own stated target dependency** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - The workspace pins `dirs = "6"` (Cargo.toml:49) and `src/config.rs:93` (`dirs::config_dir()`) uses it for path resolution. architecture.md:808 explicitly states 'Path resolution uses `directories::ProjectDirs`' (a different, API-incompatible crate by a different maintainer providing `ProjectDirs::from()` rather than bare `config_dir()`/`data_dir()`), and architecture.md's dependency table (line 966) also lists `directories`, not `dirs`, as the target for per-OS default data paths. Since `dirs` and `directories` return different path layouts (`dirs` has no per-app `ProjectDirs::from()` qualifier/organization/application triple), switching later is not a drop-in replacement - it will change the on-disk data/config directory path on at least one platform, which is a user-visible migration, not a transparent one. _Evidence: Cargo.toml:49 (`dirs = "6"`); src/config.rs:93 (`dirs::config_dir()`); architecture.md:808 ('Path resolution uses `directories::ProjectDirs`') and architecture.md:966 (dependency table lists `directories`, not `dirs`) - the shipped crate diverges from the documented target in both prose and the dependency table._
555. **`chrono` is pinned instead of `time`, with no documented one-time evaluation despite `vbuff-sync`'s future need to reason about cross-device clock skew** `[idea]` 🟢 `[low]` - The workspace depends on `chrono = { version = "0.4", features = ["serde"] }` (Cargo.toml:26) for `ClipMeta::created_at`/`updated_at` (crates/vbuff-types/src/lib.rs:210,216) and general timestamp handling. `chrono` has historically been the more security-sensitive of the two mainstream Rust time crates (RUSTSEC-2020-0071 concerned `chrono::Local`'s environment-variable handling on Unix, fixed years ago but a reminder that time-handling crates draw advisories). Since `vbuff-sync` will eventually need to reason about clock skew and timestamp ordering across devices for conflict resolution, this is worth a deliberate one-time evaluation (not necessarily a switch) of whether `chrono` or `time` better fits the cross-device ordering story before three more crates (`vbuff-daemon`, `vbuff-ipc`, `vbuff-sync`) each add their own `chrono::DateTime<Utc>` usages that would need updating together if the choice changes later. _Evidence: Cargo.toml:26 (`chrono = { version = "0.4", features = ["serde"] }`); crates/vbuff-types/src/lib.rs:210,216 (`ClipMeta::created_at`/`updated_at` typed as `DateTime<Utc>`)._
556. **`[workspace] members = ["crates/*"]` is a bare glob with no explicit exclusion list, so any new directory dropped under `crates/` silently joins the build** `[problem]` 🟢 `[low]` - Root Cargo.toml:2 sets `members = ["crates/*"]` - a wildcard, not an explicit `["crates/vbuff-types", "crates/vbuff-core", ...]` list. That's convenient today with five crates, but it means there is no single reviewable place that enumerates 'these are the crates in this workspace': dropping a scratch/experimental directory under `crates/` (e.g. a half-finished `crates/vbuff-sync-spike`) makes it a full workspace member - built, linted, and tested by `cargo build --workspace` - the moment it contains a `Cargo.toml`, with no opt-in step and no `exclude` list to catch it. As the workspace grows toward the six-plus crates architecture.md plans, an explicit member list (or at least a documented `exclude`) would make workspace membership an intentional, reviewable decision rather than 'whatever happens to have a Cargo.toml under crates/ right now'. _Evidence: Cargo.toml:2 (`members = ["crates/*"]`, a glob pattern with no `exclude` key anywhere in the `[workspace]` table)._
